# Unified Cost-Correctness Audit — Findings & Remediation

**Date:** 2026-06-27  
**Scope:** all 34 service adapters of the AWS Cost Optimization Scanner — strictly cost-fidelity (every emitted recommendation must produce a concrete, account-specific $ saving).  
**Method:** one read-only audit agent per service (Claude Opus 4.8, `Explore` read-only tools) executed that service's `docs/audits/prompts/<svc>_AUDIT_PROMPT.md` against the real adapter code, helper shims, `PricingEngine`, Cost Hub / Compute Optimizer wiring, and reporter handlers — with material pricing rates validated live via the AWS Pricing MCP. Every CRITICAL/HIGH finding was then re-checked by an independent adversarial verifier instructed to refute it.  
**Coverage:** 34/34 adapters audited — complete.

## How to read this

- **Severity:** 🔴 CRITICAL · 🟠 HIGH · 🟡 MEDIUM · 🟢 LOW.
- **Kind:** `confirmed_bug` (defect in current code) vs `limitation` (known coverage/accuracy gap).
- **Verify verdict** (CRITICAL/HIGH only): ✅ confirmed · ✏️ revised (real, but details corrected) · ❌ refuted (not a real issue) · ❓ uncertain (needs a live scan / live Pricing-API value). Findings with no badge are MEDIUM/LOW (not separately verified) or were not reached by the verifier.
- Each finding is self-contained for remediation: exact `file:lines`, evidence, $/coverage/safety impact, and a concrete fix.

## Summary

| Severity | Count |
|---|---|
| 🔴 CRITICAL | 29 |
| 🟠 HIGH | 84 |
| 🟡 MEDIUM | 109 |
| 🟢 LOW | 120 |
| **Total** | **342** |

**Adversarial verification:** 113 CRITICAL/HIGH findings checked — confirmed: 108 · revised: 4 · refuted: 1.

## Prioritized remediation plan

Priority = severity × verification confidence. **P0** = confirmed/revised CRITICAL · **P1** = confirmed/revised HIGH · **P2** = MEDIUM + unverified-but-likely CRITICAL/HIGH · **P3** = LOW. Refuted findings are excluded; uncertain CRITICAL/HIGH are flagged for a live-scan check.

### P0 — Confirmed CRITICAL (29)

- **AMI C1** — Launch-template / ASG resolution swallows errors with except: pass — a permission gap turns a LIVE in-use AMI into a delete-the-snapshots recommendation  (`services/ami.py:92-119`)
- **API Gateway C1** — Flat $50-per-recommendation fabrication when service total is $0 (the common case)  (`html_report_generator.py:82, 3076-3094 (consumed at 3113-3119, 2831, 2281-2284)`)
- **App Runner C1** — Shim emits ZERO recs for every account — adapter is a permanent no-op and its pricing loop is dead code  (`services/apprunner.py + services/adapters/apprunner.py:services/apprunner.py:24-60; services/adapters/apprunner.py:81-99`)
- **Athena C1** — Shim emits zero recommendations — adapter produces no Athena findings for any account  (`services/athena.py:24-53`)
- **Aurora C1** — Serverless v2 ACU savings fabricated from max capacity, not billed consumption  (`services/adapters/aurora.py:302-328`)
- **Batch C1** — Only Graviton recs count a dollar; Fargate-Spot / EC2-Spot / Job-Rightsizing advertise percentages but count $0 (string-vs-counted desync)  (`services/adapters/batch.py + services/batch_svc.py:batch.py:55-62; batch_svc.py:43-99`)
- **Batch C2** — Graviton saving multiplies by ×730 (24/7) with no usage metric — fabricated hours on the only counted check  (`services/adapters/batch.py:59-61`)
- **Bedrock C1** — Adapter reads nonexistent field 'modelId' — every PT prices at the $1/hr default AND both counted PT checks short-circuit, so PT analysis is structurally DEAD against real API responses  (`services/adapters/bedrock.py:138,142,148,180,183,189; CW dims 71,98,113`)
- **DMS C1** — Intra-adapter double-count: a <5% CPU instance is counted twice at 0.35× monthly  (`services/adapters/dms.py + services/dms.py:dms.py:39-48 (loop); services/dms.py:74-99 (buckets)`)
- **DMS C2** — Zero-datapoint CloudWatch → avg_cpu=0.0 flags metric-less instances as unused AND rightsizable  (`services/dms.py:70-99`)
- **DMS C3** — Swallowed CloudWatch failure still emits a counted 35% rec with no metric and no warning  (`services/dms.py:100-113`)
- **DynamoDB C1** — Over-Provisioned + Reserved Capacity stack on the same table -> savings exceed 100% of table cost  (`services/adapters/dynamodb.py:114-130`)
- **ElastiCache C1** — Cost Optimization Hub bucket ctx.cost_hub_splits["elasticache"] is populated but consumed by NO adapter — every ElastiCache CoH recommendation is silently dropped  (`services/adapters/elasticache.py + core/scan_orchestrator.py:elasticache.py:26-95 (scan never references cost_hub_splits); scan_orchestrator.py:57,92,135-142`)
- **ElastiCache C2** — Node price is mis-rated: MaxResults=1 with no usagetype/cacheEngine filter returns a non-NodeUsage / wrong-engine SKU, so every counted ElastiCache dollar is wrong  (`core/pricing_engine.py:1290-1298 (_fetch_generic_instance_price) and 1598-1611 (_call_pricing_api)`)
- **Glue C1** — Worker-based (current-gen) jobs priced at $0 — MaxCapacity=0 shadows the NumberOfWorkers fallback  (`services/adapters/glue.py:52-58 (with services/glue.py:33-43)`)
- **Glue C2** — ASSUMED_MONTHLY_DPU_HOURS=160 fabricates always-runs hours with no usage evidence  (`services/adapters/glue.py:44-49, 66-74`)
- **Lightsail C1** — oversized_instances counted at 100% of bundle cost (metric-less nudge) while card displays 30% — fabricated/inflated counted dollars + headline desync  (`services/adapters/lightsail.py / services/lightsail.py:adapter 48-52; shim 73-86`)
- **MediaStore C1** — Silent CloudWatch read failures yield false-unused + fabricated saving (no warn, no permission classification)  (`services/mediastore.py:45-58, 60-73, 75-89, 95-109`)
- **MSK C1** — Counted savings = (broker+storage) x 0.30 blanket factor with no utilization metric and no target instance — fabricated dollars  (`services/adapters/msk.py:40-56`)
- **Network (Data Transfer) C1** — Usage-type classifier scrambles the three transfer buckets against real AWS usage-type names (validated live)  (`services/adapters/network_cost.py:219-228`)
- **OpenSearch C1** — Orphaned Cost Optimization Hub bucket: ctx.cost_hub_splits['opensearch'] populated but never consumed  (`services/adapters/opensearch.py + core/scan_orchestrator.py:opensearch.py 29-100 (scan); scan_orchestrator.py 58, 93, 144`)
- **OpenSearch C2** — Idle Domain priced at $0 - largest real saving (full domain delete) never counted  (`services/adapters/opensearch.py + services/opensearch.py:opensearch.py 46-49, 58-64, 87; services/opensearch.py 147-155`)
- **QuickSight C1** — Edition-blind flat SPICE rate overcharges every Standard-edition account by 52%  (`services/adapters/quicksight.py:38-50`)
- **Redshift C1** — Orphaned Cost-Hub bucket: ctx.cost_hub_splits['redshift'] populated by orchestrator but never consumed by the adapter  (`services/adapters/redshift.py:35-83`)
- **Redshift C2** — Non-deterministic node-price SKU lookup (MaxResults=1; 3-4 SKUs share instanceType) corrupts the only counted dollar figure  (`core/pricing_engine.py:1290-1298, 1590-1622`)
- **SageMaker C1** — idle_notebooks fabricates a full-monthly saving for EVERY running notebook with zero idle evidence  (`services/adapters/sagemaker.py:175-217`)
- **Step Functions C1** — Counted savings lever is dead: eligible_for_migration is always False, so total_monthly_savings is always $0  (`services/adapters/step_functions.py:73-92`)
- **Step Functions C2** — Flat-$50-per-rec fabrication renders as account savings with no rate/metric/basis  (`html_report_generator.py:82, 3076-3094, 3113-3119`)
- **Transfer C1** — Counted savings region-scale a region-FLAT Transfer rate, inflating the headline and desyncing from the rendered string  (`services/adapters/transfer.py; services/transfer_svc.py:transfer.py:59-63; transfer_svc.py:54`)

### P1 — Confirmed HIGH (83)

- **AMI H1** — Outer except empties the entire AMI tab silently (logger.warning only, no ctx.warn/permission_issue)  (`services/ami.py:174-175`)
- **AMI H2** — describe_launch_templates / versions / auto_scaling_groups / launch_configurations are NOT paginated — large accounts drop in-use AMIs off the first page  (`services/ami.py:93-117`)
- **AMI H3** — Unused-detection misses reference paths: EC2 Fleet / Spot Fleet, cross-account (shared) usage, Image Builder  (`services/ami.py:84-119,140`)
- **API Gateway H1** — Silent per-API failure: except Exception: pass drops an API with no warn / permission classification  (`services/api_gateway.py:65-109 (108-109)`)
- **API Gateway H2** — CloudWatch metric except maps a throttled/failed read to monthly_requests=0.0, feeding the $50 fabrication  (`services/api_gateway.py:78-89`)
- **API Gateway H3** — Render-string vs counted-number desync: percentage string shown as 'Estimated Savings' while headline shows dollars  (`reporter_phase_a.py:316, 450-451 (rec source: services/api_gateway.py:102)`)
- **API Gateway H4** — REST-only coverage despite REST/HTTP docstring; HTTP and WebSocket (apigatewayv2) APIs never scanned  (`services/api_gateway.py:57-60 (docstring: services/adapters/api_gateway.py:28-32)`)
- **App Runner H1** — CloudWatch active-hours read is a guaranteed no-op (invalid dimension name AND invalid '*' value); requires_cloudwatch declared for a read that never affects any number  (`services/adapters/apprunner.py:54-72`)
- **App Runner H2** — Permission/throttle failures are swallowed or downgraded to generic warns — AccessDenied never classified as a permission_issue  (`services/apprunner.py + services/adapters/apprunner.py:services/apprunner.py:50-51, 53-54; services/adapters/apprunner.py:70-71`)
- **Athena H1** — CloudWatch failure silently converted to a $0 finding (no ctx.warn/permission_issue)  (`services/adapters/athena.py:62-64`)
- **Athena H2** — Bytes converted to TiB (2^40) while Athena bills per TB (10^12) — understates saving by 9.05%  (`services/adapters/athena.py:61`)
- **Aurora H1** — I/O-Optimized storage premium constant 5x too low vs live pricing  (`services/adapters/aurora.py:24,370-382`)
- **Aurora H2** — I/O-tier savings ignore the ~30% I/O-Optimized instance-price premium  (`services/adapters/aurora.py:369-386`)
- **Aurora H3** — Cross-adapter double count: same Aurora instance/cluster in Aurora tab and RDS tab  (`services/adapters/aurora.py:181-277`)
- **Aurora H4** — _describe_aurora_clusters swallows all errors silently — Aurora vanishes on AccessDenied/throttle  (`services/adapters/aurora.py:46-59`)
- **Batch H1** — is_fargate detection is broken — every Fargate CE is misclassified into the EC2 branch  (`services/batch_svc.py:39-41`)
- **Batch H2** — Inner `except Exception: pass` swallows describe_job_definitions failures (incl. AccessDenied) silently  (`services/batch_svc.py:80-101`)
- **Batch H3** — Outer except routes AccessDenied to a generic ctx.warn instead of ctx.permission_issue  (`services/batch_svc.py:102-103`)
- **Bedrock H1** — PT_HOURLY_DEFAULT = 1.0 is fabricated and ~20-24x too low, and the unknown-rate PT is still COUNTED at that rate (no Counted=False demotion)  (`services/adapters/bedrock.py:25,148-150,183-184,199-200`)
- **Bedrock H2** — PT_HOURLY_PRICE keys are truncated and cannot match full model ids; the four Claude entries are unverifiable (no Claude PT SKU exists) and commitment term is ignored  (`services/adapters/bedrock.py:18-24,148,183`)
- **Bedrock H3** — Breakeven on-demand estimate uses one flat $0.000003/token for input+output across all models — 12x too high for Haiku input and ignores that output bills ~5x input  (`services/adapters/bedrock.py:189-198`)
- **Bedrock H4** — CloudWatch dimension ModelId=<base model id> is wrong for a Provisioned Throughput — it measures on-demand traffic of the base model, not the PT  (`services/adapters/bedrock.py:71,98,113,142,189`)
- **CloudFront H1** — Swallowed CloudWatch exceptions silently drop the only live recommendation (no ctx.warn/permission_issue)  (`services/cloudfront.py:80-81, 127-128`)
- **CloudFront H2** — Un-gated CloudWatch reads; reads_fast_mode/requires_cloudwatch not declared so --fast does not skip CW  (`services/adapters/cloudfront.py (declaration) + services/cloudfront.py (reads):cloudfront.py:12-21 (no override); services/cloudfront.py:46-126`)
- **Commitment Analysis H1** — Advisory dollars (sp_coverage_gaps, purchase_recommendations) render as plain savings with no 'not counted' disclaimer  (`reporter_phase_b.py:1812-1876 (renderer); 1381 (dispatch); commitment_analysis.py:282,555,638 (advisory $)`)
- **Containers (ECS/EKS Fargate) H1** — Compute Optimizer ECS recs are never deduped against Cost Hub — same ECS service double-counted across the two AWS-native sources  (`services/adapters/containers.py:91-98, 138-139, 141`)
- **Containers (ECS/EKS Fargate) H2** — ECS Compute Optimizer helper swallows non-opt-in errors (AccessDenied/throttling) with logger-only, no ctx.warn/permission_issue  (`services/advisor.py:338-342`)
- **DMS H1** — Non-deterministic Single-AZ vs Multi-AZ SKU — counted rate can be 2× off  (`core/pricing_engine.py (consumed by services/adapters/dms.py:44-46,69-71):pricing_engine.py:1290-1298 (_fetch_generic_instance_price) + 1590-1613 (_call_pricing_api)`)
- **DMS H2** — Multi-AZ→Single-AZ saving halved when the lookup returns the Single-AZ SKU  (`services/adapters/dms.py:69-73`)
- **DynamoDB H1** — Fabricated $ from a capacity dimension with no utilization gate (0.30 default and 0.40 over-provisioned)  (`services/adapters/dynamodb.py:96-103, 114-124`)
- **DynamoDB H2** — Reserved Capacity counted instead of demoted to advisory (commitment lever)  (`services/adapters/dynamodb.py:114-130`)
- **DynamoDB H3** — GSI provisioned throughput invisible — base cost and over-provisioning under-counted  (`services/dynamodb.py:137-145, 306-309`)
- **EBS H1** — Intra-heuristic dedup gap: unattached volumes are double-counted with gp2_migration (and over_provisioned_iops)  (`services/ebs_logic.py + services/ebs.py + services/adapters/ebs.py:ebs_logic.py:113-119; ebs.py:570; ebs.py:464; ebs.py:288; adapters/ebs.py:170-202`)
- **EC2 H1** — _asg_member_instance_ids swallows AccessDenied and returns set(), silently disabling ASG-member dedup  (`services/adapters/ec2.py:48-70`)
- **EC2 H2** — Counted savings fabricated from Name/Environment tags with no usage evidence (cron 0.85, batch 0.75, instance-store 0.15, nonprod 0.64)  (`services/ec2.py:995-1093`)
- **EKS H1** — No CoH-vs-cluster dedup — same cluster counted by Cost Optimization Hub AND a heuristic cluster finding  (`services/adapters/eks.py:508-535 (build) / 145-153 (count)`)
- **EKS H2** — Idle-cluster false positive: Karpenter/self-managed clusters flagged idle → counts full control plane + recommends deleting a live cluster  (`services/adapters/eks.py:124-138 (is_idle) / 262-287 (idle rec)`)
- **EKS H3** — Reporter sums advisory (Counted=False) dollars into per-category card savings — rendered savings desync from counted headline and double-counts Spot+Graviton alternatives  (`reporter_phase_b.py:2034-2056`)
- **ElastiCache H1** — Graviton and Underutilized recs omit NumNodes -> priced for 1 node; multi-node clusters undercounted and the per-cluster 'best lever' dedup is distorted  (`services/elasticache.py + services/adapters/elasticache.py:elasticache.py (shim):96-104 (graviton, no NumNodes) and 149-158 (underutilized, no NumNodes); adapter elasticache.py:57`)
- **ElastiCache H2** — Graviton flat 0.20 factor overstates the realizable node-price saving (~4.6%) by ~4x; '20-40%' is a price-performance figure, not a cost reduction  (`services/adapters/elasticache.py:49 (rate_by_category 'Graviton Migration': 0.20) + 60-62`)
- **ElastiCache H3** — fast_mode not honored: CloudWatch get_metric_statistics runs per-cluster even under --fast; reads_fast_mode not declared  (`services/adapters/elasticache.py + services/elasticache.py:adapter elasticache.py:12-24 (no reads_fast_mode); shim elasticache.py:121-133 (ungated get_metric_statistics)`)

## Per-service findings

### AMI — `services/adapters/ami.py`

**Module identity:** key="ami", display_name="AMI", cli_aliases=("ami",), required_clients()=("ec2","autoscaling"); declares neither reads_fast_mode nor requires_cloudwatch (services/adapters/ami.py:15-21). AmiModule.scan is a thin wrapper over services/ami.py:compute_ami_checks. AMI has NO Cost Optimization Hub source, NO Compute Optimizer source, and NO CloudWatch reads (confirmed: no AmiImage entry in scan_orchestrator type_map; ctx.cost_hub_splits unused), so CoH/CO/CW axes do not apply. Pricing is locally derived: backing EBS-snapshot storage GB x get_ebs_snapshot_price_per_gb() (Standard tier), fallback 0.05 x pricing_multiplier. Emits two mutually-exclusive (by age) SourceBlocks old_amis (>90d) and unused_amis (30<age<=90d); both are quantified, counted deletion candidates.

**Verdict:** The AMI snapshot rate is correct and live-validated ($0.05/GB-mo Standard, region-scaled once), and the dollars that ARE emitted render and reconcile (counted==rendered via the dedicated _get_amis_content; no $0 or blank-card emission; instance-store AMIs with 0 GB are skipped; the AMI<->EBS snapshot-ownership boundary holds one-directionally because _current_ami_snapshot_ids excludes every snapshot backing any current AMI, a superset of what AMI counts). The fidelity risk is concentrated in deletion-SAFETY, not over-counting: the launch-template/ASG except: pass (C1) and the unpaginated LT/ASG describe calls (H2) silently shrink the in-use set on a permission gap or large account, converting live AMIs into destructive delete recs, and the outer except (H1) can empty the whole tab without any ctx signal. Secondary cost issues are no cross-AMI snapshot-id dedup (M1, headline inflation) and an upper-bound savings figure summed as if exact with no AuditBasis (M3).

**Pricing validation:** Validated LIVE via AWS Pricing MCP (get_pricing, AmazonEC2, us-east-1, productFamily='Storage Snapshot' + usagetype='EBS:SnapshotUsage'): SKU 7U7TWP44UP36AT3R returns $0.0500000000/GB-Mo (publicationDate 2026-06-26). This exactly matches FALLBACK_EBS_SNAPSHOT_GB_MONTH=0.05 (core/pricing_engine.py:79) and the engine's _fetch_ebs_snapshot_price filters (productFamily='Storage Snapshot', suffix 'EBS:SnapshotUsage', location=display_name) at core/pricing_engine.py:1134-1143. Region scaling is correct and single-applied: the engine path returns a region-correct price (location pinned to display_name) with NO extra multiplier in the adapter; the fallback path multiplies 0.05 by _fallback_multiplier inside the engine, and the adapter only applies pricing_multiplier when pricing_engine is None or raises (services/ami.py:124-130) — no double-multiply. Archive tier ($0.0125, FALLBACK_EBS_SNAPSHOT_ARCHIVE_GB_MONTH) exists but is not used by AMI (Standard tier only), which is correct.

**Cost checks:**

| Check | Status | Trigger | Savings basis |
|---|---|---|---|
| old_amis (unused AMI older than 90 days) | counted | Self-owned AMI (describe_images Owners=[self]) NOT in running_amis in-use set, age_days > OLD_SNAPSHOT_DAYS(90), and resolvable backing-snapshot storage > 0 (services/ami.py:140-153,173) | total_snapshot_size_gb x snapshot_rate, summed monthly. total_snapshot_size_gb from _snapshot_storage_gb (FullSnapshotSizeInBytes/1024^3, else snapshot VolumeSize, else block-device VolumeSize/8 on error). snapshot_rate = PricingEngine.get_ebs_snapshot_price_per_gb() Standard tier (productFamily=Storage Snapshot, usagetype suffix EBS:SnapshotUsage) = $0.05/GB-mo us-east-1 (live-validated), else 0.05 x pricing_multiplier fallback (services/ami.py:124-130,152) |
| unused_amis (unused AMI 30 < age <= 90 days) | counted | Same as old_amis but UNUSED_MIN_DAYS(30) < age_days <= OLD_SNAPSHOT_DAYS(90); is_old=False branch (services/ami.py:140,153,171,173) | Identical formula total_snapshot_size_gb x snapshot_rate; only the Recommendation text ('verify then delete') and CheckCategory ('Unused AMIs') differ. Counted into total_monthly_savings via float EstimatedMonthlySavings (services/adapters/ami.py:44-46) |

**Findings:**

#### 🔴 C1 · Launch-template / ASG resolution swallows errors with except: pass — a permission gap turns a LIVE in-use AMI into a delete-the-snapshots recommendation  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/ami.py:92-119`
- **Evidence:** try: lt_response = ec2.describe_launch_templates() ... except Exception: pass (93-104); try: asg_response = autoscaling.describe_auto_scaling_groups() ... describe_launch_configurations(...) except Exception: pass (106-119). If any of describe_launch_templates / describe_launch_template_versions / describe_auto_scaling_groups / describe_launch_configurations is denied or throttled, the referenced ImageIds never enter running_amis, so the in-use AMI passes the 'if ami_id in running_amis' guard at line 140 and is emitted with Recommendation 'deregister and delete snapshots'.
- **Impact:** Deletion-safety: a single AccessDenied (e.g. autoscaling:DescribeAutoScalingGroups not granted) silently converts every LT/ASG-referenced AMI into a false-positive destructive rec. Deregistering + deleting those snapshots breaks live launch configs/ASG scale-out. No ctx.warn/permission_issue is recorded, so the operator has no signal the in-use set is incomplete.
- **Fix:** Replace except: pass with services/_aws_errors.record_aws_error-style classification (AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation -> ctx.permission_issue, else ctx.warn) and FAIL SAFE: when any reference source cannot be enumerated, suppress unused-AMI emission (treat unresolved references as in-use) rather than emitting deletion recs against a partial in-use set.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified at services/ami.py:92-119. The LT-resolution block (try at 92 -> describe_launch_templates at 93; nested try at 95 -> describe_launch_template_versions at 96; nested except Exception: pass at 101-102; outer except Exception: pass at 103-104) and the ASG block (try at 106 -> describe_auto_scaling_groups at 107; nested try -> describe_launch_configurations at 111; nested except: pass at 116-117; outer except: pass at 118-119) swallow ALL exceptions with bare pass — no logging, no ctx.warn, no ctx.permission_issue. ctx.permission_issue/warn DO exist (core/scan_context.py:59,49) but are not called. A denied/throttled call therefore leaves the referenced ImageIds out of running_amis; an AMI referenced only via LT/ASG then passes the 'if ami_id in running_amis' guard at line 140 and is emitted with Recommendation 'deregister and delete snapshots' (line 164, for age_days > 90). Destructive false-positive with zero operator signal is real. Minor nuance (does not change severity): an AMI ALSO referenced by a running/stopped instance is still captured via the instance path at 84-90, so the at-risk set is precisely AMIs referenced only by LT/ASG (e.g., scaled-to-0 ASGs / scale-out-only launch templates) — exactly the 'breaks ASG scale-out' scenario the finding describes; the word 'every' is therefore slightly overbroad but the safety defect holds exactly as stated.

#### 🟠 H1 · Outer except empties the entire AMI tab silently (logger.warning only, no ctx.warn/permission_issue)  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/ami.py:174-175`
- **Evidence:** except Exception as e: logger.warning(f"Warning: Could not get AMI checks: {e}"). The try wraps describe_images and describe_instances pagination (76-173). ctx exposes warn()/permission_issue() (core/scan_context.py:49,59) but neither is called here.
- **Impact:** A denied/throttled describe_images or describe_instances makes compute_ami_checks return empty lists, so the AMI tab renders 'no unused AMIs' — indistinguishable from a clean account. Real recoverable snapshot storage is silently hidden and the permission gap is invisible in the report.
- **Fix:** Catch and classify on ctx: AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation/OptInRequired -> ctx.permission_issue(service='ami', action=...); other exceptions -> ctx.warn(service='ami', ...). Mirror the EBS shim pattern (services/ebs.py:434-435 already uses ctx.warn).
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified at services/ami.py:174-175: 'except Exception as e: logger.warning(f"Warning: Could not get AMI checks: {e}")'. The enclosing try opens at line 76 and wraps the describe_images paginator (78-82) and describe_instances paginator (85-90) plus all downstream logic through 173. A denied/throttled describe_images or describe_instances propagates to this handler, which only logs and falls through to 'return {recommendations: [], total_count: 0, ...}' (177-181) — empty unused/old lists. Neither ctx.warn nor ctx.permission_issue (available per core/scan_context.py:49,59) is invoked, so a permission gap is indistinguishable from a clean account in the rendered report. Real exactly as described.

#### 🟠 H2 · describe_launch_templates / versions / auto_scaling_groups / launch_configurations are NOT paginated — large accounts drop in-use AMIs off the first page  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/ami.py:93-117`
- **Evidence:** ec2.describe_launch_templates() (93), ec2.describe_launch_template_versions(LaunchTemplateId=...) (96), autoscaling.describe_auto_scaling_groups() (107), autoscaling.describe_launch_configurations(...) (111) are all single, non-paginated calls. By contrast describe_images (78-82) and describe_instances (85-90) correctly use get_paginator.
- **Impact:** Deletion-safety + coverage: an account with more LTs/LT-versions/ASGs than the default page returns only the first page; an in-use AMI referenced beyond the page boundary is omitted from running_amis and flagged 'unused -> deregister and delete snapshots'. Silent false-positive destructive rec.
- **Fix:** Use get_paginator('describe_launch_templates'), paginate describe_launch_template_versions, get_paginator('describe_auto_scaling_groups') and get_paginator('describe_launch_configurations') (or batch LC names) so the entire in-use set is enumerated.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified at services/ami.py:93-117. ec2.describe_launch_templates() (93), ec2.describe_launch_template_versions(LaunchTemplateId=...) (96), autoscaling.describe_auto_scaling_groups() (107), and autoscaling.describe_launch_configurations(...) (111) are all single direct calls with no get_paginator and no NextToken loop — contrast describe_images via get_paginator (78-82) and describe_instances via get_paginator (85-90). All four of these APIs are server-side paginated, so on accounts exceeding the default page size, in-use ImageIds beyond the first page are omitted from running_amis and the corresponding AMI is flagged unused -> destructive false positive. Lines and mechanism accurate.

#### 🟠 H3 · Unused-detection misses reference paths: EC2 Fleet / Spot Fleet, cross-account (shared) usage, Image Builder  ·  `limitation` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/ami.py:84-119,140`
- **Evidence:** running_amis is built only from running/stopped instance ImageId (84-90), all launch-template versions' ImageId (92-104, global so ASG-via-LaunchTemplate and MixedInstancesPolicy ARE indirectly covered), and ASG LaunchConfiguration ImageId (106-119). No consideration of EC2 Fleet / Spot Fleet launch specifications, AMIs shared to other accounts (a self-owned AMI consumed by another account still lists under Owners=[self] and would be flagged unused), or EC2 Image Builder pipeline outputs.
- **Impact:** Deletion-safety: an AMI actively used by a Spot Fleet override or shared to a sibling account is emitted as a delete candidate; deleting its snapshots breaks the consumer. Lower frequency than C1 but the same destructive outcome.
- **Fix:** Extend the in-use set with describe_fleets / describe_spot_fleet_requests launch-spec ImageIds; for shared AMIs, check describe_image_attribute(Attribute='launchPermission') and treat shared AMIs as in-use (or downgrade them to advisory). Document the residual gaps in the rec text.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified. running_amis is populated only from: running/stopped instance ImageId (84-90), launch-template-version ImageId (92-104), and ASG LaunchConfiguration ImageId (106-119). There is no describe_fleets / describe_spot_fleet_requests path, no Image Builder path, and describe_images uses Owners=['self'] (line 80) — so a self-owned AMI that is shared (LaunchPermission) to and launched by another account still lists under self and, absent a local instance/LT/ASG reference, is emitted as a delete candidate at lines 154-173. The candidate guard at line 140 only checks running_amis membership, confirming none of these reference paths are consulted. Same destructive snapshot-deletion outcome as C1 at lower frequency, as the finding itself scopes. The finding's own caveat that ASG-via-LaunchTemplate / MixedInstancesPolicy are indirectly covered by the global LT-version scan is also correct.

#### 🟡 M1 · No cross-AMI snapshot-id dedup — two AMIs sharing a backing snapshot each count the same storage, inflating the account total  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/ami.py:38,143-152`
- **Evidence:** _snapshot_storage_gb appends every backing snapshot_id and sums its size per-AMI (38,42-46); compute_ami_checks calls it independently for each AMI and adds monthly_snapshot_cost = total_snapshot_size_gb x snapshot_rate (152). There is no global set of already-counted snapshot ids across AMIs.
- **Impact:** Dollar inflation: EBS snapshots are incremental and a block/snapshot id can be shared across an AMI lineage (copies, re-registrations). When two emitted unused AMIs reference the same SnapshotId, that storage is summed twice into total_monthly_savings and the executive headline, so the counted figure can exceed real billable storage.
- **Fix:** Track a module-level seen_snapshot_ids set across the AMI loop; only add a snapshot's GB to the savings the first time its id is encountered (still list it under each AMI for context, but count the dollars once).

#### 🟡 M2 · _snapshot_storage_gb inner except inflates to VolumeSize/8GB on a describe_snapshots permission error without surfacing it  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/ami.py:39-49`
- **Evidence:** try: ec2.describe_snapshots(SnapshotIds=[snapshot_id]) ... except Exception as e: logger.warning(...); total_gb += ebs.get("VolumeSize", 8). A denied snapshots:DescribeSnapshots silently substitutes the provisioned block-device VolumeSize (or a hardcoded 8 GB) and the AMI is still emitted with an overstated saving.
- **Impact:** Dollar overstatement + hidden permission gap: the saving is computed on provisioned size (VolumeSize) rather than stored blocks (FullSnapshotSizeInBytes, ~2x smaller), and the failure is not recorded on ctx, so the 'max estimate' figure silently drifts upward with no operator signal.
- **Fix:** Classify the exception on ctx (AccessDenied -> ctx.permission_issue) instead of logger.warning only; consider skipping the AMI (or marking its basis 'unpriced') rather than substituting a fabricated VolumeSize/8 GB into a counted dollar figure.

#### 🟡 M3 · Counted savings is an upper-bound (provisioned/full size), but the float is summed into the executive headline as if exact; no structured AuditBasis  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/ami.py:152,159-170`
- **Evidence:** monthly_snapshot_cost = total_snapshot_size_gb x snapshot_rate (152) where total_snapshot_size_gb prefers FullSnapshotSizeInBytes but falls back to provisioned VolumeSize. The string EstimatedSavings carries a 'max estimate' qualifier (166-169) but the numeric EstimatedMonthlySavings (170) — summed into total_monthly_savings (services/adapters/ami.py:44-46) and the headline — carries no qualifier and no structured AuditBasis (rate/region/GB/formula), unlike the EBS snapshot recs.
- **Impact:** The headline AMI savings is an over-estimate (incremental snapshots bill only changed blocks; VolumeSize overstates ~2x) presented as a precise dollar total. Defensibility gap vs the EBS snapshot tab which carries an AuditBasis.
- **Fix:** Attach a structured AuditBasis (rate, region, GB source = FullSnapshotSizeInBytes vs VolumeSize-fallback, formula) to each rec mirroring the EBS snapshot recs, and keep the 'max estimate' qualifier visible wherever the numeric total is surfaced.

#### 🟢 L1 · Doc/code mismatch: services/adapters/CLAUDE.md lists ami.py as parse_dollar_savings() parse-rate, but the adapter sums the float EstimatedMonthlySavings field  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/CLAUDE.md:Parse-rate table row 'ami.py | parse_dollar_savings()'`
- **Evidence:** CLAUDE.md 'Parse-rate (5 adapters)' table: '| `ami.py` | `parse_dollar_savings()` |'. Actual code: services/adapters/ami.py:44-46 sums float(rec.get('EstimatedMonthlySavings', 0) or 0) — parse_dollar_savings is never imported or called in ami.py or services/ami.py.
- **Impact:** Documentation misclassifies the AMI pricing strategy (field-extraction, not parse-rate). Misleads future audits about whether per-unit rate strings are parser-guarded (they are bypassed entirely, which is safe here because EstimatedMonthlySavings is a true monthly float, not a $/GB rate).
- **Fix:** Move the ami.py row out of Parse-rate; describe it as field-extraction summing the float EstimatedMonthlySavings derived from snapshot GB x EBS snapshot rate.

#### 🟢 L2 · AMI render path differs from the brief and mislabels 30-90 day AMIs as '90-180 days'; brief's generic-per-rec assumption is moot  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `html_report_generator.py:2416-2424,2711-2745`
- **Evidence:** AMI is NOT rendered via the generic per-rec fallback — _get_tabs routes service_key=='ami' to the dedicated self._get_amis_content (2416-2424), which buckets by age_groups starting at '90-180 days' with 'if age_days <= 180' (2714,2738). unused_amis (age 31-90) therefore render under the '90-180 days' label. Fields read (ImageId, Name, AgeDays, EstimatedSavings, EstimatedMonthlySavings) all exist on the rec, so cards are NOT blank and counted==rendered holds (both sum the same float field).
- **Impact:** Cosmetic: a 45-day unused AMI is displayed under a '90-180 days' heading. No dollar/coverage impact; the per-service total and executive headline reconcile because _get_amis_content sums the same EstimatedMonthlySavings and the two sources are ImageId-disjoint so the ImageId dedup (2719-2734) drops nothing.
- **Fix:** Add a sub-90-day bucket (e.g. '30-90 days') to age_groups so unused_amis recs are labeled honestly; update the brief's Phase 0c note (AMI uses _get_amis_content, not render_generic_per_rec).

#### 🟢 L3 · AMI panel body merges EC2 enhanced 'ami' CheckCategory recs, which can desync the panel total from the strip/headline savings  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `html_report_generator.py:2588-2612,2449-2453`
- **Evidence:** _extract_amis_data pulls AMI-service recs AND any EC2 enhanced_checks rec whose CheckCategory contains 'ami' (2602-2610). The strip tile and executive headline use the AMI service's total_monthly_savings only (2414), while _get_amis_content totals the merged set (2761). If EC2 ever emits an 'ami' CheckCategory rec, the panel body total would exceed the strip/headline figure.
- **Impact:** Currently dormant (AMI logic was extracted to its own adapter; EC2 is not expected to emit 'ami' CheckCategory recs), but it is a latent counted-vs-rendered desync and a potential cross-adapter double-count if EC2 re-introduces AMI recs.
- **Fix:** Either drop the EC2 enhanced 'ami' merge in _extract_amis_data now that AMI is a first-class adapter, or compute the strip/headline AMI savings from the same merged+deduped set the panel renders so the two always agree.

---

### API Gateway — `services/adapters/api_gateway.py`

**Module identity:** key="api_gateway", cli_aliases=("api_gateway",), display_name="API Gateway", reads_fast_mode=True, requires_cloudwatch=True, required_clients()=("apigateway","cloudwatch") (services/adapters/api_gateway.py:15-25). Thin wrapper: scan() calls get_enhanced_api_gateway_checks(ctx) in the legacy shim services/api_gateway.py and sums rec["EstimatedMonthlySavings"] × ctx.pricing_multiplier once (line 43). Emits a SINGLE SourceBlock "enhanced_checks". Pricing is module constants (REST_PER_M=3.50, HTTP_PER_M=1.00, SAVINGS_PER_M=2.50; services/api_gateway.py:14-16), NOT PricingEngine — core/pricing_engine.py has no API Gateway method. Consumes NEITHER Cost Optimization Hub NOR Compute Optimizer (absent from scan_orchestrator type_map/_HUB_SERVICES and services/advisor.py — verified by grep), so "missing CoH/CO" is out of scope. Rendered in Phase A (reporter_phase_b.py:2500-2514 _PHASE_A_SERVICES; reporter_phase_a.py:310 PHASE_A_DESCRIPTORS, savings_mode="always") AND is in html_report_generator.py:82 _FLAT_SAVINGS_SERVICES — the flat-$50-per-rec override path.

**Verdict:** The api_gateway adapter emits exactly one counted check (rest_vs_http) whose dollar is sound ONLY when CloudWatch Detailed Metrics exist and volume stays in the first pricing tier — both validated live. Its dominant cost-fidelity defect is C1: api_gateway is in _FLAT_SAVINGS_SERVICES, so whenever the service total is $0 (fast_mode, no Detailed Metrics, or a throttled Count read — the default case) every REST API is assigned a fabricated $50/month with no rate, metric, or basis, driving both the tab headline and the executive summary. Two silent excepts (services/api_gateway.py:88, 108) feed that $0→$50 path without any ctx.warn/permission_issue, and a render-string/counted-number desync (H3) can show three different numbers for one rec. Coverage is REST-only despite a 'REST/HTTP' docstring (H4), and the flat $2.50/M delta overstates high-volume savings (M1). Fix C1 first (drop from _FLAT_SAVINGS_SERVICES; make metric-less recs Counted=False $0 advisory), then the silent-failure classification and the render desync.

**Pricing validation:** Validated LIVE via AWS Pricing MCP (AmazonApiGateway, us-east-1, publicationDate 2025-11-20): REST usagetype USE1-ApiGatewayRequest = $3.50/M first 333M, then $2.80/M (333M-1B), $2.38/M (1B-20B), $1.51/M (>20B) — confirms REST_PER_M=3.50 is first-tier only. HTTP usagetype USE1-ApiGatewayHttpRequest = $1.00/M first 300M, then $0.90/M — confirms HTTP_PER_M=1.00 first-tier only. Therefore SAVINGS_PER_M=2.50/M is correct only in the first tier (M1). WebSocket message/connection-minute rates and the API Gateway dedicated-cache $/hr adder were NOT validated live (no scanner check exists for them; lower priority) — needs live Pricing-API validation if H4/L2 fixes add or quantify those paths. Region scaling: ctx.pricing_multiplier is applied exactly once (services/adapters/api_gateway.py:43); per-M request rates vary little across regions so it is an approximation.

**Cost checks:**

| Check | Status | Trigger | Savings basis |
|---|---|---|---|
| rest_vs_http (Migrate Simple REST API to HTTP API) | counted | REST (v1) API returned by apigateway.get_paginator('get_rest_apis') whose non-paginated get_resources() item count <= 10 (services/api_gateway.py:60-69). One rec appended per qualifying REST API. | EstimatedMonthlySavings = (monthly_requests / 1_000_000) * SAVINGS_PER_M if monthly_requests>0 else 0.0 (services/api_gateway.py:91-93). SAVINGS_PER_M = REST_PER_M(3.50) - HTTP_PER_M(1.00) = 2.50 /M (lines 14-16). monthly_requests = 30-day Sum of CloudWatch AWS/ApiGateway 'Count', Dimension ApiName, Period=2592000 (lines 78-87), gated on `not ctx.fast_mode`. Region-scaled once by ctx.pricing_multiplier in the adapter (services/adapters/api_gateway.py:43). Live AWS Pricing API (AmazonApiGateway, us-east-1) confirms first-tier REST=$3.50/M and HTTP=$1.00/M, so the $2.50/M delta is first-tier-only. |

**Findings:**

#### 🔴 C1 · Flat $50-per-recommendation fabrication when service total is $0 (the common case)  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `html_report_generator.py:82, 3076-3094 (consumed at 3113-3119, 2831, 2281-2284)`
- **Evidence:** _FLAT_SAVINGS_SERVICES = {"opensearch", "api_gateway", "step_functions"} (line 82). _calculate_service_savings(): `if service_data.get('total_monthly_savings',0) > 0: return ...` else for each rec `if service_key in _FLAT_SAVINGS_SERVICES: total_savings += 50` (lines 3078, 3093-3094). The rest_vs_http rec carries NO `Counted=False` flag (services/api_gateway.py:95-107), so _counted_advisory_counts (html_report_generator.py:384) treats each as COUNTED. _get_service_content overrides service_data total with this value (lines 3114-3119) and the executive summary chart (line 2831) and reconciliation footnote (line 2281) reuse the same function.
- **Impact:** Whenever the per-service total_monthly_savings == 0 — which is the DEFAULT case: fast_mode, any account without per-stage Detailed CloudWatch Metrics, or a throttled Count read all yield EstimatedMonthlySavings=0.0 — every emitted REST API is assigned a fabricated $50/month with no rate, no metric, no basis. N qualifying REST APIs => $50N headline + executive-summary dollars out of thin air. All-or-nothing: a single API with a non-zero metric suppresses the override, so the number is wildly bimodal.
- **Fix:** Remove "api_gateway" from _FLAT_SAVINGS_SERVICES (html_report_generator.py:82). In the shim, when monthly_requests==0 emit the rec with `Counted=False` and EstimatedMonthlySavings=0.0 so it renders as $0 advisory (rendered, not counted) — never a bare $50 constant. Same bug applies to sibling _FLAT_SAVINGS_SERVICES members opensearch and step_functions (note as follow-up, do not fix unprompted).
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified exactly as described. html_report_generator.py:82 defines _FLAT_SAVINGS_SERVICES = {"opensearch","api_gateway","step_functions"}. _calculate_service_savings (3076) returns total early only if total_monthly_savings>0 (3078), otherwise loops every rec in every source and adds $50 per rec for _FLAT_SAVINGS_SERVICES (3093-3094) with no rate/metric/Counted check. _get_service_content (3111) copies service_data and overrides total_monthly_savings with this value (3117-3119); the tab headline at 3187-3188 renders that overridden value as ${savings_value:.2f}. The same function feeds the executive-summary chart (2831) and the reconciliation footnote (2281-2284). api_gateway reaches this path: _get_tabs routes non-AMI services through _get_service_content (2431), and the rest_vs_http rec (services/api_gateway.py:95-107) carries no Counted flag, so _counted_advisory_counts (logic at 384) counts each as COUNTED (advisory only when Counted is False). total_monthly_savings is 0 in the default cases: fast_mode skips the CW block (api_gateway.py:71) leaving monthly_requests=0.0, and any 0-datapoint/throttled Count read yields EstimatedMonthlySavings=0.0 (91-93) → adapter sum=0 (adapters/api_gateway.py:43). The override is all-or-nothing: a single API with a non-zero metric makes the adapter sum >0, suppressing the $50 path for all recs — bimodal as stated. Lines, mechanism, and impact all accurate.

#### 🟠 H1 · Silent per-API failure: except Exception: pass drops an API with no warn / permission classification  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/api_gateway.py:65-109 (108-109)`
- **Evidence:** The per-API block `resources = apigateway.get_resources(...)` ... CloudWatch read ... is wrapped by `except Exception: pass` (lines 108-109). An AccessDenied / UnauthorizedOperation / throttling error on get_resources silently discards that REST API. ScanContext exposes ctx.permission_issue(message, service, action) and ctx.warn (core/scan_context.py:49,59) but neither is called here. Only the OUTER except (lines 117-118) calls ctx.warn — and even that does not classify AccessDenied → permission_issue.
- **Impact:** Coverage under-count with zero operator signal: APIs the scanner lacks apigateway:GetResources permission for, or that throttle, vanish from the only emitted check. The user sees fewer recs and assumes the account is clean. No permission_issue is recorded for IAM gaps.
- **Fix:** Replace `except Exception: pass` with a classified handler: detect AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation/AccessDeniedException → ctx.permission_issue(..., 'api_gateway', 'apigateway:GetResources'); else ctx.warn(..., 'api_gateway'). Also classify the outer except (line 117-118) the same way. Mirror the EC2/network record_aws_error pattern.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified. The per-API block (services/api_gateway.py:65 try → get_resources at 66 → CW read) is wrapped by `except Exception:` / `pass` at 108-109, silently discarding that REST API. ScanContext exposes permission_issue (scan_context.py:59) and warn (49), but neither is called in the inner block. The only ctx.warn is the OUTER handler at 117-118, and it does not classify AccessDenied → permission_issue. The codebase has services/_aws_errors.record_aws_error which does AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation/OptInRequired → permission_issue classification, but api_gateway.py does not import or use it (only import is ScanContext). So an AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation on get_resources (not retried by boto adaptive retries) silently drops the API with zero operator signal, exactly as described.

#### 🟠 H2 · CloudWatch metric except maps a throttled/failed read to monthly_requests=0.0, feeding the $50 fabrication  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/api_gateway.py:78-89`
- **Evidence:** `resp = cw.get_metric_statistics(... MetricName='Count' ...)` is wrapped by `except Exception: monthly_requests = 0.0` (lines 88-89). A throttled or AccessDenied CloudWatch read is indistinguishable from a genuinely idle API: both yield monthly_requests=0.0 → EstimatedMonthlySavings=0.0 (lines 91-93) → with C1, $50 fabricated rather than a recorded warning.
- **Impact:** A transient CloudWatch throttle or missing cloudwatch:GetMetricStatistics permission silently converts to a $0/$50 path with no ctx.warn/permission_issue. The counted dollar is fabricated, not measured.
- **Fix:** In the inner except, classify the error: AccessDenied/throttling → ctx.permission_issue/ctx.warn('api_gateway') AND mark the rec Counted=False (advisory) so it is never assigned $50. Only treat a successful empty Datapoints response as a genuine 0.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified. cw.get_metric_statistics(...MetricName='Count'...) at services/api_gateway.py:78-87 is wrapped by `except Exception:` / `monthly_requests = 0.0` at 88-89, with no ctx.warn or permission_issue. estimated_savings is then 0.0 when monthly_requests is 0 (91-93), making a failed/AccessDenied CW read indistinguishable from a genuinely idle API. Combined with C1, this $0 then becomes a fabricated $50 in the headline/exec-summary rather than a recorded warning. Note: boto adaptive retries (core/session.py) absorb transient throttles, so the strongest case is missing cloudwatch:GetMetricStatistics permission — but that case fully validates the finding; mechanism and lines are correct.

#### 🟠 H3 · Render-string vs counted-number desync: percentage string shown as 'Estimated Savings' while headline shows dollars  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `reporter_phase_a.py:316, 450-451 (rec source: services/api_gateway.py:102)`
- **Evidence:** PHASE_A_DESCRIPTORS['api_gateway'] sets savings_mode='always' (reporter_phase_a.py:316). render_grouped_by_category then prints `Estimated Savings: {resources[0]['EstimatedSavings']}` (line 450-451), and EstimatedSavings is the LITERAL string "10-30% cost reduction for simple APIs" (services/api_gateway.py:102) — a percentage, not a dollar. Meanwhile the tab headline (html_report_generator.py:3187-3188) shows total_monthly_savings (the request-delta) OR the C1 flat-$50 override. The per-rec real dollar (EstimatedMonthlySavings) is never rendered anywhere.
- **Impact:** For one rec the card text ('10-30%'), the counted request-delta, and the flat-$50 headline can be three different, mutually inconsistent numbers. A FinOps reader cannot reconcile the card against the headline; erodes trust and hides the fabricated basis.
- **Fix:** Render a real per-rec dollar (EstimatedMonthlySavings, region-scaled) in the card, or relabel the percentage string as a qualitative note (not 'Estimated Savings'). Ensure card sum == tab headline == executive-summary contribution. Carry a structured AuditBasis (rate $2.50/M, region, 30-day Count window, formula) on each counted rec.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified. reporter_phase_a.py PHASE_A_DESCRIPTORS['api_gateway'] sets savings_mode='always' (316); render_grouped_by_category then emits `Estimated Savings: {resources[0]['EstimatedSavings']}` (450-451), and EstimatedSavings is the literal string '10-30% cost reduction for simple APIs' (services/api_gateway.py:102) — a percentage, not a dollar. The tab headline (html_report_generator.py:3187-3188) shows total_monthly_savings (the request-delta) OR the C1 flat-$50 override. The per-rec real dollar EstimatedMonthlySavings is never rendered for api_gateway: _extract_api_gateway_details (reporter_phase_a.py:213-216) returns only the resource id with empty detail, and grep confirms EstimatedMonthlySavings is rendered only for AMI (html_report_generator.py:2451/2761/2775) and phase_b (1039), never on the api_gateway card. Minor nuance: the headline cannot show the request-delta and the flat-$50 simultaneously (the $50 override only fires when the delta sum is 0), so 'three different numbers at once' is a slight overstatement — but the core desync (percentage string on the card vs dollars in the headline, real per-rec dollar never shown) is real at the cited lines.

#### 🟠 H4 · REST-only coverage despite REST/HTTP docstring; HTTP and WebSocket (apigatewayv2) APIs never scanned  ·  `limitation` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/api_gateway.py:57-60 (docstring: services/adapters/api_gateway.py:28-32)`
- **Evidence:** get_enhanced_api_gateway_checks paginates ONLY apigateway.get_paginator('get_rest_apis') (line 59) — REST v1 APIs. HTTP APIs and WebSocket APIs live under the separate apigatewayv2 client (get_apis) and are never enumerated; required_clients() omits 'apigatewayv2' (services/adapters/api_gateway.py:23-25). The adapter docstring claims it scans 'REST/HTTP APIs' (line 28).
- **Impact:** Whole API classes invisible. WebSocket APIs are billed (live AWS Pricing API, AmazonApiGateway: USE1-ApiGatewayMessage $1.00/M messages + connection-minute charge) and idle WebSocket APIs are a real, unflagged cost. HTTP APIs ($1/M) over-provisioned/unused are also uncovered. No fabricated dollar, but a coverage blind spot the docstring misrepresents.
- **Fix:** Either add apigatewayv2 coverage (add 'apigatewayv2' to required_clients, paginate get_apis, branch checks by ProtocolType HTTP/WEBSOCKET) or correct the docstring/CLAUDE.md to state REST-only scope explicitly. If adding WebSocket, validate USE1-ApiGatewayMessage / connection-minute rates live before counting.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified. get_enhanced_api_gateway_checks paginates only apigateway.get_paginator('get_rest_apis') (services/api_gateway.py:59) — REST v1 only. There is no apigatewayv2/get_apis enumeration anywhere, and required_clients() returns only ('apigateway','cloudwatch') (services/adapters/api_gateway.py:23-25), omitting apigatewayv2. Meanwhile the scan() docstring states 'Scan API Gateway REST/HTTP APIs for cost optimization opportunities.' (services/adapters/api_gateway.py:28), so HTTP and WebSocket (apigatewayv2) APIs are never scanned despite the REST/HTTP claim — a genuine coverage blind spot with a misleading docstring. The finding itself notes no fabricated dollar here. The specific AWS WebSocket/HTTP pricing figures in the impact are external claims not verifiable from this repo, but the code-level coverage gap and docstring overclaim are confirmed.

#### 🟡 M1 · Tiered-pricing flat delta overstates savings for high-volume APIs  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/api_gateway.py:14-16, 91-93`
- **Evidence:** SAVINGS_PER_M = REST_PER_M(3.50) - HTTP_PER_M(1.00) = 2.50 /M, applied flat for all volumes (lines 14-16, 91-93). Live AWS Pricing API (AmazonApiGateway us-east-1): REST USE1-ApiGatewayRequest is tiered $3.50/M (first 333M), $2.80/M (333M-1B), $2.38/M (1B-20B), $1.51/M (>20B); HTTP USE1-ApiGatewayHttpRequest is $1.00/M (first 300M), $0.90/M (>300M). So beyond the first tier the true REST→HTTP delta is $2.80-$0.90=$1.90 or $2.38-$0.90=$1.48, not $2.50.
- **Impact:** $2.50/M is correct only in the first tier. For a >333M-req/mo REST API the flat delta overstates the migration saving by ~24-41%. Counted dollar is mis-rated upward for high-traffic APIs.
- **Fix:** Apply the tiered REST and HTTP schedules (validated above) when computing the delta, or explicitly label the $2.50/M number a first-tier upper bound in the AuditBasis. REST/HTTP per-M rates barely vary by region, so ctx.pricing_multiplier remains an approximation — acceptable.

#### 🟡 M2 · CloudWatch ApiName-dimension fragility: requires Detailed Metrics, non-unique, no Stage dimension  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/api_gateway.py:78-87`
- **Evidence:** Count is queried with Dimensions=[{'Name':'ApiName','Value':api_name}] only (line 81), Period=2592000, 30-day Sum. The AWS/ApiGateway Count metric is only published when Detailed CloudWatch Metrics are enabled per stage (extra cost, off by default). ApiName is non-unique across stages and across duplicate-named APIs, and no Stage/Method dimension is supplied.
- **Impact:** On the (majority) of stages without Detailed Metrics, Datapoints is empty → monthly_requests=0.0 → EstimatedMonthlySavings=0.0 → C1 flat-$50. Where two APIs share a name, the Sum conflates them. This is the coverage-vs-fabrication interaction that makes C1 fire by default.
- **Fix:** Document the Detailed-Metrics dependency; when Datapoints is empty, emit Counted=False advisory (paired with C1 fix) rather than $0→$50. Consider keying the metric by the API's stage(s) or noting the ApiName collision risk in the AuditBasis.

#### 🟡 M3 · resource_count<=10 gate runs against a non-paginated get_resources and is an unvalidated proxy  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/api_gateway.py:66-69`
- **Evidence:** `resources = apigateway.get_resources(restApiId=api_id)` is a single, non-paginated call (line 66; no `limit`/`position` handling), then `if resource_count <= 10` (line 69). AWS get_resources default page size is 25, so resource_count = min(actual, 25).
- **Impact:** Two effects. (1) The brief's 'wrongly passes the <=10 gate' scenario is NOT actually reachable: with default page size 25, an API with >10 resources returns >=11 on the first page, so it is correctly excluded — under-count only matters cosmetically for APIs with >25 resources (already excluded). (2) The real gap is the cutoff itself: a high-cost 'simple' REST API with 11+ resources is silently excluded from the ONLY savings check, and <=10 is an arbitrary, unvalidated proxy for HTTP-API feature compatibility.
- **Fix:** Paginate get_resources via the `position` token for an accurate count (defensive), and replace/justify the <=10 threshold with a feature-compatibility signal (e.g. absence of REST-only features) or widen it. Document the cutoff rationale.

#### 🟢 L1 · Module-identity doc drift: 'Keyword-based'/'Keyword-rate' label and 'REST/HTTP' docstring contradict real behaviour  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/api_gateway.py:13, 28-33 (and services/adapters/CLAUDE.md 'Parse-rate (5 adapters)' row)`
- **Evidence:** Class docstring says 'Keyword-rate savings strategy' (line 13); scan() docstring says it scans 'REST/HTTP APIs' and computes '(REST $3.50/M - HTTP $1.00/M) × monthly_requests' (lines 28-32). services/adapters/CLAUDE.md lists api_gateway under 'Parse-rate (5 adapters)' / Method 'Keyword-based'. Reality: REST-only, CloudWatch-Count-driven request delta with a reporter-side flat-$50 override — not keyword parsing of a dollar string.
- **Impact:** Documentation misrepresents both the pricing mechanism (no keyword parse; a metric-driven delta plus a $50 fabrication) and the coverage (REST-only, not REST/HTTP). Misleads future auditors/maintainers; no direct dollar impact.
- **Fix:** Update the class/scan docstrings and the CLAUDE.md row to: REST-only coverage, CloudWatch-Count request-delta at $2.50/M first-tier, and the _FLAT_SAVINGS_SERVICES flat-$50 path (to be removed per C1).

#### 🟢 L2 · Orphaned optimization descriptions (incl. wrong-direction caching) are dead config, never rendered  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/api_gateway.py:18-44 (29-33)`
- **Evidence:** API_GATEWAY_OPTIMIZATION_DESCRIPTIONS defines unused_stages, caching_opportunities, throttling_optimization, request_validation (lines 24-43); get_enhanced_api_gateway_checks initializes these check buckets empty (lines 49-55) and never appends. caching_opportunities claims caching 'Enable API Gateway Caching ... unnecessary backend calls that increase costs' (lines 29-33) — wrong cost direction: a dedicated API Gateway cache is a $0.020-$3.80/hr ADDER (productFamily 'Amazon API Gateway Cache'). Moreover the reporter's opportunities loop keys on source name (html_report_generator.py:3203-3217): the adapter emits only the 'enhanced_checks' source, so sources.get('caching_opportunities')/etc. are always {} and NONE of these descriptions ever render.
- **Impact:** No user-facing harm today (the misleading caching nudge is never displayed because the desc key never matches the single 'enhanced_checks' source key), but the descriptions are dead weight and the caching text is a latent non-cost/misleading nudge if wiring changes. The caching FINDING was already removed (lines 111-115); the description should follow.
- **Fix:** Delete the four never-emitted description entries (or at minimum the caching_opportunities entry) from API_GATEWAY_OPTIMIZATION_DESCRIPTIONS so the wrong-direction caching nudge cannot resurface.

### App Runner — `services/adapters/apprunner.py`

**Module identity:** key="apprunner", cli_aliases=("apprunner",), display_name="App Runner", reads_fast_mode=True, requires_cloudwatch=True, required_clients()=("apprunner","cloudwatch") — all confirmed at services/adapters/apprunner.py:21-29. Registered in ALL_MODULES (services/__init__.py:9,63), so it runs every scan. Pricing is module-constant (APP_RUNNER_VCPU_HOURLY=0.064, APP_RUNNER_MEM_GB_HOURLY=0.007, DEFAULT_ACTIVE_HOURS_PER_MONTH=160, RIGHTSIZING_SAVINGS_RATE=0.12); there is NO PricingEngine method for App Runner. Cost Optimization Hub and Compute Optimizer correctly DO NOT apply: apprunner is absent from core/scan_orchestrator.py _HUB_SERVICES (lines 52-74) and there is no services/advisor.py App Runner helper — so "missing CoH/CO" is NOT a defect here. CloudWatch is declared (requires_cloudwatch=True) but the read is a no-op (see H1).

**Verdict:** App Runner's per-unit rates are all correct (vCPU $0.064, active+provisioned memory $0.007, validated live against AWSAppRunner). But the adapter is cost-inert: the shim get_enhanced_apprunner_checks initializes three empty buckets and never populates any of them, so it returns recommendations=[] for every account, the dual-billing pricing loop (scan:82-99) is dead code, and total_recommendations/total_monthly_savings are always 0/$0 (committed in the golden fixture). Beneath that headline sit latent defects that would corrupt any future saving: a no-op CloudWatch read (invalid 'Service'/'*' dimension) that pins active_hours to a fabricated 160, a blanket 0.12 reduction factor instead of a config delta, PAUSED/idle services excluded, unpaginated list_services, and AccessDenied swallowed as generic warns rather than permission_issues. CoH/CO correctly do not apply, and the per-rec render fallback is wired correctly (renders nothing today, no desync).

**Pricing validation:** Validated live via AWS Pricing MCP (serviceCode=AWSAppRunner, region us-east-1): USE1-AppRunner-vCPU-hours = $0.0640/vCPU-hour (SKU 8FZ3ANRH34DG5WJ2) matches APP_RUNNER_VCPU_HOURLY=0.064; USE1-AppRunner-GB-hours = $0.0070/GB-hour (SKU DH9DXBVSTZFG449B) and USE1-AppRunner-Provisioned-GB-hours = $0.0070/GB-hour (SKU YYWUT3AQDJMRWWGA) both match APP_RUNNER_MEM_GB_HOURLY=0.007 — confirming the single 0.007 constant is correct for BOTH the active and provisioned memory terms. All three per-unit rates are correct; region scaling via ctx.pricing_multiplier is applied exactly once on each term (services/adapters/apprunner.py:94-96). No rate is mis-stated. The constants are not the problem — the problems are structural (dead inventory, no-op metric, fabricated hours, blanket factor).

**Cost checks:**

| Check | Status | Trigger | Savings basis |
|---|---|---|---|
| auto_scaling_optimization (bucket) | advisory | Initialized as empty list in get_enhanced_apprunner_checks and never appended to; the former Auto Scaling finding was deleted (services/apprunner.py:46-49 comment '# App Runner Auto Scaling Optimization finding removed') | None — bucket stays empty; contributes 0 recs / $0 for every account |
| instance_rightsizing (bucket) | advisory | Initialized empty (services/apprunner.py:24-28); no code path appends to it | None — never populated |
| unused_services (bucket) | advisory | Initialized empty (services/apprunner.py:24-28); no idle/zero-request/PAUSED detection implemented | None — never populated |
| (latent) dual-billing rightsizing price (scan loop) | counted | Would fire for each rec returned by the shim — but the shim returns recommendations=[] for every account, so this loop never executes | provisioned_monthly = mem_gb*0.007*730*multiplier; active_monthly = (vcpus*0.064 + mem_gb*0.007)*active_hours*multiplier; saving = (provisioned_monthly+active_monthly)*0.12. Constants validated live: USE1-AppRunner-vCPU-hours=$0.064, USE1-AppRunner-GB-hours=$0.007, USE1-AppRunner-Provisioned-GB-hours=$0.007 (serviceCode=AWSAppRunner, us-east-1). Region-scaled once via ctx.pricing_multiplier (correct, single application). |

**Findings:**

#### 🔴 C1 · Shim emits ZERO recs for every account — adapter is a permanent no-op and its pricing loop is dead code  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/apprunner.py + services/adapters/apprunner.py:services/apprunner.py:24-60; services/adapters/apprunner.py:81-99`
- **Evidence:** services/apprunner.py:24-28 initializes checks={'auto_scaling_optimization':[], 'instance_rightsizing':[], 'unused_services':[]}; the only loop body (lines 41-51) does `service_details = describe_service(...)`, `instance_config = ...`, then `_ = instance_config` / `except Exception: pass` — nothing is ever appended. Lines 56-58 flatten the (still-empty) buckets into all_recommendations, so it returns {'recommendations': []}. Consequently the adapter's pricing loop services/adapters/apprunner.py:82-99 (`for rec in recs:` ... `savings += monthly_cost * RIGHTSIZING_SAVINGS_RATE`) never executes. Golden fixture confirms committed behavior: tests/fixtures/golden_scan_results.json:491-498 apprunner total_recommendations=0, total_monthly_savings=0, enhanced_checks.count=0.
- **Impact:** $0 / 0 recs produced for 100% of accounts regardless of App Runner spend. The entire adapter, the dual-billing math, the CloudWatch read, and the constants are dead weight. No App Runner saving is ever surfaced. Every other finding below is latent (would-fire-only-if-a-rec-existed).
- **Fix:** Implement at least one defensible counted check in services/apprunner.py — e.g. idle/zero-request or PAUSED-but-provisioned service flagged delete/pause, priced at the real provisioned+active cost — and append it to a bucket so all_recommendations is non-empty. Until then the module should be removed from ALL_MODULES or explicitly documented as inert.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified in real code. services/apprunner.py:24-28 initializes checks with three empty lists; the only loop body (34-51) calls describe_service, binds `_ = instance_config`, and on failure `except Exception: pass`. No `.append(...)` to any bucket exists anywhere in the function (the auto_scaling finding was deliberately removed per the comment at 46-48). Lines 56-58 flatten the still-empty buckets, so get_enhanced_apprunner_checks always returns {'recommendations': []}. In services/adapters/apprunner.py:76 `recs` is therefore always [], so the `for rec in recs:` pricing loop (82-99) never executes and `savings` stays 0.0; total_recommendations=len(recs)=0. tests/fixtures/golden_scan_results.json confirms apprunner total_recommendations=0, total_monthly_savings=0, enhanced_checks.count=0. The adapter is a permanent $0/0-rec no-op and the dual-billing pricing math is dead code, exactly as described. (Pricing-loop line span is 82-99; cited '81-99' merely includes the preceding `savings = 0.0` init — immaterial.)

#### 🟠 H1 · CloudWatch active-hours read is a guaranteed no-op (invalid dimension name AND invalid '*' value); requires_cloudwatch declared for a read that never affects any number  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/apprunner.py:54-72`
- **Evidence:** _estimate_active_hours calls cw.get_metric_statistics(Namespace='AWS/AppRunner', MetricName='CpuUtilization', Dimensions=[{'Name':'Service','Value':'*'}], ...). The AWS/AppRunner namespace exposes dimensions ServiceName and ServiceID — there is no 'Service' dimension — and CloudWatch matches dimensions exactly ('*' is not a wildcard). So resp['Datapoints'] is always empty, the `if datapoints:` branch (lines 64-69) is dead, and the function always returns DEFAULT_ACTIVE_HOURS_PER_MONTH (160). reads_fast_mode/requires_cloudwatch are declared (lines 24-29) for a read that can never change the result; fast vs full mode produce identical numbers.
- **Impact:** Wasted CloudWatch GetMetricStatistics call + a falsely-advertised CloudWatch capability. active_hours is never traffic-derived, so even if C1 were fixed every saving would rest on the fabricated 160 (see M4). Latent today because no rec consumes active_hours.
- **Fix:** Either (a) wire real per-service dimensions ([{'Name':'ServiceName','Value':<name>}] or ServiceID) and derive active hours from RequestCount/ActiveInstances per service, or (b) drop the CW read entirely and remove requires_cloudwatch/reads_fast_mode. Do not keep a declared-but-inert CloudWatch dependency.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified in real code. services/adapters/apprunner.py:54-62 calls cw.get_metric_statistics(Namespace='AWS/AppRunner', MetricName='CpuUtilization', Dimensions=[{'Name':'Service','Value':'*'}], ...). App Runner publishes metrics under AWS/AppRunner with dimensions ServiceName and ServiceID only — there is no 'Service' dimension — and CloudWatch get_metric_statistics matches the dimension set exactly ('*' is a literal value, not a wildcard). So resp['Datapoints'] is always empty, the `if datapoints:` 5%/20% tier branch (64-69) is unreachable, and the function falls through to `return DEFAULT_ACTIVE_HOURS_PER_MONTH` (72) = 160. Fast mode (48-49) returns 160 immediately; full mode also returns 160, so the two are identical and the CloudWatch GetMetricStatistics call cannot change any number. requires_cloudwatch=True (26) and reads_fast_mode=True (24) advertise a CW capability that never affects the result. Mechanism accurate. Latent today because no rec consumes active_hours (consequence of C1) — which the finding's own impact statement acknowledges.

#### 🟠 H2 · Permission/throttle failures are swallowed or downgraded to generic warns — AccessDenied never classified as a permission_issue  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/apprunner.py + services/adapters/apprunner.py:services/apprunner.py:50-51, 53-54; services/adapters/apprunner.py:70-71`
- **Evidence:** services/apprunner.py:50-51 inner `except Exception: pass` around describe_service — a per-service AccessDenied/Throttling vanishes with no record on ctx. services/apprunner.py:53-54 outer `except Exception as e: ctx.warn(...)` wraps the whole list_services loop — a denied apprunner:ListServices yields one generic warn and an empty report indistinguishable from 'account has no services'. services/adapters/apprunner.py:70-71 `_estimate_active_hours` `except Exception as e: ctx.warn(...)` treats a CloudWatch AccessDenied as a generic warn. None call ctx.permission_issue (available: core/scan_context.py:59 `def permission_issue(self, message, service, action=None)`).
- **Impact:** A missing apprunner:ListServices / cloudwatch:GetMetricStatistics IAM grant produces a clean-looking empty/zero report rather than a surfaced permission gap — the user cannot tell 'no opportunities' from 'I couldn't look'. Coverage-safety defect.
- **Fix:** Classify botocore ClientError codes AccessDenied/AccessDeniedException/UnauthorizedOperation/OptInRequired → ctx.permission_issue(..., action='apprunner:ListServices'|'apprunner:DescribeService'|'cloudwatch:GetMetricStatistics'); route other errors to ctx.warn. Replace the bare `except Exception: pass` with a recorded classification.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified in real code. All three swallow/downgrade sites exist exactly as cited: services/apprunner.py:50-51 inner `except Exception: pass` around describe_service (a per-service AccessDenied/Throttling vanishes with no record on ctx); 53-54 outer `except Exception as e: ctx.warn(...)` wraps the entire list_services loop (a denied apprunner:ListServices yields one generic warn and an empty report indistinguishable from 'no services'); services/adapters/apprunner.py:70-71 `_estimate_active_hours` `except Exception as e: ctx.warn(...)` treats a CloudWatch AccessDenied as a generic warn. ctx.permission_issue exists at core/scan_context.py:59 and is the intended classifier; neither apprunner file imports services/_aws_errors.record_aws_error nor calls permission_issue. This deviates from the established convention — _aws_errors.py's module docstring explicitly states adapters 'must never swallow a describe/CloudWatch failure with a logger call alone,' and ~12 other adapters (rds, ec2, s3, ebs, lambda_svc, eks, network, advisor, containers, efs_fsx, commitment_analysis) route errors through record_aws_error/permission_issue. A missing apprunner:ListServices or cloudwatch:GetMetricStatistics grant therefore produces a clean-looking empty/zero report rather than a surfaced permission gap. Real coverage-safety defect as described.

#### 🟡 M1 · PAUSED services excluded — the clearest real App Runner saving (24/7 provisioned $0.007/GB-hr) is invisible  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/apprunner.py:38`
- **Evidence:** Loop guards `if status == 'RUNNING':` (services/apprunner.py:38) before any inspection. A PAUSED App Runner service still incurs the provisioned-memory charge (USE1-AppRunner-Provisioned-GB-hours = $0.007/GB-hr, billed while the service exists) but is never examined.
- **Impact:** Coverage gap on the most defensible delete/resume lever. e.g. a paused 4 GB service still costs ~4*0.007*730 = $20.44/mo that is never flagged. Latent behind C1 but a true allowlist-by-state skip.
- **Fix:** Inspect PAUSED (and any provisioned-but-idle) services and emit a delete/resume rec priced at provisioned_monthly = mem_gb*0.007*730*multiplier. Do not gate inspection on Status=='RUNNING'.

#### 🟡 M2 · No idle / zero-request detection — the strongest cost lever (unused_services) is unimplemented  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/apprunner.py:24-28, 56-58`
- **Evidence:** The unused_services bucket is declared (line 27) and never populated. App Runner exposes RequestCount / ActiveInstances in CloudWatch, but no idle/zero-request check exists.
- **Impact:** Services receiving zero traffic over a window are never flagged for delete/pause even though they bill provisioned memory 24/7. Largest missed-saving class.
- **Fix:** Add a CloudWatch-gated RequestCount==0 (over N days) check that emits a delete/pause rec at full provisioned+active cost; mark it Counted only when metric evidence exists, else $0 advisory (Counted=False).

#### 🟡 M3 · list_services is not paginated — accounts with many services are silently truncated  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/apprunner.py:31-32`
- **Evidence:** `response = ctx.client('apprunner').list_services(); services = response.get('ServiceSummaryList', [])` — a single call with no NextToken loop. App Runner ListServices is paginated via NextToken/MaxResults.
- **Impact:** Services beyond the first page are dropped with no warning. Latent today (0 recs), but becomes a real coverage truncation the moment any check is implemented.
- **Fix:** Use the apprunner ListServices paginator or loop on NextToken, accumulating ServiceSummaryList across pages.

#### 🟡 M4 · DEFAULT_ACTIVE_HOURS_PER_MONTH = 160 is a fabricated assumption with no usage evidence  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/apprunner.py:14, 38-49, 64-72`
- **Evidence:** Constant 160 (line 14) = '8 hr/day x 20 workdays'; the docstring itself admits (lines 38-41) it 'was an invented average that didn't reflect actual traffic.' The CW tiers only scale it to 160*0.5 / 160 / 160 by CPU thresholds (5%/20%, lines 66-69) that are themselves invented — and that branch is dead anyway (H1), so active_hours is ALWAYS 160.
- **Impact:** Any active_monthly term (and therefore any counted saving, once C1 is fixed) is anchored to a number that is never derived from this account's traffic — fabricated dollars. Canonical 'fixed hours, no metric' issue.
- **Fix:** Derive active hours from per-service RequestCount/ActiveInstances CloudWatch metrics; if unavailable or fast_mode, render the rec as a $0 advisory (Counted=False) rather than fabricating 160 hours. Record an AuditBasis (rate/region/active-hours-window/formula).

#### 🟡 M5 · RIGHTSIZING_SAVINGS_RATE = 0.12 is an arbitrary blanket reduction factor, not an exact current→target config delta  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/apprunner.py:15, 99`
- **Evidence:** `savings += monthly_cost * RIGHTSIZING_SAVINGS_RATE` (line 99) applies a flat 12% to the ENTIRE modeled monthly cost rather than computing (current_config − target_config) on vCPU/GB (e.g. 2 vCPU→1 vCPU, 4 GB→2 GB) at the validated $0.064/$0.007 rates.
- **Impact:** Saving magnitude is invented — a service that cannot be downsized still books 12% 'savings'; one that can halve books only 12%. Mirrors the Glue 0.30 / EC2 exact-delta findings.
- **Fix:** Replace the 0.12 factor with an exact current→target price delta: target_cost computed from the next-smaller valid App Runner Cpu/Memory config using the same per-unit rates; saving = current_cost − target_cost.

#### 🟢 L1 · Dual-billing model double-counts active-period memory  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/apprunner.py:94-98`
- **Evidence:** provisioned_monthly = mem_gb*0.007*730 (memory billed for ALL 730 hr) and active_monthly adds mem_gb*0.007*active_hours on top (lines 94-97). During active hours an instance is billed at the active rate INSTEAD of the provisioned rate for that hour, so summing full-month provisioned memory plus active-hours memory overstates memory by active_hours worth.
- **Impact:** Overstates modeled monthly cost (and thus the 12%-derived saving) by mem_gb*0.007*active_hours. With active_hours=160 and 4 GB that is ~$4.48/mo of phantom basis per service. Latent behind C1.
- **Fix:** Bill provisioned memory only for non-active hours: provisioned_monthly = mem_gb*0.007*(730−active_hours), or model active instances as replacing (not adding to) provisioned memory for the active window.

#### 🟢 L2 · Malformed InstanceConfiguration silently priced at a 1 vCPU / 2 GB default  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/apprunner.py:83-93`
- **Evidence:** cpu_str/mem_str default to '1 vCPU'/'2 GB' (lines 84-85) and the parses fall back to vcpus=1.0 / mem_gb=2.0 on `except (ValueError, IndexError)` (lines 88-93). A rec with a missing/garbled InstanceConfiguration is priced as a real 1 vCPU/2 GB service with no warning.
- **Impact:** Once C1 is fixed, a config-parse failure yields a fabricated counted dollar at default sizing instead of an honest $0/advisory. Latent today.
- **Fix:** On parse failure, ctx.warn and emit the rec as a $0 advisory (Counted=False) rather than substituting a 1 vCPU/2 GB priced default.

#### 🟢 L3 · services/adapters/CLAUDE.md misclassifies App Runner as Live Pricing and states a formula the code does not use  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/CLAUDE.md:apprunner.py row under 'Live Pricing (19 adapters)'`
- **Evidence:** The table row reads `apprunner.py | $0.064/vCPU/hr + $0.007/GB/hr × 730 | Module constants` but is listed inside the 'Live Pricing' section, implying a PricingEngine method that does not exist. The actual code is module-constant only, and the formula is provisioned(mem*0.007*730) + active((vcpu*0.064+mem*0.007)*160), NOT a single '×730' term.
- **Impact:** Doc/code mismatch misleads future maintainers into expecting a PricingEngine path and a simpler formula; obscures the dual-billing model and the 160-hour assumption.
- **Fix:** Move the apprunner row to a 'Module-constant' grouping and restate the formula as provisioned (mem*0.007*730) + active ((vcpu*0.064+mem*0.007)*active_hours), noting active_hours defaults to the fabricated 160 and that no rec currently fires.

#### 🟢 L4 · describe_service result is fetched then discarded (_ = instance_config)  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/apprunner.py:41-51`
- **Evidence:** Inside the RUNNING branch, `service_details = describe_service(ServiceArn=service_arn)` and `instance_config = service_config.get('InstanceConfiguration', {})` are computed (lines 42-44) only to be thrown away with `_ = instance_config` (line 49). The Cpu/Memory the (dead) pricing loop expects is never attached to any rec.
- **Impact:** A per-service API call (apprunner:DescribeService) is made for every RUNNING service with zero use of the result — wasted API calls and the data the pricing loop needs is never wired through. Latent behind C1.
- **Fix:** Attach InstanceConfiguration (Cpu/Memory) to an emitted rec dict so the adapter's pricing loop can read rec['InstanceConfiguration'], or remove the describe_service call until a check consumes it.

---

### Athena — `services/adapters/athena.py`

**Module identity:** key="athena", cli_aliases=("athena",), display_name="Athena", reads_fast_mode=True, requires_cloudwatch=True, required_clients()=("athena","cloudwatch") — all confirmed in services/adapters/athena.py:22-30. Pricing is a module constant ATHENA_PRICE_PER_TB=5.0 (line 36); there is NO PricingEngine method for Athena — the $5/TB literal is multiplied once by ctx.pricing_multiplier (correct single region application) plus a hardcoded 0.75 compression factor (line 69). The adapter emits a single SourceBlock "enhanced_checks" (line 83). CoH/CO correctly do NOT apply: athena is absent from scan_orchestrator _HUB_SERVICES/type_map and has no services/advisor.py CO helper — so "missing CoH/CO" is out of scope. athena is absent from PHASE_A_DESCRIPTORS, PHASE_B_HANDLERS, and _PHASE_B_SKIP_PER_REC (reporter_phase_b.py:2436-2530), so should_fallback_to_per_rec("athena")=True and enhanced_checks renders via the generic per-rec renderer (render_generic_per_rec → _render_generic_other_rec).

**Verdict:** The athena adapter is currently a dead adapter: services/athena.py:get_enhanced_athena_checks initializes an empty checks dict and never appends to it, so recommendations is always empty and the adapter emits zero findings for every account (C1) — yet services/adapters/CLAUDE.md advertises a live $5/TB CloudWatch-priced check (M4).
