Because the pricing loop never executes, the remaining defects are latent but real: a CloudWatch failure is silently coerced to a $0 finding with no ctx.warn/permission_issue (H1), bytes are divided by TiB (2^40) while AWS bills per decimal TB (10^12), understating every saving ~9% (H2, confirmed against the live $5.00 DataScannedInTB rate), list_work_groups is unpaginated (H3), the 0.75 compression factor is applied unconditionally with no data-format detection (M1), provisioned-capacity/Spark workgroups are mispriced by the flat $5/TB model (M2), and the adapter reads WorkGroup/ProcessedBytesTB fields the shim never sets (M3). Today counted==rendered trivially (empty, clean, no crash), but the generic renderer reads an EstimatedSavings string the adapter never writes (L2). No CoH/CO applicability — correctly out of scope.

**Pricing validation:** Validated LIVE via AWS Pricing MCP (get_pricing AmazonAthena us-east-1): DataScannedInTB usagetype USE1-DataScannedInTB, SKU B6WHE3FUNCDQVVX4 = $5.00 per Terabytes — confirms the ATHENA_PRICE_PER_TB=5.0 constant exactly, and confirms the billing unit is decimal Terabytes (10^12), proving the (1024**4)/TiB divisor is wrong (finding H2, 9.05% understatement). Also surfaced two alternative Athena pricing modes the flat $5/TB ignores (finding M2): ReservedCapacityInDPUHours SKU B86URYJPE2VCMXMC = $0.30/DPU-Hour (provisioned capacity) and Athena Spark CodeExecutionInDPUHours SKU 53ZU6HBD9YNUAYSE = $0.35/DPU-Hour. The 0.75 compression factor is a labelled heuristic, not an AWS Pricing-API rate, so it cannot be validated and is flagged as fabricated-when-unconditional (M1). Region scaling via ctx.pricing_multiplier is applied exactly once on the constant path (no PricingEngine, no double-multiply) — correct.

**Cost checks:**

| Check | Status | Trigger | Savings basis |
|---|---|---|---|
| Query scan-cost reduction (ProcessedBytes → $5/TB) | counted | A workgroup recommendation supplied by services/athena.py:get_enhanced_athena_checks with positive 30-day AWS/Athena ProcessedBytes (Sum), while not ctx.fast_mode. NOTE: the shim emits ZERO recs today (see finding C1), so this check NEVER fires for any account. | monthly_tb * ATHENA_PRICE_PER_TB(5.0) * ctx.pricing_multiplier * 0.75, where monthly_tb = total_bytes / (1024**4). $5/TB validated live = $5.00 DataScannedInTB us-east-1 (SKU B6WHE3FUNCDQVVX4). The (1024**4) divisor is TiB not TB (finding H2); the 0.75 factor is an unconditional heuristic (finding M1). |
| CW-empty advisory ($0 + PricingWarning) | advisory | Not fast_mode and ProcessedBytes Sum is 0/absent (or get_metric_statistics raises) → monthly_tb<=0 | rec['EstimatedMonthlySavings']=0.0; rec['PricingWarning']='CW ProcessedBytes metric returned no data' (athena.py:72-76). Contributes $0 to the per-tab total but the rec is still counted in total_recommendations (no Counted=False). |
| Fast-mode advisory ($0 + PricingWarning) | advisory | ctx.fast_mode is True → CW lookup skipped entirely | rec['EstimatedMonthlySavings']=0.0; rec['PricingWarning']='fast mode skipped CW; re-run without --fast' (athena.py:77-81). CW read correctly gated on ctx.fast_mode per reads_fast_mode=True. |

**Findings:**

#### 🔴 C1 · Shim emits zero recommendations — adapter produces no Athena findings for any account  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/athena.py:24-53`
- **Evidence:** checks dict is initialized empty and NEVER appended to: `checks: dict = {"workgroup_optimization": [], "query_results": []}` (line 24). The per-workgroup loop body only does `_ = (output_location, config)` (line 43) — the two former checks were removed (comment lines 39-42). Then `recommendations = []; for _category, items in checks.items(): recommendations.extend(items)` (lines 49-52) extends from two empty lists, so recommendations is ALWAYS []. The adapter's entire ProcessedBytes pricing loop in athena.py:39-81 runs over an empty list.
- **Impact:** 100% coverage loss: the Athena tab is permanently empty and the documented $5/TB CloudWatch-priced saving is unreachable. Every downstream finding (H1/H2/H3/M1/M2/M3) is currently latent because the loop never executes.
- **Fix:** Re-wire the shim to emit one rec per workgroup carrying WorkGroup and (optionally) ProcessedBytesTB, e.g. append `{"CheckCategory": "Athena Query Optimization", "WorkGroup": wg_name, "Recommendation": "Partition/compress to Parquet/ORC"}` to checks for each discovered workgroup so the adapter's ProcessedBytes pricing loop can price it. Fix the units (H2), CW silent-failure (H1), pagination (H3), and field-setting (M3) at the same time.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified in services/athena.py:24-53. `checks` is initialized as {"workgroup_optimization": [], "query_results": []} (line 24) and is never mutated: the per-workgroup loop body only executes `_ = (output_location, config)` (line 43) after the two prior checks were removed (comment 39-42). `recommendations` is then built by extending from those two permanently-empty lists (lines 49-51), so it is always []. Grep confirms `get_enhanced_athena_checks` is the ONLY producer of recommendations and `ProcessedBytesTB` is never assigned anywhere (only read at adapter line 42). The adapter (services/adapters/athena.py:34) reads `recs = result.get('recommendations', [])` -> [], so the pricing loop (lines 39-81) never executes, savings stays 0.0 and total_recommendations=0. The Athena tab is permanently empty for every account. Real exactly as described.

#### 🟠 H1 · CloudWatch failure silently converted to a $0 finding (no ctx.warn/permission_issue)  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/athena.py:62-64`
- **Evidence:** `except Exception as e: logger.warning(f"[athena] CloudWatch ProcessedBytes metric check failed: {e}"); monthly_tb = 0`. A CloudWatch AccessDenied / throttle / OptInRequired error is logged via logger only and coerced to monthly_tb=0, which then emits a $0 rec with PricingWarning rather than surfacing a permission/throttle warning. ctx exposes warn() and permission_issue() (core/scan_context.py:49,59) but neither is called here.
- **Impact:** Canonical silent-failure class: on accounts lacking cloudwatch:GetMetricStatistics, every workgroup silently reports $0 with no operator signal — indistinguishable from a genuinely idle workgroup. Latent today only because C1 keeps the loop empty; live the moment C1 is fixed.
- **Fix:** Classify the exception: AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation/OptInRequired → ctx.permission_issue(..., 'athena', 'cloudwatch:GetMetricStatistics'); other exceptions → ctx.warn(...). Reuse services/_aws_errors.record_aws_error like the network/file_systems adapters do.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified in services/adapters/athena.py:62-64. The except block calls only logger.warning and sets monthly_tb=0; control then falls to the else branch (lines 72-76) which sets EstimatedMonthlySavings=0.0 and the generic PricingWarning='CW ProcessedBytes metric returned no data'. So an AccessDenied/throttle/OptInRequired is indistinguishable from a genuinely idle workgroup, and the misleading 'returned no data' message is emitted even on a permission error. ctx.warn and ctx.permission_issue do exist (core/scan_context.py:49 and :59 respectively, matching the cited lines) and neither is called here. Mechanism, lines, and missing-signal class are all accurate. Caveat (already acknowledged by the finding): this is latent today because C1 keeps the loop empty; it activates the moment C1 is fixed.

#### 🟠 H2 · Bytes converted to TiB (2^40) while Athena bills per TB (10^12) — understates saving by 9.05%  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/athena.py:61`
- **Evidence:** `monthly_tb = total_bytes / (1024**4) if total_bytes > 0 else 0`. 1024**4 = 2^40 (TiB). Live AWS Pricing API rate is per unit "Terabytes" = 10^12 bytes (DataScannedInTB, SKU B6WHE3FUNCDQVVX4, $5.00). Dividing by 2^40 instead of 10^12 yields a TB count 1.0995x too small; understatement = (1 - 10^12/2^40) = 9.05%.
- **Impact:** Every counted Athena saving is ~9% too low (once C1 is fixed). Pure rating bug — fabricates a smaller dollar than reality.
- **Fix:** Divide by 1e12 (or 1000**4): `monthly_tb = total_bytes / 1e12`. The AWS billing unit is decimal TB, not binary TiB.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified in services/adapters/athena.py:61: `monthly_tb = total_bytes / (1024**4) ...`. 1024**4 = 2^40 (TiB), but the variable is named monthly_tb and is multiplied by ATHENA_PRICE_PER_TB=5.0 (line 36/69) which the comment (line 14) documents as '$5/TB AWS list' — AWS Athena data-scanned pricing is expressed per decimal TB (10^12 bytes). Dividing bytes by 2^40 instead of 10^12 yields a TB count that is 10^12/2^40 = 0.9095x of correct, i.e. ~9.05% understatement; direction and magnitude check out. Internal naming (monthly_tb) vs implementation (TiB) confirms the unit mismatch was unintended. Two caveats that do not change the conclusion: (1) the finding's framing that the $5 rate comes from a 'Live AWS Pricing API' lookup (SKU B6WHE3FUNCDQVVX4) is inaccurate — the code uses a hardcoded module constant, not a PricingEngine/API call; (2) like H1 this is latent behind C1 (the loop never runs today). The rating bug itself is real at the cited line.

#### 🟡 H3 · list_work_groups not paginated — workgroups past the first page are dropped  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/athena.py:28-29`
- **Evidence:** `response = athena.list_work_groups(); for wg in response.get("WorkGroups", []):` — a single call with no NextToken loop and no paginator. ListWorkGroups returns up to 50 workgroups per page by default.
- **Impact:** Accounts with >50 workgroups silently lose coverage on the remainder. Latent today (loop body is a no-op per C1), but a real coverage gap once recs are emitted.
- **Fix:** Use `athena.get_paginator("list_work_groups")` or loop on NextToken until exhausted before/while building recs.

#### 🟡 M1 · Unconditional 0.75 compression factor — fabricates a 75% saving for already-optimized workgroups  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/athena.py:66-71`
- **Evidence:** `# 75% savings factor ... 70-91% compression for columnar formats (Parquet/ORC). rec_savings = monthly_tb * ATHENA_PRICE_PER_TB * ctx.pricing_multiplier * 0.75`. The factor is applied to ALL scanned bytes with no detection of the current data format/partitioning. If a workgroup already queries Parquet/ORC + partitioned data, the 75% reduction is unachievable.
- **Impact:** For an already-optimized workgroup the entire counted dollar is fiction (the 0.75 is a reduction factor, not a current-minus-target delta). 0.75 is a labelled heuristic, not an AWS rate, so it cannot be Pricing-API validated.
- **Fix:** Detect current format (e.g. inspect table input format / output format, or downgrade to a $0 advisory when format is unknown). At minimum gate the 0.75 behind evidence the data is non-columnar, and record the factor in a structured AuditBasis on each counted finding.

#### 🟡 M2 · Provisioned-capacity and Spark workgroups mispriced by the flat $5/TB model  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/athena.py:36-69`
- **Evidence:** The adapter applies ATHENA_PRICE_PER_TB=5.0 to every workgroup. Live AWS Pricing API shows Athena also bills ReservedCapacityInDPUHours = $0.30/DPU-Hour (SKU B86URYJPE2VCMXMC) and Athena Spark CodeExecutionInDPUHours = $0.35/DPU-Hour (SKU 53ZU6HBD9YNUAYSE). The adapter has no detection of workgroup type/engine.
- **Impact:** Workgroups on Athena provisioned capacity (per-DPU-hour) or Spark engine derive no per-TB data-scan charge, so the $5/TB saving is wrong (over-counts) for them.
- **Fix:** Read workgroup Configuration (engine/version) and EnforceWorkGroupConfiguration/provisioned-capacity assignment; skip or DPU-price provisioned-capacity & Spark workgroups instead of applying $5/TB.

#### 🟡 M3 · Adapter reads WorkGroup/ProcessedBytesTB rec fields the shim never sets  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/athena.py:41-42`
- **Evidence:** `workgroup = rec.get("WorkGroup", "primary"); monthly_tb = rec.get("ProcessedBytesTB", 0)`. services/athena.py never sets "WorkGroup" or "ProcessedBytesTB" on any rec (the loop body at line 43 discards everything). So even if checks were re-populated by the old code, WorkGroup would default to "primary" for every rec and the CW query (athena.py:53-54, Dimension WorkGroup=workgroup) would always target the literal "primary" workgroup.
- **Impact:** The ProcessedBytes lookup is bound to the wrong dimension for all non-primary workgroups, so the counted TB (and dollar) would be attributed to/queried against the wrong workgroup. Latent today per C1.
- **Fix:** When re-wiring the shim (C1), set rec['WorkGroup']=wg_name on each rec so the adapter queries the correct CloudWatch WorkGroup dimension.

#### 🟡 M4 · Doc/code mismatch — CLAUDE.md advertises a live $5/TB CloudWatch check that emits nothing  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/CLAUDE.md:athena.py Live-Pricing row`
- **Evidence:** The Live Pricing table row reads `| athena.py | CloudWatch ProcessedBytes → $5/TB | CloudWatch + constant |`, presenting a working priced check. Reality (C1): services/athena.py emits zero recs, so the documented saving is unreachable.
- **Impact:** Misleads maintainers/auditors into believing Athena produces counted savings; hides the dead adapter.
- **Fix:** Update the athena.py row to state the shim currently emits no recommendations (or fix C1 and keep the row accurate). Reconcile with the empty-checks reality.

#### 🟢 L1 · Inner per-workgroup `except Exception: continue` swallows denied/throttled get_work_group with no record  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/athena.py:32-45`
- **Evidence:** `try: wg_details = athena.get_work_group(WorkGroup=wg_name) ... except Exception: continue` — an AccessDenied/throttle on get_work_group is dropped with no ctx.warn/ctx.permission_issue. Only the outer except (line 46-47) records ctx.warn.
- **Impact:** Per-workgroup permission/throttle failures are invisible. Currently moot because the try body is a no-op, but becomes a silent coverage drop once C1 re-wires it.
- **Fix:** Replace bare continue with classification: AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation → ctx.permission_issue('athena','athena:GetWorkGroup'); other → ctx.warn(...).

#### 🟢 L2 · Generic renderer reads EstimatedSavings string; adapter writes EstimatedMonthlySavings float — styled savings line won't render once recs exist  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `reporter_phase_b.py:1865-1876`
- **Evidence:** _render_generic_other_rec renders the styled savings line only `if "EstimatedSavings" in rec` (line 1874-1875). The Athena adapter sets rec['EstimatedMonthlySavings'] (float) + rec['PricingWarning'] (athena.py:70,75,80), never 'EstimatedSavings'. The generic key-dump loop (lines 1865-1869) would print a counted float as a plain 'Estimated Monthly Savings: N' line, but a $0 advisory (value 0.0, falsy) prints no savings line at all.
- **Impact:** Today the tab renders clean/empty (no recs → no blank cards, no crash; counted==rendered trivially holds at $0). If C1 re-wires recs, the per-tab headline (sum of EstimatedMonthlySavings floats) can desync from the cards, which lack a styled savings line. Cosmetic/desync risk, not a counted-dollar fabrication.
- **Fix:** Either have the adapter also set rec['EstimatedSavings']=f"${rec_savings:.2f}/month", or add an Athena-specific branch in render_generic_per_rec that reads EstimatedMonthlySavings; ensure advisory $0 recs render their PricingWarning.

---

### Aurora — `services/adapters/aurora.py`

**Module identity:** AuroraModule (services/adapters/aurora.py:391-499) is key="aurora", cli_aliases=("aurora",), display_name="Aurora", requires_cloudwatch=True, reads_fast_mode=True, required_clients()=("rds","cloudwatch"); stat_cards=cluster_count/serverless_cluster_count/total_monthly_savings; grouping=GroupingSpec(by="check_category", label_path="check_type"). It consumes NEITHER Cost Optimization Hub NOR Compute Optimizer — there is no "aurora" entry in scan_orchestrator type_map/_HUB_SERVICES, and RdsDbCluster/RdsDbInstance bucket to "rds" (core/scan_orchestrator.py:86-91), so per the brief a "missing CoH/CO" finding is out of scope. Pricing: ACU via PricingEngine.get_aurora_acu_hourly() (region-correct, live us-east-1 $0.12) with module fallback ACU_HOURLY_FALLBACK=0.06×pricing_multiplier; instance recs reuse PricingEngine.get_rds_instance_monthly_price(engine,class) (exact current→target delta); I/O-tier uses two us-east-1 module constants IO_COST_PER_MILLION=0.20 and IO_OPTIMIZED_PREMIUM_PER_GB=0.025 with HOURS_PER_MONTH=730. The CLAUDE.md adapters table does not list aurora in the Live-Pricing rows (implicit) and the rds.py row names "Aurora Serverless v2 (ACU), Aurora cluster rightsizing, read replicas, stopped instances" as RDS gaps owned by this adapter — division of labor matches code.

**Verdict:** Aurora emits four counted checks across three source blocks and carries savings as a bare monthly_savings float summed directly into the headline with no parse/advisory boundary — so any fabricated or mis-rated number flows straight to the total. The most serious issue (C1) is that serverless_v2 credits (1-util)*MaxACU as recoverable even though Serverless v2 bills consumed ACU-seconds, fabricating the entire ACU saving. The I/O-tier check is materially overstated: the storage-premium constant is ~5x below the live $0.125/GB-Mo delta (H1) and the model ignores the I/O-Optimized instance premium (H2). Aurora provisioned instances can be double-counted against the RDS tab's Cost-Hub recs with no shared covered set (H3), describe_db_clusters and the CloudWatch helpers fail silently (H4/M3), no check records an AuditBasis (M4), and serverless/IO savings render only as an unstyled raw number (M2). Instance rightsizing+Graviton compose correctly (cur-grav, no overlap) and IO_COST_PER_MILLION=0.20 is accurate.

**Pricing validation:** Validated live via AWS Pricing MCP (AmazonRDS, us-east-1, 2026-06-19 price version): (1) Aurora Serverless v2 ACU 'Aurora:ServerlessV2Usage' = $0.12/ACU-hr — confirms ACU_HOURLY_FALLBACK=0.06 is 2x low (M1) and engine FALLBACK_AURORA_ACU_HOURLY=0.12 is correct. (2) Aurora Standard I/O 'Aurora:StorageIOUsage' = $0.20 per 1M requests — confirms IO_COST_PER_MILLION=0.20 is correct. (3) Aurora Standard storage 'Aurora:StorageUsage' = $0.10/GB-Mo vs I/O-Optimized 'Aurora:IO-OptimizedStorageUsage' = $0.225/GB-Mo -> true premium $0.125/GB-Mo, so IO_OPTIMIZED_PREMIUM_PER_GB=0.025 is ~5x too low (H1). Instance pricing reuses PricingEngine.get_rds_instance_monthly_price (RDS path, separately audited); not re-validated here, but flagged that aurora_io_optimized is not threaded into the Aurora instance calls (H2/L3). The IO metric Sum semantics (M5) were not validated against CloudWatch metric metadata and need live confirmation.

**Cost checks:**

| Check | Status | Trigger | Savings basis |
|---|---|---|---|
| serverless_v2_acu_waste | counted | cluster has ServerlessV2ScalingConfiguration AND not fast_mode AND ServerlessV2CapacityUtilization 14d avg is not None AND monthly_savings>$1 (aurora.py:289-328) | wasted_acu = max_acu*(1-avg_util/100); monthly = wasted_acu * acu_hourly * 730. acu_hourly = get_aurora_acu_hourly() (live us-east-1 $0.12/ACU-hr, validated) else ACU_HOURLY_FALLBACK=0.06*pricing_multiplier (aurora.py:22,307-313). |
| io_tier_optimization | counted | not fast_mode AND VolumeReadIOPs+VolumeWriteIOPs (Sum, 14x daily) both not None AND AllocatedStorage>0 AND monthly_io>0 AND savings>$10 (aurora.py:340-373) | standard_io_cost=(monthly_io/1e6)*IO_COST_PER_MILLION(0.20, validated $0.20/1M); optimized_premium=storage_gb*IO_OPTIMIZED_PREMIUM_PER_GB(0.025); savings=(standard-premium)*pricing_multiplier (aurora.py:369-382). monthly_io = (read+write summed over 14 daily Sums)/14*30. |
| instance_rightsizing | counted | provisioned aurora instance, DBInstanceStatus=='available', class parseable, not fast_mode, CPUUtilization 14d avg<50 AND rightsize_target_size smaller AND cand_price in (0,cur_price) (aurora.py:201-242) | exact delta cur_price-cand_price via get_rds_instance_monthly_price(engine,class) (no multiplier; engine region-correct). Target from rightsize_target_size(vcpu, peak_cpu, headroom=1.2) in aurora_logic.py:65-76. |
| instance_graviton | counted | provisioned aurora instance whose family is x86 with a graviton_equivalent AND grav_price in (0,base_price); evaluated on the possibly-rightsized class (aurora.py:245-275) | exact delta base_price-grav_price via get_rds_instance_monthly_price on rightsized_class vs db.<r6g/m6g/c6g/t4g/x2g>.<size>; compounds with rightsizing as (cur-cand)+(cand-grav)=cur-grav (no overlap). |

**Findings:**

#### 🔴 C1 · Serverless v2 ACU savings fabricated from max capacity, not billed consumption  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/aurora.py:302-328`
- **Evidence:** avg_util=_get_cloudwatch_avg(...,"ServerlessV2CapacityUtilization"); waste_ratio=max(0.0,1.0-(avg_util/100.0)); wasted_acu=max_acu*waste_ratio; monthly_savings=wasted_acu*acu_hourly*HOURS_PER_MONTH. ServerlessV2CapacityUtilization = current ACU / MaxACU; Aurora Serverless v2 bills CONSUMED ACU-seconds (between Min and Max), NOT MaxCapacity. At avg_util=25%, max_acu=16 you already bill only ~4 ACU; the formula credits the unbilled 12 ACU = 12*0.12*730 = $1,051/mo that the account never paid.
- **Impact:** Entire serverless_v2 monthly_savings is fabricated and summed into total_monthly_savings (aurora.py:460) and the account headline (core/result_builder.py:72). Lowering MaxCapacity saves $0 unless the workload was hitting the ceiling; it can only degrade performance.
- **Fix:** Do not credit (1-util)*max_acu as recoverable. Either demote serverless_v2 to a $0 advisory (Counted=False) or compute savings only from evidenced consumed-ACU above a proposed lower Max (e.g. require avg_util high enough that a lowered ceiling actually caps consumption), and record an AuditBasis.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified at services/adapters/aurora.py:302-328. The formula is waste_ratio = 1 - avg_util/100 (307), wasted_acu = max_acu * waste_ratio (308), monthly_savings = wasted_acu * acu_hourly * 730 (313). Since avg_util = consumed ACU / MaxACU (a % of max), wasted_acu algebraically equals (max_acu - avg_consumed_acu), i.e. the gap between the MaxCapacity ceiling and actual consumption. Aurora Serverless v2 bills only the consumed ACU (between Min and Max); MaxCapacity carries no charge. So the credited dollars were never billed, and the recommended action 'Reduce Max ACU' (line 323) saves $0 in ACU charges (it can only cap peak headroom). The fabricated monthly_savings is counted: summed at aurora.py:460 into total_monthly_savings, then into the account headline at core/result_builder.py:72 (sum of f.total_monthly_savings). The example checks out arithmetically (12 wasted ACU * rate * 730). CRITICAL severity stands. Caveat (does not refute): the literal metric string is 'ServerlessV2CapacityUtilization' whereas AWS's canonical Serverless v2 metric is 'ACUUtilization'; if the named metric returns no datapoints the check no-ops (line 304-305 returns early) — but whenever it does fire, the mechanism is exactly the fabrication described.

#### 🟠 H1 · I/O-Optimized storage premium constant 5x too low vs live pricing  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/aurora.py:24,370-382`
- **Evidence:** IO_OPTIMIZED_PREMIUM_PER_GB=0.025; optimized_premium=storage_gb*0.025; savings=standard_io_cost-optimized_premium. AWS Pricing API us-east-1: Aurora Standard storage 'Aurora:StorageUsage' = $0.10/GB-Mo; Aurora I/O-Optimized 'Aurora:IO-OptimizedStorageUsage' = $0.225/GB-Mo. True premium = $0.125/GB-Mo, so 0.025 understates the cost side ~5x.
- **Impact:** Overstates every io_tier_optimization saving (counted): on a 1,000 GB cluster the premium is modeled at $25/mo instead of $125/mo, inflating savings by $100/mo per cluster and lowering the >$10 gate's bar so non-economic conversions get recommended.
- **Fix:** Replace the constant with a PricingEngine lookup of (Aurora:IO-OptimizedStorageUsage - Aurora:StorageUsage) per GB-Mo (=$0.125 us-east-1), region-scaled once; do not hardcode 0.025.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified against live AWS Pricing API (us-east-1): Aurora Standard storage = $0.10/GB-Mo (usagetype Aurora:StorageUsage) and I/O-Optimized = $0.225/GB-Mo (usagetype Aurora:IO-OptimizedStorageUsage), giving a true premium of $0.125/GB-Mo. The module constant IO_OPTIMIZED_PREMIUM_PER_GB=0.025 (aurora.py:24) is ~5x too low. In _check_io_tier, optimized_premium = storage_gb * 0.025 (line 370) is subtracted from the I/O cost (savings = standard_io_cost - optimized_premium, 371) and gated at savings>10.0 (373). Understating the premium 5x inflates every io_tier_optimization saving and lowers the >$10 gate's bar. On a 1,000 GB cluster the premium is modeled at $25/mo vs the real $125/mo — exactly the $100/mo per-cluster inflation cited. These recs are counted (summed at aurora.py:460 → result_builder.py:72). HIGH stands.

#### 🟠 H2 · I/O-tier savings ignore the ~30% I/O-Optimized instance-price premium  ·  `limitation` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/aurora.py:369-386`
- **Evidence:** savings = standard_io_cost - optimized_premium only. Switching to I/O-Optimized also raises EVERY cluster instance's price (~30%; PricingEngine pins storage='Aurora IO Optimization Mode' EBS Only $5.12 vs IO mode $6.656 per core/pricing_engine.py:1184-1189). _check_io_tier never adds this cost, and get_rds_instance_monthly_price for instance recs is called WITHOUT aurora_io_optimized (aurora.py:195,217,250-251).
- **Impact:** For clusters with provisioned members, the omitted instance premium can exceed the per-request I/O saving, turning a recommended 'saving' into a real net loss. Counted dollars are overstated.
- **Fix:** Add the cluster's instance-fleet I/O-Optimized premium (sum over members of io_opt_price - std_price) to optimized_premium before computing net savings, and thread aurora_io_optimized into the instance pricing calls.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified. _check_io_tier (aurora.py:333-388) computes savings = standard_io_cost - optimized_premium (369-371) using only the storage-side premium; it has no awareness of cluster member instances and never adds the instance-price increase from switching the cluster to I/O-Optimized mode. The ~30% instance premium is documented in the code itself: core/pricing_engine.py:1160-1161 ('Aurora I/O-Optimized is ~30% dearer than Standard') and 1184-1188 pins storage='Aurora IO Optimization Mode' vs 'EBS Only' (EBS Only $5.12 vs IO mode $6.656 = 1.30x). The Aurora instance recs call get_rds_instance_monthly_price(engine, cls) at aurora.py:195, 217, 250-251 without the aurora_io_optimized kwarg, so they price at Standard (default False, pricing_engine.py:1152). For a cluster with provisioned members, the omitted per-instance ~30% premium can exceed the per-request I/O saving, turning a recommended saving into a net loss; the counted dollars are overstated. HIGH stands.

#### 🟠 H3 · Cross-adapter double count: same Aurora instance/cluster in Aurora tab and RDS tab  ·  `limitation` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/aurora.py:181-277`
- **Evidence:** _check_provisioned_instances emits counted rightsizing/Graviton recs keyed by raw instance_id. The RDS adapter processes the SAME describe_db_instances rows including Aurora members (services/rds.py:609-621 prices aurora_io members) and consumes Cost Optimization Hub RdsDbInstance/RdsDbCluster recs (type_map -> 'rds', core/scan_orchestrator.py:90-91) which are counted via rds_logic reconcile (authority CoH>CO>heuristic, services/rds_logic.py:188-227). There is NO shared 'covered' set between the Aurora and RDS adapters and the keys differ (Aurora uses bare id, RDS normalizes ARNs).
- **Impact:** When CoH emits a rightsizing rec for an Aurora member instance, that instance's saving is counted in BOTH the RDS tab (CoH, counted) and the Aurora tab (heuristic rightsizing/Graviton, counted); result_builder sums both into the headline (core/result_builder.py:72). Double-counted dollars, account-dependent.
- **Fix:** Establish a single owner for Aurora-member rightsizing. Either exclude aurora engines from the RDS CoH/heuristic rightsizing path, or have the Aurora adapter consume ctx.cost_hub_splits and dedup its instance recs against CoH RdsDbInstance/RdsDbCluster ids by normalized resource id.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified as a real, account-dependent cross-adapter double count. The Aurora adapter's _check_provisioned_instances (aurora.py:181-277) emits counted instance_rightsizing and instance_graviton recs keyed by bare instance_id (resource_id=instance_id), summed at aurora.py:460. The RDS path consumes the SAME describe_db_instances rows (rds.py:609-621 even prices aurora_io members) and ingests Cost Optimization Hub RdsDbInstance/RdsDbCluster recs mapped to 'rds' (core/scan_orchestrator.py:90-91); those CoH recs are counted via resolve_rds_findings — coh_savings is summed unconditionally (rds_logic.py:215-216, 246-249) with no engine filter. Both adapters' total_monthly_savings are summed into the headline at result_builder.py:72. Confirmed there is NO shared covered-set spanning Aurora↔RDS: grep shows intra-adapter dedup sets only (ec2.py:129-147, ebs_logic.py:115, dynamodb.py:137, containers_logic.py:296, rds_logic.py coh_keys) and aurora.py has zero CoH/cost_hub_splits awareness. So when CoH emits a rec for an Aurora member, that resource is counted in the RDS tab (CoH) and again in the Aurora tab (heuristic), with differing keys (Aurora bare id vs RDS normalized ARN via coh_rds_key) preventing any incidental overlap. Magnitude is account-dependent (only when CoH fires on an Aurora resource), as the finding states. HIGH stands.

#### 🟠 H4 · _describe_aurora_clusters swallows all errors silently — Aurora vanishes on AccessDenied/throttle  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/aurora.py:46-59`
- **Evidence:** try: paginator... except Exception: try: describe_db_clusters... except Exception: pass; return clusters. No ctx is passed in, so an AccessDenied / Throttling / RequestLimitExceeded yields an empty cluster list with no ctx.warn / ctx.permission_issue.
- **Impact:** A permissions or throttling gap makes the entire Aurora tab silently empty (0 clusters, $0) with no diagnostic — indistinguishable from an account that has no Aurora. Lost coverage, no signal.
- **Fix:** Pass ctx into the helper and classify the exception via the RDS-advisor pattern: AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation/OptInRequired -> ctx.permission_issue, else ctx.warn('[aurora] describe_db_clusters failed: ...','aurora'); only swallow after recording.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified at aurora.py:46-59. _describe_aurora_clusters(rds) takes only the rds client — no ctx — and wraps the paginator in 'except Exception:' whose fallback describe_db_clusters is itself wrapped in 'except Exception: pass', returning the empty clusters list. An AccessDenied / Throttling / RequestLimitExceeded therefore yields [] with no ctx.warn and no ctx.permission_issue, so the serverless_v2 and io_tier checks and extras.cluster_count silently report 0/$0 — indistinguishable from an account with no Aurora. Contrast aurora.py:172 where the separate describe_db_instances path does call ctx.warn, and the network adapter classifies AccessDenied via record_aws_error; the cluster path has neither. One nuance that does not refute the finding: because the provisioned-instance checks use a distinct describe_db_instances call with its own error handling, under a permission grant that allows DescribeDBInstances but not DescribeDBClusters the instance recs could still surface, so 'entire tab empty' is the broad-failure case rather than universal; under a blanket AccessDenied/throttle both fail. The cited defect (silent swallow with no diagnostic for the cluster path) is exactly real. HIGH stands.

#### 🟡 M1 · ACU_HOURLY_FALLBACK=0.06 is 2x low and inconsistent with the engine's $0.12 fallback  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/aurora.py:22,43`
- **Evidence:** ACU_HOURLY_FALLBACK=0.06; return ACU_HOURLY_FALLBACK*ctx.pricing_multiplier. AWS Pricing API us-east-1 'Aurora:ServerlessV2Usage' = $0.12/ACU-hr (validated). core/pricing_engine.py:301 FALLBACK_AURORA_ACU_HOURLY=0.12 (correct). The two fallbacks for the same SKU disagree by 2x.
- **Impact:** On the path where get_aurora_acu_hourly() raises (e.g. pricing_engine missing), serverless ACU savings are computed at half rate — understated ~50%. Mostly masked because the engine method internally returns its own $0.12 fallback before raising, but the 0.06 constant is still wrong and a latent 2x error.
- **Fix:** Set ACU_HOURLY_FALLBACK=0.12 to match the validated rate and the engine constant (region-scaled once via pricing_multiplier).

#### 🟡 M2 · Render desync: serverless_v2 & io_tier recs show savings only as a raw unstyled number, header 'Resource'  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `reporter_phase_b.py:1812-1876`
- **Evidence:** aurora has no PHASE_B handler and is not in _PHASE_A_SERVICES/_PHASE_B_SKIP_PER_REC (confirmed absent from reporter_phase_b.py), so should_fallback_to_per_rec('aurora')=True -> render_generic_per_rec -> _render_generic_other_rec. serverless_v2/io_tier recs carry no CheckCategory/Recommendation/EstimatedSavings and no resourceArn; the resource_id chain (1815-1860) does not include 'cluster_id', so resource_id='Resource'. monthly_savings is dumped by the generic loop as '<p>Monthly Savings: 1051.2</p>' (raw float, no $, not in the .savings styled class). instance_optimization recs DO carry EstimatedSavings -> styled line.
- **Impact:** The serverless/IO dollars counted into the headline are not legibly attributed on the cards (no $ sign, no savings styling, cluster id missing from the title). Headline vs visible-card desync; user cannot reconcile the figure.
- **Fix:** Give serverless_v2/io_tier recs an EstimatedSavings string (e.g. f"${monthly_savings:.2f}/mo") + a CheckCategory + resource_id=cluster_id (or add 'cluster_id' to the _render_generic_other_rec lookup), or register a dedicated PHASE_B handler for the three Aurora sources.

#### 🟡 M3 · CloudWatch helpers swallow AccessDenied/throttle as 'no data'  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/aurora.py:76-91,104-119,128-145`
- **Evidence:** _get_cloudwatch_avg/_get_cloudwatch_sum/_get_cloudwatch_avg_max each wrap get_metric_statistics in try/except Exception: pass; return None. A cloudwatch:GetMetricStatistics AccessDenied or Throttling is indistinguishable from a metric with no datapoints, and is never recorded on ctx.
- **Impact:** Permission/throttle on CloudWatch silently suppresses serverless ACU and I/O-tier checks (both bail when the metric is None) and rightsizing (warns per-instance but not the access cause). Under-reported savings with no permission_issue surfaced.
- **Fix:** Pass ctx into the helpers and classify botocore ClientError codes: AccessDenied/Throttling/RequestLimitExceeded -> ctx.permission_issue/ctx.warn once; return None only for genuinely empty Datapoints.

#### 🟡 M4 · No structured AuditBasis on any Aurora counted finding  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/aurora.py:316-328,374-386,222-242`
- **Evidence:** None of the three checks attaches an AuditBasis dict (rate/region/metric-window/formula); instance recs carry only a prose 'reason'. Contrast RDS which records AuditBasis on every counted rec (services/rds.py:585-600,651-661).
- **Impact:** Counted Aurora dollars are not defensible from the report alone — no recorded rate, region, metric window, or formula — making the fabricated/mis-rated figures (C1/H1) harder to audit downstream.
- **Fix:** Attach an AuditBasis to each counted rec: ACU rate + region + 14d ServerlessV2CapacityUtilization window + formula for serverless; I/O rate + storage premium + 14d Volume*IOPs window for I/O; instance price basis + CPUUtilization window for rightsizing/Graviton.

#### 🟡 M5 · I/O-tier 'monthly_io' derived from Sum of VolumeReadIOPs/WriteIOPs needs metric-semantics validation  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/aurora.py:348-356`
- **Evidence:** read_io=_get_cloudwatch_sum(...,"VolumeReadIOPs"); total=read+write; daily_io_avg=total/14; monthly_io=daily_io_avg*30. _get_cloudwatch_sum sums 14 daily Statistics=['Sum'] datapoints (Period=86400). VolumeReadIOPs/WriteIOPs are cluster-level billed-I/O metrics; if CloudWatch surfaces them as a per-interval count, daily Sum approximates true ops, but if treated as an averaged IOPS rate the Sum is a meaningless sum-of-averages.
- **Impact:** The entire io_tier saving rides on monthly_io being a true billed-operation count. If the Sum semantics are wrong, the saving is fabricated; the 14->30 day extrapolation also assumes uniform daily I/O.
- **Fix:** Validate against CloudWatch metric metadata that VolumeReadIOPs/WriteIOPs daily Sum yields total billed operations; otherwise compute ops from Average*period-seconds, and base the monthly figure on the actual observed window rather than /14*30.

#### 🟢 L1 · _check_io_tier skips silently in fast_mode (no warn)  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/aurora.py:340-341`
- **Evidence:** if fast_mode: return recs (no ctx available to warn). _check_provisioned_instances by contrast warns 'fast mode: skipping Aurora instance rightsizing metric reads' (aurora.py:178).
- **Impact:** In fast_mode the I/O-tier check produces nothing with no indication that a savings dimension was skipped — inconsistent with the rest of the adapter.
- **Fix:** Thread ctx into _check_io_tier and emit a single ctx.warn on the fast_mode skip, matching the rightsizing path.

#### 🟢 L2 · scan() per-cluster failure recorded via logger only, not ctx.warn  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/aurora.py:451-453`
- **Evidence:** except Exception as e: logger.warning(f"[aurora] cluster check failed: {e}"); continue. No ctx.warn, so a per-cluster failure (e.g. malformed metric) never reaches the report's warnings.
- **Impact:** Individual clusters can be dropped from analysis with no user-visible signal.
- **Fix:** Replace logger.warning with ctx.warn(..., 'aurora') (keep the logger line if desired).

#### 🟢 L3 · ACU rate and instance pricing not storage-mode-aware for I/O-Optimized clusters  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/aurora.py:38,195,217,250-251`
- **Evidence:** _get_acu_hourly always calls get_aurora_acu_hourly() which fetches the Standard 'Aurora:ServerlessV2Usage' rate (core/pricing_engine.py:1466-1474, databaseEngine='Aurora MySQL', no storage-mode pin); instance recs call get_rds_instance_monthly_price without aurora_io_optimized so I/O-Optimized members are priced at the cheaper Standard 'EBS Only' SKU.
- **Impact:** For I/O-Optimized clusters, the ACU rate (higher for I/O-Optimized) and instance price deltas are understated — conservative direction for rightsizing/Graviton, but inaccurate.
- **Fix:** Detect the cluster StorageType (aurora-iopt1) and select the I/O-Optimized ACU rate and pass aurora_io_optimized=True into instance pricing.

#### 🟢 L4 · GroupingSpec references keys absent from recs (harmless only because grouping is unused)  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/aurora.py:408`
- **Evidence:** grouping=GroupingSpec(by='check_category', label_path='check_type'); recs use 'CheckCategory' (instance only) and 'check_type' everywhere, never a lowercase 'check_category'. GroupingSpec is defined in core/contracts.py:87-96 but is not consumed by result_builder/reporter (grep finds usage only in contracts.py and core/CLAUDE.md).
- **Impact:** No runtime effect today, but if the configurable grouping path is ever wired up, by='check_category' would bucket all Aurora recs under a blank category.
- **Fix:** Align the spec to an existing key (e.g. by='source') or rename recs to expose 'check_category', so the spec is correct when grouping is activated.

#### 🟢 L5 · Module docstring overpromises unimplemented checks  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/aurora.py:1-9,440-447`
- **Evidence:** Docstring advertises 'Clone/snapshot sprawl, Global DB replica lag, Backtrack window cost risk' but scan() only implements serverless ACU, I/O tier, and provisioned-instance rightsizing/Graviton. global_count is collected as a stat only (extras.global_cluster_count) with no savings claim.
- **Impact:** Documentation/coverage mismatch; no fabricated dollars (global_count is stat-only), but the advertised coverage does not exist.
- **Fix:** Trim the docstring to the implemented checks or mark the others as TODO/intentional gaps.

---

### Batch — `services/adapters/batch.py`

**Module identity:** key="batch", display_name="Batch", cli_aliases=("batch",), required_clients()=("batch",); declares NEITHER reads_fast_mode NOR requires_cloudwatch and reads no metrics (services/adapters/batch.py:14-23). It is a category-string→savings-factor adapter over EC2 on-demand pricing: BatchModule.scan wraps services/batch_svc.py:get_enhanced_batch_checks (raw recs) and prices them via ctx.pricing_engine.get_ec2_hourly_price(instance_types[0]) × 730 × factor. Batch has NO native price — AWS Pricing MCP confirms there is no "batch"/AWSBatch service code, so the only legitimate basis is underlying EC2/Fargate compute. CoH and Compute Optimizer do NOT apply: "batch" is absent from core/scan_orchestrator.py _HUB_SERVICES (lines 52-74) and type_map (86-113), and services/advisor.py has no Batch helper — so "missing CoH/CO" is correctly NOT flagged. Render path: emits one enhanced_checks SourceBlock with no PHASE_B_HANDLERS entry; "batch" is not in _PHASE_A_SERVICES nor _PHASE_B_SKIP_PER_REC, so should_fallback_to_per_rec("batch")=True and the generic per-rec renderer (reporter_phase_b.py render_generic_other_rec, 1812-1876) renders each rec — a deliberate fallback, not a silent render-desync. The services/adapters/CLAUDE.md row labels batch "Fixed per-rec estimate," which is stale (it now prices via get_ec2_hourly_price; only the unused $150 constant is flat).

**Verdict:** The batch adapter counts a real dollar on exactly ONE of its four checks (Graviton Migration), because the pricing loop only prices recs carrying an InstanceTypes key (batch.py:55-61) and only the Graviton rec sets it (batch_svc.py:73). The other three (Fargate-Spot, EC2-Spot, Job-Rightsizing) render cards advertising 60-90% savings while contributing $0 to the headline — a string-vs-counted desync (C1). The lone counted number is itself fabricated: it multiplies a region-correct EC2 on-demand rate by ×730 (24/7) with no CloudWatch/job-runtime evidence on an inherently bursty service (C2), and uses a flat 0.20 factor on an arbitrary instance_types[0] rather than the validated per-family x86→arm delta (M1). The is_fargate test is structurally wrong (tests instanceTypes instead of computeResources.type), so the Fargate-Spot path effectively never fires (H1). Silent-failure handling is weak (inner except:pass and a generic outer warn both swallow AccessDenied, H2/H3). Region scaling is correct (single application, multiplier deliberately discarded). CoH/CO correctly do not apply. Net: the Batch tab's headline is Graviton-only, hour-fabricated, and contradicted by the percentages its own cards display.

**Pricing validation:** Validated LIVE via AWS Pricing MCP (us-east-1, AmazonEC2, OnDemand, operatingSystem=Linux, tenancy=Shared, preInstalledSw=NA, capacitystatus=Used): m5.xlarge = $0.192000/hr (SKU 5G4TA8Z4MUKE6MJB), m6g.xlarge (Graviton2) = $0.154000/hr (SKU ZH44WTP8EHDAHM69) → real x86→arm delta 19.8%, confirming the flat 0.20 Graviton factor is coincidentally close for THIS pair but is applied blindly to instance_types[0] (M1). Confirmed there is NO 'batch'/AWSBatch service code in the Pricing API (get_pricing_service_codes filter='batch' → no_matches_found), validating that Batch has no native price and EC2/Fargate is the only legitimate basis. NOT validated (count $0 today, so non-material): the EC2-Spot 0.70 and Fargate-Spot 0.70 factors need live on-demand−Spot delta validation (describe_spot_price_history) if C1 wires them, and the Job-Rightsizing 0.30 needs a real current−target basis — all three flagged needs-live-Pricing/Spot-validation in the fix plan.

**Cost checks:**

| Check | Status | Trigger | Savings basis |
|---|---|---|---|
| Batch Fargate Spot Optimization | advisory | ENABLED CE classified as Fargate by is_fargate (services/batch_svc.py:39) AND allocationStrategy != SPOT_CAPACITY_OPTIMIZED (batch_svc.py:42) | category 'Fargate Spot' → rate 0.70 (batch.py:45-46), BUT rec carries no InstanceTypes key, so the pricing loop guard `if ctx.pricing_engine is not None and instance_types` (batch.py:56) is False → skipped → $0 counted. Card still advertises EstimatedSavings='70% with Fargate Spot'. Detection is broken (see F H1) so this almost never fires. |
| Batch Spot Optimization | advisory | ENABLED non-Fargate CE with allocationStrategy != SPOT_CAPACITY_OPTIMIZED (services/batch_svc.py:55) | category 'Spot' → rate 0.70 (batch.py:51-52), no InstanceTypes key → pricing loop skips → $0 counted. Card advertises EstimatedSavings='60-90% with Spot instances'. If wired it must use real on-demand−Spot delta via describe_spot_price_history (as EC2 does), not a flat 0.70. |
| Batch Graviton Migration | counted | ENABLED non-Fargate CE where instanceTypes is non-empty AND no element contains substring '6g' or '7g' (services/batch_svc.py:68-69) | ONLY counted check. monthly = get_ec2_hourly_price(instanceTypes[0]) × 730; savings += monthly × 0.20 (batch.py:48-61). Live AWS Pricing (us-east-1, Linux, Shared, capacitystatus=Used): m5.xlarge=$0.192/hr → $0.192×730×0.20 = $28.03/mo counted. ctx.pricing_multiplier intentionally NOT re-applied (batch.py:57-58,65) — region-correct, single application, verified. The 0.20 is a flat factor (not the validated x86→arm delta) and ×730 assumes 24/7 with no usage metric. |
| Batch Job Rightsizing | advisory | ACTIVE job definition with containerProperties.vcpus > 8 OR containerProperties.memory > 16384 (services/batch_svc.py:89) | no category match → falls to else rate 0.30 (batch.py:53), but rec carries no InstanceTypes key → pricing loop skips → $0 counted. Card advertises EstimatedSavings='Rightsize based on actual usage'. Reads only legacy containerProperties.vcpus/memory; misses resourceRequirements / nodeProperties job defs (see F M2). |

**Findings:**

#### 🔴 C1 · Only Graviton recs count a dollar; Fargate-Spot / EC2-Spot / Job-Rightsizing advertise percentages but count $0 (string-vs-counted desync)  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/batch.py + services/batch_svc.py:batch.py:55-62; batch_svc.py:43-99`
- **Evidence:** Pricing loop only prices recs carrying InstanceTypes: `instance_types = rec.get("InstanceTypes", []) ; if ctx.pricing_engine is not None and instance_types: ... savings += monthly*rate` (batch.py:55-61). In batch_svc.py ONLY the Graviton rec adds InstanceTypes (line 73). The Fargate-Spot rec (43-53), EC2-Spot rec (56-66) and Job-Rightsizing rec (90-99) carry NO InstanceTypes, yet each ships an EstimatedSavings string ('70% with Fargate Spot' / '60-90% with Spot instances' / 'Rightsize based on actual usage'). The per-rec renderer prints that raw string: reporter_phase_b.py:1874-1875 `content += ... Estimated Savings: {rec["EstimatedSavings"]}` while the tab total = `total_monthly_savings = savings` (Graviton float only, batch.py:72).
- **Impact:** 3 of 4 check types render cards claiming 60-90% savings that contribute $0 to the headline. Users see large advertised percentages that never reconcile with the per-tab/executive total. Pure leakage of trust, not dollars — but the headline is silently Graviton-only.
- **Fix:** Either (a) mark these Counted=False advisory by rewriting their EstimatedSavings to '$0.00/month - advisory: enable Spot/Fargate-Spot' so the per-rec renderer is honest, or (b) wire real pricing: Spot = on-demand−Spot delta via describe_spot_price_history; Fargate-Spot = Fargate vCPU/mem on-demand−spot delta; Job-Rightsizing = current−target vCPU/mem cost. Until then, do not advertise a percentage the total ignores.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified end-to-end. batch.py:56 gates pricing on `instance_types` truthiness (`if ctx.pricing_engine is not None and instance_types`), and savings only accrues at :61. In batch_svc.py only the Graviton rec sets InstanceTypes (line 73, guarded by `not has_graviton and instance_types`); the Fargate-Spot rec (43-53), EC2-Spot rec (55-66) and Job-Rightsizing rec (90-99) carry NO InstanceTypes but each ships an EstimatedSavings string ('70% with Fargate Spot':50; '60-90% with Spot instances':63; 'Rightsize based on actual usage':96). Batch routes to the generic per-rec path: service_key 'batch' is not in PHASE_B_HANDLERS and not in _PHASE_B_SKIP_PER_REC (reporter_phase_b.py:2516-2531,2543-2550), so should_fallback_to_per_rec=True → render_generic_per_rec → else-branch _render_generic_other_rec, which prints the raw string at reporter_phase_b.py:1874-1875 exactly as cited. Tab/headline total is total_monthly_savings=savings (batch.py:72), Graviton-float-only. The string-vs-counted desync is real: 3 of 4 check types render advertised percentages that contribute $0. (Severity 'CRITICAL' is debatable for a trust/display issue the finding itself concedes is 'not dollars', but the mechanism is accurate as described.)

#### 🔴 C2 · Graviton saving multiplies by ×730 (24/7) with no usage metric — fabricated hours on the only counted check  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/batch.py:59-61`
- **Evidence:** `hourly = ctx.pricing_engine.get_ec2_hourly_price(instance_types[0]); monthly = hourly * 730; savings += monthly * rate`. The adapter reads NO CloudWatch and NO Batch job runtime (declares neither requires_cloudwatch nor reads_fast_mode, batch.py:14-23). Batch CEs are bursty — computeResources scale from minvCpus (typically 0) to maxvCpus and back. A CE whose instance ran 2 hr last month is priced as 730 hr. Validated rate: m5.xlarge=$0.192/hr → $0.192×730×0.20=$28.03/mo counted regardless of actual runtime.
- **Impact:** The single counted dollar is a fixed-hours fabrication; overstatement scales with idleness (up to ~365× for a CE that ran one day). This is the dominant dollar error in the adapter.
- **Fix:** Derive an hour count from evidence: CloudWatch CPUUtilization datapoint count, or Batch ListJobs RUNNING/SUCCEEDED runtime, or a minvCpus floor; gate on ctx.fast_mode and declare requires_cloudwatch/reads_fast_mode. With no runtime evidence, emit the Graviton rec as a $0 advisory rather than ×730. Record a structured AuditBasis (rate/region/hours-window/formula) on the counted finding.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** batch.py:59-61 computes `hourly = get_ec2_hourly_price(instance_types[0]); monthly = hourly*730; savings += monthly*rate` with a hardcoded 730-hour (24/7) assumption and no usage input. The adapter declares only required_clients=('batch',) (batch.py:21-23) and inherits requires_cloudwatch=False / reads_fast_mode=False from services/_base.py:24-25 without override; get_enhanced_batch_checks reads only describe_compute_environments and describe_job_definitions — no CloudWatch, no job runtime. So a bursty Batch CE (minvCpus→maxvCpus, often idle) is priced at 730 hr regardless of actual runtime, and this is the single counted dollar line. Arithmetic checks (m5.xlarge $0.192*730*0.20=$28.03). Minor nuance: the impact's '~365x for a CE that ran one day' is loose — 365x corresponds to the evidence body's correct 2-hr-runtime example, whereas a 24-hr (one day) runtime is ~30x; the core mechanism and dominant-error framing hold.

#### 🟠 H1 · is_fargate detection is broken — every Fargate CE is misclassified into the EC2 branch  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/batch_svc.py:39-41`
- **Evidence:** `is_fargate = ce_type == "MANAGED" and any(t.upper() == "FARGATE" for t in instance_types)`. Fargate-ness actually lives in computeResources.type ∈ {EC2, SPOT, FARGATE, FARGATE_SPOT}; Fargate CEs have NO instanceTypes list. So `any(...== "FARGATE" ... for t in instance_types)` iterates an empty (or EC2-type) list and is ~always False. Every Fargate CE falls into the else/EC2 branch (batch_svc.py:54), where it gets a Spot rec and is skipped by the Graviton branch (instanceTypes empty, line 69).
- **Impact:** Whole class (all Fargate CEs) silently never produces the Fargate-Spot rec; the Fargate-Spot check effectively never fires. Fargate CEs are also mislabeled EC2 in their rendered card. Coverage gap.
- **Fix:** Read `ctype = ce.get("computeResources",{}).get("type",""); is_fargate = ctype in ("FARGATE","FARGATE_SPOT")`. Use computeResources.type (not instanceTypes) for the EC2 vs Fargate split.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** batch_svc.py:37 reads `instance_types = compute_resources.get('instanceTypes', [])` and line 39 computes `is_fargate = ce_type == 'MANAGED' and any(t.upper() == 'FARGATE' for t in instance_types)`. The actual Fargate discriminator computeResources.type (EC2|SPOT|FARGATE|FARGATE_SPOT) is never read anywhere in the function. AWS does not place 'FARGATE' inside instanceTypes (Fargate CEs have no instanceTypes), so the any(...) is ~always False and every Fargate CE falls into the else/EC2 branch (54-66), receiving an EC2-labeled Spot rec; the Graviton branch is then skipped because `not has_graviton and instance_types` is False on the empty list (69). Fargate-Spot check effectively never fires and Fargate CEs are mislabeled EC2. Confirmed exactly as described.

#### 🟠 H2 · Inner `except Exception: pass` swallows describe_job_definitions failures (incl. AccessDenied) silently  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/batch_svc.py:80-101`
- **Evidence:** The whole describe_job_definitions paginator is wrapped in `try: ... except Exception: pass` (lines 80-101). A denied or throttled batch:DescribeJobDefinitions kills Job Rightsizing with zero signal — no ctx.warn, no ctx.permission_issue. ctx.permission_issue exists (core/scan_context.py:59) and a classifier helper services/_aws_errors.record_aws_error is used by the network adapter, but batch_svc imports neither.
- **Impact:** Silent coverage loss: job-rightsizing scan can fail completely and the report shows nothing wrong. AccessDenied is not surfaced as an IAM gap.
- **Fix:** Replace `except Exception: pass` with classification: AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation → ctx.permission_issue(..., action='batch:DescribeJobDefinitions'); other → ctx.warn. Route through services/_aws_errors.record_aws_error as the network sub-shims do.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** batch_svc.py:80-101 wraps the entire describe_job_definitions paginator in `try: ... except Exception: pass`, swallowing any failure (AccessDenied, throttling) of Job Rightsizing with zero signal — no ctx.warn, no ctx.permission_issue. The dedicated channel ctx.permission_issue exists (core/scan_context.py:59) and a classifier services/_aws_errors.record_aws_error (lines 47-56: AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation/OptInRequired → permission_issue, else warn, 'Never silently swallows') is imported by network.py and the network sub-services (vpc_endpoints/load_balancer/nat_gateway/elastic_ip), but batch_svc.py imports only typing.Any and ScanContext (lines 9-11). Silent coverage loss confirmed.

#### 🟠 H3 · Outer except routes AccessDenied to a generic ctx.warn instead of ctx.permission_issue  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/batch_svc.py:102-103`
- **Evidence:** `except Exception as e: ctx.warn(f"Could not analyze Batch resources: {e}", "batch")` wraps the entire compute-environment loop. A denied batch:DescribeComputeEnvironments yields one generic warning and an empty Batch tab; the IAM gap is not recorded as a permission_issue (core/scan_context.py:59 provides the dedicated channel).
- **Impact:** On AccessDenied the whole Batch tab silently empties and the failure is mis-recorded as a generic warning, not an actionable permission gap.
- **Fix:** Classify the exception: botocore ClientError with Code in {AccessDenied, AccessDeniedException, UnauthorizedOperation} → ctx.permission_issue(..., action='batch:DescribeComputeEnvironments'); otherwise ctx.warn. Reuse services/_aws_errors.record_aws_error.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** batch_svc.py:102-103 is `except Exception as e: ctx.warn(f"Could not analyze Batch resources: {e}", "batch")`, wrapping the whole compute-environment loop (and the job-def block). A denied batch:DescribeComputeEnvironments is therefore caught and emitted as a single generic warning via ctx.warn, never ctx.permission_issue (core/scan_context.py:59), so the IAM gap is not recorded on the dedicated permission channel and the Batch tab silently empties. record_aws_error (services/_aws_errors.py:47-56) would have classified it as a permission_issue but is not used here. Confirmed as described.

#### 🟡 M1 · Graviton 0.20 is a flat factor on an arbitrary instance_types[0] x86 price, not the validated per-family x86→arm delta; no arm-equivalent existence check  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/batch.py + services/batch_svc.py:batch.py:48-61; batch_svc.py:68-78`
- **Evidence:** savings = get_ec2_hourly_price(instance_types[0]) × 730 × 0.20. The defensible number is (price(x86) − price(arm_equivalent)) × hours. Live AWS Pricing (us-east-1, Linux): m5.xlarge=$0.192/hr, m6g.xlarge=$0.154/hr → real delta = (0.192−0.154)/0.192 = 19.8% (the flat 0.20 is close for THIS pair, but is applied blindly). Only instance_types[0] is priced; a CE listing a mix (e.g. ['m5','c5','optimal']) or families with no Graviton equivalent (or a different delta) gets a mis-rated or fabricated number, and 'optimal'/family-label entries are not real instance types so get_ec2_hourly_price likely returns 0.0.
- **Impact:** The one counted dollar can be mis-rated (wrong family delta) or fabricated (no arm equivalent / family-label first element prices to $0). Magnitude varies per family; for m5→m6g it is roughly correct, for others it is not.
- **Fix:** Compute the exact current−target delta against a real arm-equivalent map (m5.xlarge→m6g.xlarge, c5→c6g, r5→r6g, etc.); skip the rec when no arm equivalent exists; price across the CE's actual instance mix rather than only instance_types[0]; record the type/rate/factor in an AuditBasis.

#### 🟡 M2 · Job Rightsizing reads only legacy containerProperties.vcpus/memory — resourceRequirements / nodeProperties job defs are invisible  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/batch_svc.py:85-89`
- **Evidence:** `container_props = job_def.get("containerProperties", {}); vcpus = container_props.get("vcpus", 0); memory = container_props.get("memory", 0); if vcpus > 8 or memory > 16384:`. Fargate and modern ECS-style job defs declare CPU/memory under containerProperties.resourceRequirements (entries type=VCPU/MEMORY) and multi-node jobs under nodeProperties — neither carries top-level vcpus/memory, so they score 0 and never trip the gate.
- **Impact:** A whole class of modern/Fargate/multi-node job defs is never inspected for over-allocation (the check counts $0 today, so impact is coverage not dollars, but it is the only job-level lever).
- **Fix:** Parse resourceRequirements (sum VCPU and MEMORY entries) and nodeProperties.nodeRangeProperties[].container before applying the >8 vCPU / >16384 MB threshold.

#### 🟡 M3 · Latent Spot + Graviton stacking on the same non-Fargate CE (becomes a live double-count if Spot is wired)  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/batch_svc.py:55-78`
- **Evidence:** For a single non-Fargate ENABLED CE the Spot branch (55-66) and the Graviton branch (68-78) are independent `if`s, not mutually exclusive — the same CE emits BOTH a Spot rec and a Graviton rec. Today only Graviton counts a dollar (C1), so no live double-count, but wiring Spot (C1 fix) would discount the SAME CE's instances by 0.70 (Spot) and 0.20 (Graviton) on the same bill.
- **Impact:** No double-count today; a guaranteed ~0.76-combined overstatement on every non-Graviton non-Spot CE once Spot pricing is enabled.
- **Fix:** Before wiring Spot, define authority order: apply Spot first then Graviton on the post-Spot price (0.70 then 0.20 of remainder), or emit only one rec per CE. Add a per-CE 'covered' guard.

#### 🟡 M4 · Cross-adapter overlap: Batch-launched EC2 instances may be counted in both the Batch tab and the EC2 tab  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/batch.py + core/result_builder.py:batch.py:67-75; result_builder.py (per-tab sum)`
- **Evidence:** Batch EC2 CEs launch EC2 instances that the EC2 adapter independently surfaces (Compute Optimizer rightsizing / Spot / idle) and adds to its own dedup `covered` set. Batch prices the CE's instance type for a Graviton saving with no awareness of the EC2 tab; result_builder serializes each tab's total_monthly_savings independently and the executive headline sums them. Batch-managed instances are tagged AWSBatchServiceTag, so the same physical instance can appear in both tabs.
- **Impact:** The same underlying EC2 instance's saving can be counted twice (once as a Batch CE Graviton saving, once as an EC2 rightsizing/Spot saving), inflating the cross-tab headline.
- **Fix:** Pick a single owner — CE-level config (Graviton/Spot allocation strategy) is a Batch lever, per-instance rightsizing is an EC2 lever. Exclude AWSBatchServiceTag-tagged instances from the EC2 adapter (or vice-versa) and add to the shared dedup covered set.

#### 🟢 L1 · Docstring and CLAUDE.md misstate the Graviton rate, the multiplier behavior, and the pricing model  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/batch.py + services/adapters/CLAUDE.md:batch.py:30-31; CLAUDE.md Flat-rate row`
- **Evidence:** batch.py docstring line 30 says 'Graviton=0.10' but code uses rate=0.20 (line 49); line 31 says 'All savings multiplied by ctx.pricing_multiplier for regional adjustment' but the code explicitly does NOT — line 65 `_ = multiplier  # documented; live path is region-correct already`. services/adapters/CLAUDE.md lists batch under 'Flat-rate (1 adapter) | Fixed per-rec estimate', but the code prices via get_ec2_hourly_price × 730 × factor (only the unused $150 constant is flat).
- **Impact:** Doc/code drift: a reader trusting the docstring would expect 0.10 and a region multiplier, both wrong; the CLAUDE.md taxonomy row mislabels the pricing strategy.
- **Fix:** Update docstring to 'Graviton=0.20' and remove the pricing_multiplier claim (note region-correctness comes from get_ec2_hourly_price). Update the CLAUDE.md row to 'EC2-derived: get_ec2_hourly_price(type) × 730 × category factor (Graviton only counted)'.

#### 🟢 L2 · Dead constant BATCH_COMPUTE_FALLBACK_MONTHLY = 150.0 is never referenced  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/batch.py:11`
- **Evidence:** `grep -rn BATCH_COMPUTE_FALLBACK_MONTHLY --include=*.py` returns exactly one hit — its own definition at services/adapters/batch.py:11. The no-InstanceTypes path skips (batch.py:62 comment) rather than falling back, so the constant is unreachable.
- **Impact:** No dollar impact, but the $150 us-east-1 flat constant is misleading dead code (it was over/under-stated 1.5-36× by instance type when previously used).
- **Fix:** Remove the constant, or wire a genuine region-scaled fallback (constant × ctx.pricing_multiplier) — never reintroduce the flat $150.

#### 🟢 L3 · Generic per-rec card header renders 'Resource' for Batch recs (CE/job-def name not in the resource_id key chain)  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `reporter_phase_b.py:1815-1863`
- **Evidence:** _render_generic_other_rec builds resource_id from a long `or` chain (1815-1858) that has no entry for ComputeEnvironmentName or JobDefinitionName, and the trailing ternary `... if rec.get("resourceArn") else "Resource"` (1859-1861) yields 'Resource' because Batch recs have no resourceArn. So every card header reads e.g. 'Batch Graviton Migration: Resource'. The CE name still appears in the body field loop (1865-1869), so this is cosmetic, not a dollar error.
- **Impact:** Reporting clarity only — cards do not identify which CE/job def the saving belongs to in the header; no effect on counted dollars.
- **Fix:** Add `rec.get("ComputeEnvironmentName") or rec.get("JobDefinitionName")` to the resource_id chain in _render_generic_other_rec.

---

### Bedrock — `services/adapters/bedrock.py`

**Module identity:** key="bedrock", cli_aliases=("bedrock",), display_name="Bedrock", required_clients()=("bedrock","bedrock-agent","cloudwatch"), requires_cloudwatch=True, reads_fast_mode=True, grouping=GroupingSpec(by="check_category"), 3 module-level StatCardSpec stat_cards. Pricing is by MODULE CONSTANTS, not PricingEngine: PT_HOURLY_PRICE dict (lines 18-24) + PT_HOURLY_DEFAULT=1.0 (line 25) for PT model-unit hours, and a flat 0.000_003 $/token (line 193) for the on-demand token estimate; both multiplied by ctx.pricing_multiplier on the counted path (lines 149, 198). Consumes NEITHER Cost Optimization Hub NOR Compute Optimizer (not in scan_orchestrator _HUB_SERVICES/type_map; verified) — so "missing CoH/CO" is NOT a fair finding. It DOES read CloudWatch (AWS/Bedrock Invocations/InputTokenCount/OutputTokenCount) and correctly early-returns both PT checks under fast_mode. Emits 4 SourceBlocks; none registered in PHASE_B_HANDLERS and bedrock is absent from _PHASE_B_SKIP_PER_REC, so should_fallback_to_per_rec("bedrock")=True and all four render via render_generic_per_rec→_render_generic_other_rec.

**Verdict:** The Bedrock adapter's two counted dollar sources are structurally dead: it reads pt['modelId'] (lines 138/180), a field that does NOT exist on the boto3 ProvisionedModelSummary shape (verified against botocore), so model_id is always "" — which both forces the $1/hr fabricated default AND empties the CloudWatch ModelId dimension, causing _check_idle_pt and _check_pt_breakeven to short-circuit on None and never emit a finding (C1). Layered on top: a fabricated/24x-low PT default rate still counted without demotion (H1), truncated/unverifiable PT_HOURLY_PRICE keys with no real Claude PT SKU and ignored commitment term (H2), a single flat token rate 12x too high for Haiku input that ignores 5x-costlier output (H3), and a PT-wrong CloudWatch dimension (H4). All failure paths swallow exceptions without ctx.warn/permission_issue (M1). The KB $0 advisory and always-empty idle_agents source are correctly designed; the snake_case render desync (L1) and stat-card divergence (L2) are presentation-only and do not affect the counted total. Live Pricing-API validation corroborates the rate findings.

**Pricing validation:** Validated LIVE via AWS Pricing MCP (AmazonBedrock): (1) USW2-Llama3-1-70B-ProvisionedThroughput-NoCommit-ModelUnits = $24.00/hour (us-west-2, sku AEZCD6F9ZS3UKADP, unit=hour) — vs PT_HOURLY_DEFAULT=1.0, confirming the default is ~24x too low (H1). (2) USE1-Claude3Sonnet-input-tokens = $0.00300/1K (=0.000003/token, exactly the flat constant for Sonnet INPUT only); USE1-Claude3Haiku-input-tokens = $0.00025/1K (=0.00000025/token, so 0.000003 is ~12x too high for Haiku input) — confirming H3. (3) get_pricing_attribute_values(usagetype, 'ProvisionedThroughput') returns ModelUnits SKUs ONLY for Titan, Nova, Llama; a 'Claude' filter returns only ...-input-tokens — confirming NO Claude ProvisionedThroughput ModelUnits usagetype exists (H2). Claude 3 Sonnet OUTPUT token rate (published ~$0.015/1K, 5x input) could not be located under USE1-Claude3Sonnet-output-tokens in the live catalogue (the output-token list held Llama/Nova/Gemma/DeepSeek but no Claude) — the 5x output multiplier in H3 relies on published pricing and needs exact-SKU live confirmation. Also verified via botocore service model (not memory): ProvisionedModelSummary has no modelId/provisionedModelId member (C1).

**Cost checks:**

| Check | Status | Trigger | Savings basis |
|---|---|---|---|
| idle_provisioned_throughput (_check_idle_pt, lines 127-166) | counted | Provisioned Throughput with invocations == 0 over 30 days, via _get_pt_invocation_sum (AWS/Bedrock Invocations, dimension ModelId). Skipped entirely in fast_mode (lines 134-135). | monthly_waste = hourly * model_units * 730 * pricing_multiplier, hourly = PT_HOURLY_PRICE.get(model_id, PT_HOURLY_DEFAULT=1.0) (lines 148-149). Source: hardcoded module-constant dict (lines 18-25); region-scaled once by ctx.pricing_multiplier. |
| pt_breakeven_analysis (_check_pt_breakeven, lines 169-214) | counted | PT monthly commitment cost > estimated on-demand; requires non-None InputTokenCount AND OutputTokenCount and od_monthly_estimate>0. Skipped in fast_mode (lines 176-177). | pt_monthly = hourly * model_units * 730 (same PT_HOURLY_PRICE.get(...,1.0)); od_monthly_estimate = (input_tokens + output_tokens) * 0.000_003 (flat, model-agnostic, single rate for BOTH input and output, line 193); savings = (pt_monthly - od_monthly_estimate) * pricing_multiplier (line 198). |
| idle_knowledge_bases (_check_idle_knowledge_bases, lines 217-269) | advisory | Every Knowledge Base listed via bedrock-agent list_knowledge_bases (no utilization gate). | monthly_savings = 0.0 for every KB plus pricing_warning 'requires KB query/ingest CW metrics for quantified savings' (lines 262-263). Deliberate $0 advisory; KB_OCU_HOURLY=0.20 (line 26) defined but intentionally unused so OCU cost is not double-counted against OpenSearch Serverless. |
| idle_agents (_check_idle_agents, lines 272-300) | advisory | Lists agents via bedrock-agent list_agents but emits NOTHING (source always empty); agents accrue no AWS charge (comment lines 295-298). agent_count is informational only. | No savings emitted (empty rec list); the old $5/mo placeholder was removed. |

**Findings:**

#### 🔴 C1 · Adapter reads nonexistent field 'modelId' — every PT prices at the $1/hr default AND both counted PT checks short-circuit, so PT analysis is structurally DEAD against real API responses  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/bedrock.py:138,142,148,180,183,189; CW dims 71,98,113`
- **Evidence:** Code line 138/180: model_id = pt.get("modelId", ""). Verified botocore shape ProvisionedModelSummary (.venv/.../botocore/data/bedrock/2023-04-20/service-2.json.gz) members: provisionedModelName, provisionedModelArn, modelArn, desiredModelArn, foundationModelArn, modelUnits, desiredModelUnits, status, commitmentDuration, commitmentExpirationTime, creationTime, lastModifiedTime — NO modelId (and NO provisionedModelId). So model_id is ALWAYS "". Effects: (a) PT_HOURLY_PRICE.get("",1.0) always returns the $1 default (lines 148,183); (b) _get_pt_invocation_sum/_get_pt_token_counts query Dimensions=[{Name:ModelId,Value:""}] (lines 71,98,113) -> no Datapoints -> return None; (c) _check_idle_pt returns at 144-145 (if invocations is None: return recs) and _check_pt_breakeven returns at 190-191 -> NEITHER counted source ever emits a finding.
- **Impact:** 100% coverage loss on the adapter's only two counted dollar sources: idle_provisioned_throughput and pt_breakeven_analysis can never fire against a live AWS response. The tab renders only the $0 KB advisory. Even absent the dimension issue, every PT would be mis-rated at a fabricated $1/hr.
- **Fix:** Derive the rate key from the real foundation model id parsed from pt['foundationModelArn'] (or pt['modelArn']); use pt['provisionedModelArn'] as the CloudWatch ModelId dimension value (see H4) and as the rec id (line 137/179 already falls back to provisionedModelArn). Add a unit test driving _check_idle_pt with a realistic ProvisionedModelSummary asserting a finding is produced.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified against the live botocore shape: .venv/.../botocore/data/bedrock/2023-04-20/service-2.json.gz ProvisionedModelSummary members are exactly [provisionedModelName, provisionedModelArn, modelArn, desiredModelArn, foundationModelArn, modelUnits, desiredModelUnits, status, commitmentDuration, commitmentExpirationTime, creationTime, lastModifiedTime] — NO modelId, NO provisionedModelId. The adapter reads raw botocore dicts (ctx.client('bedrock'), _list_provisioned_throughputs appends page['provisionedModelSummaries'] unmodified; no normalization), so pt.get('modelId','') at lines 138 and 180 is ALWAYS ''. Effects all hold at the cited lines: (a) PT_HOURLY_PRICE.get('', 1.0) returns the $1 default (148,183); (b) _get_pt_invocation_sum/_get_pt_token_counts query Dimensions=[{Name:ModelId,Value:''}] (71,98,113) which matches no metric -> empty Datapoints -> return None; (c) _check_idle_pt returns at 144-145 (invocations is None) and _check_pt_breakeven returns at 190-191 (input/output None). Neither idle_provisioned_throughput nor pt_breakeven_analysis can emit a finding against a real API response; only the $0 KB advisory renders. modelUnits/status/provisionedModelArn DO exist so pt_id/model_units survive, but the model identifier is dead. All cited line numbers are exact.

#### 🟠 H1 · PT_HOURLY_DEFAULT = 1.0 is fabricated and ~20-24x too low, and the unknown-rate PT is still COUNTED at that rate (no Counted=False demotion)  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/bedrock.py:25,148-150,183-184,199-200`
- **Evidence:** Line 25 PT_HOURLY_DEFAULT=1.0. Live AWS Pricing API (AmazonBedrock, us-west-2, sku AEZCD6F9ZS3UKADP): USW2-Llama3-1-70B-ProvisionedThroughput-NoCommit-ModelUnits = $24.00/hour. Idle/breakeven recs are counted purely on monthly_savings > 1.0 (lines 150,199) with no Counted flag, so a defaulted-rate PT is reported as a hard dollar at a fabricated $1/hr.
- **Impact:** When the rate defaults (the common path even after C1, due to H2), idle-PT waste is under-stated ~20-24x and breakeven pt_monthly is under-stated, suppressing real recs and/or emitting a fabricated counted dollar with no audit trail.
- **Fix:** Resolve the real model-unit hourly rate from the Pricing API by region+model+commitment term, or from the account's PT commitment. When unconfirmable, demote to a $0 advisory (Counted=False, like the KB path) instead of counting at $1/hr.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Line 25 PT_HOURLY_DEFAULT=1.0 is a hardcoded fabricated rate; it is the value actually applied whenever model_id is not a dict key (which after C1 is every PT, and after H2 still every PT). No Counted demotion exists: bedrock.py never imports services/_savings and never sets rec['Counted'] on idle-PT or breakeven recs; the reporter (_counted_advisory_counts, html_report_generator.py:380-388) treats every rec lacking Counted is False as COUNTED, and the adapter's total (line 358) sums monthly_savings unconditionally. Gating is purely monthly_waste>1.0 (150) / savings>1.0 (199). A single idle unit at the $1 default yields 1.0*1*730=$730/mo reported as a hard dollar with no audit trail, vs a real ~$24/hr NoCommit rate (~$17,520/mo) — i.e. ~24x understatement of true waste while still emitting a fabricated counted figure. Both impact directions in the finding hold. Note: like H2-H4 this is currently masked by C1 (idle path returns None before pricing), exactly as the finding states ('even after C1'); it is a genuine latent defect, not independently firing today.

#### 🟠 H2 · PT_HOURLY_PRICE keys are truncated and cannot match full model ids; the four Claude entries are unverifiable (no Claude PT SKU exists) and commitment term is ignored  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/bedrock.py:18-24,148,183`
- **Evidence:** Keys truncated: anthropic.claude-3-haiku / -3-sonnet / -3-5-sonnet / -3-opus / amazon.titan-text-lite (lines 19-23). A real foundation model id is the full string (e.g. anthropic.claude-3-haiku-20240307-v1:0), so even after C1 a .get() misses to the $1 default. Live Pricing API: ProvisionedThroughput-*-ModelUnits usagetypes exist ONLY for Titan/Nova/Llama; NO Claude PT ModelUnits usagetype (Claude only appears as ...-input-tokens). The four Claude PT rates (0.80/4.00/8.00/21.50) have no public SKU and are guesses. PT has distinct NoCommit/1-month/6-month SKUs; the adapter prices one hourly with no term, ignoring pt['commitmentDuration'].
- **Impact:** Even after the field fix, Claude PTs (most common) can't be priced from a real SKU and Titan/Nova/Llama PTs miss the truncated keys -> default $1/hr. The term-blind rate over/under-states by the NoCommit-vs-committed spread.
- **Fix:** Match on the full foundation model id (or a robust prefix map); source Titan/Nova/Llama PT ModelUnits rates from the Pricing API per pt['commitmentDuration']; for Claude PTs (no public PT SKU) read the actual commitment rate or emit advisory rather than a hardcoded guess.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Keys at lines 19-23 are truncated stems ('anthropic.claude-3-haiku', '-3-sonnet', '-3-5-sonnet', '-3-opus', 'amazon.titan-text-lite'). Lookups at 148/183 use dict.get(model_id, default) which is EXACT-match. A real Bedrock model identifier is never a bare stem: the API exposes only modelArn/foundationModelArn (botocore shape verified) whose values are full ARNs (arn:aws:bedrock:...::foundation-model/anthropic.claude-3-haiku-20240307-v1:0), and even a parsed bare id carries the -20240307-v1:0 suffix. So even after the C1 field fix, .get() always misses -> $1 default. Term-blindness confirmed: commitmentDuration is a real member of the shape but is never read anywhere in bedrock.py; a single hourly rate is applied with no NoCommit/1-month/6-month distinction (184). The supporting claim that the four Claude PT rates (0.80/4.00/8.00/21.50) correspond to no public Claude PT ModelUnits SKU (Claude priced per-token, not PT ModelUnits) is plausible but rests on the live Pricing API, not the repo; it does not change the verdict because the load-bearing defects (exact-match truncated keys + ignored commitment term) are proven in code.

#### 🟠 H3 · Breakeven on-demand estimate uses one flat $0.000003/token for input+output across all models — 12x too high for Haiku input and ignores that output bills ~5x input  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/bedrock.py:189-198`
- **Evidence:** Line 193: od_monthly_estimate = (input_tokens + output_tokens) * 0.000_003. Live Pricing API (us-east-1): USE1-Claude3Sonnet-input-tokens = $0.00300/1K (=0.000003/token, equals the constant for Sonnet INPUT only); USE1-Claude3Haiku-input-tokens = $0.00025/1K (=0.00000025/token, ~12x lower than the constant). Published Claude 3 Sonnet output ~$0.015/1K (5x input). _get_pt_token_counts already fetches InputTokenCount and OutputTokenCount separately, then they are collapsed to one rate.
- **Impact:** Breakeven od_monthly_estimate is wrong in both directions by model and input/output mix, so pt_breakeven_analysis counted savings is unreliable: can fabricate a 'switch to on-demand' saving (Haiku) or suppress a real one.
- **Fix:** Price input_tokens and output_tokens separately at the per-model ...-input-tokens / ...-output-tokens rates keyed off the resolved foundation model id, using the already-fetched counts.
