- **Verifier (confirmed):** Line 193 computes od_monthly_estimate = (input_tokens + output_tokens) * 0.000_003 — a single flat per-token rate applied to the summed input+output token counts, identical for every model. _get_pt_token_counts deliberately fetches InputTokenCount and OutputTokenCount as separate CloudWatch sums (lines 95-124) and they are then collapsed at 193, discarding both the per-model rate differences and the input-vs-output (~5x) spread. The structural defect (one model-agnostic, direction-agnostic rate) is fully proven in code. The exact magnitudes (0.000003/tok = $0.003/1K equals Sonnet INPUT only; ~12x too high for Haiku input; output ~5x input) depend on the live Pricing API and aren't repo-verifiable, but they only quantify a defect whose existence is certain from the code. Like H1/H4, currently unreachable due to C1 (breakeven returns None at 190-191), consistent with the finding's framing.

#### 🟠 H4 · CloudWatch dimension ModelId=<base model id> is wrong for a Provisioned Throughput — it measures on-demand traffic of the base model, not the PT  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/bedrock.py:71,98,113,142,189`
- **Evidence:** Both metric helpers pass Dimensions=[{Name:ModelId,Value:model_id}] where model_id is meant to be the base/foundation model id (lines 71,98,113). AWS/Bedrock PT metrics are emitted under the provisioned-model identifier (PT ARN), not the shared base model id. Querying the base id either aggregates unrelated on-demand traffic (busy on-demand model masks an idle PT -> false negative) or returns nothing (false 'idle'). Currently compounded by C1 (value is ""); resurfaces once the field name is fixed.
- **Impact:** Idle-PT detection is unsound: real idle PTs hidden by sibling on-demand usage, or active PTs flagged idle — corrupting the only idle-delete dollar signal.
- **Fix:** Query with Dimensions=[{Name:ModelId,Value: pt['provisionedModelArn']}] (PT-scoped); confirm the exact PT metric dimension via AWS docs before counting.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Lines 71/98/113 pass Dimensions=[{Name:ModelId,Value:model_id}] and model_id is unmistakably intended as the base/foundation model id (it is also used as the PT_HOURLY_PRICE key, which is keyed by foundation ids), not the provisioned-model ARN. AWS docs (docs.aws.amazon.com/bedrock/latest/userguide/monitoring-runtime-metrics) confirm the AWS/Bedrock runtime metrics Invocations/InputTokenCount/OutputTokenCount expose only the ModelId dimension, valued by the modelId used in the request; PT traffic is invoked with the provisioned-model ARN, so PT metrics are recorded under the PT ARN, not the shared base foundation-model id. Therefore querying the base id is the wrong identifier for a PT: a base model that also serves on-demand traffic returns nonzero Invocations and suppresses a truly-idle-PT finding (false negative) — the primary failure mode. Correct dimension would be provisionedModelArn. Confirmed at the code level and grounded in AWS docs; currently compounded by C1 (value=''), resurfacing once the field is fixed, exactly as stated. Minor caveat: the secondary 'returns nothing -> false idle' sub-case does not match THIS code (None -> early return at 144-145 emits no rec), but the core wrong-identifier defect stands.

#### 🟡 M1 · Every failure path swallows the exception and returns empty/None — AccessDenied/throttling is indistinguishable from 'no resources'/'idle'; nothing recorded on ctx  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/bedrock.py:50-55,80-81,107-108,122-123,232-233,247-248,277-278,292-293,348-352`
- **Evidence:** _list_provisioned_throughputs: paginator except -> list_* except Exception: pass -> returns [] (50-55): bedrock:ListProvisionedModelThroughputs AccessDenied silently vanishes the PT analysis. _get_pt_invocation_sum/_get_pt_token_counts: except: pass -> None (80-81,107-108,122-123): a GetMetricStatistics denial/throttle reads as 'no data' -> PT treated as idle-without-metrics. _check_idle_knowledge_bases/_check_idle_agents: client + list except -> return recs/[] (232-233,247-248,277-278,292-293): bedrock-agent permission gap drops the KB advisory silently. scan per-PT loop: except Exception: continue (348-352): malformed PT silently dropped. ctx exposes warn() and permission_issue() (core/scan_context.py 49-68) but neither is called in this adapter.
- **Impact:** Silent under-reporting: a permission/throttle gap produces an empty or KB-only Bedrock tab with zero operator signal, indistinguishable from a genuinely clean account.
- **Fix:** Classify each except: AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation/AccessDeniedException -> ctx.permission_issue(..., service='bedrock', action=<api>); else ctx.warn. Distinguish 'no metrics' (idle) from 'couldn't read metrics' (permission/throttle) before deciding idle.

#### 🟡 M2 · Counted PT findings carry no structured AuditBasis (rate / region / commitment-term / metric-window / formula)  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/bedrock.py:151-164,200-212`
- **Evidence:** Both counted recs emit only free-text current_value/recommended_value/reason and a monthly_savings number; no machine-readable basis (rate source, region multiplier, commitment term, 30-day window, formula). Sibling Lambda/RDS adapters attach a structured AuditBasis per counted finding (per the brief and CLAUDE.md).
- **Impact:** The dollar figure is not defensible from the report alone — a reviewer cannot tell the rate used, whether it was the $1 default, or the metric window.
- **Fix:** Attach an AuditBasis dict (rate, rate_source, region_multiplier, commitment_term, metric_window_days, formula) to each counted idle/breakeven rec, mirroring lambda_svc.py.

#### 🟢 L1 · snake_case rec keys vs PascalCase generic renderer — card header degrades to '<source>: Resource' and monthly_savings is dumped as a plain key (money total still correct)  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `reporter_phase_b.py:1812-1876 (id resolution 1845-1847; key dump 1865-1869)`
- **Evidence:** _render_generic_other_rec resolves id from PascalCase ProvisionedModelId/KnowledgeBaseId/AgentId (1845-1847) and category from CheckCategory (1814), but Bedrock recs use snake_case provisioned_model_id/knowledge_base_id/check_category/monthly_savings. resource_id falls to 'Resource' (no resourceArn) and check_category falls to source_name.title(); every snake_case key is dumped as a generic <p> (1865-1869) — monthly_savings shows as plain 'Monthly Savings: 123.45' (no $, not the .savings class). KB monthly_savings=0.0 is falsy so skipped by 'and value', but pricing_warning/reason render. Counted total unaffected (adapter self-sums; html_report_generator._calculate_service_savings returns total_monthly_savings directly when >0).
- **Impact:** Presentation desync only — PT cards titled 'Idle Provisioned Throughput: Resource' with the id buried in the body and the saving unstyled. No money desync.
- **Fix:** Add a ('bedrock', <source>) handler in PHASE_B_HANDLERS, or normalize rec keys (provisioned_model_id->ProvisionedModelId, check_category->CheckCategory, expose EstimatedSavings) so the renderer resolves id/category/savings.

#### 🟢 L2 · Module-declared stat_cards (StatCardSpec) are never rendered; the hardcoded html descriptor uses different cards and the two disagree  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/bedrock.py:315-319 (vs html_report_generator.py 156-162)`
- **Evidence:** BedrockModule.stat_cards declares 'Provisioned Throughputs' (extras.pt_count), 'Idle PTs' (sources.idle_provisioned_throughput.count), 'Monthly Savings' (total_monthly_savings). But _get_service_stats (html_report_generator.py ~3232-3248) renders from _SERVICE_STATS_CONFIG['bedrock']['multi_source_cards'] (156-162): 'Provisioned Throughputs'/'Knowledge Bases'/'Agents' (extras.pt_count/kb_count/agent_count). The module StatCardSpec tuple is not consumed for the tab, so 'Idle PTs' and 'Monthly Savings' never appear.
- **Impact:** Cosmetic/maintenance: the two card definitions diverge; the module's intent (surface idle-PT count and savings) is silently dropped. Rendered cards (pt/kb/agent counts) still reconcile with extras.
- **Fix:** Reconcile: drive stat cards from the module StatCardSpec, or update module stat_cards to match the descriptor, and document which is authoritative.

#### 🟢 L3 · services/adapters/CLAUDE.md has no bedrock row — undocumented module-constant adapter  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/CLAUDE.md:12-33 (Live-Pricing table), 34-48`
- **Evidence:** The Pricing-Models tables list 19 live-pricing + 5 parse-rate + 1 flat-rate adapters; bedrock appears in none. It is module-constant (PT_HOURLY_PRICE + flat token rate), consumes no CoH/CO, reads CloudWatch, renders 4 sources via generic per-rec — none captured.
- **Impact:** Doc/code drift: a reader cannot find Bedrock's pricing strategy or its CloudWatch/no-CoH-CO posture in the adapter index.
- **Fix:** Add a bedrock row (module-constant section): 'PT_HOURLY_PRICE dict + PT_HOURLY_DEFAULT + flat 0.000003/token; no CoH/CO; CloudWatch-gated (requires_cloudwatch/reads_fast_mode); 4 sources rendered via generic per-rec.'

#### 🟢 L4 · Near-idle PTs and committed-term lock-in escape the checks; 'switch to on-demand' may be unactionable mid-commitment  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/bedrock.py:147-150,186-207`
- **Evidence:** The idle gate fires only on exactly invocations==0 over 30 days (line 147); a PT with 1 invocation in 30 days still bills full model-unit hours but is not flagged, and breakeven only partially catches it (and only when token metrics exist — currently never, per C1). The breakeven rec recommends 'Switch to on-demand pricing' (line 207) but ignores pt['commitmentDuration']/pt['commitmentExpirationTime'] — a 1-month/6-month committed PT cannot be switched off mid-term without penalty, so the saving may be unrealizable until expiry.
- **Impact:** Coverage gap (under-utilized PT escapes both checks) plus a potentially unactionable recommendation for committed PTs; reduces trust but does not fabricate a counted dollar beyond H1/H3.
- **Fix:** Add a low-utilization threshold (not just ==0) for idle/right-size, and gate or annotate the breakeven 'switch to on-demand' rec by commitmentDuration/commitmentExpirationTime so it is advisory until the commitment expires.

---

### CloudFront — `services/adapters/cloudfront.py`

**Module identity:** key="cloudfront", cli_aliases=("cloudfront",), display_name="CloudFront", required_clients()=("cloudfront",) — a global service routed through the global-client path (services/adapters/cloudfront.py:15-21). It consults ONE helper, services/cloudfront.py:get_enhanced_cloudfront_checks, and emits a single "enhanced_checks" SourceBlock. It consumes NEITHER Cost Optimization Hub (absent from core/scan_orchestrator.py _HUB_SERVICES set lines 52-74 and from type_map lines 86-96) NOR Compute Optimizer — so "missing CoH/CO" is correctly out of scope. Pricing strategy is effectively "honest $0 advisory": scan() forces EstimatedMonthlySavings=0.0 on every rec and attaches a PricingWarning; total_monthly_savings is hard 0.0. It does NOT override requires_cloudwatch/reads_fast_mode (both inherit False from services/_base.py:24-25) despite the helper issuing AWS/CloudFront CloudWatch reads. Rendering is Phase A: cloudfront ∈ _PHASE_A_SERVICES (reporter_phase_b.py:2500-2514) with PHASE_A_DESCRIPTORS["cloudfront"] (savings_mode="always") rendered by render_grouped_by_category; there is intentionally no PHASE_B_HANDLERS entry.

**Verdict:** Cost-fidelity is honest but lossy. CloudFront emits zero counted dollars: scan() forces EstimatedMonthlySavings=0.0 + PricingWarning on every rec, total_monthly_savings is hard 0.0, and cloudfront is absent from both the CoH type_map and every _calculate_service_savings fabrication set (_SAVINGS_KEYWORDS/_FLAT_SAVINGS_SERVICES/_DEFAULT_SAVINGS at html_report_generator.py:60-82), so its grand-total contribution is genuinely $0 — no fabricated, double-counted, or mis-rated dollars. The deliberate $0-advisory stance is a defensible tradeoff, not a bug. The real defects are: (H1) two `except Exception: pass` blocks that silently drop the only live recommendation on any CloudWatch permission/throttle failure; (H2) un-gated CloudWatch + get_distribution_config reads with reads_fast_mode/requires_cloudwatch never declared, so --fast cannot skip them; (M1) the Phase A card renders the leftover '20-50%' EstimatedSavings string while never rendering the PricingWarning caveat, desyncing card from the $0 headline; (M2) doc/docstrings claim a non-existent $25/rec flat rate; and (M3) dead code (discarded origin-shield CW math, two empty buckets, a dead adapter branch) that wastes API calls. Fix order: H1, H2, M1, M2, M3, then L1-L3.

**Pricing validation:** Validated LIVE via AWS Pricing MCP (service_code='AmazonCloudFront', region omitted — global). US 'CloudFront Outbound' DataTransfer-Out-Bytes tiers (SKU GV2WFGX37Q9PDSHF, effective 2025-04-01): first 10 TB = $0.085/GB, next 40 TB = $0.080/GB, then $0.060 / $0.040 / $0.030 / $0.025 / $0.020 across higher tiers. This exactly matches the adapter's own comment (cloudfront.py:42-44: '$0.085/GB US/EU first 10TB, $0.080 next 40TB'). The Asia tier-1 rate (~$0.120/GB cited in the same comment) was NOT separately validated this run — needs live Pricing-API validation if a quantified PriceClass-delta saving is re-enabled. No rate is counted in production today (every finding is $0), so nothing is currently mis-rated; the validated tiers are provided as grounding for a future BytesDownloaded × tiered-rate quantification.

**Cost checks:**

| Check | Status | Trigger | Savings basis |
|---|---|---|---|
| price_class_optimization (CheckCategory='CloudFront Price Class Optimization') | advisory | PriceClass=='PriceClass_All' AND Enabled AND total Requests over trailing 7 days > 1000 (AWS/CloudFront 'Requests' Sum, Period=86400) | Helper sets EstimatedSavings='20-50% on data transfer costs for regional traffic' (percentage string, no $). Adapter (cloudfront.py:60-64) overwrites EstimatedMonthlySavings=0.0 and adds PricingWarning. No rate/constant; would-be basis is (current PriceClass blended DTO rate − target blended rate) × measured BytesDownloaded GB — not implemented. Live AWS Pricing API US DTO-out: first 10TB $0.085/GB, next 40TB $0.080/GB (validated). |
| CloudFront Unused Distribution (adapter branch, scan() line 56) | advisory | rec['CheckCategory']=='CloudFront Unused Distribution' — but get_enhanced_cloudfront_checks NEVER emits this category, so the branch never fires (dead branch) | Sets EstimatedMonthlySavings=0.0 unconditionally; dead code, $0 |
| low_traffic_distributions (helper key) | advisory | Initialized as [] at services/cloudfront.py:31 and NEVER appended to (disabled-distribution finding removed, comment lines 83-84) | Never produces a rec; empty list returned via **checks at line 143 |
| origin_shield_unnecessary (helper key) | advisory | Initialized as [] at services/cloudfront.py:32 and NEVER appended to; CacheHitRate + Requests CW math is fully computed (lines 90-126) then discarded via `_ = (should_check_origin_shield, origins)` at line 132 | Never produces a rec; computed evidence thrown away (wasted get_distribution_config + up to 2 CW reads per distribution) |

**Findings:**

#### 🟠 H1 · Swallowed CloudWatch exceptions silently drop the only live recommendation (no ctx.warn/permission_issue)  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/cloudfront.py:80-81, 127-128`
- **Evidence:** Price-class read: `request_metrics = cloudwatch.get_metric_statistics(Namespace='AWS/CloudFront', MetricName='Requests', ...)` wrapped by `except Exception:\n    pass` (lines 80-81). Origin-shield reads (CacheHitRate/Requests) wrapped by a second `except Exception:\n    pass` (lines 127-128). Neither calls ctx.warn or ctx.permission_issue.
- **Impact:** The only populated category (price_class_optimization) depends entirely on the Requests CW read at lines 52-60. An AccessDenied/Unauthorized or throttling failure on that read is swallowed → the distribution is silently dropped with zero recommendations and zero operator signal. Permission/throttle gaps masquerade as 'no opportunities'. This is the canonical silent-failure class.
- **Fix:** Replace both `except Exception: pass` blocks with classification: on botocore ClientError with code in {AccessDenied, AccessDeniedException, UnauthorizedOperation} call ctx.permission_issue(...); on Throttling/RequestLimitExceeded/other call ctx.warn(...). Mirror services/_aws_errors.record_aws_error used by the network adapter.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified exactly at services/cloudfront.py:80-81 (`except Exception:` / `pass`) wrapping the price-class `Requests` get_metric_statistics read at lines 52-60, and a second `except Exception:`/`pass` at 127-128 wrapping the origin-shield CacheHitRate/Requests reads (96-126). Neither calls ctx.warn or ctx.permission_issue. The claim that price_class_optimization is the only populated category holds: it is the ONLY list ever appended to (line 65); `low_traffic_distributions` and `origin_shield_unnecessary` are declared (lines 30-32) but never populated, and the origin-shield finding was explicitly removed (lines 130-132, `_ = (should_check_origin_shield, origins)`). The outer ctx.warn at line 137 only catches list_distributions/client-creation failures; a per-distribution cloudwatch AccessDenied/Unauthorized/throttle is caught by the inner `pass` at 80-81 BEFORE it can reach line 137, so the distribution is silently dropped with zero recs and zero operator signal. An account-wide cloudwatch:GetMetricStatistics denial would empty the entire category while the CloudFront tab reports 'no opportunities'. Mechanism, lines, and impact all match.

#### 🟠 H2 · Un-gated CloudWatch reads; reads_fast_mode/requires_cloudwatch not declared so --fast does not skip CW  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✏️ revised**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/cloudfront.py (declaration) + services/cloudfront.py (reads):cloudfront.py:12-21 (no override); services/cloudfront.py:46-126`
- **Evidence:** Adapter declares neither requires_cloudwatch nor reads_fast_mode, so both inherit False from services/_base.py:24-25 (contrast lambda_svc.py:58-61 which sets both True). The helper issues `cloudwatch.get_metric_statistics(... 'Requests' ...)` (lines 52-60), `... 'CacheHitRate' ...` (lines 96-104) and `... 'Requests' ...` (lines 113-121) plus `cloudfront.get_distribution_config(Id=dist_id)` (line 87) per distribution, with no `if ctx.fast_mode` guard anywhere (grep of services/cloudfront.py shows no fast_mode reference).
- **Impact:** Up to 1 describe + 3 CW GetMetricStatistics calls PER distribution run unconditionally; `--fast` cannot skip them. On accounts with many distributions this is slow and raises throttling risk, which (via H1) silently drops recs. Also misreports capability metadata (requires_cloudwatch=False).
- **Fix:** Set reads_fast_mode=True and requires_cloudwatch=True on CloudfrontModule, and in get_enhanced_cloudfront_checks bail out of the CW reads (and skip get_distribution_config) when getattr(ctx,'fast_mode',False) is True, mirroring the Lambda/network fast-mode short-circuit.
- **Verifier (revised):** The observable facts are real and verified: CloudfrontModule (services/adapters/cloudfront.py:12-21) overrides neither requires_cloudwatch nor reads_fast_mode, so both inherit False from services/_base.py:24-25; grep of services/cloudfront.py finds NO fast_mode reference, so the CW reads run regardless of --fast; per distribution it issues up to 1 get_distribution_config (line 87) + 3 GetMetricStatistics (Requests 52-60, CacheHitRate 96-104, Requests 113-121), and the describe + CacheHitRate run for every distribution. BUT the finding's stated mechanism/causation is wrong and must be corrected.  _Correction:_ The CW reads being un-skippable by --fast is NOT caused by the missing flag declarations. requires_cloudwatch/reads_fast_mode are dead metadata at runtime: scan_orchestrator.py:22-23 (safe_scan) simply calls module.scan(ctx) and never reads either flag; an attribute-access grep across the repo finds the flags consumed ONLY by tests (tests/test_s3_adapter.py:177-181, tests/test_containers_adapter.py:385), never by the orchestrator/runner/reporting. Therefore declaring reads_fast_mode=True would NOT by itself make --fast skip CloudFront's CW reads. The lambda contrast is misleading: lambda_svc skips CW via in-adapter `if not fast_mode` checks (services/lambda_svc.py:128,160,220,247), not because reads_fast_mode=True. So there are TWO independent real defects, not the single causal chain claimed: (1) services/cloudfront.py lacks any `if ctx.fast_mode` guard (the actual reason --fast cannot skip the up-to-3 CW reads + 1 describe per distribution, the genuine perf/throttling concern), and (2) the capability metadata is misreported (requires_cloudwatch=False despite the helper using CloudWatch) — but this is cosmetic since nothing consumes it. Severity is better characterized as MEDIUM: the un-gated reads are a performance/throttling cost whose correctness impact (silent rec drop) only materializes via H1, not a standalone HIGH correctness bug.

#### 🟡 M1 · Card renders leftover '20-50%' EstimatedSavings string while total is $0; PricingWarning caveat never rendered  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `reporter_phase_a.py + services/cloudfront.py + services/adapters/cloudfront.py:reporter_phase_a.py:450-451; services/cloudfront.py:76; services/adapters/cloudfront.py:60-64`
- **Evidence:** Helper sets `'EstimatedSavings': '20-50% on data transfer costs for regional traffic'` (services/cloudfront.py:76); the adapter overwrites EstimatedMonthlySavings=0.0 and adds PricingWarning (cloudfront.py:60-64) but never clears EstimatedSavings. Phase A render with savings_mode='always' prints it verbatim: `content += f'<p class="savings"><strong>Estimated Savings:</strong> {resources[0].get("EstimatedSavings", "Cost optimization")}</p>'` (reporter_phase_a.py:451). render_grouped_by_category renders only CheckCategory, Recommendation, EstimatedSavings and the resource list — it never renders PricingWarning.
- **Impact:** The tab headline reports $0/advisory but each card claims 'Estimated Savings: 20-50% on data transfer costs for regional traffic' — a savings claim with no dollar figure and no caveat. The one honest-basis string the adapter attaches (PricingWarning) is invisible. Headline vs card desync; overstates confidence in an unquantified rec.
- **Fix:** Either drop the EstimatedSavings percentage string in the adapter (set rec['EstimatedSavings']='' or to the PricingWarning text) so savings_mode='always' renders the honest caveat, or have the Phase A renderer emit PricingWarning when EstimatedMonthlySavings==0. Reject any non-dollar EstimatedSavings string from the savings line.

#### 🟡 M2 · Doc/code mismatch: CLAUDE.md and adapter docstrings claim flat/parse-rate $25/rec; adapter emits $0  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/CLAUDE.md + services/adapters/cloudfront.py:CLAUDE.md Parse-rate table row 'cloudfront.py | Fixed $25/rec'; cloudfront.py:1,13,27`
- **Evidence:** services/adapters/CLAUDE.md lists cloudfront under Parse-rate as 'Fixed $25/rec'. The code never parses a rate and never uses $25: scan() forces `rec['EstimatedMonthlySavings'] = 0.0` (lines 58,60) + PricingWarning and `total_monthly_savings = savings` where savings stays 0.0 (lines 49,67). Adapter module docstring says 'Flat-rate adapter for CloudFront' (line 1) and class docstring 'Flat-rate savings strategy' (line 13); scan docstring says 'Traffic-based savings' (line 27) — all false.
- **Impact:** Anyone trusting the docs believes CloudFront contributes counted $25/rec to the grand total; in reality it contributes $0. Misleads audit/triage; the 'Fixed $25/rec' row is stale.
- **Fix:** Update the CLAUDE.md row to '$0 honest advisory (needs CW BytesDownloaded + PriceClass)' and correct the adapter docstrings to describe the $0-advisory stance, not flat/traffic-based savings.

#### 🟡 M3 · Dead code burns API calls: origin-shield CW math computed then discarded; two empty check buckets; dead adapter branch  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/cloudfront.py + services/adapters/cloudfront.py:services/cloudfront.py:31-32,86-132; cloudfront.py:56-59`
- **Evidence:** checks['low_traffic_distributions'] and checks['origin_shield_unnecessary'] are initialized (lines 31-32) and never appended to. The origin-shield block computes should_check_origin_shield via CacheHitRate (lines 96-110) and a fallback Requests read (lines 113-126) then discards everything: `_ = (should_check_origin_shield, origins)` (line 132). get_distribution_config (line 87) is also only used to feed that discarded math. In the adapter, `if rec.get('CheckCategory') == 'CloudFront Unused Distribution':` (line 56) matches a category the helper never emits.
- **Impact:** No dollar impact, but each distribution pays for 1 get_distribution_config + up to 2 CW GetMetricStatistics whose results are thrown away — wasted cost/latency and throttling pressure that compounds H1's silent drops. Maintenance hazard (dead branches imply a feature that doesn't exist).
- **Fix:** Remove the origin-shield CW computation and get_distribution_config call (or actually emit a quantified finding), delete the unused low_traffic_distributions/origin_shield_unnecessary buckets, and remove the dead 'CloudFront Unused Distribution' branch in scan().

#### 🟢 L1 · Card omits current PriceClass: extractor reads 'PriceClass' but rec key is 'CurrentPriceClass'  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `reporter_phase_a.py + services/cloudfront.py:reporter_phase_a.py:136,143-144; services/cloudfront.py:70`
- **Evidence:** Helper emits `'CurrentPriceClass': price_class` (services/cloudfront.py:70). The extractor reads `price_class = rec.get('PriceClass', '')` (reporter_phase_a.py:136) and only appends 'Price Class: ...' if truthy (lines 143-144). The keys never match, so price_class is always '' and the line never renders.
- **Impact:** The distribution's current PriceClass — the entire premise of the price-class recommendation — never appears on the card, leaving the operator without the basis to act. No dollar impact.
- **Fix:** In _extract_cloudfront_details read rec.get('CurrentPriceClass') (with 'PriceClass' as fallback).

#### 🟢 L2 · Source badge 'Metric Backed' overstates confidence for a $0 config-pattern rec  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `reporter_phase_b.py:2366-2367, 2377-2379`
- **Evidence:** No (cloudfront, enhanced_checks) override exists in SOURCE_TYPE_MAP (only s3 and network entries, e.g. ('s3','enhanced_checks'):'Audit Based' at line 2367), so source_type_badge/source_type_label fall through to `_GENERIC_SOURCE_TYPES['enhanced_checks'] = 'Metric Backed'` (line 2378).
- **Impact:** Cards carry a green 'Metric Backed' badge though the rec is a $0, unquantified config-pattern nudge gated only on a request-count threshold. Overstates confidence relative to the honest-$0 stance.
- **Fix:** Add ('cloudfront','enhanced_checks') -> 'Audit Based' to SOURCE_TYPE_MAP, matching the S3 precedent.

#### 🟢 L3 · Coverage gated to PriceClass_All + >1000 req/week + Enabled only  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/cloudfront.py:46, 64`
- **Evidence:** `if price_class == 'PriceClass_All' and enabled:` (line 46) and `if total_requests > 1000:` (line 64). A PriceClass_200 distribution that could drop to PriceClass_100, and low-but-nonzero-traffic distributions, are never considered; disabled distributions are excluded.
- **Impact:** Real (future) savings on PriceClass_200->100 downgrades and sub-1000-req/week distributions are never surfaced. No false dollars today (all $0), so this is a coverage tradeoff, not a counted-dollar bug.
- **Fix:** When quantification is re-enabled, extend the gate to PriceClass_200 (target PriceClass_100) and lower/justify the request threshold; document the disabled-distribution exclusion.

---

### Commitment Analysis — `services/adapters/commitment_analysis.py`

**Module identity:** MATCH with minor doc drift. key="commitment_analysis"; cli_aliases=("commitment_analysis","commitments","savings_plans","ri"); display_name="Commitment Analysis"; required_clients()=("ce","savingsplans") (commitment_analysis.py:72-93); requires_cloudwatch=False (line 89). It has NO PricingEngine method and NO module $/unit constant — dollars come from Cost Explorer / Cost Optimization Hub / live SavingsPlans offering rates. services/adapters/CLAUDE.md correctly omits it from all three pricing tables (Live/Parse-rate/Flat-rate) and documents the CoH-via-ctx.cost_hub_splits + reservation/SP→commitment_analysis routing in its top note — consistent with reality. NO ctx.pricing_multiplier / ctx.pricing_engine is used anywhere in the adapter or services/commitment_logic.py (the only "pricing_multiplier" hit is a stale Args docstring line at 314 for a parameter the method does not take). DRIFT: the class/module docstring (lines 6-16, 69) claims "~7 calls per scan (~$0.07/scan)", but the adapter actually issues ~20 CE calls/scan (util 1 + util_details 2 [sp_util + expiry] + coverage 1 + reservation_util 1 + reservation_coverage 1 + SP purchase matrix 6 + RI purchase matrix 6 + account_coverage_ratio 1 + Fargate get_cost_and_usage 1) ≈ $0.20, plus 3 free SavingsPlans offering-rate calls. CLAUDE.md has no commitment_analysis cross-reference entry to update beyond the existing top note.

**Verdict:** commitment_analysis is a composite, strictly-advisory-aware adapter and its single most important invariant HOLDS: the buy-vs-rightsize advisory boundary is correctly enforced. In scan() (commitment_analysis.py:136-142), sp_coverage_gaps + ri_coverage_gaps + cost_hub_recs are forced Counted=False; purchase_recommendations and Fargate cells are built Counted=False at source (lines 557, 640, 710); Fargate recs carry monthly_savings=0.0 and are excluded from all_recs entirely. total_monthly_savings therefore sums ONLY sp_utilization + ri_utilization (expiry is $0), so NO projected/buy/coverage dollar leaks into the headline, and the executive summary's _calculate_service_savings returns that counted total for this service (commitment_analysis not in any keyword/flat savings set). No pricing_multiplier is used (correct - CE/CoH/live rates are region-correct), and the six non-handler sources render via the generic fallback rather than going blank. No CRITICAL was found. The material issues are presentation/observability, not headline-dollar correctness: H1 (HIGH) - sp_coverage_gaps and purchase_recommendations render their advisory monthly_savings through _render_generic_other_rec with NO 'not counted' disclaimer (unlike the Fargate handler), so projected dollars read as realized per-card. M1 - total_recommendations omits Fargate recs while the '(counted, advisory)' header counts them, so the header self-contradicts. M2 - _account_coverage_ratio's bare except swallows AccessDenied/throttle with no ctx.warn (the lone deviation from the otherwise-canonical _route_ce_error routing). M3 - the two counted findings use formally-inconsistent waste bases (sp x730, ri none) and carry no structured AuditBasis (numbers are correct but undefendable from the report alone). Lower-severity: missing-CE-client silent empty (L1), unlabeled 0.30 flat SP-discount factor (L2), stat_cards/html-descriptor divergence (L3), 3x-understated CE API-cost docstring (L4). Limitations (likely intentional): cross-tab RI shown as two advisory cards (L5) and the coverage-breadth gaps - empty RI coverage, SP-only expiry, COMPUTE_SP/EC2-only purchase matrix, ECS-only Fargate legs (L6). Fix order: H1, M1, M2, M3, then L1-L4; L5/L6 are documentation/tradeoff decisions.

**Pricing validation:** Best-effort live validation attempted. The only hardcoded dollar factor in the adapter is AVG_SP_DISCOUNT_RATE = 0.30 (commitment_analysis.py:76), used ONLY for the advisory sp_coverage_gaps potential. It cannot be validated via the AWS Pricing API: get_pricing_service_codes(filter='SavingsPlans|Compute|Fargate|ECS') returns only ['AWSComputeOptimizer','AmazonECS'] - there is no Savings Plans service code; SP discount rates live in the SavingsPlans offering-rates API (which the Fargate path already calls live, region-filtered). A flat 30% Compute-SP discount is a defensible CONSERVATIVE typical figure (AWS markets Compute SP discounts up to ~66% for 3yr All-Upfront; blended realized discounts commonly land ~20-40%), but it is an estimate applied as a reduction factor and is rendered without an 'estimate/advisory' label (see H1, L2). The two COUNTED figures (sp_utilization, ri_utilization) derive from Cost Explorer amortized data (AWS-computed, region-correct) - there is no static rate to validate, and correctly NO pricing_multiplier is applied. Purchase recs (CE EstimatedMonthlySavings), CoH recs (flat float), and Fargate cell discounts (live offering rate vs CE on-demand) are all data-driven, not memory constants. Net: no fabricated/region-wrong hardcoded rate reaches the headline.

**Cost checks:**

| Check | Status | Trigger | Savings basis |
|---|---|---|---|
| sp_utilization | counted | per-SP UtilizationPercentage < 0.95 from ce.get_savings_plans_utilization_details (paginated) | waste = AmortizedCommitment.TotalHourlyCommitment x (1 - rate) x 730 (monthly unused commitment); commitment_analysis.py:226-240 |
| ri_utilization | counted | per-SUBSCRIPTION_ID UtilizationPercentage < 0.95 from ce.get_reservation_utilization (paginated) | waste = Utilization.TotalAmortizedCost x (1 - rate); NO x730 (the 30-day tp amortized cost is already monthly); commitment_analysis.py:340-354 |
| expiring_commitments | counted | SP EndDateTime within 90 days, re-reads ce.get_savings_plans_utilization_details; SP-only (no RI expiry) | monthly_savings = 0.0 (alert only); commitment_analysis.py:436 |
| sp_coverage_gaps | advisory | per-SERVICE SP coverage < 0.80 from ce.get_savings_plans_coverage (paginated) | potential = OnDemandCost x (1 - rate) x AVG_SP_DISCOUNT_RATE(0.30) flat factor; forced Counted=False in scan() line 136-137; commitment_analysis.py:282 |
| ri_coverage_gaps | advisory | NONE - method takes overall ce.get_reservation_coverage rate for the stat card only and returns recs=[] (no groupBy); commitment_analysis.py:368-393 | n/a (always empty) |
| purchase_recommendations | advisory | CE (term x payment) matrix: SP via get_savings_plans_purchase_recommendation (COMPUTE_SP only, 2x3); RI via get_reservation_purchase_recommendation (EC2 only, 2x3); dropped when savings<=0 | SP: summary.EstimatedMonthlySavingsAmount; RI: sum(EstimatedMonthlySavings); built Counted=False at source (lines 557, 640) |
| cost_optimization_hub | advisory | ctx.cost_hub_splits['commitment_analysis'] populated by scan_orchestrator type_map (*ReservedInstances / *SavingsPlans -> commitment_analysis) | CoH estimatedMonthlySavings (flat float); forced Counted=False in scan() line 136-137 |
| fargate_savings_plan | advisory | SP-eligible Fargate on-demand spend > 0 (ce.get_cost_and_usage, ECS service + region); priced from live describe_savings_plans_offering_rates | recommended_saving = (eligible_od - sp_cost_full) x (rightsized_od/eligible_od) x coverage_ratio; rec monthly_savings forced 0.0 + Counted=False (commitment_analysis.py:709-710); NOT in all_recs nor total_recommendations |

**Findings:**

#### 🟠 H1 · Advisory dollars (sp_coverage_gaps, purchase_recommendations) render as plain savings with no 'not counted' disclaimer  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `reporter_phase_b.py:1812-1876 (renderer); 1381 (dispatch); commitment_analysis.py:282,555,638 (advisory $)`
- **Evidence:** commitment_analysis is NOT in _PHASE_B_SKIP_PER_REC (reporter_phase_b.py:2516-2530), so sp_coverage_gaps and purchase_recommendations fall through render_generic_per_rec -> _render_generic_other_rec. That renderer prints EVERY scalar field: `for key,value in rec.items(): ... content += f"<p><strong>{formatted_key}:</strong> {value}</p>"` (lines 1865-1869), emitting 'Monthly Savings: 123.45' plus a `reason` that reads '$X/mo (Y% off)... upfront $Z'. Counted=False is a bool (falsy) so it is never printed, and no advisory note is added. Contrast the dedicated _render_fargate_savings_plan which DOES print 'Advisory - ... not added to the tab total' (reporter_phase_b.py:2243-2246).
- **Impact:** Projected/advisory buy-and-coverage dollars (mutually-exclusive with per-service rightsizing levers, and AWS-projected not realized) read as realized savings on each card. The headline total is unaffected (these are excluded from total_monthly_savings), but a human adding the visible per-card dollars over-counts. The tab header's '(X counted, Y advisory)' line only partially mitigates and is itself inconsistent (see M1).
- **Fix:** Give sp_coverage_gaps and purchase_recommendations dedicated handlers in PHASE_B_HANDLERS, or have _render_generic_other_rec append the same 'Advisory - not added to the tab total' muted note whenever rec.get('Counted') is False (and/or suppress the raw monthly_savings field for advisory recs).
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified end-to-end in real code. (1) reporter_phase_b.py:2516-2530 defines _PHASE_B_SKIP_PER_REC and commitment_analysis is NOT a member. (2) commitment_analysis is not a PHASE_A_DESCRIPTORS key (reporter_phase_a.py keys: lambda/cloudfront/lightsail/dms/glue/api_gateway/step_functions/auto_scaling/backup/route53), so html_report_generator.py:3312 does not short-circuit it; it enters the source loop at 3317. (3) PHASE_B_HANDLERS (reporter_phase_b.py:2436-2498) registers only ('commitment_analysis','cost_optimization_hub') and ('commitment_analysis','fargate_savings_plan'); sp_coverage_gaps and purchase_recommendations have NO handler, so should_use_handler is False (3337) and should_fallback_to_per_rec returns True since commitment_analysis is not skip-listed (2548-2550), routing to render_generic_per_rec (3362) -> else branch (1381) -> _render_generic_other_rec. (4) _RECOMMENDATION_FILTERS (html_report_generator.py:453-455) holds only 'ec2', so advisory recs are not stripped. (5) The renderer loop at reporter_phase_b.py:1865-1869 prints each truthy scalar as a plain <p>, so 'Monthly Savings: <float>' and 'Reason: ...' render with no 'savings' class and no advisory disclaimer. (6) Counted=False is correctly never printed: bool is an int subclass so isinstance passes, but 'and value' is falsy and skips it. (7) The headline-unaffected claim holds: commitment_analysis.py:136-137 mutates sp_cov_recs to Counted=False and 557 sets purchase recs Counted=False explicitly, and total_savings at 140-142 sums only Counted-true recs. (8) The contrast is real: _render_fargate_savings_plan at 2243-2246 emits 'Advisory — ... not added to the tab total', which the generic path lacks. Minor nuance (not verdict-changing): the dollar-laden reason string '$X/mo (Y% off)... upfront $Z' is specific to purchase_recommendations (commitment_analysis.py:558-562); sp_coverage_gaps emits a non-dollar coverage-percentage reason (292) but still surfaces a plain 'Monthly Savings:' line (290). Both sources therefore render advisory dollars with no per-card 'not counted' note, exactly as described.

#### 🟡 M1 · Recommendation count desync: total_recommendations omits Fargate recs, and the counted/advisory header self-contradicts  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/commitment_analysis.py:150 (count); html_report_generator.py:3181-3186 (header)`
- **Evidence:** scan() sets total_recommendations = len(all_recs) + len(cost_hub_recs) (commitment_analysis.py:150); all_recs (line 139) excludes fargate_sp_recs, which nonetheless render via the fargate handler. The per-tab header builds `f"{total_recs} ({counted_n} counted, {advisory_n} advisory)"` where _counted_advisory_counts (html_report_generator.py:371-388) iterates ALL sources INCLUDING fargate_savings_plan and cost_optimization_hub. So counted_n+advisory_n = total_recs + len(fargate_recs): whenever Fargate cells exist, X+Y > N and the header contradicts itself (e.g. '6 (2 counted, 10 advisory)').
- **Impact:** Rendered card count != headline item count; the 'N (X counted, Y advisory)' line does not add up, reading as inattention. No dollar impact (Fargate recs are $0).
- **Fix:** Either include len(fargate_sp_recs) in total_recommendations (documented) or exclude fargate/CoH-only sources from _counted_advisory_counts so the header reconciles with total_recommendations. Pick one source of truth for the count.

#### 🟡 M2 · _account_coverage_ratio bare 'except Exception' swallows AccessDenied/throttle with no ctx.warn  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/commitment_analysis.py:803-820`
- **Evidence:** `try: rec = ce.get_savings_plans_purchase_recommendation(...) ... except Exception: return DEFAULT_COVERAGE_RATIO` (lines 803-820). Every other CE call in this file routes exceptions through _route_ce_error (lines 35-49), which classifies AccessDenied/AccessDeniedException/UnauthorizedOperation -> ctx.permission_issue else ctx.warn. This path silently falls back to the 0.70 default with NO ctx.warn / ctx.permission_issue.
- **Impact:** A denied or throttled account-wide SP purchase-recommendation call silently degrades the Fargate coverage ratio to a guessed 0.70, with zero operator signal of the IAM gap or throttle. Bounded to advisory Fargate numbers ($0 counted), but violates the 'nothing fails quietly' rule and hides a permission gap that also affects the purchase matrix.
- **Fix:** Replace the bare except with `except Exception as e: _route_ce_error(ctx, 'ce:GetSavingsPlansPurchaseRecommendation[account_coverage]', e); return DEFAULT_COVERAGE_RATIO` so the failure is classified and surfaced.

#### 🟡 M3 · Inconsistent utilization-waste bases and no structured AuditBasis on the two COUNTED findings  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/commitment_analysis.py:227-236 (sp); 341-350 (ri)`
- **Evidence:** sp_utilization waste = hourly x (1-rate) x 730 (line 228); ri_utilization waste = TotalAmortizedCost x (1-rate) with NO x730 (line 342). Both are the only findings that reach total_monthly_savings. Neither rec carries a structured rate/window/formula basis - only a free-text `reason`. The numbers are result-consistent (both monthly) ONLY because get_reservation_utilization runs over the 30-day tp with no Granularity, so TotalAmortizedCost is already a ~monthly figure - but this is undocumented and the differing form (x730 vs none) invites a future regression if either window changes.
- **Impact:** The dollar values are correct today, but a reviewer cannot defend either number from the report alone, and the asymmetric formula is fragile (change the tp/Granularity and the SP/RI bases diverge silently).
- **Fix:** Attach an AuditBasis dict (rate, window='30d', formula) to each counted rec, and make the two bases explicitly consistent (both expressed as monthly), e.g. document that ri TotalAmortizedCost is the 30-day amortized monthly cost and that sp hourly x 730 normalizes the hourly commitment to the same window.

#### 🟢 L1 · Missing CE client returns empty findings with no warn/permission_issue  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/commitment_analysis.py:110-112`
- **Evidence:** `ce = ctx.client('ce'); if not ce: return self._empty_findings()` - no ctx.warn or ctx.permission_issue is recorded.
- **Impact:** A region/permission problem that yields no CE client is indistinguishable from a healthy account with no commitments; the operator gets a clean empty tab with no signal to investigate.
- **Fix:** Emit ctx.warn (or ctx.permission_issue if attributable) before returning _empty_findings(), mirroring the pattern used by sibling adapters when a required client is absent.

#### 🟢 L2 · AVG_SP_DISCOUNT_RATE=0.30 is a flat reduction factor, not an exact SP-rate delta, and is unlabeled as an estimate  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/commitment_analysis.py:76, 282`
- **Evidence:** sp_coverage_gaps potential = OnDemandCost x (1-rate) x 0.30 (line 282) using the class constant AVG_SP_DISCOUNT_RATE (line 76) instead of the exact Compute-SP rate delta (which the Fargate path already pulls live from describe_savings_plans_offering_rates). Cannot be validated via Pricing API (no SavingsPlans service code).
- **Impact:** Advisory only (forced Counted=False), so no headline impact, but the value is a coarse estimate presented as a concrete dollar figure (compounded by H1's missing disclaimer).
- **Fix:** Label it an estimate in the rendered output, and/or derive the per-service discount from the live offering-rate matrix already fetched for Fargate; at minimum document 0.30 as a conservative typical Compute-SP discount.

#### 🟢 L3 · Adapter stat_cards tuple diverges from the html descriptor that actually renders  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/commitment_analysis.py:80-85 vs html_report_generator.py:178-184`
- **Evidence:** The adapter's StatCardSpec tuple exposes SP Utilization, SP Coverage, RI Utilization, and Monthly Savings (no RI Coverage). The rendering descriptor at html_report_generator.py:178-184 exposes four RATE cards (SP Util, SP Cov, RI Util, RI Cov) and NO savings card. ri_coverage_rate IS computed (extras, scan() line 193) so the rendered 4th card has data; the adapter-side tuple appears vestigial for this surface.
- **Impact:** Cosmetic/maintenance: two competing stat-card definitions; an editor changing the StatCardSpec tuple would have no effect on the report.
- **Fix:** Reconcile the two: either drop/align the unused StatCardSpec tuple or make the html descriptor derive from it, so there is a single source of truth for the four cards.

#### 🟢 L4 · Module docstring understates CE API cost (~7 calls/$0.07 vs ~20 calls/$0.20)  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/commitment_analysis.py:6-16, 69`
- **Evidence:** Docstring claims '~7 calls per scan (~$0.07/scan)' and lists 7 APIs, but scan() issues: util(1) + util_details(1) + coverage(1) + reservation_util(1) + reservation_coverage(1) + expiring util_details(1) + SP purchase matrix(6) + RI purchase matrix(6) + account_coverage_ratio(1) + Fargate get_cost_and_usage(1) ~= 20 CE calls (~$0.20), plus 3 free SavingsPlans offering-rate calls (grep of ce./describe_ at lines 211,221,271,331,387,414,509,590,732,774,804).
- **Impact:** Operators reading the cost disclosure underestimate the per-scan Cost Explorer charge by ~3x.
- **Fix:** Update the docstring to reflect the ~12-call purchase matrix + account-coverage + Fargate cost-and-usage calls (~$0.20/scan).

#### 🟢 L5 · Cross-tab RI presented as two separate advisory cards (RDS heuristic card + CoH rec here)  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/rds_logic.py:16-25, 79 (RDS); core/scan_orchestrator.py:104-112 (routing)`
- **Evidence:** CoH RdsReservedInstances recs route to the commitment_analysis bucket (scan_orchestrator.py:105), rendered advisory here. Separately, rds_logic demotes its own heuristic 'Reserved Instance Opportunities' to ADVISORY_CATEGORIES (rds_logic.py:23-25) and the RDS reporter excludes them from the tab total (reporter_phase_b.py:575-578). Both are advisory, so there is NO dollar double-count in the headline.
- **Impact:** Presentation only: the same RDS RI opportunity can appear as an advisory card in BOTH the RDS tab and the commitment_analysis tab, reading as two opportunities. No headline impact (both excluded from counted totals).
- **Fix:** Reconcile to a single advisory surface (e.g. suppress the RDS-tab heuristic RI card when a CoH RI rec for the same resource is routed to commitment_analysis), or add a cross-reference note so the reader sees one advisory.

#### 🟢 L6 · Coverage breadth gaps: empty RI coverage, SP-only expiry, narrow purchase matrix, EKS-Fargate miss  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/commitment_analysis.py:368-393, 408-448, 478-485, 728-767`
- **Evidence:** ri_coverage_gaps always returns [] (no groupBy, stat-card rate only; lines 368-393). _check_expiring reads SP utilization details only - RI expiry is never detected (lines 408-448). Purchase matrix is SP=('COMPUTE_SP',) only and RI=EC2 only (_SP_TYPES line 478, _RI_SERVICES lines 483-485) - RDS/ElastiCache/Redshift/OpenSearch/SageMaker RI/SP purchase recs arrive ONLY via CoH. _fargate_legs filters SERVICE='Amazon Elastic Container Service' (line 738), so EKS-Fargate spend billed under the EKS service dimension is excluded.
- **Impact:** Whole classes of buy/coverage/expiry opportunities are never surfaced natively (CoH partially backfills RI/SP buys). All advisory, so no headline distortion; pure coverage breadth. Per the brief these are likely intentional tradeoffs.
- **Fix:** Document each as a deliberate limitation (or extend: add RI expiry via get_reservation_utilization end dates, broaden _SP_TYPES/_RI_SERVICES, and add the EKS service value to _fargate_legs if EKS-Fargate coverage is desired).

---

### Containers (ECS/EKS Fargate) — `services/adapters/containers.py`

**Module identity:** key="containers", display_name="Containers", cli_aliases=("containers","ecs","ecr"), required_clients=("ecs","eks","ecr","compute-optimizer","cloudwatch"), requires_cloudwatch=True, reads_fast_mode=True (all confirmed at containers.py:30-42). Multi-source adapter aggregating three SourceBlocks: enhanced_checks (local ECS Fargate rightsizing + ECR untagged-layer reclaim), cost_optimization_hub (ctx.cost_hub_splits["containers"] from CoH EcsService/EcsTask/EcsCluster — orchestrator type_map lines 99-101, bucket consumed at containers.py:75), and compute_optimizer (services/advisor.get_ecs_compute_optimizer_recommendations). CoH and CO BOTH apply here (unlike network); CloudWatch (AWS/ECS CPU/MemoryUtilization, 7d) gates the rightsizing path. EKS is intentionally out of scope (owned by eks_cost) and scanned only for the service_counts extra. Pricing is LIVE/arch+OS-aware via PricingEngine.get_fargate_vcpu_hourly / get_fargate_gb_hourly / get_fargate_windows_os_hourly / get_ecr_storage_gb_month, region-correct, with region-scaled FALLBACK_FARGATE_*/FALLBACK_ECR_GB_MONTH constants only on API failure — NOT bare module constants as the CLAUDE.md row claims.

**Verdict:** The counted Fargate and ECR dollar math is sound: SKUs are arch/OS-correct, region scaling is applied exactly once (no pricing_multiplier double-apply), the Windows OS leg is symmetric across current/target, targets snap to valid Fargate combos and never size below measured peak, and all three material rates match the live AWS Pricing API. The headline structure is also correct — $0 results are dropped, the ECR oversized-repo advisory is Counted=False and rendered at $0, and all three sources have PHASE_B_HANDLERS entries. The cost-fidelity risk is concentrated in cross-source aggregation: Compute Optimizer recs are never deduped against Cost Hub (H1), so any ECS service surfaced by both AWS-native sources is double-counted in both savings and rec count — the one place this adapter diverges from the canonical Lambda pattern. Secondary issues are a silent-failure class in the ECS CO helper (H2) and several coverage/limitation items (Container-Insights gating, dead Spot constant, dedup name-collision, doc drift).

**Pricing validation:** Validated LIVE against the AWS Pricing API (MCP, us-east-1, 2026-06): (1) Fargate vCPU x86 Linux usagetype USE1-Fargate-vCPU-Hours:perCPU = $0.0404800 — exactly matches FALLBACK_FARGATE_VCPU_HOURLY[('x86','linux')]=0.04048 and the live get_fargate_vcpu_hourly SKU map. (2) Fargate GB x86 Linux usagetype USE1-Fargate-GB-Hours, memorytype perGB = $0.0044450 — exactly matches FALLBACK_FARGATE_GB_HOURLY[('x86','linux')]=0.004445; memory leg correctly uses GB (mem_mb/1024). (3) ECR AmazonECR TimedStorage-ByteHrs = $0.10/GB-Mo — exactly matches FALLBACK_ECR_GB_MONTH=0.10; adapter converts ReclaimableBytes/1024**3 to GiB and prices once. NOT live-validated this session (needs live Pricing-API validation, but constants present and consistent with the brief's 2026-06 verification): ARM Linux vCPU $0.03238 / GB $0.00356 (Fargate-ARM-*), Windows vCPU $0.046552 / GB $0.0051117 / OS-license $0.046 (Fargate-Windows-*-:perCPU). Region scaling is applied once: PricingEngine returns region-correct values and the adapter/_normalize_ecs_co_rec do NOT re-multiply by pricing_multiplier (no double-apply). Windows OS license leg is applied symmetrically to both current and target legs in fargate_task_hourly, so the delta is correct (not double-charged), and only for Windows tasks.

**Cost checks:**

| Check | Status | Trigger | Savings basis |
|---|---|---|---|
| ECS Fargate rightsizing (Metric-Backed) | counted | enhanced_checks source: Container Insights enabled on cluster (_container_insights_enabled) AND measured avg CPU<20% AND avg mem<30% over 7d (AWS/ECS CPU/MemoryUtilization) AND LaunchType resolves to FARGATE AND quantified saving>0 | quantify_fargate_rightsizing -> (cur_task_hourly - tgt_task_hourly) x 730 x task_count, where task_hourly = vcpu*vcpu_rate + mem_gb*gb_rate + vcpu*win_os_rate; target is peak-aware (rightsize_fargate_target with FARGATE_RIGHTSIZE_HEADROOM=1.2) snapped to a valid Fargate combo. Rates from PricingEngine.get_fargate_vcpu_hourly/get_fargate_gb_hourly (live, region-correct). Validated us-east-1 x86 Linux: vCPU $0.04048, GB $0.004445 (live Pricing API 2026-06). |
| ECR untagged-layer reclaim (ECR Lifecycle Management) | counted | enhanced_checks source: repo has >=1 untagged image, <=600 images, and compute_untagged_reclaimable_bytes>0 (layers referenced ONLY by untagged images). Skipped entirely in fast_mode. | reclaimable_GiB (ReclaimableBytes / 1024**3) x get_ecr_storage_gb_month(); validated us-east-1 = $0.10/GB-Mo (AmazonECR TimedStorage-ByteHrs, live Pricing API 2026-06). Priced once in _quantify_rec (containers.py:174-202). |
| ECR oversized-repo advisory | advisory | enhanced_checks source: repo has untagged images but >600 total images (ECR_MANIFEST_ANALYSIS_MAX_IMAGES) — too large for per-image manifest analysis | No dollar quantified; rec carries Advisory=True, Counted=False, EstimatedMonthlySavings=0.0 — rendered, contributes $0 (containers.py:114-117, services/containers.py:574-588) |
| Cost Optimization Hub ECS recs | counted | cost_optimization_hub source: CoH currentResourceType in {EcsService, EcsTask, EcsCluster} bucketed into ctx.cost_hub_splits['containers'] by orchestrator | sum of each rec's flat estimatedMonthlySavings (region-priced upstream, no pricing_multiplier re-applied). containers.py:138. |
| Compute Optimizer ECS service rightsizing | counted | compute_optimizer source: get_ecs_service_recommendations, normalized by _normalize_ecs_co_rec, filtered to estimatedMonthlySavings>0 (advisor.py:345-346) | sum of each rec's estimatedMonthlySavings, region-priced upstream; pricing_multiplier accepted but intentionally NOT applied in _normalize_ecs_co_rec (advisor.py:414-447). containers.py:139. |
| CO opt-in placeholder (ResourceId==compute-optimizer-service) | advisory | compute_optimizer disabled: synthetic placeholder returned by helper | Converted to ctx.warn and dropped before counting (containers.py:80-87) — never inflates count or savings |

**Findings:**

#### 🟠 H1 · Compute Optimizer ECS recs are never deduped against Cost Hub — same ECS service double-counted across the two AWS-native sources  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/containers.py:91-98, 138-139, 141`
- **Evidence:** dedupe_by_authority(cost_hub_recs, co_recs, enhanced_recs, ...) returns ONLY the filtered heuristics (containers_logic.py:305-311 returns `kept` = heuristics) and is assigned back to enhanced_recs; co_recs is passed in only to build the `covered` set for heuristic suppression and is itself NEVER filtered. Then both sources are summed independently: line 138 `savings += sum(... cost_hub_recs)` and line 139 `savings += sum(... co_recs)`, and line 141 `total_recs = len(enhanced_recs) + len(cost_hub_recs) + len(co_recs)`. The canonical Lambda adapter does the missing step: lambda_svc.py:119-131 explicitly drops a CO rec whose normalized name is already covered by CoH ('Compute Optimizer is lower authority than Cost Hub'). CoH EcsService recommendations routinely re-expose the same CO rightsizing data, so an ECS service present in both CoH and CO has its estimatedMonthlySavings added twice and its count inflated by one.
- **Impact:** Fabricated/double-counted dollars: any ECS service surfaced by BOTH Cost Hub (EcsService/EcsTask) and Compute Optimizer is counted twice in total_monthly_savings and once-extra in total_recommendations. Direct headline inflation; magnitude = full CO savings of every CoH-overlapping service.
- **Fix:** Mirror lambda_svc.py:113-131 / the EC2 pattern: build `covered` from cost_hub_recs via normalize_resource_name(coh_key), then filter co_recs to drop any whose normalize_resource_name(co_key) is in `covered` BEFORE summing/counting; only then run dedupe_by_authority for heuristics. Enforce the stated authority order CoH > CO > heuristic across all three populations, not just heuristics.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Real, exactly at the cited lines. containers.py:91-98 calls dedupe_by_authority(cost_hub_recs, co_recs, enhanced_recs, ...) and binds the result back to enhanced_recs ONLY. In containers_logic.py:280-311 that function builds a `covered` set from both cost_hub AND compute_optimizer (lines 297-304) but then iterates and returns only `kept` = filtered heuristics (lines 305-311). co_recs is therefore used solely to suppress overlapping heuristics; it is never itself filtered against cost_hub. The adapter then sums the two AWS-native sources independently — line 138 `savings += sum(... cost_hub_recs)` and line 139 `savings += sum(... co_recs)` — and counts line 141 `len(enhanced_recs)+len(cost_hub_recs)+len(co_recs)`. There is no CoH↔CO dedup anywhere in containers.py. The canonical Lambda adapter performs exactly the missing step at lambda_svc.py:119-131 (drops a CO rec whose normalized name is already in seen_functions built from cost_hub_recs, 'Compute Optimizer is lower authority than Cost Hub'). containers.py:75 confirms the adapter consumes ctx.cost_hub_splits['containers'], whose EcsService rightsizing entries are sourced from Compute Optimizer, so a service present in both CoH and CO has its CO estimatedMonthlySavings added on top of its CoH savings (line 139 over line 138) and its count inflated by one. Double-count magnitude = full CO savings of every CoH-overlapping ECS service, exactly as described. Only residual unknown is whether any given live account actually has an overlapping service, but the code-level defect (missing dedup guard that every sibling adapter has) is unambiguous and the savings are summed without protection.

#### 🟠 H2 · ECS Compute Optimizer helper swallows non-opt-in errors (AccessDenied/throttling) with logger-only, no ctx.warn/permission_issue  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/advisor.py:338-342`
- **Evidence:** except Exception as e: logger.warning('ECS Compute Optimizer not available: %s', e); if 'OptInRequiredException' in str(e) or 'not registered' in str(e): return [_compute_optimizer_opt_in_rec('ECS', 'task-rightsizing')]; return []. Unlike the sibling EBS (advisor.py:223-230), RDS (271-278) and Lambda (305-312) helpers — which classify AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation -> ctx.permission_issue and other errors -> ctx.warn — the ECS helper records nothing on ctx for a permission or throttling failure. The outer adapter try/except (containers.py:62-72) only wraps get_container_services_analysis/get_enhanced_container_checks, NOT get_ecs_compute_optimizer_recommendations (called at containers.py:76 outside any try), so the empty list propagates silently.
- **Impact:** Entire ECS Compute Optimizer rightsizing source silently vanishes on a permission gap or throttle, with no audit trail in the report — under-reports savings with zero operator visibility (the canonical silent-failure class the brief flags).
- **Fix:** Add the same classification block used by EBS/RDS/Lambda: elif 'AccessDenied' in msg or 'UnauthorizedOperation' in msg: ctx.permission_issue('Compute Optimizer ECS recommendations denied', service='containers', action='compute-optimizer:GetECSServiceRecommendations'); else: ctx.warn('Compute Optimizer ECS recommendations unavailable: '+msg, service='containers'). (Same gap exists in get_ec2/get_asg CO helpers — note as out-of-scope follow-up.)
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Real, exactly at advisor.py:338-342. The ECS CO helper's except block is: `logger.warning('ECS Compute Optimizer not available: %s', e); if 'OptInRequiredException' in str(e) or 'not registered' in str(e): return [_compute_optimizer_opt_in_rec('ECS','task-rightsizing')]; return []`. There is no AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation -> ctx.permission_issue branch and no else -> ctx.warn branch. The three siblings DO classify: EBS advisor.py:223-230 (AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation -> ctx.permission_issue, else -> ctx.warn), RDS 271-278, and Lambda 305-312 all do this. ECS records nothing on ctx for a permission gap or throttle — logger-only. The outer adapter call is at containers.py:76 (`co_raw = get_ecs_compute_optimizer_recommendations(ctx)`), which sits OUTSIDE the two try/except blocks (62-66 wrapping get_container_services_analysis, 68-72 wrapping get_enhanced_container_checks); the helper swallows its own exception and returns [], so the empty list propagates with no audit trail in the report. Entire ECS Compute Optimizer rightsizing source silently vanishes on AccessDenied or throttling with zero operator visibility — the silent-failure class the brief flags. Confirmed as described.

#### 🟡 M1 · Fargate rightsizing emits nothing when Container Insights is disabled — silent under-report on the common case  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/containers.py:416, 424-429`
- **Evidence:** container_insights_enabled = _container_insights_enabled(ctx, ecs, cluster_name) (line 416); inside the service loop `if not service.get('serviceName') or not container_insights_enabled: continue` (line 425) — so a cluster without Container Insights produces NO rec, not even a $0 advisory. The reporter even has a dedicated 'ECS Container Insights Required' group (reporter_phase_b.py:945, 983-984) that the adapter never populates (dead branch).
- **Impact:** Most accounts do not enable Container Insights, so the dominant Fargate rightsizing lever silently yields zero findings with no signal that data was unavailable. Coverage hole (no fabricated $, but large missed-savings + no advisory).
- **Fix:** When a cluster has running Fargate services but Container Insights is disabled, emit a Counted=False, EstimatedMonthlySavings=0.0 advisory with CheckCategory='ECS Container Insights Required' (which the reporter already renders) so the gap is visible; keep it out of total_monthly_savings.

#### 🟡 M2 · SPOT_SAVINGS_FACTOR is dead code in containers.py — the advertised Fargate Spot lever is never implemented  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/containers.py:17-19`
- **Evidence:** SPOT_SAVINGS_FACTOR: float = 0.70 is defined with a docstring ('Applied to the rightsized on-demand base when a rec is explicitly a Fargate->Spot move') but grep across the repo shows it is referenced nowhere in containers.py or services/containers*.py (only eks.py defines+uses its own separate copy). Meanwhile get_ecs_analysis advertises 'Consider Fargate Spot for fault-tolerant tasks (Save 70%)' (services/containers.py:140) as text that is never converted into a counted/advisory rec.
- **Impact:** Dead pricing constant implying an unimplemented or silently-dropped Fargate->Spot recommendation; a real ~50-70% saving lever is never surfaced. No wrong dollar, but missed coverage + misleading dead code.
- **Fix:** Either wire a defensible, interruptible-workload-gated Fargate Spot delta (published Fargate Spot rate vs on-demand, as a Counted=False advisory unless an explicit interruptible signal exists) or remove the constant and the 'Save 70%' prose so no dead lever remains.

#### 🟡 M3 · Cross-source dedup collapses ECS services to last path segment — same service name in two clusters over-dedups a legitimate heuristic saving  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/containers_logic.py:269-277, 296-311`
- **Evidence:** normalize_resource_name returns value.split('/')[-1].split(':')[-1] (line 277), so an ECS service ARN '...:service/clusterA/web' and CO resource_id 'clusterB/web' both normalize to 'web'. dedupe_by_authority (lines 296-311) drops any heuristic whose normalized key is in `covered`. The heuristic key extractor (containers.py:290-296) uses ServiceName ('web') with no cluster qualification.
- **Impact:** Two distinct services named 'web' in different clusters collide: a CoH/CO rec for clusterA/web suppresses the genuine heuristic rightsizing rec for clusterB/web -> under-counts real savings. Conversely, if CoH uses an ARN shape CO does not, the same service could escape dedup (H1 amplifier).
- **Fix:** Make the dedup key cluster-qualified (e.g. normalize to 'cluster/service' for ECS) consistently across coh_key/co_key/heuristic_key so collisions require both cluster and service to match.

#### 🟢 L1 · Reporter category-name drift and dead grouping branches in _render_containers_enhanced_checks  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `reporter_phase_b.py:944-973, 983-992`
- **Evidence:** Adapter emits CheckCategory='ECR Lifecycle Management' but the group key is 'ECR Lifecycle Missing' (line 950); the match at line 957 misses, and ECR recs only render via the `'RepositoryName' in rec` fallback (line 970-971). The groups 'ECS Container Insights Required', 'Unused ECS Clusters', 'Unused EKS Clusters' (lines 945,948,949) are never populated by this adapter (EKS is out of scope; ECS rightsizing recs match 'ECS Rightsizing - Metric-Backed' first). Empty groups are skipped (`if not resources: continue`, line 977) so no blank card renders.
- **Impact:** Cosmetic only: ECR still renders (via fallback) and no blank card appears, but the category-name mismatch is fragile and three renderer branches are dead.
- **Fix:** Rename the group key to 'ECR Lifecycle Management' to match the emitted CheckCategory, and remove the EKS / Unused-ECS / Container-Insights dead branches (or wire M1's advisory into the Container-Insights group).

#### 🟢 L2 · get_ecr_analysis uses un-paginated describe_repositories — ecr_repositories service-count under-reports on >100-repo accounts  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/containers.py:224`
- **Evidence:** repos_response = ecr.describe_repositories(); repositories = repos_response.get('repositories', []) — single call, no paginator, while the reclaim path get_enhanced_container_checks paginates describe_repositories (lines 343-346).
- **Impact:** Cosmetic count only (extras.service_counts.ecr_repositories), not a savings path; inconsistent with the paginated reclaim path and silently caps the displayed repo count at one page (~100).
- **Fix:** Use ecr.get_paginator('describe_repositories') in get_ecr_analysis to match the reclaim path.

#### 🟢 L3 · ECR image-count failure in get_ecr_analysis logged via logger only, not recorded on ctx  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/containers.py:241-243`
- **Evidence:** except Exception as e: logger.warning(f'... Error getting image count for ECR repo {repo_name}: {str(e)}'); image_count = 0 — bypasses ctx.warn/ctx.permission_issue (contrast _ecr_failure used elsewhere).
- **Impact:** Affects only the cosmetic ImageCount in service_counts (not a savings figure), but a permission/throttle on list_images is invisible in the report.
- **Fix:** Route through _ecr_failure(ctx, f'list_images({repo_name})', e) so AccessDenied -> permission_issue and other -> warn, consistent with the rest of the shim.

#### 🟢 L4 · CLAUDE.md adapter row misdescribes containers pricing and omits its CoH+CO sources  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/CLAUDE.md:containers.py row (Live Pricing table)`
- **Evidence:** Row reads 'Fargate vCPU/mem hourly rates x 730 | Module constants'. Reality: live region-correct PricingEngine.get_fargate_vcpu_hourly/get_fargate_gb_hourly/get_fargate_windows_os_hourly/get_ecr_storage_gb_month with FALLBACK_* constants only on API failure; the adapter also consumes Cost Optimization Hub (EcsService/EcsTask/EcsCluster) and Compute Optimizer (ECS) — neither mentioned in the row.
- **Impact:** Documentation/code mismatch; misleads future auditors into believing pricing is bare constants and that there are no CoH/CO sources (dimension 0 drift).
- **Fix:** Update the row to 'Live Fargate vCPU/GB/Windows-OS + ECR storage via PricingEngine (region-correct; FALLBACK_* on failure); consumes Cost Hub + Compute Optimizer (ECS)' and move it conceptually alongside lambda_svc/rds in the AWS-Pricing-API + CoH/CO group.

---

### DMS — `services/adapters/dms.py`

**Module identity:** key="dms", cli_aliases=("dms",), display_name="DMS", reads_fast_mode=True; required_clients() -> ("dms","cloudwatch") (services/adapters/dms.py:15-22). Live-only pricing: ctx.pricing_engine.get_instance_monthly_price("AWSDatabaseMigrationSvc", class.replace("dms.","")) with NO fallback constant — a pricing miss (monthly==0) is skipped, not fabricated (dms.py:44-50). Counted dollars are computed independently in scan() as monthly*0.35 (rightsizing/unused) and monthly*0.5 (Multi-AZ→Single-AZ); EstimatedSavings strings are display-only and do NOT route through parse_dollar_savings. DMS consumes NEITHER Cost Optimization Hub NOR Compute Optimizer (absent from scan_orchestrator type_map/_HUB_SERVICES and from services/advisor.py) — "missing CoH/CO" is out of scope. Rendering is Phase A (reporter_phase_a.py PHASE_A_DESCRIPTORS["dms"], savings_mode="conditional", inner close group); no PHASE_B_HANDLERS entry; CloudWatch CPUUtilization is the only metric.

**Verdict:** The DMS adapter's pricing lookup is region-correct and avoids fabricated fallbacks, but its counted dollars are unreliable on four axes proven against live code and the AWS Pricing API. (1) Every very-low-CPU instance is counted twice at 0.35× monthly because scan() applies monthly*0.35 to BOTH the instance_rightsizing and unused_instances copies of the same InstanceId (C1). (2) Zero-datapoint CloudWatch collapses to avg_cpu=0.0, flagging metric-less instances as unused AND rightsizable with no evidence (C2). (3) A swallowed CloudWatch exception still emits a counted 35% rec and hides AccessDenied/throttling (C3). (4) The Single-AZ vs Multi-AZ SKU is non-deterministic (MaxResults=1, instanceType-only filter), so every counted rate — and the Multi-AZ 0.5 lever — can be 2× high or low, confirmed live where t3.medium returns Single-AZ first but c5.large returns Multi-AZ first (H1/H2). Multi-AZ stacking on rightsizing (M1), a 'Unknown'-id render desync (M2), and an unhonored reads_fast_mode (M3) round out the confirmed bugs. CoH/CO are correctly out of scope.

**Pricing validation:** Validated LIVE via AWS Pricing MCP (AWSDatabaseMigrationSvc, us-east-1, attribute instanceType). dms.t3.medium: TWO SKUs — InstanceUsg:dms.t3.medium $0.0745/hr (Single-AZ, ≈$54.39/mo) returned FIRST, Multi-AZUsg:dms.t3.medium $0.149/hr (Multi-AZ, ≈$108.77/mo) — exactly 2×. dms.c5.large: Multi-AZUsg:dms.c5.large $0.238/hr returned FIRST, then InstanceUsg:dms.c5.large $0.119/hr — also 2×, and the first-row ordering is OPPOSITE to t3.medium. This directly confirms H1/H2: _call_pricing_api MaxResults=1 + PriceList[0] returns a non-deterministic Single/Multi SKU per type. instanceType is un-prefixed (filter on 'dms.t3.medium' returned empty; 't3.medium' succeeded), so instance_class.replace('dms.','') is correct. Region scaling is applied once via _display_name (no double-multiply). DMS Serverless (DCU) confirmed NOT priced — no fabricated serverless dollars leak. The 0.35 and 0.5 factors are heuristics, not Pricing-API values, and were not validated against a live target-class delta (none exists in code).

**Cost checks:**

| Check | Status | Trigger | Savings basis |
|---|---|---|---|
| instance_rightsizing (CPU<30) | counted | ReplicationInstanceStatus=="available" AND ReplicationInstanceClass set AND 7-day AWS/DMS CPUUtilization (Period=3600, Average) avg_cpu < 30 (services/dms.py:54-87) | scan() loop: monthly = get_instance_monthly_price("AWSDatabaseMigrationSvc", class.replace("dms.","")) (= hourly*730), savings += monthly*0.35 (services/adapters/dms.py:44-48). Rate source = AWS Pricing API live, region via _display_name; no region double-scaling. Flat 0.35 reduction factor, NO target class. Display string 'Rightsize for ~35% savings on instance cost'. |
| unused_instances (CPU<5) | counted | same instance additionally has avg_cpu < 5 (services/dms.py:89-99); appended in ADDITION to its instance_rightsizing rec | NOT separately priced — but the scan() loop iterates ALL recommendations (rightsizing + unused flattened) and applies monthly*0.35 to EACH, so the unused rec adds a SECOND monthly*0.35 for the same InstanceId. Display string 'Full instance cost if terminated' (inconsistent with the 0.35 actually counted). |
| instance_rightsizing (CloudWatch-failure fallback) | counted | the inner try around get_metric_statistics raises ANY Exception (services/dms.py:100) — incl. AccessDenied/Throttling/OptInRequired or empty-metric parse error | Appends a rightsizing rec with no AvgCPU (services/dms.py:101-113); scan() still prices it monthly*0.35. No metric behind the number; no ctx.warn/permission_issue. |
| multi_az_review (non-prod Multi-AZ→Single-AZ) | counted | rec.get("MultiAZ") truthy AND (ReplicationInstanceIdentifier OR any Tag Value) lowercased contains one of dev\|test\|staging\|sandbox\|nonprod (services/adapters/dms.py:53-62) | az_savings = monthly*0.5 where monthly = get_instance_monthly_price(...same lookup...) (dms.py:69-73); savings += az_savings (dms.py:92). When monthly==0, az_savings=0.0, EstimatedMonthlySavings=0, PricingWarning set, display string '~50% of instance cost (Multi-AZ doubles the price)'. 0.5 factor is only correct if the priced SKU is the Multi-AZ SKU. |
| serverless_migration | advisory | describe_replication_configs paginator runs but the bucket is intentionally never populated (services/dms.py:115-122) | None — SourceBlock(count=0); emits nothing, contributes $0 and 0 recommendations. |

**Findings:**

#### 🔴 C1 · Intra-adapter double-count: a <5% CPU instance is counted twice at 0.35× monthly  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/dms.py + services/dms.py:dms.py:39-48 (loop); services/dms.py:74-99 (buckets)`
- **Evidence:** services/dms.py appends the SAME instance to checks['instance_rightsizing'] when avg_cpu<30 (line 74) AND to checks['unused_instances'] when avg_cpu<5 (line 89). get_enhanced_dms_checks flattens BOTH buckets into result['recommendations'] (services/dms.py:129-133). scan() then iterates `for rec in recs:` and does `savings += monthly * 0.35` (services/adapters/dms.py:39-48) for EVERY rec, so one InstanceId contributes monthly*0.35 twice ≈ 0.70× its monthly bill. The unused rec's own string says 'Full instance cost if terminated' — a third, inconsistent basis.
- **Impact:** Every very-low-CPU instance over-counts savings by ~2× (≈0.70× monthly instead of one defensible number). e.g. an idle dms.c5.large priced at Single-AZ $86.87/mo is counted as 2×$30.40=$60.81 instead of one figure. Inflates total_monthly_savings and the executive headline.
- **Fix:** Dedup by InstanceId before pricing: an instance with avg_cpu<5 should be counted ONCE (either as a terminate/full-cost candidate or as a single rightsizing lever), never in both buckets' contributions. Either drop the unused rec from the priced loop, or compute savings from a per-InstanceId set rather than the flattened rec list.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Real exactly as described. In services/dms.py the `if avg_cpu < 5:` block (line 89) is NESTED inside the `if avg_cpu < 30:` block (line 74), so any instance with avg_cpu<5 is appended to BOTH checks['instance_rightsizing'] (lines 75-87, InstanceClass at line 78) AND checks['unused_instances'] (lines 90-99, InstanceClass at line 93). get_enhanced_dms_checks flattens every bucket into all_recommendations (lines 129-133). scan() in services/adapters/dms.py:39-48 iterates `for rec in recs:` and, because both recs carry InstanceClass, adds monthly*0.35 for EACH → 0.70x monthly for one InstanceId. That sum feeds total_monthly_savings (line 104), so it reaches the headline. The unused rec's EstimatedSavings string 'Full instance cost if terminated' (line 96) is purely cosmetic and never used by scan(), confirming the inconsistent third basis. Arithmetic checks (0.35*86.87=30.40; 2x=60.81).

#### 🔴 C2 · Zero-datapoint CloudWatch → avg_cpu=0.0 flags metric-less instances as unused AND rightsizable  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/dms.py:70-99`
- **Evidence:** avg_cpu = sum(point['Average'] for point in Datapoints) / max(len(Datapoints), 1) (services/dms.py:70-72). When CloudWatch returns zero datapoints (brand-new instance, metric-less, or wrong dimension) the result is 0/1 = 0.0, which passes BOTH `avg_cpu < 30` (line 74) and `avg_cpu < 5` (line 89). The instance is emitted into instance_rightsizing AND unused_instances with no usage evidence.
- **Impact:** Fabricated savings on instances with NO usage signal — counted at ~0.70× monthly (compounding C1). A healthy but freshly-created replication instance is reported as 'unused' and a termination candidate. False-positive deletion guidance + fabricated dollars.
- **Fix:** Guard on datapoint count: if len(Datapoints)==0 (or below a minimum coverage threshold) skip the CPU-gated recs or emit them as $0 advisory (Counted=False), never as counted savings. Compute avg only over real datapoints.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Real exactly as described. services/dms.py:70-72 computes avg_cpu = sum(...) / max(len(Datapoints), 1); with zero datapoints this is 0/1 = 0.0. 0.0 satisfies both `avg_cpu < 30` (line 74) and `avg_cpu < 5` (line 89), so a metric-less/brand-new instance is emitted into instance_rightsizing AND unused_instances with no usage evidence. There is no empty-Datapoints guard anywhere in the block. Because it lands in both buckets it is then double-counted at ~0.70x monthly via C1. Confirmed.

#### 🔴 C3 · Swallowed CloudWatch failure still emits a counted 35% rec with no metric and no warning  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/dms.py:100-113`
- **Evidence:** The `except Exception:` at services/dms.py:100 catches ANY failure of cloudwatch.get_metric_statistics (incl. AccessDenied, ThrottlingException, OptInRequired) and unconditionally appends a rightsizing rec (lines 101-113) which scan() prices at monthly*0.35. There is no ctx.warn and no ctx.permission_issue — the permission/throttle problem is hidden AND a saving is fabricated on an instance whose CPU was never read.
- **Impact:** Permission/throttling failures are invisible to the operator, and every such instance contributes a fabricated monthly*0.35 with zero evidence. On an account-wide AccessDenied for cloudwatch:GetMetricStatistics, EVERY available DMS instance gets a fabricated 35% saving.
