- **Fix:** In the except, classify the error: AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation/OptInRequired → ctx.permission_issue, else ctx.warn (mirror services/_aws_errors.record_aws_error used by network.py). Do NOT emit a counted rec on metric failure — drop it or make it a $0 advisory.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Real exactly as described. The `except Exception:` at services/dms.py:100 wraps the cloudwatch.get_metric_statistics call (lines 60-68), so any AccessDenied/Throttling/OptInRequired is swallowed and unconditionally appends a rightsizing rec (lines 101-113) with InstanceClass set, which scan() (adapters/dms.py:44-48) prices at monthly*0.35. The block contains no ctx.warn and no ctx.permission_issue — the only ctx.warn is on the OUTER except (line 126-127) which covers dms-client/paginator failures, not this inner CloudWatch failure. So a permission/throttle error is invisible and a 35% saving is fabricated per available instance. On account-wide AccessDenied every instance hits this path. Confirmed.

#### 🟠 H1 · Non-deterministic Single-AZ vs Multi-AZ SKU — counted rate can be 2× off  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `core/pricing_engine.py (consumed by services/adapters/dms.py:44-46,69-71):pricing_engine.py:1290-1298 (_fetch_generic_instance_price) + 1590-1613 (_call_pricing_api)`
- **Evidence:** _fetch_generic_instance_price filters on instanceType + location ONLY (pricing_engine.py:1291-1294); _call_pricing_api uses MaxResults=1 and returns _extract_usd(PriceList[0]) (pricing_engine.py:1598-1611). Live AWS Pricing API confirms each DMS type has TWO SKUs under one instanceType: t3.medium → InstanceUsg:dms.t3.medium $0.0745/hr (Single, returned FIRST) and Multi-AZUsg:dms.t3.medium $0.149/hr (Multi); c5.large → Multi-AZUsg:dms.c5.large $0.238/hr returned FIRST, then InstanceUsg:dms.c5.large $0.119/hr. The first-row ordering flips by type, so MaxResults=1 returns Single for t3.medium but Multi for c5.large — genuinely non-deterministic.
- **Impact:** A Single-AZ instance priced off the Multi-AZ SKU is counted at exactly 2× its real rate (and vice-versa). For a Single-AZ c5.large the rightsizing saving is counted as 0.35×$173.74=$60.81 instead of 0.35×$86.87=$30.40. Affects every counted DMS dollar.
- **Fix:** Pin usagetype in the lookup: add a TERM_MATCH filter on usagetype ('InstanceUsg:dms.<type>' for Single-AZ, 'Multi-AZUsg:dms.<type>' for Multi-AZ) selected from instance.MultiAZ. Add a dedicated DMS price method rather than the generic instanceType-only filter.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Code mechanism confirmed at the cited lines. _fetch_generic_instance_price (pricing_engine.py:1290-1298) filters ONLY on instanceType + location; _call_pricing_api (1590-1622) uses MaxResults=1 and returns _extract_usd(json.loads(PriceList[0])) (line 1611) — no deploymentOption/AZ pin, unlike RDS (deploymentOption, line 1160) and EC2 tenancy (line 1072) where the codebase explicitly guards against exactly this MaxResults=1 ambiguity. That two distinct prices exist for one DMS class is corroborated by the adapter itself ('Multi-AZ DMS doubles the instance hourly rate', adapters/dms.py:62-65,81). So the Single-vs-Multi-AZ rate selection for DMS is structurally non-deterministic and can be 2x off. LIVE-EVIDENCE CAVEAT: the specific per-type first-row ordering (t3.medium→Single first, c5.large→Multi first) and the exact $/hr figures cannot be settled from code; they require a live AWS Pricing API call. The defect (no AZ disambiguation) is fully present in code regardless of which way each type happens to order.

#### 🟠 H2 · Multi-AZ→Single-AZ saving halved when the lookup returns the Single-AZ SKU  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/dms.py:69-73`
- **Evidence:** az_savings = monthly * 0.5 (dms.py:73) where monthly comes from the same un-pinned get_instance_monthly_price (dms.py:69-71). The 0.5 factor is only correct if monthly is the Multi-AZ price (Single = 0.5×Multi). Live API: for t3.medium the lookup returns the Single-AZ row first ($0.0745 → $54.39/mo), so monthly*0.5 = $27.19, whereas the true saving of dropping Multi-AZ→Single = Multi−Single = $108.77−$54.39 = $54.39. The reported saving is half the real one.
- **Impact:** Systematic 2× UNDERSTATEMENT of the Multi-AZ lever whenever the non-deterministic lookup returns the Single-AZ SKU (observed for t3.medium); for c5.large it returns Multi-AZ first so it happens to be correct — the error direction is unpredictable per type.
- **Fix:** Pin the Multi-AZ SKU (Multi-AZUsg:dms.<type>) for this lever, then saving = monthly_multi * 0.5 == the Single-AZ price; or look up the Single-AZ price directly and report saving = single_az_monthly. Tie to H1's usagetype pinning.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Code mechanism confirmed at adapters/dms.py:69-73. For a Multi-AZ instance (actual cost 2S where S=Single-AZ price) the true Multi->Single saving is S. The code sets az_savings = monthly * 0.5 (line 73) where `monthly` comes from the same un-pinned get_instance_monthly_price (lines 69-71). That is correct only if the lookup returns the Multi-AZ SKU (2S*0.5=S); if it returns the Single-AZ SKU it yields S*0.5=0.5S, i.e. half the real saving. Since the lookup does not pin Multi-AZ (per H1), the lever is understated 2x whenever the Single-AZ SKU is returned. LIVE-EVIDENCE CAVEAT: which SKU is returned per type (e.g. t3.medium understated, c5.large happens correct) depends on live Pricing API ordering and cannot be settled from code; the halving logic and the un-pinned source are confirmed in code.

#### 🟡 M1 · Multi-AZ factor stacks on rightsizing for the same instance/bill  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/dms.py:39-48 + 52-92`
- **Evidence:** A non-prod Multi-AZ instance with avg_cpu<5 is counted in the rec loop at monthly*0.35 (rightsizing, and again via C1 for the unused bucket) AND in the multi_az loop at monthly*0.5 (dms.py:48 and dms.py:92). Combined: 0.35 + 0.35 + 0.5 = up to 1.2× the (possibly wrong-SKU) monthly cost for one instance.
- **Impact:** Over-counts savings on non-prod Multi-AZ idle instances by stacking three heuristic levers that all discount the same monthly bill — can exceed 100% of the instance cost.
- **Fix:** Decide a single owner per instance and order the levers: if Multi-AZ→Single-AZ is recommended, compute rightsizing against the post-Single-AZ baseline (or make Multi-AZ removal exclusive of rightsizing). Remove the rec from the rightsizing loop when it is claimed by multi_az_review, rather than summing both.

#### 🟡 M2 · Phase A render desync — multi_az_review recs show resource id 'Unknown'  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/dms.py + reporter_phase_a.py:dms.py:76-91 (rec uses 'Resource'); reporter_phase_a.py:185-196`
- **Evidence:** multi_az_recs are built with key 'Resource': name (services/adapters/dms.py:78) and carry no 'InstanceId' and no 'AvgCPU'. _extract_dms_details reads rec.get('InstanceId', 'Unknown') (reporter_phase_a.py:187), so every Multi-AZ card lists the resource as 'Unknown (<class>)'. The DMS-Multi-AZ-in-Non-Prod group renders without identifying the instance.
- **Impact:** Operator cannot tell WHICH instance to switch to Single-AZ — the counted Multi-AZ saving is unactionable. Cosmetic-to-actionability, no dollar mis-count.
- **Fix:** Add 'InstanceId': name to the multi_az rec (services/adapters/dms.py:77-90), or make _extract_dms_details fall back to rec.get('Resource') when InstanceId is absent.

#### 🟡 M3 · reads_fast_mode=True declared but CloudWatch read is never gated on ctx.fast_mode  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/dms.py + services/dms.py:dms.py(adapter):18; services/dms.py:54-72`
- **Evidence:** DmsModule declares reads_fast_mode=True (services/adapters/dms.py:18), but get_enhanced_dms_checks calls cloudwatch.get_metric_statistics (services/dms.py:60-68) unconditionally — there is no `ctx.fast_mode` reference anywhere in services/dms.py. The CLAUDE.md guidance (step 5) says to check ctx.fast_mode first and bail cheaply.
- **Impact:** A fast scan still issues a per-instance CloudWatch GetMetricStatistics call, defeating fast_mode and the declared contract. Also means C2/C3 fabricated paths run even in fast mode.
- **Fix:** Gate the CPUUtilization read on ctx.fast_mode: when set, skip the metric and emit the CPU-gated recs as $0 advisory (Counted=False) — mirror the Lambda fast-mode fix — or drop the reads_fast_mode claim.

#### 🟢 L1 · 0.35 is a flat reduction factor, not a current→target price delta  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/dms.py:48`
- **Evidence:** savings += monthly * 0.35 (services/adapters/dms.py:48) with no target instance class selected — unlike EC2 which uses the exact current→target delta. The 35% is asserted by the string 'Rightsize for ~35% savings on instance cost' (services/dms.py:84) with no sizing basis.
- **Impact:** The counted rightsizing dollar is a heuristic guess, not a defensible delta; could be high or low depending on the real right-size target. Defensibility limitation, not a wrong rate.
- **Fix:** Pick a concrete target (one size down within the DMS family, or the Single-AZ baseline) and count current_price − target_price; or demote rightsizing to a $0 advisory until a target is chosen. Record an AuditBasis (rate/region/metric-window/SKU/formula).

#### 🟢 L2 · describe_replication_configs permission gap swallowed by except: pass  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/dms.py:115-124`
- **Evidence:** The serverless paginator is wrapped in `try: ... except Exception: pass` (services/dms.py:115-124). A dms:DescribeReplicationConfigs AccessDenied/throttle vanishes with no ctx.warn/permission_issue.
- **Impact:** No dollar impact today (serverless bucket is intentionally empty), but the silent swallow hides a permission gap and would mask future serverless pricing. Observability limitation.
- **Fix:** Replace `except Exception: pass` with classification via ctx.warn / ctx.permission_issue (AccessDenied/OptInRequired → permission_issue). Since the bucket emits nothing, consider removing the paginator entirely.

#### 🟢 L3 · Outer except records via ctx.warn but does not classify permission errors  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/dms.py:126-127`
- **Evidence:** `except Exception as e: ctx.warn(f"Could not analyze DMS resources: {e}", "dms")` (services/dms.py:126-127). An AccessDenied on dms:DescribeReplicationInstances is recorded only as a generic warn, never as ctx.permission_issue.
- **Impact:** Permission failures are not surfaced as permission issues in the report — operator sees a soft warning instead of an actionable IAM gap. No dollar impact.
- **Fix:** Classify the exception: AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation/OptInRequired → ctx.permission_issue, else ctx.warn (reuse services/_aws_errors.record_aws_error).

#### 🟢 L4 · status=='available' gate may exclude billable non-available instances  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/dms.py:54`
- **Evidence:** Only instances with ReplicationInstanceStatus=='available' are evaluated (services/dms.py:54). States like 'modifying', 'storage-full', 'upgrading' still incur instance cost but are silently skipped for all levers.
- **Impact:** Idle/over-provisioned instances momentarily in a non-'available' state are missed (coverage gap / under-count), not a wrong dollar.
- **Fix:** Broaden the gate to all billable states (exclude only 'creating'/'deleting'/'failed' where no charge applies) and rely on the metric/price evidence rather than status alone.

#### 🟢 L5 · Display EstimatedSavings string diverges from the counted dollar; card never shows the counted number  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/dms.py + reporter_phase_a.py:services/dms.py:84,96; reporter_phase_a.py:450-454`
- **Evidence:** Phase A renders the prose EstimatedSavings of resources[0] only (reporter_phase_a.py:452-454). The unused bucket's string is 'Full instance cost if terminated' while the counted contribution is monthly*0.35; the rightsizing string is '~35% savings' with no dollar. The executive headline (_calculate_service_savings → total_monthly_savings) sums the 0.35/0.5 numbers, which the cards never display.
- **Impact:** Headline dollars and card text describe different bases ('full cost' vs 35%), so the report is internally inconsistent and a reader cannot reconcile the per-card claim with the counted total. No additional fabrication beyond C1, but a reporting-fidelity gap.
- **Fix:** Make the unused card reflect what is counted (or count what it claims — full terminate value), and render the per-rec counted dollar (EstimatedMonthlySavings) on the card so counted==rendered, mirroring the Lambda AuditBasis pattern.

---

### DynamoDB — `services/adapters/dynamodb.py`

**Module identity:** key="dynamodb", cli_aliases=("dynamodb",), display_name="DynamoDB", requires_cloudwatch=True, required_clients()=("dynamodb","cloudwatch") — all confirmed in services/adapters/dynamodb.py:50-59. reads_fast_mode is NOT declared (inherits BaseServiceModule default False, services/_base.py:25) even though both shim functions call cloudwatch.get_metric_statistics — a gap (see M3). Pricing is module constants only (no PricingEngine method for DynamoDB); RCU/WCU hourly × 730, region-scaled by ctx.pricing_multiplier at the emit site. Cost Optimization Hub APPLIES (DynamoDBTable→"dynamodb" bucket, core/scan_orchestrator.py:66,97; consumed at adapter 139-147). Compute Optimizer does NOT cover DynamoDB, so no CO source is expected. The services/adapters/CLAUDE.md row ("RCU/WCU hourly rates × 730 | Module constants") is rate-accurate but understates reality: it omits that the adapter also consumes Cost Hub (cost_hub_splits["dynamodb"]) and holds on-demand per-request constants — minor doc drift.

**Verdict:** The four DynamoDB pricing constants are correct against the live AWS Pricing API, so the dollar errors are methodological, not rate errors. The most serious is C1: a table with RCU and WCU both >100 fires BOTH the Over-Provisioned (0.40) and Reserved (0.66) checks and the adapter sums them, producing a counted saving of 1.06x the table's entire monthly cost — a physically impossible, double-counted figure. Beyond that, savings are fabricated from capacity dimensions with no utilization gate (the 0.30 default on every provisioned table and the 0.40 over-provisioned factor applied even when CloudWatch says 'Utilization acceptable'), reserved capacity is counted rather than demoted to advisory like RDS, GSI throughput is invisible, the on-demand cost conflates a 1-hour Average with monthly volume (~60x undercount), CloudWatch permission/throttle failures are swallowed into recommendation strings, fast-mode is not honored, and well-sized tables are counted into the headline while rendering no card. The pricing is trustworthy; the savings methodology is not defensible from the report and needs utilization-gating, single-lever dedup, and advisory demotion before the counted total is reliable.

**Pricing validation:** All four module constants validated LIVE against the AWS Pricing API (AmazonDynamoDB, us-east-1, publication 2026-06-08) and are numerically correct: provisioned RCU $0.00013/RCU-hr (SKU 4V475Q49DCKGXQZ2, usagetype ReadCapacityUnit-Hrs) matches _DYNAMODB_RCU_HOURLY; provisioned WCU $0.00065/WCU-hr (SKU R6PXMNYCEDGZ2EYN, WriteCapacityUnit-Hrs) matches _DYNAMODB_WCU_HOURLY; on-demand reads $0.125 per million read request units (SKU 4W4ZMC46EHE8XTTZ) matches _ON_DEMAND_RCU_PER_REQUEST=0.125/1e6; on-demand writes $0.625 per million write request units (SKU FGXVD96DKJMUASY3) matches _ON_DEMAND_WCU_PER_REQUEST=0.625/1e6. The x730 hours/month and a single pricing_multiplier are applied once on each path (provisioned recomputed in the adapter; on-demand multiplied once at adapter 110, shim carries no multiplier) — no double region-scaling. The reserved_capacity 0.66 factor is a heuristic midpoint of AWS's published 53-76% reserved-capacity range, NOT a specific reserved SKU rate (reserved terms were not re-derived) — needs live validation if it stays counted, though H2 recommends demoting it to advisory. The Pricing API also confirms separately-billed ReplWriteCapacityUnit-Hrs ($0.00065, SKU QM7WV2JADZJDV45W) and GSI throughput at the same RCU/WCU rates, corroborating the H3 (GSI) and L3 (Global Tables) coverage gaps.

**Cost checks:**

| Check | Status | Trigger | Savings basis |
|---|---|---|---|
| Provisioned table baseline (table_analysis, default factor) | counted | Provisioned table in optimization_opportunities NOT also in enhanced_checks, with rcu>0 or wcu>0 (adapter 89-103) | (rcu*0.00013 + wcu*0.00065)*730*pricing_multiplier*0.30. RCU SKU 4V475Q49DCKGXQZ2=$0.00013/RCU-hr, WCU SKU R6PXMNYCEDGZ2EYN=$0.00065/WCU-hr (AWS Pricing API us-east-1, validated). 0.30 = DYNAMODB_SAVINGS_FACTORS['default'] |
| On-demand table baseline (table_analysis, default factor) | counted | On-demand table NOT in enhanced_checks with EstimatedMonthlyCost>0 (adapter 104-110) | EstimatedMonthlyCost * pricing_multiplier * 0.30, where shim EstimatedMonthlyCost = (avg ConsumedReadCapacityUnits*0.125/1e6 + avg ConsumedWriteCapacityUnits*0.625/1e6)*730 (services/dynamodb.py:193-195). Per-request rates validated: reads $0.125/M SKU 4W4ZMC46EHE8XTTZ, writes $0.625/M SKU FGXVD96DKJMUASY3 |
| Unused DynamoDB Tables (enhanced_checks) | advisory | ItemCount==0 and TableStatus=='ACTIVE' (services/dynamodb.py:294-304) | factor unused_table=1.00, BUT rec carries no ReadCapacityUnits/WriteCapacityUnits keys -> rcu=wcu=0 -> rec_savings=0.0 (adapter 116-128). EstimatedSavings string says '100% of table costs' but counted=$0 |
| DynamoDB Over-Provisioned Capacity (enhanced_checks) | counted | Provisioned table with ReadCapacityUnits>100 OR WriteCapacityUnits>100 — emitted regardless of measured utilization (services/dynamodb.py:311,374-383) | (rcu*0.00013 + wcu*0.00065)*730*pricing_multiplier*0.40 (rightsize_provisioned). Blanket factor over WHOLE table cost, not a current-target delta |
| DynamoDB Reserved Capacity (enhanced_checks) | counted | Provisioned table with ReadCapacityUnits>=100 AND WriteCapacityUnits>=100 (services/dynamodb.py:385-395) | (rcu*0.00013 + wcu*0.00065)*730*pricing_multiplier*0.66 (reserved_capacity, AWS 53-76% midpoint). Counted on the SAME table that also fires Over-Provisioned (see C1) |
| DynamoDB Billing Mode - Metric-Backed (enhanced_checks) | advisory | On-demand table with steady high usage over 14d (services/dynamodb.py:440-469) | factor billing_mode_switch=0.40 but rec has only AvgReadCapacity string, no ReadCapacityUnits -> rcu=wcu=0 -> $0 (adapter 116-128) |
| DynamoDB Monitoring Required (enhanced_checks) | advisory | On-demand table with no CloudWatch datapoints (services/dynamodb.py:470-486) | no rcu/wcu -> rec_savings=0.0; pure 'enable monitoring' nudge |
| DynamoDB CloudWatch Required (enhanced_checks) | advisory | On-demand table where the CloudWatch query raised an exception (services/dynamodb.py:488-503) | no rcu/wcu -> $0; this is also where AccessDenied/throttle silently lands (see M2) |
| DynamoDB Data Lifecycle (enhanced_checks) | advisory | TableSizeBytes > 10 GiB (services/dynamodb.py:505-514) | factor data_lifecycle=0.60 but rec carries no rcu/wcu -> $0; storage $/GB-mo never modeled |
| Cost Optimization Hub DynamoDBTable recs (cost_optimization_hub) | counted | ctx.cost_hub_splits['dynamodb'] rec whose resourceId.split('/')[-1] is NOT in covered_tables (adapter 137-147) | sum of rec['estimatedMonthlySavings'] (AWS-provided, region-correct, no multiplier applied) |

**Findings:**

#### 🔴 C1 · Over-Provisioned + Reserved Capacity stack on the same table -> savings exceed 100% of table cost  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/dynamodb.py:114-130`
- **Evidence:** A provisioned table with RCU>=101 AND WCU>=101 produces BOTH an over_provisioned_capacity rec (CheckCategory 'DynamoDB Over-Provisioned Capacity', services/dynamodb.py:374-383) and a reserved_capacity rec (services/dynamodb.py:385-395). Both carry ReadCapacityUnits/WriteCapacityUnits, so the enhanced loop applies a factor per rec: rec_savings = monthly_current*0.40 (over-prov) and monthly_current*0.66 (reserved), then `savings += rec_savings` for each. For RCU=WCU=200: monthly_current=(200*0.00013+200*0.00065)*730=$113.88; counted savings = 113.88*0.40 + 113.88*0.66 = $120.71 = 1.06x the table's ENTIRE monthly cost.
- **Impact:** Physically impossible >100% saving on every large table; the two are mutually-exclusive remediations (rightsize OR reserve), so the headline double-counts. Inflates total_monthly_savings by up to 1.06x the cost of every table with RCU and WCU both >100.
- **Fix:** Treat the two as alternatives: emit only one rec per table (or demote reserved to advisory per H2) and never sum both factors. Cap any single table's counted saving at its monthly_current.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified exactly as described. services/dynamodb.py: over_provisioned_capacity rec is appended unconditionally at :374-383 whenever read>100 OR write>100, and reserved_capacity at :385-395 whenever read>=100 AND write>=100; for RCU>=101 AND WCU>=101 both fire and both carry ReadCapacityUnits/WriteCapacityUnits. In the adapter enhanced loop (services/adapters/dynamodb.py:114-130) _enhanced_savings_factor maps over-provisioned->rightsize_provisioned=0.40 and reserved->reserved_capacity=0.66 (DYNAMODB_SAVINGS_FACTORS at services/dynamodb.py:82-89), both applied to the same monthly_current and both added to savings. No within-enhanced_recs dedup exists (only opt_opps->enhanced at :90 and CoH->covered_tables at :137-147). Math checks: (200*0.00013+200*0.00065)*730=113.88; 113.88*(0.40+0.66)=120.71 = 1.06x full table cost. Physically >100% on every table where both checks fire.

#### 🟠 H1 · Fabricated $ from a capacity dimension with no utilization gate (0.30 default and 0.40 over-provisioned)  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/dynamodb.py:96-103, 114-124`
- **Evidence:** table_analysis applies DYNAMODB_SAVINGS_FACTORS['default']=0.30 to EVERY provisioned table's full RCU/WCU cost (adapter 96-103) with no usage signal. The over_provisioned rec is appended unconditionally after the utilization branch (services/dynamodb.py:374-383) even when its own recommendation_text reads 'Utilization acceptable (Read: X%, Write: Y%) - monitor usage patterns' (services/dynamodb.py:361-367); the adapter then multiplies the whole table cost by 0.40. The measured read_utilization/write_utilization are computed but never used to gate or size the saving.
- **Impact:** Counted dollars on well-utilized and on un-measured tables that have no real saving — fabricated savings. The 0.40/0.30 are blanket factors over the whole cost, not a current-target delta.
- **Fix:** Gate the counted saving on measured low utilization (read_utilization<20% or write_utilization<20%, already computed at services/dynamodb.py:346-354) and compute current-target = current_cost - rightsized_cost where target capacity = ceil(avg_consumed * buffer). With no CloudWatch evidence, emit $0 advisory (Counted=False).
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Both fabrication paths real. (a) opt_opps loop adapter :96-103 applies DYNAMODB_SAVINGS_FACTORS['default']=0.30 to monthly_current for any provisioned table not in enhanced_table_names, with zero usage signal. (b) The over_provisioned rec is appended at services/dynamodb.py:374 OUTSIDE the if/else that builds recommendation_text, so it emits even when the text is 'Utilization acceptable...' (:362-367); adapter :114-124 then applies factor 0.40 to full table cost. read_utilization/write_utilization (:346-349) are computed but only interpolated into a display string, never used to gate or size savings. Minor nuance: high-capacity provisioned tables do not flow through the 0.30 opt_opps branch (they are routed to enhanced), but there they receive blanket 0.40/0.66 factors, so the no-utilization-gate fabrication holds across all provisioned tables.

#### 🟠 H2 · Reserved Capacity counted instead of demoted to advisory (commitment lever)  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/dynamodb.py:114-130`
- **Evidence:** _enhanced_savings_factor maps 'reserved' -> 0.66 (adapter 36-37) and the enhanced loop counts it into total_monthly_savings. RDS treats the identical lever as advisory: services/rds_logic.py:25 `ADVISORY_CATEGORIES = frozenset({RI_CATEGORY, BACKUP_CATEGORY})` with Counted=False, and CoH routes *ReservedInstances/*SavingsPlans to commitment_analysis (core/scan_orchestrator.py:104-113). DynamoDB reserved capacity is a 1/3-yr commitment purchase that overlaps the rightsizing lever on the same table.
- **Impact:** Commitment savings counted into the rightsizing headline and double-counted against the over-provisioned rec (C1). Belongs in the commitment view, not the per-service rightsizing total.
- **Fix:** Mark reserved_capacity recs Counted=False (mirror services/_savings.mark_zero_savings_advisory / RDS ADVISORY_CATEGORIES) so they render but are excluded from total_monthly_savings.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** _enhanced_savings_factor maps 'reserved'->0.66 (adapter :36-37); the reserved rec always has rcu/wcu>0 so monthly_current*0.66 is added to savings and returned as total_monthly_savings (:130,:154) with no Counted=False flag or demotion. The project's own convention treats this commitment lever as advisory: services/rds_logic.py:23-25 places Reserved Instances in ADVISORY_CATEGORIES (excluded from headline, is_advisory at :79), and core/scan_orchestrator.py:104-113 routes all *ReservedInstances/*SavingsPlans CoH recs to commitment_analysis. DynamoDB heuristic reserved capacity is instead counted into the per-service rightsizing headline. Independently valid beyond the C1 double-count overlap.

#### 🟠 H3 · GSI provisioned throughput invisible — base cost and over-provisioning under-counted  ·  `limitation` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/dynamodb.py:137-145, 306-309`
- **Evidence:** Both shims read only the table-level ProvisionedThroughput (services/dynamodb.py:138-140 and 307-309). grep for GlobalSecondaryIndexes/GSI/IndexName across services/dynamodb.py and services/adapters/dynamodb.py returns nothing. GlobalSecondaryIndexes[].ProvisionedThroughput is billed separately at the same RCU/WCU rates and is never summed.
- **Impact:** A table with small base throughput but large GSIs is materially under-costed; over-provisioned GSIs are completely invisible. Both the baseline cost and every factor-based saving are understated for GSI-heavy tables.
- **Fix:** Sum table ProvisionedThroughput + each GlobalSecondaryIndexes[].ProvisionedThroughput RCU/WCU before computing monthly_current; surface per-GSI over-provisioning.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Both code paths read only table-level ProvisionedThroughput: services/dynamodb.py:138-140 (base cost computed at :142-145 from table_info RCU/WCU only) and :307-309 (enhanced check). grep for GlobalSecondaryIndex|GSI|IndexName|LocalSecondaryIndex across services/dynamodb.py and services/adapters/dynamodb.py returns no matches. GlobalSecondaryIndexes[].ProvisionedThroughput is billed separately at the same RCU/WCU rates and is never summed, so baseline cost and every factor-based saving are understated for GSI-heavy tables and over-provisioned GSIs are invisible.

#### 🟡 M1 · On-demand monthly cost conflates capacity-unit Average over a 1-hour period with monthly request volume (~60x undercount)  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/dynamodb.py:184-195`
- **Evidence:** avg_r/avg_w = mean of the 'Average' statistic of ConsumedReadCapacityUnits/ConsumedWriteCapacityUnits over Period=3600 (services/dynamodb.py:166-188). EstimatedMonthlyCost = (avg_r*0.125/1e6 + avg_w*0.625/1e6)*730. The Average statistic over a 1-hour period is the average per-sample consumed units, not the hourly total; multiplying by 730 hours (not 730*60) understates monthly request volume by ~60x, and ConsumedReadCapacityUnits is a capacity-unit metric, not a request-unit count.
- **Impact:** On-demand table baseline saving (0.30 x cost x multiplier) is understated ~60x; the number is not defensible from the report. Per-request rate itself is correct ($0.125/M, $0.625/M validated).
- **Fix:** Use Statistics=['Sum'] over the window and divide by lookback to get true monthly request units (Sum_over_window * 30/lookback_days), or read the per-request Sum metric; do not multiply a 1-hour Average by 730 hours.

#### 🟡 M2 · CloudWatch AccessDenied/throttle swallowed into a recommendation string, never classified  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/dynamodb.py:201-203, 371-372, 488-503`
- **Evidence:** Both shims wrap the get_metric_statistics calls in bare `except Exception:`. On-demand: services/dynamodb.py:201-203 sets EstimatedMonthlyCost=0.0 + a PricingWarning dict field (never surfaced to ctx) and 488-503 emits a 'DynamoDB CloudWatch Required' rec. Provisioned: 371-372 falls to recommendation_text='High provisioned capacity - CloudWatch analysis recommended' and still appends the over_provisioned rec that gets counted at 0.40. grep shows no ctx.permission_issue / record_aws_error / AccessDenied handling anywhere in the dynamodb path.
- **Impact:** A cloudwatch:GetMetricStatistics AccessDenied or throttle is invisible to the operator and, worse, the over-provisioned 0.40 saving is still counted on a table with zero metric evidence. permission_issue/warn classification (action cloudwatch:GetMetricStatistics) is missing.
- **Fix:** Catch ClientError and route AccessDenied/Unauthorized/OptInRequired -> ctx.permission_issue and throttling -> ctx.warn (mirror services/_aws_errors.record_aws_error used by network.py); do not count a capacity rec whose CloudWatch read failed.

#### 🟡 M3 · reads_fast_mode not declared; CloudWatch reads not gated on ctx.fast_mode  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/dynamodb.py:50-59`
- **Evidence:** DynamoDbModule declares requires_cloudwatch=True but not reads_fast_mode, so it inherits BaseServiceModule.reads_fast_mode=False (services/_base.py:25). grep for fast_mode in services/dynamodb.py and services/adapters/dynamodb.py returns nothing, yet get_metric_statistics is called per provisioned (>100) table (services/dynamodb.py:317-335) and per on-demand table (166-183, 403-421). rds.py:46 and lambda_svc.py:61 both set reads_fast_mode=True and bail cheaply.
- **Impact:** A --fast scan still pays for CloudWatch on every qualifying table, contradicting the fast-mode contract.
- **Fix:** Declare reads_fast_mode=True on the adapter and skip the get_metric_statistics blocks when ctx.fast_mode is set (return the $0 advisory path).

#### 🟡 M4 · Counted-but-not-rendered: well-sized provisioned tables add 0.30x savings to the headline but render no card  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `reporter_phase_b.py:909-912`
- **Evidence:** Adapter counts 0.30*monthly_current for ANY provisioned table with rcu>0 (adapter 96-103) — including small, well-sized tables that generate no OptimizationOpportunities text (services/dynamodb.py:149-158 only adds opportunities for RCU/WCU>100, ItemCount==0, or size>1GiB). In _render_dynamodb_enhanced_checks those recs have no CheckCategory and an empty opportunities list, so they fall to `else: continue` (reporter_phase_b.py:911-912). If every table_analysis rec is empty-opp, the handler returns '' and html_report_generator.py:3340-3342 drops the whole source (`if not handler_output: continue`), while total_monthly_savings and total_recommendations still include them.
- **Impact:** Tab headline (savings + rec count) does not reconcile with the rendered cards; counted != rendered.
- **Fix:** Only count a table_analysis rec when it carries a concrete rendered remediation, or render a card for every counted rec; gate the 0.30 default behind a real opportunity (ties to H1).

#### 🟢 L1 · $0 'enable monitoring' nudges reported as counted, not advisory  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/dynamodb.py:114-130`
- **Evidence:** The adapter never imports or calls services/_savings.mark_zero_savings_advisory and never sets rec['Counted']=False. 'DynamoDB Monitoring Required', 'DynamoDB CloudWatch Required', 'DynamoDB Billing Mode - Metric-Backed', 'DynamoDB Data Lifecycle' and 'Unused DynamoDB Tables' all yield rec_savings=0.0 (no rcu/wcu), but html_report_generator.py:_counted_advisory_counts (380-388) classifies them as 'counted' because Counted is not False.
- **Impact:** total_recommendations and the 'N counted' header are inflated by $0 best-practice/monitoring nudges, producing counted findings with no dollar saving.
- **Fix:** Call mark_zero_savings_advisory(enhanced_recs, lambda r: r.get('EstimatedMonthlySavings', 0)) (or set Counted=False on the $0 categories) so they render but are excluded from the counted total.

#### 🟢 L2 · Empty PROVISIONED table deletion saving is $0 (string says '100% of table costs')  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/dynamodb.py:294-304`
- **Evidence:** The unused_tables rec (services/dynamodb.py:294-304) carries TableName/ItemCount/TableSizeBytes but NO ReadCapacityUnits/WriteCapacityUnits, so the adapter's enhanced loop computes rec_savings=0.0 (adapter 116-128) even for an empty PROVISIONED table that still bills full provisioned capacity. EstimatedSavings string is '100% of table costs' while counted=$0 — string vs counted desync. For an empty provisioned table with RCU/WCU>100 the over-provisioned (0.40) and reserved (0.66) recs ARE counted instead — the wrong lever.
- **Impact:** Real deletion savings on empty provisioned tables are missed; an empty high-capacity table is recommended to rightsize/reserve rather than delete.
- **Fix:** Attach the table's provisioned RCU/WCU to the unused rec so factor 1.00 yields the full provisioned monthly cost; suppress over-provisioned/reserved when the table is empty (ItemCount==0).

#### 🟢 L3 · CoH ARN->table dedup breaks on index ARNs; Global Tables / storage unmodeled  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/dynamodb.py:141-147`
- **Evidence:** resourceId.split('/')[-1] (adapter 143) yields 'Name' for table ARNs (...:table/Name) but 'GSI' for index ARNs (...:table/Name/index/GSI), so a CoH index-level rec on an already-covered table would not dedup. Separately, the global_tables_optimization bucket is declared but never populated (services/dynamodb.py:269), replicated-write capacity (ReplWriteCapacityUnit-Hrs $0.00065, validated SKU QM7WV2JADZJDV45W) and storage $/GB-mo are not modeled, and data_lifecycle (0.60) is emitted as $0.
- **Impact:** Possible CoH double-count on GSI-ARN recs; Global Tables replica writes and storage savings are out of scope (documented gaps).
- **Fix:** Parse the table name as resource_id.split(':table/')[-1].split('/')[0]; document Global Tables/storage as intentional gaps or populate them.

#### 🟢 L4 · Non-ACTIVE-table handling inconsistent; ItemCount==0 staleness can mis-flag active tables  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/dynamodb.py:291-292`
- **Evidence:** enhanced_checks skips any table where TableStatus!='ACTIVE' (services/dynamodb.py:291-292), but table_analysis does NOT skip non-ACTIVE tables (services/dynamodb.py:120-218), so an UPDATING/CREATING provisioned table still gets the counted 0.30 default in table_analysis but no enhanced rec — inconsistent. ItemCount (used for the unused check, services/dynamodb.py:294) is refreshed by DynamoDB only ~every 6 hours, so an actively-written table can read ItemCount==0.
- **Impact:** Transitional tables counted in one source but not the other; a freshly-populated table may be flagged 'unused'.
- **Fix:** Apply the same TableStatus=='ACTIVE' gate in both shims; corroborate ItemCount==0 with recent ConsumedWriteCapacityUnits before flagging unused.

---

### EBS — `services/adapters/ebs.py`

**Module identity:** key="ebs", cli_aliases=("ebs",), display_name="EBS", reads_fast_mode=True, requires_cloudwatch=True, required_clients()=("ec2","compute-optimizer","cloudwatch") — all confirmed in services/adapters/ebs.py:106-114. EBS is a 6-SourceBlock multi-source adapter: it CONSUMES Cost Optimization Hub (ctx.cost_hub_splits["ebs"], type_map["EbsVolume"]="ebs" at core/scan_orchestrator.py:89) AND Compute Optimizer (services/advisor.get_ebs_compute_optimizer_recommendations), plus three heuristic sources (unattached, gp2_migration, enhanced/over-provisioned-IOPS) and a non-counted ebs_snapshots leak-out routed to the Snapshots tab. Pricing strategy is live PricingEngine (get_ebs_monthly_price_per_gb / get_ebs_iops_monthly_price / get_ebs_io2_iops_cost / get_ebs_throughput_monthly_price / get_ebs_snapshot_price_per_gb) with us-east-1 FALLBACK_EBS_* constants region-scaled by pricing_multiplier ONLY on the fallback path. CoH and CO both apply. Minor doc gap: the services/adapters/CLAUDE.md ebs.py row lists only "AWS Pricing API" and does not state that EBS consumes Cost Hub + Compute Optimizer (the RDS row does), so the row understates the adapter's sources.

**Verdict:** EBS pricing fidelity is strong: every material rate (gp2/gp3 $/GB, gp3 IOPS, io2 tier breakpoints, snapshot $/GB) was confirmed live against the AWS Pricing API and matches the engine + fallback constants, region scaling is applied once (fallback-only), and the ebs_snapshots leak-out IS consumed by the Snapshots-tab extractor (html_report_generator.py:2538-2586) — not a dead renderer. The one HIGH cost-correctness defect is a real double-count: dedupe_by_authority dedups heuristics only against CoH/CO and never against each other, while the gp2 and IOPS scans apply no status filter, so unattached gp2 (and CloudWatch-active available gp3/io1/io2) volumes are counted in two sources at once — deterministically inflating the EBS headline. Two MEDIUM silent-failure bugs (enhanced-path except and CloudWatch IOPS-read failures are not permission-classified, unlike the unattached path) hide coverage loss. Remaining items are documented limitations: gp2->gp3 throughput parity omission (overstates large-gp2 savings), delete-only CoH revalidation, a duplicate get_unattached_volumes call, and CoH/CO findings lacking a structured AuditBasis.

**Pricing validation:** Validated LIVE via AWS Pricing MCP (AmazonEC2, us-east-1, 2026-06-26 publication) — all match the scanner's FALLBACK_EBS_* constants: gp2 = $0.10/GB-Mo (usagetype EBS:VolumeUsage.gp2) and gp3 = $0.08/GB-Mo (EBS:VolumeUsage.gp3), delta $0.02 confirmed; gp3 provisioned IOPS = $0.005/IOPS-Mo (EBS:VolumeP-IOPS.gp3, group 'EBS IOPS'); io2 tiered IOPS confirmed exactly at the code's breakpoints — base 0-32,000 $0.065 (group 'EBS IOPS'), tier2 32,001-64,000 $0.0455 (group 'EBS IOPS Tier 2'), tier3 >64,000 $0.0319/~$0.032 (group 'EBS IOPS Tier 3'); EBS Standard snapshot = $0.05/GB-Mo (usagetype suffix EBS:SnapshotUsage, matching _fetch_ebs_snapshot_price's suffix selector, correctly distinct from EBS:SnapshotArchiveStorage $0.0125 and the .outposts/UnderBilling variants). The PricingEngine fetch filters (productFamily Storage / System Operation / Storage Snapshot + volumeApiName + group) align with the live SKU shape. gp3 throughput fallback ($0.04/MiBps-Mo = $40.96/GiBps ÷ 1024) and io1 flat $0.065/IOPS-Mo were not re-pulled live this session (needs live Pricing-API validation) but are consistent with the io2 base rate and published gp3 throughput SKU.

**Cost checks:**

| Check | Status | Trigger | Savings basis |
|---|---|---|---|
| cost_optimization_hub | counted | ctx.cost_hub_splits['ebs'] rec passing _coh_is_renderable (actionType present, ebsVolume detail present, finding!=Optimized) AND surviving _drop_stale_delete_recs live re-check of 'delete' actions (services/adapters/ebs.py:141-143) | flat rec['estimatedMonthlySavings'] summed (AWS-priced; no scanner rate applied) — services/adapters/ebs.py:198 |
| compute_optimizer | counted | get_ebs_compute_optimizer_recs actionable finding (is_actionable_co_finding drops Optimized/UnderProvisioned), opt-in placeholder dropped+warned, then compute_optimizer_savings(r)>0 (services/adapters/ebs.py:150-167) | compute_optimizer_savings = volumeRecommendationOptions[rank1].savingsOpportunity.estimatedMonthlySavings.value (services/_savings.py:46-69) — services/adapters/ebs.py:199 |
| unattached_volumes | counted | describe_volumes status=available, NOT attached to a stopped instance, zero Attachments (services/ebs.py:288-297) | EstimatedMonthlyCost = size_gb×get_ebs_monthly_price_per_gb(type) + gp3 IOPS>3000×$/IOPS + gp3 throughput>125×$/MiBps + io1 flat IOPS + io2 tiered IOPS; 100% on delete (services/ebs.py:342-413) — services/adapters/ebs.py:200 |
| gp2_migration | counted | describe_volumes volume-type=gp2 (NO status filter — includes available volumes) (services/ebs.py:570) | gp2_to_gp3_net_savings = size×(gp2−gp3 $/GB delta) − max(0, gp2_baseline_iops(size)−3000)×gp3 IOPS rate; throughput parity NOT netted (services/ebs_logic.py:127-140; adapter delta from _gp2_to_gp3_savings_per_gb services/adapters/ebs.py:31-44,183-195) |
| over_provisioned_iops (enhanced_checks/other) | counted | describe_volumes volume-type io1/io2/gp3 (NO status filter) with billable IOPS, NOT fast_mode, CloudWatch peak×1.3<provisioned (recommend_iops_from_usage) (services/ebs.py:439-529) | (billable_current_iops − billable_recommended_iops)×rate: gp3 above 3000×$0.005; io2 tiered get_ebs_io2_iops_cost delta; io1 flat $/IOPS; parsed via parse_dollar_savings (services/adapters/ebs.py:202) |
| old_snapshots (ebs_snapshots leak-out) | advisory | self-owned snapshot age>old_snapshot_days, NOT backing a currently-registered self-owned AMI, description NOT 'Created by CreateImage' (services/ebs.py:597-645) | VolumeSize×get_ebs_snapshot_price_per_gb() labelled '(max estimate)'; routed to ebs_snapshots SourceBlock, NOT added to EBS savings — consumed by Snapshots tab _extract_snapshots_data (html_report_generator.py:2538-2586) |
| orphaned_snapshots (ebs_snapshots leak-out) | advisory | self-owned 'Created by CreateImage' snapshot NOT backing a current AMI (deregistered-AMI orphan), age>threshold (services/ebs.py:615-630) | VolumeSize×snapshot rate '(max estimate)'; ebs_snapshots block, NOT counted in EBS total; rendered in Snapshots tab |

**Findings:**

#### 🟠 H1 · Intra-heuristic dedup gap: unattached volumes are double-counted with gp2_migration (and over_provisioned_iops)  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/ebs_logic.py + services/ebs.py + services/adapters/ebs.py:ebs_logic.py:113-119; ebs.py:570; ebs.py:464; ebs.py:288; adapters/ebs.py:170-202`
- **Evidence:** dedupe_by_authority computes `covered = coh_ids | co_ids` ONCE (ebs_logic.py:115) and filters every heuristic list against the SAME set (ebs_logic.py:116-118) — it never removes a volume in one heuristic list from the others. Meanwhile the gp2 scan `paginate(Filters=[{'Name':'volume-type','Values':['gp2']}])` (ebs.py:570) and the IOPS scan `Values:['io1','io2','gp3']` (ebs.py:464) apply NO status filter, while the unattached scan is `status=available` (ebs.py:288). So an available (unattached) gp2 volume appears in BOTH `unattached_volumes` and `gp2_migration` with the same normalized vol- id, and dedup keeps both. The adapter then sums `unattached_kept` EstimatedMonthlyCost (adapters/ebs.py:200) AND `gp2_total` (adapters/ebs.py:201) for that same volume.
- **Impact:** Double-counts the gp2->gp3 migration delta on top of the full delete cost for every unattached gp2 volume (deterministic, no CloudWatch needed; gp2 + unattached are the most common EBS case). E.g. a 1,000 GB unattached gp2: delete=$100/mo (1000x$0.10, validated live) is counted, PLUS migration=$20/mo (1000x$0.02) — ~20% headline inflation per volume. The same gap lets an available gp3/io1/io2 volume with recent CloudWatch datapoints be counted in both unattached_volumes (100%) and over_provisioned_iops (the IOPS subset). Inflates both total_monthly_savings and total_recommendations.
- **Fix:** Either (a) exclude available volumes from the gp2 scan (ebs.py:570) and IOPS scan (ebs.py:464) — you would never migrate/rightsize a volume you are recommending to delete; or (b) make dedupe_by_authority accumulate ids across the heuristic lists in priority order (unattached first) so gp2/other drop any vol- already claimed by unattached: iterate heuristic_rec_lists adding each list's kept ids to `covered` before filtering the next.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** All cited evidence verified in the real code. dedupe_by_authority (ebs_logic.py:113-119) computes covered = coh_ids | co_kept_ids ONCE (line 115) and filters every heuristic list against only that CoH/CO set (lines 116-118: `heuristic_volume_id(r) not in covered`); it performs NO cross-heuristic dedup, so a volume in unattached_volumes is never removed from gp2_recs. The unattached scan (ebs.py:288) filters status=available and requires `not attachments`, admitting available volumes of any type including gp2. The gp2 scan (ebs.py:570) filters volume-type=gp2 with NO status filter and appends every gp2 volume unconditionally (lines 571-581, no attachment check). Therefore a truly-unattached gp2 volume appears in BOTH lists with the same VolumeId (heuristic_volume_id, ebs_logic.py:51-53, keys off rec['VolumeId'] for both), and since neither is CoH/CO-covered, dedup keeps both. The adapter (adapters/ebs.py:170-202) passes [unattached_volumes, gp2_recs, other_recs] to dedupe_by_authority (line 171), then sums unattached_kept EstimatedMonthlyCost = full delete cost (line 200) AND gp2_total = migration delta (line 201) for the same volume; total_recs counts both unattached_kept and gp2_kept (line 206). Impact math checks out: 1,000 GB unattached gp2 -> delete $100/mo + migration gp2_to_gp3_net_savings(1000,0.02,rate)=$20/mo (gp2 baseline IOPS=3000, provisioned_iops=max(0,3000-3000)=0, so storage delta only) = ~20% per-volume inflation, deterministic, no CloudWatch needed. The over_provisioned_iops variant is also real: IOPS scan (ebs.py:464) has no status filter, the recs land in other_recs (partition_enhanced_recs lines 88-91, 'Over Provisioned Iops' is not gp2/snapshot/unattached) and other_kept is summed at line 202 — but it is gated on _observed_peak_iops returning CloudWatch data (lines 475-482), so the unattached+IOPS overlap requires a recently-detached volume with datapoints (the finding correctly frames this as the conditional, rarer case). Lines, mechanism, severity (inflates both total_monthly_savings and total_recommendations on the most common EBS case), and impact are all accurate.

#### 🟡 M1 · compute_ebs_checks outer except is not permission-classified (denied describe_volumes/snapshots -> generic warn)  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/ebs.py:647-648`
- **Evidence:** The single try wrapping the gp2 scan, _scan_over_provisioned_iops, _current_ami_snapshot_ids, and describe_snapshots ends in `except Exception as e: ctx.warn(f"Could not perform enhanced EBS checks: {e}", service='ebs')`. Contrast get_unattached_volumes (ebs.py:322-329) and get_ebs_volume_count (ebs.py:231-238), which catch ClientError and route UnauthorizedOperation/AccessDenied to ctx.permission_issue.
- **Impact:** An AccessDenied on ec2:DescribeVolumes (gp2 filter), ec2:DescribeSnapshots, or ec2:DescribeImages silently aborts the entire enhanced path (gp2 migration + IOPS rightsizing + snapshots) and surfaces only a generic warning — the operator cannot distinguish 'no findings' from 'permission lost', so whole-check $0 coverage loss is invisible in the permission report.
- **Fix:** Split the bare except into `except ClientError as e:` classifying e.response['Error']['Code'] in ('UnauthorizedOperation','AccessDenied') -> ctx.permission_issue(action='ec2:DescribeVolumes'/'ec2:DescribeSnapshots'), RequestLimitExceeded -> warn, else warn; keep a trailing `except Exception` for the truly unexpected. Mirror get_unattached_volumes.

#### 🟡 M2 · CloudWatch IOPS read failures (AccessDenied/Throttling) misreported as 'no data' and logger-only  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/ebs.py:60-62, 475-482`
- **Evidence:** _observed_peak_iops wraps the get_metric_statistics calls in `except Exception as e: logger.warning(...); return None` (ebs.py:60-62) — failures go to the module logger, never to ctx. The caller then treats None uniformly and emits per-volume `ctx.warn(f"Skipped IOPS rightsizing for {volume_id}: no CloudWatch IOPS data ...")` (ebs.py:476-482).
- **Impact:** A cloudwatch:GetMetricStatistics AccessDenied or Throttling/RateExceeded mass-suppresses the IOPS-rightsizing check across every io1/io2/gp3 volume while reporting it to the user as 'no data in the window' — a permission/throttle gap is misclassified as a benign empty-metric result and is never recorded as ctx.permission_issue. Real IOPS savings can be silently lost with no permission flag.
- **Fix:** In _observed_peak_iops catch ClientError separately: AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation -> ctx.permission_issue(action='cloudwatch:GetMetricStatistics'); Throttling/RequestLimitExceeded -> ctx.warn (once, not per-volume); return a sentinel distinct from genuine empty datapoints so the caller does not print 'no CloudWatch IOPS data' for a permission error.

#### 🟡 M3 · gp2->gp3 throughput parity not modelled — overstates net saving for large gp2 volumes  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/ebs_logic.py:127-140`
- **Evidence:** gp2_to_gp3_net_savings nets only IOPS parity (max(0, gp2_baseline_iops-3000)*gp3_iops_rate); the docstring states 'Throughput parity is not modelled'. The adapter AuditBasis records 'throughput parity not modelled' (adapters/ebs.py:193). gp2 volumes >170 GB deliver >125 MiB/s baseline; >=334 GB deliver 250 MiB/s. gp3's free throughput is 125 MiB/s, so matching parity needs (gp2_baseline_throughput-125) MiB/s provisioned at get_ebs_throughput_monthly_price (~$0.04/MiBps-mo, fallback FALLBACK_EBS_THROUGHPUT_MIBPS_MONTH).
- **Impact:** For a 334 GB gp2 (250 MiB/s): storage saving=334x$0.02=$6.68 but throughput parity=125x$0.04=$5.00, so true net ~$1.68 — overstated ~4x. For a 1,000 GB gp2: $20 storage saving vs $5 throughput -> ~33% overstated. Materially inflates the gp2 migration line for >170 GB volumes. (Conservative for workloads that do not actually need the throughput, hence a limitation not a hard bug.)
- **Fix:** Add a throughput-parity term mirroring the IOPS term: subtract max(0, gp2_baseline_throughput(size)-125)*get_ebs_throughput_monthly_price('gp3') from the net, where gp2_baseline_throughput = min(250, max(128, 0.25*size_in_GiB))-style curve; record it in AuditBasis.

#### 🟢 L1 · _drop_stale_delete_recs only re-validates 'delete' CoH actions  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/ebs.py:61-100`
- **Evidence:** delete_recs = [r for r in coh_recs if 'delete' in actionType.lower()] (ebs.py:71); only those volumes are live-checked for State=='available'. Non-delete actions (Rightsize/Upgrade) pass through unverified (ebs.py:90-99).
- **Impact:** A stale Cost Hub Rightsize/upgrade rec on a volume that has since been deleted or changed type is still counted at AWS's cached estimatedMonthlySavings — small over-count bounded by CoH data lag and limited to non-delete CoH recs.
- **Fix:** Optionally re-validate non-delete CoH recs (volume still exists and matches the rec's current configuration) before counting, or document the lag explicitly in the CoH card basis.

#### 🟢 L2 · get_unattached_volumes is invoked twice per scan (wasted describe calls + latent double-count surface)  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/ebs.py + services/adapters/ebs.py:ebs.py:557; adapters/ebs.py:161`
- **Evidence:** compute_ebs_checks seeds checks['unattached_volumes']=get_unattached_volumes(ctx,...) (ebs.py:557) and emits them with CheckCategory 'Unattached Volumes'; the adapter ALSO calls get_unattached_volumes separately (adapters/ebs.py:161). partition_enhanced_recs then discards the compute_ebs_checks copy via is_unattached_category->continue (ebs_logic.py:88-89).
- **Impact:** Duplicate describe_instances(stopped) + describe_volumes(available) pagination and duplicate _estimate_volume_cost work every scan; the discarded copy is dead weight and a latent double-count if the partition exclusion is ever changed. No current $ error.
- **Fix:** Stop seeding unattached_volumes inside compute_ebs_checks (it is owned by the adapter's own get_unattached_volumes call), or have the adapter reuse one result.

#### 🟢 L3 · CoH/CO findings lack a structured AuditBasis; CO card renders no dollar amount  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/ebs.py + reporter_phase_b.py:adapters/ebs.py:198-199; reporter_phase_b.py:409-437`
- **Evidence:** Only unattached (ebs.py:313-319), gp2 (adapters/ebs.py:187-194), and IOPS (ebs.py:520-527) recs carry an AuditBasis; CoH and CO counted recs do not. _render_ebs_compute_optimizer lists volumes by finding but prints no savings figure, although compute_optimizer_savings is added to the counted headline (adapters/ebs.py:199).
- **Impact:** CoH/CO counted dollars are not independently defensible from a structured basis in the JSON, and the CO card's contribution to the headline is invisible on the card (counted-but-not-shown, though totals still reconcile). Reporting completeness only.
- **Fix:** Attach an AuditBasis (source='Cost Hub'/'Compute Optimizer', lookback, savingsOpportunity path) to CoH/CO recs and render the per-finding $ in _render_ebs_compute_optimizer.

#### 🟢 L4 · Coverage gaps: st1/sc1 and gp3 throughput-only over-provisioning are not priced  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/ebs.py:464-472, 403-411`
- **Evidence:** _scan_over_provisioned_iops filters only io1/io2/gp3 and skips gp3 with iops<=3000 (ebs.py:464,472), so a gp3 volume over-provisioned on THROUGHPUT (>125 MiB/s) but with IOPS<=3000 yields no rec. st1/sc1 are excluded from gp2 migration and IOPS checks entirely (no path).
- **Impact:** Throughput-over-provisioned gp3 volumes and any st1/sc1 over-provisioning produce $0 — missed savings, not over-counts. Intentional/documented coverage scope.
- **Fix:** Add a gp3-throughput rightsizing check gated on CloudWatch VolumeThroughputPercentage/throughput bytes; document st1/sc1 exclusion in the EBS row of services/adapters/CLAUDE.md.

---

### EC2 — `services/adapters/ec2.py`

**Module identity:** EC2Module (services/adapters/ec2.py:73-191): key="ec2", cli_aliases=("ec2",), display_name="EC2", reads_fast_mode=True, requires_cloudwatch=True, required_clients()=("ec2","compute-optimizer","autoscaling") — all match the brief and the services/adapters/CLAUDE.md row. It is a 5-source aggregator: cost_optimization_hub (consumed via ctx.cost_hub_splits["ec2"], bucketed by scan_orchestrator type_map["Ec2Instance"]="ec2"), compute_optimizer + asg_compute_optimizer (inline via services.advisor), enhanced_checks + advanced_ec2_checks (heuristics in the shim services/ec2.py), plus extras.instance_count. EC2 HAS both AWS advisory sources (CoH + CO) and applies CoH>CO>heuristic + ASG-member dedup. Pricing strategy: OS/license-aware ctx.pricing_engine.get_ec2_hourly_price (region-correct via location filter, no pricing_multiplier double-apply); prev-gen/rightsizing/burstable use exact current→target hourly deltas; idle/dedicated/cron/batch/instance-store/nonprod use EC2_SAVINGS_FACTORS reduction factors; spot uses describe_spot_price_history. CLAUDE.md is accurate; no doc/code mismatch found.

**Verdict:** The EC2 adapter's exact-delta pricing path (prev-gen, rightsizing, burstable) is sound, region-correct (no pricing_multiplier double-apply), validated live, and correctly returns $0/no-finding when pricing is absent — no fabricated fallback dollars there. The cross-source CoH>CO>heuristic + ASG-member dedup and the CO opt-in placeholder->warn pattern are implemented. The material cost-fidelity risks are: (1) ASG-member dedup is silently disabled on a denied describe_auto_scaling_groups with no audit trace, enabling managed-instance double counting (H1); and (2) four advanced checks (cron/batch/instance-store/nonprod) count account-specific dollars from Name/Environment tags alone with no usage evidence, contrary to the codebase's own advisory discipline (H2). Secondary issues: a silently-dropped burstable check on throttling (M1), a non-deterministic single-AZ spot read feeding a counted saving (M2), asymmetric CoH/CO id normalization that breaks dedup if CoH returns ARN-form ids (M3), and an overstated 0.30 dedicated factor (M4).

**Pricing validation:** Validated live via AWS Pricing MCP (AmazonEC2, us-east-1, exact filters matching _fetch_ec2_price: operatingSystem=Linux, tenancy=Shared, capacityStatus=Used, preInstalledSw=NA, licenseModel='No License required'): m4.xlarge On-Demand = $0.2000/hr, m6i.xlarge = $0.1920/hr. This confirms the previous_generation EXACT-delta path is correct and conservative ((0.20-0.192)×730 ≈ $5.84/mo) and that the m4.→m6i. mapping is x86→x86 and genuinely cheaper. Reviewed all _PREVIOUS_GEN_TARGETS entries: every target is an Intel current-gen family (t3, m6i, r6i, c6i, i4i, d3, g5) — arch-safe (no Graviton), and g2.→g5. correctly self-suppresses (g5 is dearer -> delta<=0 -> no finding). The engine's _fetch_ec2_price pins licenseModel so Windows BYOL vs license-included is deterministic (no MaxResults=1 ambiguity). NOT independently validated and flagged needs-validation: the reduction FACTORS (idle 1.0, dedicated 0.30 [M4], cron 0.85, batch 0.75, instance-store 0.15, nonprod 0.64) — these are heuristic multipliers, not Pricing-API-derived rates, and 0.30 for dedicated appears overstated against the true Dedicated-Instances pricing model.

**Cost checks:**

| Check | Status | Trigger | Savings basis |
|---|---|---|---|
| Cost Optimization Hub EC2 rightsizing/migration | counted | ctx.cost_hub_splits['ec2'] rec passes _coh_is_renderable (not ebsVolume, not PurchaseReservedInstances, resourceId!='N/A') | flat float rec['estimatedMonthlySavings'] (AWS Cost Optimization Hub, region-priced upstream); summed at ec2.py:162 |
| Compute Optimizer EC2 instance rightsizing | counted | compute-optimizer get_ec2_instance_recommendations finding != 'optimized' (advisor.py:174-183) AND _co_instance_id not already covered by CoH | compute_optimizer_savings(rec) = recommendationOptions[rank1].savingsOpportunity.estimatedMonthlySavings.value (_savings.py:46-69); AWS-priced upstream, no multiplier |
| ASG Compute Optimizer instance rightsizing | counted | compute-optimizer get_auto_scaling_group_recommendations (advisor.py:349-372), normalized via _normalize_asg_co_rec | instanceRecommendationOptions[0].savingsOpportunity.estimatedMonthlySavings.value (advisor.py:497-500); flat, no dedup applied |
| idle_instances (enhanced) | counted | running, non-EKS, non-Spot; CloudWatch CPU avg<5% & max<10% & not network-active (>5MB/hr) — _classify_utilization='idle'; CW-gated, skipped in fast_mode | factor 1.0 = full on-demand monthly: hourly×730×1.0 (EC2_SAVINGS_FACTORS['Idle Instances'], ec2.py:23); priced by real OS+license via get_ec2_hourly_price |
| rightsizing_opportunities (enhanced) | counted | running, non-EKS, non-Spot; CW CPU avg<20% & max<40% & not memory-bound (>80%); _classify_utilization='rightsize'; CW-gated | EXACT delta (current_hourly - target_hourly)×730 where target=_one_size_down(type) (ec2.py:407); priced real OS+license; emits nothing if target unpriced or not cheaper |
| previous_generation (enhanced) | counted | instance_type startswith a _PREVIOUS_GEN_TARGETS prefix (ec2.py:88-106); structural, runs in fast_mode | EXACT delta (current - target)×730 where target=migration map (e.g. m4.→m6i.); validated live m4.xlarge $0.20 vs m6i.xlarge $0.192 → ~$5.84/mo; all maps x86→x86 |
| dedicated_hosts (enhanced) | counted | instance Placement.Tenancy=='dedicated'; structural, runs in fast_mode | factor 0.30 = hourly×730×0.30 (EC2_SAVINGS_FACTORS['Dedicated Hosts']); NOT an exact delta — see finding M4 |
| burstable_credits (enhanced) | counted | type startswith t2./t3./t4g. AND CW CPUCreditBalance min<10 AND avg CPU<=40% AND _one_size_down exists; CW-gated (Period=300) | EXACT delta (current - target)×730, target=_one_size_down (ec2.py:783-786); priced real OS+license |
| cron_job_instances (advanced) | counted | running, non-EKS, non-Spot; Name tag contains 'cron'/'scheduler' (ec2.py:995); NO usage metric | factor 0.85 = hourly×730×0.85 (EC2_SAVINGS_FACTORS['Cron Job Instances']); tag-only heuristic — see finding H2 |
| batch_job_instances (advanced) | counted | Name contains 'batch'/'job'/'worker'/'process' AND not 'web' AND not is_cron (mutually exclusive, ec2.py:996-1000); NO usage metric | factor 0.75 = hourly×730×0.75; tag-only heuristic — see finding H2 |
| underutilized_instance_store (advanced) | counted | family_token in _INSTANCE_STORE_FAMILIES AND Name lacks database/cache/storage/data/analytics (ec2.py:1037-1047); NO usage metric | factor 0.15 = hourly×730×0.15; config+name heuristic — see finding H2 |
| nonprod_scheduling (advanced) | counted | Environment/Env/Stage tag in {dev,test,staging,qa,uat,sandbox,demo,...} (ec2.py:1073); NO uptime metric (assumes current 24/7) | factor 0.64 = hourly×730×0.64 (~12h/weekday off-fraction); tag-only heuristic — see finding H2 |
| spot_migration (advanced) | counted | _is_spot_eligible(tags) explicit interruptible tag (ec2.py:1097) AND live on-demand>spot | (on_demand_hourly - spot_hourly)×730; spot via describe_spot_price_history(MaxResults=1) — non-deterministic single-AZ datapoint, see finding M2 |

**Findings:**

#### 🟠 H1 · _asg_member_instance_ids swallows AccessDenied and returns set(), silently disabling ASG-member dedup  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/ec2.py:48-70`
- **Evidence:** try: ... paginator=autoscaling.get_paginator('describe_auto_scaling_groups') ... return ids / except Exception: return set() — no ctx.warn or ctx.permission_issue. covered |= _asg_member_instance_ids(ctx) at line 136 is the ONLY thing keeping per-instance heuristics off ASG members.
- **Impact:** A denied/throttled describe_auto_scaling_groups returns an empty covered set with no audit trace, so every ASG member becomes eligible for the enhanced/advanced heuristics. That instance's savings can then be counted in BOTH the EC2 heuristic block AND the asg_compute_optimizer block (which is summed unconditionally at ec2.py:164) — double counting managed-instance dollars, and the operator never learns dedup was disabled.
- **Fix:** Wrap in botocore ClientError handling: classify Error.Code in {AccessDenied,UnauthorizedOperation} -> ctx.permission_issue(action='autoscaling:DescribeAutoScalingGroups'); any other error -> ctx.warn(service='ec2'); still return the partial/empty set but make the degradation visible (mirror get_ec2_instance_count at ec2.py:445-460).
- **Verifier (confirmed):** services/adapters/ec2.py:48-70: _asg_member_instance_ids ends in a bare `except Exception: return set()` (lines 69-70) with NO ctx.warn / record_aws_error / permission classification — unlike network.py which uses _aws_errors.record_aws_error per CLAUDE.md. Line 136 `covered |= _asg_member_instance_ids(ctx)` is the ONLY ASG-member dedup; no other dedup exists. get_enhanced_ec2_checks/get_advanced_ec2_checks iterate ALL running instances via describe_instances without filtering ASG members, so a denied/throttled describe_auto_scaling_groups yields an empty covered set, leaving every ASG member eligible for the heuristic blocks counted at adapter lines 165-166. Meanwhile asg_co_recs (from the SEPARATE compute-optimizer client, unaffected by an autoscaling:DescribeAutoScalingGroups denial) are summed unconditionally at line 164 — so the same managed compute is double-counted. The design comment at lines 134-135 ('never rightsize a managed instance individually') confirms dedup is the intended guard. The silent dedup-disable with no audit trace is unconditional once the except fires; the double-count is the worst-case realization. HIGH severity stands.

#### 🟠 H2 · Counted savings fabricated from Name/Environment tags with no usage evidence (cron 0.85, batch 0.75, instance-store 0.15, nonprod 0.64)  ·  `limitation` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/ec2.py:995-1093`
- **Evidence:** is_cron=any(k in name_l for k in ('cron','scheduler')); is_batch=...'batch','job','worker','process'; family_token in _INSTANCE_STORE_FAMILIES; _is_nonprod(tags). Each then appends a COUNTED rec with EstimatedSavings=f'${factor_savings:.2f}/month' using hourly×730×factor. No CloudWatch/utilization metric gates any of these four — savings derive purely from a tag/family string.
- **Impact:** These dollars feed best_by_instance and the EC2 headline total (ec2.py:165-166) yet assert, with no evidence, that an instance named '*cron*' can move to serverless and recover 85% of full cost, a '*batch*' instance 75% via Spot, a store-family instance 15%, and any non-prod instance 64% (assuming it runs 24/7 today, unverified). This is the catalogue's 'config-dimension-only savings -> fabricated $' pattern and is inconsistent with the codebase's own advisory discipline (Lambda ARM/excessive-memory and S3 cold-bytes are $0 advisory until metric-proven).
- **Fix:** Demote cron/batch/instance-store/nonprod to advisory (mark_zero_savings_advisory style Counted=False) unless corroborated by a usage signal — e.g. require the same CW idle/low-CPU evidence the idle/rightsizing checks already gather, or a CloudWatch uptime/schedule signal for nonprod — so only evidence-backed dollars are counted.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** services/ec2.py: EC2_SAVINGS_FACTORS (lines 30-36) defines Cron 0.85, Batch 0.75, Underutilized Instance Store 0.15, Non-Prod Scheduling 0.64. All four triggers are pure string/tag matches with no utilization evidence: is_cron on name substring (995), is_batch on name substring (996-1000), family_token in _INSTANCE_STORE_FAMILIES (1038), _is_nonprod(tags) on Environment/Stage tag values (47-52, 1073). Each calls _compute_ec2_savings WITHOUT target_type, hitting the factor branch that returns hourly*730*factor (line 417), and appends a rec carrying a real dollar EstimatedSavings (1014, 1031, 1064, 1089). The adapter counts these via parse_dollar_savings into best_by_instance and the headline total (adapter lines 149, 165-166) — they are NOT $0 advisory. get_advanced_ec2_checks docstring (946-948) confirms checks read only describe_instances fields and run identically in fast_mode, so no CloudWatch/metric gate exists. This is inconsistent with the codebase's metric-gated $0-advisory discipline for Lambda ARM/excessive-memory and S3 cold-bytes (CLAUDE.md). The nonprod rec text even asserts 'runs 24/7' unverified. Mechanism, factors, counting, and line range all check out; minor: EstimatedSavings f-strings carry descriptive suffixes rather than a bare '${x}/month', but value/factor/counting are exactly as described. HIGH severity stands.

#### 🟡 M1 · Burstable CPUCreditBalance non-permission failure logged via logger.debug only, not ctx.warn  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/ec2.py:803-814`
- **Evidence:** except ClientError as ce: if code in (Unauthorized,AccessDenied): ctx.permission_issue(...) else: logger.debug('Burstable credit lookup failed for %s: %s', instance_id, code); except Exception as burst_err: logger.debug(...). Contrast the sibling CPU lookup at lines 662-675 which calls ctx.warn on the same throttling/transient branch.
- **Impact:** A throttled or transient CPUCreditBalance read drops the entire burstable_credits finding (a real counted saving) for that instance with no entry in the scan's warnings — the operator cannot tell the check was silently skipped. Inconsistent silent-failure handling within the same function.
- **Fix:** Replace both logger.debug calls with ctx.warn(f'CloudWatch CPUCreditBalance lookup failed for {instance_id} ({code or type(err).__name__}) - burstable check skipped', service='ec2'), matching the CPU-lookup branch.

#### 🟡 M2 · Spot price read via describe_spot_price_history(MaxResults=1) is a non-deterministic single-AZ datapoint feeding a COUNTED saving  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/ec2.py:344-364, 1097-1118`
- **Evidence:** resp=ec2.describe_spot_price_history(InstanceTypes=[...], ProductDescriptions=[product], MaxResults=1); return float(history[0]['SpotPrice']). The API returns rows across all AZs newest-first; MaxResults=1 yields whichever AZ AWS lists first. spot_migration then counts (on_demand - spot)×730 (line 1101).
- **Impact:** The counted spot_migration dollar depends on an arbitrary AZ's latest spot quote rather than a window average or the AZ the instance runs in; the figure is non-reproducible between scans and can over- or under-state the saving. It is a real counted dollar (not advisory), so the headline EC2 total inherits the noise.
- **Fix:** Pass the instance's AvailabilityZone and request a multi-point window (e.g. StartTime=now-7d) then average, or pin AZ + take the max over the window for a conservative figure; alternatively demote spot_migration to advisory. Product-description mapping (_PRICING_OS_TO_SPOT_PRODUCT) is correct.

#### 🟡 M3 · Cross-source dedup id-normalization is asymmetric: CoH id not ARN-stripped while CO id is  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/ec2.py:37-45, 129-132`
- **Evidence:** _coh_instance_id returns rec.get('resourceId') verbatim (no split). _co_instance_id does arn.split('/')[-1]. covered is built from raw CoH resourceId (line 129); CO recs are dropped only if _co_instance_id (bare i-xxx) is in covered.
- **Impact:** If Cost Optimization Hub ever returns resourceId in ARN form (arn:aws:ec2:...:instance/i-xxx) rather than the bare instance id, the covered set holds ARNs while CO ids are bare i-xxx, so the CoH>CO dedup silently fails and the same instance is counted by both CoH (line 162) and CO (line 163) — 2x the saving. The dedup correctness hinges on an unverified assumption about CoH's resourceId format.
- **Fix:** Normalize both sides identically: define a single _normalize_instance_id that strips any '/' ARN suffix and apply it in _coh_instance_id too, so covered and CO ids are always comparable regardless of CoH's id form.

#### 🟡 M4 · Dedicated-tenancy saving counted at flat 0.30 of full on-demand cost, likely overstated vs real dedicated->shared delta  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/ec2.py:32, 707-723`
- **Evidence:** EC2_SAVINGS_FACTORS['Dedicated Hosts']=0.30; the dedicated_hosts check (Placement.Tenancy=='dedicated') calls _compute_ec2_savings without target_type -> factor mode -> hourly×730×0.30. For Dedicated *Instances*, the per-instance On-Demand rate equals the shared rate; the dedicated premium is largely a per-region $2/hr fee shared across all dedicated instances, not 30% of each instance's cost.
- **Impact:** Counts ~30% of each dedicated instance's full monthly cost as recoverable, which for Dedicated Instances overstates the true dedicated->shared saving (the catalogue's 'reduction factor instead of exact price delta; factors off 2-3x'). The figure is labelled (PricingBasis shows the factor) but still feeds the counted headline.
- **Fix:** Either derive an exact delta (price the same type at tenancy=Shared vs the dedicated rate via the Pricing API) or recompute the saving as the per-region dedicated fee amortized across dedicated instances; failing that, demote to advisory.

#### 🟢 L1 · _coh_is_renderable does not mirror two extra render-time skips in _render_ec2_cost_hub (counted-but-not-shown)  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/ec2.py:20-34`
- **Evidence:** Adapter _coh_is_renderable only drops ebsVolume/PurchaseReservedInstances/N-A recs and matches html_report_generator._filter_ec2_recommendations (425-436) byte-for-byte. But the renderer reporter_phase_b._render_ec2_cost_hub additionally `continue`s on `if 'actionType' not in rec` (line 83-84) and `if finding=='optimized'` (line 94-95) — skips the adapter does not apply before counting at ec2.py:162.
- **Impact:** A CoH EC2 rec lacking an actionType field, or carrying finding=='optimized', is counted toward the EC2 headline savings/count by the adapter but skipped by the renderer, leaving counted dollars with no visible card. Low impact in practice because CoH EC2 recs normally carry actionType and have no CO-style finding field.
- **Fix:** Add the same two predicates to _coh_is_renderable (return False when 'actionType' not in rec, or str(rec.get('finding','')).lower()=='optimized') so the source-level filter and the renderer stay in lockstep.

#### 🟢 L2 · Linux price fallback in _ec2_hourly can understate non-Linux (Windows/RHEL/SUSE) savings  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/ec2.py:317-333`
- **Evidence:** if hourly<=0.0 and os_name!='Linux': hourly=ctx.pricing_engine.get_ec2_hourly_price(instance_type,'Linux',quiet=quiet); priced_os='Linux'. For prev-gen/rightsizing/burstable deltas both current and target legs fall back to Linux when the OS-specific SKU misses.
- **Impact:** When a Windows SKU lookup misses, the saving is computed on the (cheaper) Linux rate, understating the real Windows recovery (Windows ~2x Linux). This is conservative (never fabricates or overstates a dollar) and PricingBasis records priced_os='Linux', so it is a precision/disclosure gap rather than a counted-dollar error.
- **Fix:** On a non-Linux miss, either ctx.warn that the OS-specific rate was unavailable and the figure is a Linux lower bound, or skip the finding; document that the Linux fallback is a lower bound in PricingBasis.

#### 🟢 L3 · get_auto_scaling_checks oversized_instances uses 0.40 factor, no >0 guard (emits $0 cards), and skips EKS-ASG/Spot exclusion  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/ec2.py:847-936`
- **Evidence:** asg_node_savings,_=_compute_ec2_savings(ctx,instance_type,'Rightsizing Opportunities') (no target_type -> factor 0.40, no os/license); then checks['oversized_instances'].append({...}) with NO `if asg_node_savings>0` guard. The helper _is_eks_nodegroup_asg exists but is not applied here; Spot launch templates are not excluded.
- **Impact:** Consumed only by the network adapter, which forces this whole block to advisory via _mark_advisory (network.py:121-124) and marks $0 recs Counted=False (mark_zero_savings_advisory, network.py:129) — so it never reaches a counted total. Residual issues are cosmetic: $0.00/month advisory cards can render, the 0.40 factor is a heuristic inconsistent with EC2's exact-delta approach, and EKS/Spot ASGs are not excluded.
- **Fix:** Add an `if asg_node_savings>0` guard before appending (suppress $0 cards), apply _is_eks_nodegroup_asg to skip EKS node groups, and either compute an exact one-size-down delta or keep it explicitly advisory.

#### 🟢 L4 · _INSTANCE_STORE_FAMILIES omits newest store-equipped families (coverage gap)  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/ec2.py:112-121`
- **Evidence:** Frozenset covers m5d/c5d/r5d/i3/i3en/i4i/im4gn/is4gen/d2/d3/z1d/x1/x2idn etc. (family-token match, correctly not substring), but lacks newer NVMe-store families such as i7ie, i8g, and trn/inf local-store variants.
- **Impact:** Instances on the newest store-bearing families are never evaluated for the underutilized_instance_store check, so a legitimate (heuristic) saving is missed. No incorrect dollar is produced — pure coverage shortfall.
- **Fix:** Refresh the family set against the current AWS instance-store family list (add i7ie, i8g, and any new *d suffix families) and add a periodic-review note.

---

### EKS — `services/adapters/eks.py`

**Module identity:** Module key is `eks_cost` (NOT `eks`); `display_name="EKS Cost Visibility"`; `cli_aliases=("eks_cost","eks_cost_visibility","eks")`. Single-file adapter (`services/adapters/eks.py`, `EksCostModule`) — no `services/eks.py` shim, no `eks_logic.py`. Required clients `("eks","ec2","cloudwatch")` but CloudWatch is never used (idle corroboration opportunity left on the table) and EC2 client is unused (EC2 pricing comes via `ctx.pricing_engine`, not a client). `requires_cloudwatch=False`, `reads_fast_mode=True` (only flips the Fargate note text). Cost Optimization Hub APPLIES: `type_map["EksCluster"]="eks_cost"` and `_HUB_SERVICES` contains `"eks_cost"` (scan_orchestrator.py:65,96) — the bucket-name==key invariant holds, so EKS CoH recs are not dropped. Compute Optimizer does NOT apply (node instances are owned by the EC2 adapter). Pricing strategy: live `PricingEngine.get_eks_control_plane_hourly` (AmazonEKS perCluster SKU, fallback 0.10×multiplier) and `get_eks_extended_support_hourly` (extendedSupport SKU, fallback 0.50×multiplier), plus `get_ec2_hourly_price` for advisory node-group magnitude.

**Verdict:** EKS counted dollars are structurally small and the two material rates ($0.10/hr control plane, $0.50/hr Extended Support) are accurate and region-scaled correctly against the live Pricing API. The cost-fidelity risks are not the rates but the plumbing: (1) CoH EksCluster recs are counted with no dedup against the adapter's own idle/extended/failed cluster findings → real double-count (H1); (2) the idle test trusts only managed node groups + Fargate, so Karpenter/self-managed clusters are fabricated as idle and told to delete (H2, safety); (3) the reporter sums Counted=False node-group advisories into the per-card savings, desyncing rendered from counted and double-counting Spot+Graviton alternatives (H3). Lower-severity items: a silent CoH-drop with no trace (M1), Linux-only/desiredSize node-group pricing (M2), missing failed_cluster audit_basis (L1), and a doc gap (L3). Fargate $0 advisory and scaled-to-zero skips are correct; extended_support+idle co-firing is legitimately additive (delete removes both), not a double-count.

**Pricing validation:** Validated LIVE via AWS Pricing MCP (us-east-1, publication 2026-06-26): (1) EKS control plane — AmazonEKS, operation=CreateOperation, usagetype USE1-AmazonEKS-Hours:perCluster, SKU ZYWMR684YSMFHWEU = $0.10000/hr → ~$73/mo. Code FALLBACK_EKS_CONTROL_PLANE_HOURLY=0.10 MATCHES; engine path filters operation+usagetype-suffix so the Outposts perCluster SKU (USE1-AmazonEKS-Local-Outposts-Hours:perCluster) is correctly excluded (no MaxResults=1 nondeterminism). (2) EKS Extended Support — AmazonEKS, operation=ExtendedSupport, usagetype USE1-AmazonEKS-Hours:extendedSupport, SKU M7977BSVFGDUJZ67 = $0.50000/hr → ~$365/mo. Code FALLBACK_EKS_EXTENDED_SUPPORT_HOURLY=0.50 MATCHES — the brief's suspicion of a stale $0.60/hr is NOT confirmed for us-east-1; fallback is current. Both fallbacks are region-scaled once via × _fallback_multiplier on the fallback path with no double-multiply on the engine path. Node-group EC2 hourly price (advisory) is engine-resolved per type and was not individually validated (advisory, Counted=False); its OS-default-Linux flaw is M2.

**Cost checks:**

| Check | Status | Trigger | Savings basis |
|---|---|---|---|
| extended_support (counted) | counted | cluster.upgradePolicy.supportType == "EXTENDED" AND extended_support_rate > 0 (eks.py:236-237) | monthly_savings = extended_support_rate × 730 (HOURS_PER_MONTH). Rate from PricingEngine.get_eks_extended_support_hourly (AmazonEKS, operation=ExtendedSupport, usagetype suffix AmazonEKS-Hours:extendedSupport); fallback FALLBACK_EKS_EXTENDED_SUPPORT_HOURLY=0.50 × _fallback_multiplier. Live us-east-1 = $0.50/hr (SKU M7977BSVFGDUJZ67) → ~$365/mo. Carries audit_basis. |
| idle_cluster (counted) | counted | status=="ACTIVE" AND is_idle (ng_count==0 AND fp_count==0) AND monthly_control_plane>0 (eks.py:265) | monthly_savings = control_plane_rate × 730.
