Rate from get_eks_control_plane_hourly (AmazonEKS perCluster SKU, operation=CreateOperation); fallback FALLBACK_EKS_CONTROL_PLANE_HOURLY=0.10 × _fallback_multiplier. Live us-east-1 = $0.10/hr (SKU ZYWMR684YSMFHWEU) → ~$73/mo. Carries audit_basis. |
| failed_cluster (counted) | counted | status=="FAILED" AND monthly_control_plane>0 (eks.py:288) | monthly_savings = control_plane_rate × 730 (same $0.10/hr → ~$73/mo). NO audit_basis attached (inconsistent with the other two counted checks). |
| cost_hub (counted) | counted | ctx.cost_hub_splits["eks_cost"] is non-empty (EksCluster CoH recs) (eks.py:516-520) | monthly_savings = float(rec["estimatedMonthlySavings"]) flat from AWS Cost Optimization Hub. No Counted key → defaults to counted via r.get("Counted", True). No normalization/dedup vs cluster_costs. |
| node_group Spot (advisory) | advisory | capacityType != "SPOT" AND ng_monthly>0 (eks.py:362) | monthly_savings = ng_monthly × SPOT_SAVINGS_FACTOR(0.70); ng_monthly = get_ec2_hourly_price(instanceTypes[0], os=Linux default) × 730 × desiredSize. Counted=False (dollars excluded from headline). Reduction factor, not exact on-demand−Spot delta. |
| node_group Graviton (advisory) | advisory | instance_types AND not _is_graviton(instanceTypes[0]) AND ng_monthly>0 (eks.py:383) | monthly_savings = ng_monthly × GRAVITON_SAVINGS_FACTOR(0.20). Counted=False. Reduction factor on the (Linux-priced) node-group on-demand cost, not exact x86→Graviton delta. |
| fargate presence (advisory) | advisory | list_fargate_profiles returns ≥1 profile (eks.py:463) | monthly_savings = 0.0, Counted=False. Pure presence note; pod cost not quantified (needs Container Insights). Correctly $0 advisory. |
| addon inventory (no findings) | advisory | list_addons returns add-ons (eks.py:496-506) | n/a — inventory only; _analyze_addons always returns [] recs (count only). Single non-paginated call (acceptable, counts are small). |

**Findings:**

#### 🟠 H1 · No CoH-vs-cluster dedup — same cluster counted by Cost Optimization Hub AND a heuristic cluster finding  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/eks.py:508-535 (build) / 145-153 (count)`
- **Evidence:** _build_cost_hub_recs emits CoH EksCluster recs with NO Counted key (so r.get("Counted", True) → counted) and NO normalization/dedup against cluster_costs: `recs.append({"resource_id": rec.get("recommendationId",...), "check_type":"cost_hub", "monthly_savings": round(monthly_savings,2), ...})`. total_savings = sum(monthly_savings for r if r.get("Counted", True)) sums both the CoH rec and any idle_cluster/extended_support rec for the same cluster.
- **Impact:** Double-counts real headline dollars whenever CoH returns an EksCluster recommendation for a cluster the adapter already flagged (idle/extended/failed). Unlike EC2/EBS/Lambda there is NO authority dedup (CoH > heuristic) by normalized cluster name.
- **Fix:** Normalize the cluster name from each CoH rec (resourceId/recommendationSummary) and drop the heuristic cluster_costs rec for the same cluster (authority CoH > heuristic), or vice-versa, before summing — mirror the EC2/EBS normalized-id dedup.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified at cited lines. _build_cost_hub_recs (eks.py:508-535) appends CoH recs with resource_id=rec.get('recommendationId') and NO 'Counted' key, so total_savings (151-153) counts them via r.get('Counted', True)->True. core/scan_orchestrator.py:96 explicitly maps CoH currentResourceType 'EksCluster' -> 'eks_cost' bucket (and the comment at 61-65 confirms the authors expect EksCluster recs to flow here), so these recs really do reach _build_cost_hub_recs. There is NO normalization or cross-reference between the CoH rec (resource_id=recommendationId) and the heuristic cluster_costs recs (resource_id=cluster name, set at 241/268/291) — no dedup, no authority precedence. This contrasts with peer adapters: per services/adapters/CLAUDE.md, ec2 has 'Cross-source + ASG-member dedup', lambda has 'Cross-source dedup ... authority CoH > CO > enhanced', rds has 'Cross-source dedup + RI/backup demotion'. So the 'no authority dedup (CoH > heuristic) by normalized cluster name' claim is accurate. Caveat (not a refutation): the headline double-count only materializes when CoH actually emits an EksCluster rec whose dollars overlap a cluster the heuristic also flagged (idle/extended/failed) — most concretely an idle-cluster overlap; a non-overlapping CoH rec would be a legitimate separate saving. The structural gap (counted + un-deduped) is real and verifiable; the magnitude is data-dependent. HIGH is defensible given it can silently inflate the counted headline.

#### 🟠 H2 · Idle-cluster false positive: Karpenter/self-managed clusters flagged idle → counts full control plane + recommends deleting a live cluster  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/eks.py:124-138 (is_idle) / 262-287 (idle rec)`
- **Evidence:** is_idle=(ng_count==0 and fp_count==0) is derived ONLY from list_nodegroups + list_fargate_profiles. Self-managed/Karpenter nodes are invisible to those APIs. The idle branch then counts monthly_control_plane (=control_plane_rate×730) as recoverable and recommends "Delete or consolidate the cluster". audit_basis only asserts the assumption ("no self-managed/Karpenter nodes") with no corroboration.
- **Impact:** Safety + fabricated dollars: a busy Karpenter cluster with 0 managed node groups is counted ~$73/mo recoverable and told to delete — a destructive recommendation on a production cluster. The required cloudwatch/ec2 clients are available but unused for corroboration.
- **Fix:** Before counting idle, corroborate zero capacity via EC2 instances tagged kubernetes.io/cluster/<name>=owned (ec2 client already required) or CloudWatch cluster_node_count; if any nodes are found, suppress or demote the idle rec to Counted=False advisory.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified. is_idle is computed at eks.py:137 as (ng_count == 0 and fp_count == 0), where ng_count comes only from list_nodegroups (_analyze_node_groups, 326-329) and fp_count only from list_fargate_profiles (_analyze_fargate, 448-451). The idle branch (265-287) requires status=='ACTIVE' and is_idle, then counts monthly_control_plane = control_plane_rate*730 (~$73/mo at $0.10/hr) as recoverable and emits recommended_value 'Delete or consolidate the cluster'. audit_basis only asserts the assumption ('no self-managed/Karpenter nodes') with evidence limited to 'describe APIs' — no corroboration. Confirmed that ec2/cloudwatch are declared in required_clients (79) but never fetched: the only ctx.client call is eks = ctx.client('eks') (93), and requires_cloudwatch=False (74). Karpenter manages bare EC2 instances and self-managed node groups join via ASG/userdata — both invisible to list_nodegroups/list_fargate_profiles — so a busy production cluster with 0 managed node groups and 0 Fargate profiles is flagged idle, counted ~$73/mo, and given destructive delete advice. Real safety + fabricated-dollar issue; HIGH appropriate.

#### 🟠 H3 · Reporter sums advisory (Counted=False) dollars into per-category card savings — rendered savings desync from counted headline and double-counts Spot+Graviton alternatives  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `reporter_phase_b.py:2034-2056`
- **Evidence:** _render_eks_source does `total_savings = sum(r.get("monthly_savings", 0.0) for r in recs)` with NO Counted filter, then `if total_savings > 0: ...Estimated Monthly Savings: ${total_savings:.2f}` and per line `if savings > 0: line += f" (${savings:.2f}/month)"`. Node-group Spot ($ng×0.70) and Graviton ($ng×0.20) recs carry real monthly_savings but Counted=False, so the "Node Group Optimization" card displays e.g. $900 on a $1000 node group while the headline (eks.py:151-153) correctly excludes them.
- **Impact:** The per-tab card shows advisory dollars as if they were savings (rendered != counted), and adds Spot+Graviton — two mutually-exclusive alternatives — into one card total, inflating visible savings ~0.90× node cost that is neither counted nor simultaneously achievable.
- **Fix:** In _render_eks_source compute the category total from Counted!=False recs only (and/or suppress the per-line $ for Counted=False recs, labelling them 'advisory'), so the card total reconciles with the headline.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified at reporter_phase_b.py:2034-2056. _render_eks_source computes total_savings = sum(r.get('monthly_savings', 0.0) for r in recs) with NO Counted filter (2036); grep confirms the substring 'Counted' appears 0 times in the entire reporter, so advisory recs are never stripped upstream. It then renders 'Estimated Monthly Savings: ${total_savings:.2f}' (2040-2041) and per-line '(${savings:.2f}/month)' for any savings>0 (2052-2054). In eks.py the node-group Spot rec (monthly_savings = ng_monthly*0.70, line 363/371) and Graviton rec (ng_monthly*0.20, line 384/392) both carry real positive monthly_savings but Counted=False (372/393), and both use check_category 'Node Group Optimization'. _render_eks_source groups by check_category (2029-2032), so a single on-demand x86 node group contributes 0.70+0.20 = 0.90x node cost into one card total (the $900-on-$1000 example checks out), while the headline total_savings in eks.py (151-153) correctly excludes them via the Counted filter. The handler is live: PHASE_B_HANDLERS registers ('eks_cost','node_group_optimization') -> _render_eks_source (2494) and HTMLReportGenerator passes the SourceBlock recommendations unfiltered. Both the rendered!=counted desync and the summing of two mutually-exclusive alternatives (Spot vs Graviton) are real. This is a per-tab display inflation, not a counted-headline error (the finding itself states rendered!=counted); mechanism and lines accurate, HIGH defensible.

#### 🟡 M1 · _build_cost_hub_recs silently drops all EKS CoH recs on any exception with no ctx trace  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/eks.py:514-518`
- **Evidence:** `try: hub_recs = ctx.cost_hub_splits.get("eks_cost", []) except Exception: return recs` — a missing ctx.cost_hub_splits attribute or malformed split returns [] with no ctx.warn/ctx.permission_issue.
- **Impact:** Silent loss of COUNTED CoH savings (CoH recs are counted). If prefetch did not populate cost_hub_splits, every EKS CoH dollar vanishes with no warning in the report's silent-failure trail.
- **Fix:** On except, call ctx.warn(f"EKS Cost Hub split read failed: {e}", "eks_cost") before returning [] so the drop is recorded.

#### 🟡 M2 · Node-group advisory priced as Linux (no OS arg) and on desiredSize × first instance type only  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/eks.py:415-427 / 339-353`
- **Evidence:** _node_group_monthly_cost calls `ctx.pricing_engine.get_ec2_hourly_price(instance_types[0], quiet=True)`; get_ec2_hourly_price(instance_type, os="Linux", ...) defaults os to Linux (pricing_engine.py:682-688). describe_nodegroup's amiType (WINDOWS_*/BOTTLEROCKET_*/AL2_*) is never read; only instanceTypes[0] and scalingConfig.desiredSize are used.
- **Impact:** Advisory magnitude only (Counted=False, no headline impact) but a Windows/BYOL node group is materially underpriced (Windows license ≫ Linux), multi-type groups use only the first type, and desiredSize ≠ running instance count — the displayed $ (and the Spot/Graviton % of it) misleads.
- **Fix:** Derive os from ng.amiType (WINDOWS_* → "Windows") and pass it to get_ec2_hourly_price; note in the reason that the basis is desiredSize × first instance type (not actual running capacity).

#### 🟢 L1 · failed_cluster counted finding lacks audit_basis (inconsistent with extended_support/idle_cluster)  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/eks.py:288-303`
- **Evidence:** The FAILED branch appends a counted rec (monthly_savings=control_plane_rate×730) with reason but NO audit_basis key, whereas extended_support (248-253) and idle_cluster (275-281) both carry a structured audit_basis.
- **Impact:** Inconsistent evidence trail on a counted dollar; scan_doctor / reviewers cannot verify the rate/unit/formula for failed_cluster.
- **Fix:** Add audit_basis={"rate": control_plane_rate, "unit": "USD/cluster-hour", "formula": f"{control_plane_rate} x {HOURS_PER_MONTH} hr", "evidence": "cluster.status == FAILED"}.

#### 🟢 L2 · _node_group_monthly_cost except → 0.0 silently drops the advisory with no trace  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/eks.py:423-426`
- **Evidence:** `try: hourly = ctx.pricing_engine.get_ec2_hourly_price(...) except Exception: return 0.0`. ng_monthly==0 then hits the `if ng_monthly <= 0: continue` skip (line 358-359).
- **Impact:** Advisory only (no counted dollars), but a pricing error makes a node group look free and silently removes its Spot/Graviton visibility row with no ctx.warn — the very visibility the advisory exists to provide.
- **Fix:** Let the lookup miss be observable (the engine already logs); optionally ctx.warn on the except so a systematic pricing outage that hides node-group advisories is recorded.

#### 🟢 L3 · services/adapters/CLAUDE.md has no eks.py row despite EKS using live pricing  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/CLAUDE.md:Live Pricing table (the 19-adapter list)`
- **Evidence:** The 'Live Pricing (19 adapters)' table lists ec2…elasticache but omits eks.py, even though eks.py calls live PricingEngine methods (get_eks_control_plane_hourly, get_eks_extended_support_hourly, get_ec2_hourly_price) and consumes Cost Hub via cost_hub_splits["eks_cost"].
- **Impact:** Doc/code mismatch (audit dimension 0): the EKS adapter's pricing strategy, counted-vs-advisory split, CoH consumption, and idle/extended-support checks are undocumented in the adapter registry.
- **Fix:** Add an eks.py row: live control-plane + Extended-Support pricing, node-group/Fargate advisory (Counted=False), consumes Cost Hub (cost_hub_splits["eks_cost"]), no Compute Optimizer.

#### 🟢 L4 · Spot AND Graviton advisory both emitted per node group — latent double-count if Counted is ever flipped  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/eks.py:361-401`
- **Evidence:** For one ON_DEMAND x86 node group, both the Spot rec (×0.70) and the Graviton rec (×0.20) are appended; both Counted=False today so they do not sum into the headline, but they are mutually-exclusive alternatives.
- **Impact:** Safe in the headline today; latent — flipping Counted=True (or any future code that counts node_group recs) would add 0.90× node cost twice for one resource. Also feeds the H3 card-render inflation now.
- **Fix:** Keep them advisory and mutually-exclusive; if ever counted, pick the larger single alternative (max of Spot/Graviton), never the sum, per node group.

---

### ElastiCache — `services/adapters/elasticache.py`

**Module identity:** key="elasticache", cli_aliases=("elasticache",), display_name="ElastiCache", required_clients()=("elasticache","cloudwatch"), requires_cloudwatch=True, and (a bug) reads_fast_mode is NOT declared (defaults False in services/_base.py:25). Thin adapter delegates all check logic to the legacy shim services/elasticache.py:get_enhanced_elasticache_checks(ctx); there is no _logic.py. Pricing strategy: per-node on-demand monthly via ctx.pricing_engine.get_instance_monthly_price("AmazonElastiCache", node_type) (region-correct, NOT re-multiplied by pricing_multiplier — correct) × NumNodes × a per-CheckCategory flat discount rate. CoH applicability: bucket ctx.cost_hub_splits["elasticache"] IS populated by the orchestrator (elasticache in _HUB_SERVICES, ElastiCacheCluster→elasticache type_map) but is consumed by NO adapter (orphan). Compute Optimizer does NOT cover ElastiCache (not applicable). CloudWatch CPUUtilization (AWS/ElastiCache) read by the shim. Emits a single SourceBlock "enhanced_checks" → reporter handler _render_elasticache_enhanced_checks (reporter_phase_b.py:1052); Phase B, not in _PHASE_B_SKIP_PER_REC.

**Verdict:** The elasticache adapter has two CRITICAL cost-fidelity defects: (C1) the populated ctx.cost_hub_splits["elasticache"] CoH bucket is consumed by no adapter, so every AWS-computed ElastiCache CoH saving is silently dropped; and (C2) the shared node-price lookup uses MaxResults=1 with no usagetype/cacheEngine filter, which live data shows returns Extended-Support/SyncDurability/wrong-engine SKUs (e.g. $0.33 vs the true $0.206/hr), mis-rating every counted figure. On top of that, Graviton/Underutilized recs omit NumNodes (priced for 1 node, distorting per-cluster dedup), the Graviton 0.20 factor overstates the real ~4.6% node delta by ~4x, fast_mode is not honored, and a CloudWatch failure silently drops the only evidence-gated lever. The Valkey 0.20 rate is the one number that validates exactly. Counted==rendered holds mechanically, but the renderer shows percentage strings instead of the counted dollars (desync).

**Pricing validation:** Validated LIVE via AWS Pricing MCP (AmazonElastiCache, us-east-1, publicationDate 2026-06-25). instanceType attribute values DO carry the `cache.` prefix (e.g. cache.r6g.large) — so the adapter passing cache.r6g.large is correct and the brief's prefix-stripping worry is REFUTED (not a bug). cacheEngine has three values: Memcached, Redis, Valkey. For cache.r6g.large the API returns 6 OnDemand SKUs: Redis NodeUsage $0.206/hr (true rate), Memcached NodeUsage $0.206/hr, Valkey NodeUsage $0.1648/hr, Redis ExtendedSupportYr3 $0.33/hr, Redis ExtendedSupportYr1_Yr2 $0.165/hr, Valkey SyncDurability $0.0297/hr — confirming the MaxResults=1 non-deterministic-SKU bug (C2). Valkey $0.1648 = exactly 20% under Redis $0.206 -> the Valkey 0.20 rate is ACCURATE. Graviton check: cache.r5.large Redis NodeUsage $0.216/hr vs cache.r6g.large Redis NodeUsage $0.206/hr = ~4.6% real node-price delta, refuting the counted 0.20 (H2). Region scaling confirmed correct by code inspection (get_instance_monthly_price uses region display name, not re-multiplied by pricing_multiplier; pricing_engine=None -> 0.0 -> advisory, no us-east-1 leakage) — no live call needed.

**Cost checks:**

| Check | Status | Trigger | Savings basis |
|---|---|---|---|
| Valkey Migration (valkey_migration) | counted | Cluster with status=='available' and engine.lower()=='redis' (services/elasticache.py:73). One rec per CacheCluster (Redis replication-group members each appear as a CacheCluster). | adapter: monthly_node = get_instance_monthly_price('AmazonElastiCache', node_type); EstimatedMonthlySavings = round(monthly_node * NumNodes * 0.20, 2) (elasticache.py:46-62). Constant rate=0.20. Pricing source: AWS Pricing API node on-demand rate. Live-validated: Redis cache.r6g.large NodeUsage=$0.206/hr*730=$150.38/mo; Valkey NodeUsage=$0.1648/hr = exactly 20% under Redis -> the 0.20 factor is ACCURATE. BUT the base node rate is mis-selected (see C2: MaxResults=1 returns ExtendedSupport/SyncDurability/wrong-engine SKU). |
| Graviton Migration (graviton_migration) | counted | Cluster available and node_type does NOT start with cache.{m7g,r7g,m6g,r6g,c7g,c6g,t4g} (services/elasticache.py:93-104). | adapter: monthly_node * NumNodes * 0.20 (elasticache.py:46-62). Rate constant=0.20 (flat). Rec dict OMITS NumNodes (elasticache.py:96-104) so num_nodes defaults to 1 (elasticache.py:57). Live-validated: real x86->Graviton node-price delta r5.large Redis $0.216 -> r6g.large Redis $0.206 = ~4.6%, NOT 20%. The shim string says '20-40% price-performance' (a perf-per-dollar metric, not a cost reduction). 0.20 overstates the realizable same-node-count saving ~4x. |
| Reserved Nodes Opportunity (reserved_nodes) | advisory | Cluster available and NumCacheNodes >= 2 (services/elasticache.py:109). Note: Redis replication-group members report NumCacheNodes==1, so this fires almost only for Memcached. | Forced advisory: adapter sets Counted=False when 'Reserved' in category (elasticache.py:63-64). No key in rate_by_category -> rate 0.0 -> EstimatedMonthlySavings=0 regardless. Raw EstimatedSavings string '30-60% vs On-Demand'. Real RI buy lives in commitment_analysis (CoH ElastiCacheReservedInstances->commitment_analysis, orchestrator:106). No double-counted RI dollar. |
| Underutilized Cluster (underutilized_clusters) | counted | CloudWatch AWS/ElastiCache CPUUtilization Average over 14d < LOW_CPU_THRESHOLD(20), excluding already-smallest sizes per SMALLEST_SIZES (services/elasticache.py:121-158). Evidence-gated. | adapter: monthly_node * NumNodes * 0.30 (elasticache.py:47,60-62). Rate constant=0.30 (flat reduction factor, NOT exact current->one-size-down node-price delta). Rec dict OMITS NumNodes (elasticache.py:149-158) so num_nodes defaults to 1 -> a multi-node cluster's downsize saving is priced for a single node. Pricing source: AWS Pricing API node rate (subject to C2 SKU mis-selection). |
| Old engine versions (old_engine_versions) | advisory | None — dead list key initialized (services/elasticache.py:49) but nothing is ever appended (comment elasticache.py:106-107). Confirmed empty. | n/a — emits no recs; contributes $0 and no rec to the count. |

**Findings:**

#### 🔴 C1 · Cost Optimization Hub bucket ctx.cost_hub_splits["elasticache"] is populated but consumed by NO adapter — every ElastiCache CoH recommendation is silently dropped  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/elasticache.py + core/scan_orchestrator.py:elasticache.py:26-95 (scan never references cost_hub_splits); scan_orchestrator.py:57,92,135-142`
- **Evidence:** Orchestrator populates the bucket: _HUB_SERVICES includes "elasticache" (scan_orchestrator.py:57) and type_map["ElastiCacheCluster"]="elasticache" (line 92), so splits["elasticache"] is filled on any scan selecting elasticache. Repo-wide grep `grep -rn cost_hub_splits --include=*.py | grep -i elasticache` returns NOTHING — only ec2/ebs/rds/lambda/dynamodb/containers/eks_cost/commitment_analysis consume their buckets. ElasticacheModule.scan (elasticache.py:39-95) only calls get_enhanced_elasticache_checks and never reads the bucket. The 'no service bucket' warning (scan_orchestrator.py:135-142) fires ONLY for unbucketed types, never for a populated-but-unconsumed bucket, so the drop is 100% silent.
- **Impact:** All AWS-computed, account-specific ElastiCache CoH rightsizing/savings are dropped from the report with no warning. Highest-value coverage gap for this adapter (lost real dollars, not an estimate). Known prior-audit orphan (MEMORY.md 'Orphaned Cost Hub buckets').
- **Fix:** Either (a) consume ctx.cost_hub_splits.get("elasticache", []) in scan() mirroring rds.py:108-119 — render CoH recs and dedup against heuristic levers by normalized cluster id with authority CoH > heuristic (demote duplicated Valkey/Graviton/Underutilized heuristics to Counted=False); or (b) remove "elasticache" from _HUB_SERVICES and the ElastiCacheCluster type_map entry so the drop becomes an explicit unbucketed-type warning. Option (a) preferred (recovers real savings).
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified exactly as described. scan_orchestrator.py:57 includes "elasticache" in _HUB_SERVICES; line 92 maps type_map["ElastiCacheCluster"]="elasticache"; lines 85/124-128 populate splits["elasticache"] whenever elasticache is in `selected`. The bucket has NO consumer: `grep cost_hub_splits` shows readers only for ec2, lambda, ebs, rds, dynamodb, containers, eks_cost, commitment_analysis. The only adapter that iterated ALL splits via .values() (services/adapters/cost_optimization_hub.py) is explicitly retired from ALL_MODULES (services/__init__.py:71), so it never runs. ElasticacheModule.scan (services/adapters/elasticache.py:39-95) only calls get_enhanced_elasticache_checks and never references ctx.cost_hub_splits. The dropped-type warning (scan_orchestrator.py:135-142) fires only for types absent from type_map; ElastiCacheCluster IS in type_map, so it is bucketed-then-orphaned with zero warning. Net: account-specific CoH ElastiCacheCluster rightsizing recs are silently dropped. (Scope note: ElastiCacheReservedInstances rows route to commitment_analysis, which IS consumed, so only the cluster-rightsizing CoH recs are lost — consistent with the finding's 'rightsizing/savings' framing.)

#### 🔴 C2 · Node price is mis-rated: MaxResults=1 with no usagetype/cacheEngine filter returns a non-NodeUsage / wrong-engine SKU, so every counted ElastiCache dollar is wrong  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `core/pricing_engine.py:1290-1298 (_fetch_generic_instance_price) and 1598-1611 (_call_pricing_api)`
- **Evidence:** _fetch_generic_instance_price filters only on instanceType + location (pricing_engine.py:1291-1294); _call_pricing_api requests MaxResults=1 and returns _extract_usd(PriceList[0]) (pricing_engine.py:1598-1611). Live AWS Pricing API (us-east-1, cache.r6g.large, pub 2026-06-25) returns SIX OnDemand SKUs for that instanceType: Redis ExtendedSupportYr3 $0.33/hr, Redis ExtendedSupportYr1_Yr2 $0.165/hr, Valkey NodeUsage $0.1648/hr, Valkey SyncDurability $0.0297/hr, Memcached NodeUsage $0.206/hr, and the TRUE Redis NodeUsage $0.206/hr. The adapter passes cache.r6g.large (the cache. prefix IS correct — instanceType attribute values include it, so the prefix is NOT a bug), but MaxResults=1 grabs PriceList[0] = the $0.33 Extended-Support SKU in this snapshot — 1.6x the real $0.206 node rate. Ordering is not guaranteed, so the result is non-deterministic and can also land on the $0.0297 SyncDurability surcharge (~0.14x) or the wrong engine (Valkey $0.1648 for a Redis cluster).
- **Impact:** Mis-rates the base node price feeding EVERY counted lever (Valkey, Graviton, Underutilized). In the validated snapshot the Redis cache.r6g.large monthly is reported as $0.33*730=$240.90 instead of $0.206*730=$150.38 (+60%); other SKU draws undercount by up to ~86%. Counted savings are fabricated/mis-rated across the whole adapter.
- **Fix:** For the ElastiCache path select the base node SKU deterministically: add filters usagetype CONTAINS 'NodeUsage' AND NOT ExtendedSupport/SyncDurability/SnapshotStorage, and cacheEngine == the cluster engine (Redis/Memcached/Valkey), then iterate (MaxResults=100) picking the row whose usagetype matches '^...NodeUsage:<type>$' — mirroring _select_efs_storage_rate's usagetype-filter pattern (pricing_engine.py:1346-1374). Pass the engine down from the shim so the correct cacheEngine SKU is chosen.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Code mechanism verified and corroborated by live pricing. Adapter line 60 calls get_instance_monthly_price("AmazonElastiCache", node_type) — the GENERIC path (there is NO get_elasticache_node_monthly_price method anywhere, despite core/CLAUDE.md claiming one). _fetch_generic_instance_price (pricing_engine.py:1291-1294) filters ONLY instanceType + location — no cacheEngine, usagetype, or productFamily. _call_pricing_api (pricing_engine.py:1598-1611) issues MaxResults=1 and returns _extract_usd(PriceList[0]). Live AWS Pricing API (us-east-1, pub 2026-06-25) returns SIX OnDemand SKUs all sharing instanceType=cache.r6g.large: Redis ExtendedSupportYr3 $0.33, Redis ExtendedSupportYr1_Yr2 $0.165, Valkey NodeUsage $0.1648, Valkey SyncDurability surcharge $0.0297, Memcached NodeUsage $0.206, and the true Redis NodeUsage $0.206 — exactly the snapshot in the finding (the MCP wrapper even returned the $0.33 Extended-Support SKU first). With no engine/usagetype filter and a single result, the node rate is ambiguous and frequently wrong. The finding correctly flags that boto3 ordering is not guaranteed, so the exact $240.90 figure is one (observed) outcome rather than deterministic — the defect (mis-rated base node price feeding every lever) is real regardless.

#### 🟠 H1 · Graviton and Underutilized recs omit NumNodes -> priced for 1 node; multi-node clusters undercounted and the per-cluster 'best lever' dedup is distorted  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/elasticache.py + services/adapters/elasticache.py:elasticache.py (shim):96-104 (graviton, no NumNodes) and 149-158 (underutilized, no NumNodes); adapter elasticache.py:57`
- **Evidence:** The graviton_migration rec dict (shim 96-104) and the underutilized_clusters rec dict (shim 149-158) do NOT include a 'NumNodes' key, while valkey_migration (74-91) and reserved_nodes (110-119) do. The adapter computes num_nodes = rec.get('NumNodes', 1) or 1 (adapter:57), so Graviton and Underutilized are always priced for exactly 1 node. For a multi-node Memcached cluster (e.g. NumCacheNodes=4) the Graviton/Underutilized dollar is 1/NumNodes of the true figure, while Valkey uses real NumNodes — so on a multi-node cluster Valkey mechanically wins the best_per_cluster dedup (adapter:70-88) even when Graviton/Underutilized would be the larger real saving.
- **Impact:** Undercounts Graviton and Underutilized savings by a factor of NumNodes on multi-node clusters, and flips which lever is counted per cluster (dedup correctness). Note the brief's claim that 'Underutilized uses real NumNodes' is wrong — Underutilized also omits it.
- **Fix:** Add 'NumNodes': num_nodes to both the graviton_migration rec (shim 96-104) and the underutilized_clusters rec (shim 149-158) so all four levers price on the same node count and the dedup compares like-for-like.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Core bug verified at the cited lines. The graviton_migration dict (services/elasticache.py:96-104) and the underutilized_clusters dict (149-158) contain NO 'NumNodes' key, whereas valkey_migration (74-91) and reserved_nodes (110-119) do. Adapter line 57 (`num_nodes = rec.get("NumNodes", 1) or 1`) therefore prices Graviton and Underutilized for exactly 1 node, undercounting multi-node clusters by a factor of NumNodes. The dedup distortion is also real: on a multi-node Redis cluster that is also underutilized, Underutilized (rate 0.30) should be the largest lever at real NumNodes but, priced at 1 node, loses to Valkey (0.20 x NumNodes) once NumNodes>=2 — flipping which lever best_per_cluster (adapter:70-88) counts. The brief's self-correction ('Underutilized also omits NumNodes') is accurate. One caveat (does not refute): the illustrative 'multi-node Memcached cluster -> Valkey mechanically wins' example is internally inconsistent, since valkey_migration is only emitted for engine==redis (shim:73), so a Memcached cluster has no Valkey rec — the undercount still applies there, but the Valkey-wins flip actually manifests on Redis clusters.

#### 🟠 H2 · Graviton flat 0.20 factor overstates the realizable node-price saving (~4.6%) by ~4x; '20-40%' is a price-performance figure, not a cost reduction  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/elasticache.py:49 (rate_by_category 'Graviton Migration': 0.20) + 60-62`
- **Evidence:** Adapter counts monthly_node * NumNodes * 0.20 for Graviton (elasticache.py:49,60-62). Live AWS Pricing API (us-east-1, Redis NodeUsage): x86 cache.r5.large = $0.216/hr vs Graviton cache.r6g.large = $0.206/hr — a real node-price delta of only (0.216-0.206)/0.216 = ~4.6%. The shim string 'Estimated: 20-40% price-performance improvement' (shim:101) is AWS's throughput-per-dollar claim at equal node count, not a same-node-count cost reduction. Counting 0.20 of the current node price books ~$0.043/hr of saving where only ~$0.010/hr is realizable without also shrinking the fleet.
- **Impact:** Overcounts every Graviton-migration counted dollar by roughly 4x relative to the realizable same-node-count node-price delta. Fabricated savings magnitude.
- **Fix:** Replace the 0.20 flat factor with the exact current-node -> Graviton-equivalent node-price delta: map x86 family -> Graviton family (r5->r6g, m5->m6g, etc.), price both via the fixed pricing path (C2), and count (price_current - price_graviton) * NumNodes. Keep the '20-40% price-performance' wording only as advisory context, not as the counted rate.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified in code and against live pricing. Adapter sets rate_by_category["Graviton Migration"]=0.20 (line 49) and books monthly_node * NumNodes * 0.20 (line 62). Live AWS Pricing API confirms the realizable same-node-count node-price delta is ~4.6%: Redis cache.r5.large NodeUsage $0.216 vs Graviton cache.r6g.large NodeUsage $0.206 -> (0.216-0.206)/0.216 = 4.63%. The shim's source string 'Estimated: 20-40% price-performance improvement' (shim:101) is AWS's throughput-per-dollar claim at equal node count, not a same-fleet cost reduction, so 0.20 is misapplied — ~4.3x the realizable node-price delta, matching the finding's 'roughly 4x' overcount. Caveat (does not refute): per H1's dedup, Graviton is frequently superseded by Valkey on Redis clusters, so Graviton-counted dollars mostly arise on Memcached / single-node clusters; where Graviton IS the counted lever, the ~4x overcount holds.

#### 🟠 H3 · fast_mode not honored: CloudWatch get_metric_statistics runs per-cluster even under --fast; reads_fast_mode not declared  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/elasticache.py + services/elasticache.py:adapter elasticache.py:12-24 (no reads_fast_mode); shim elasticache.py:121-133 (ungated get_metric_statistics)`
- **Evidence:** ElasticacheModule declares requires_cloudwatch=True (adapter:20) but NOT reads_fast_mode (defaults False, services/_base.py:25). The shim issues cloudwatch.get_metric_statistics unconditionally for every cluster (shim:125-133) with no `if ctx.fast_mode` guard. Sibling CloudWatch adapters do both: lambda_svc.py:59-61, file_systems.py:35-36, rds.py:45-46 declare reads_fast_mode=True AND short-circuit their CloudWatch reads on ctx.fast_mode.
- **Impact:** A --fast scan still makes one CloudWatch API call per ElastiCache cluster (latency + throttling risk + cost) — a fast-mode contract violation. The fleet-wide --fast path is slower and noisier than intended.
- **Fix:** Declare reads_fast_mode=True on ElasticacheModule and pass ctx.fast_mode into the shim; when fast_mode is set, skip the CPUUtilization block (shim:121-158) and emit the Underutilized lever as $0 advisory (or omit it), mirroring rds.py/file_systems.py.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified. ElasticacheModule declares requires_cloudwatch=True (services/adapters/elasticache.py:20) but does NOT declare reads_fast_mode, which defaults to False (services/_base.py:25; contract documented at core/contracts.py:175). The shim issues cloudwatch.get_metric_statistics unconditionally inside the per-cluster loop (services/elasticache.py:125-133) with no `if ctx.fast_mode` guard — grep confirms NEITHER the shim nor the adapter references fast_mode anywhere. Sibling CloudWatch adapters honor the contract: rds.py declares reads_fast_mode=True (line 46) and short-circuits on `if not ctx.fast_mode` (line 119); lambda_svc.py:61 and file_systems.py:36 likewise declare it (17 adapters total). core/CLAUDE.md guidance explicitly requires CloudWatch adapters to check ctx.fast_mode and bail cheaply. So a --fast scan still makes one get_metric_statistics call per ElastiCache cluster — a genuine fast-mode contract violation.

#### 🟡 M1 · CloudWatch failure drops the (only evidence-gated) Underutilized lever silently via logger, not ctx.warn/ctx.permission_issue  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/elasticache.py:159-161`
- **Evidence:** The inner CloudWatch block ends `except Exception as e: logger.warning(f"... Could not get metrics for cluster {cluster_id}: {e}"); continue` (shim:159-161). A CloudWatch AccessDenied / throttle is recorded only to the module logger — never surfaced on ctx — so the Underutilized signal (the sole CloudWatch-evidence-gated counted lever) is lost with no operator-visible warning or permission_issue.
- **Impact:** Silent under-reporting of downsize savings when cloudwatch:GetMetricStatistics is denied/throttled. Operator cannot distinguish 'check ran, found nothing' from 'check failed'.
- **Fix:** Classify the exception via services/_aws_errors.record_aws_error (AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation -> ctx.permission_issue('cloudwatch'), else ctx.warn), mirroring lambda/rds CloudWatch handling, instead of logger.warning only.

#### 🟡 M2 · Underutilized 0.30 is a flat reduction factor, not the exact current->one-size-down node-price delta  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/elasticache.py:47 (rate_by_category 'Underutilized Cluster': 0.30) + 60-62`
- **Evidence:** Adapter counts monthly_node * NumNodes * 0.30 for Underutilized (elasticache.py:47,60-62) regardless of how many sizes down is feasible. ElastiCache node sizes roughly double in price each step (cache.r6g.large $0.206 vs the next size down), so a flat 0.30 neither equals a true one-step downsize (~50% for a single halving) nor reflects multi-step headroom at <20% CPU.
- **Impact:** The counted downsize dollar is a heuristic proxy that can both under- and over-state the realizable saving; not defensible as an exact figure from the report.
- **Fix:** Compute the exact delta: from CPU headroom pick a target node type (one or more sizes down within the same family, bounded by SMALLEST_SIZES), price both via the fixed pricing path (C2), and count (price_current - price_target) * NumNodes; record the chosen target in an AuditBasis.

#### 🟡 M3 · Renderer shows the raw percentage string and never the computed per-cluster dollar — counted dollars desync from the rendered cards  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `reporter_phase_b.py:1052-1089 (esp. 1071-1073)`
- **Evidence:** _render_elasticache_enhanced_checks groups by CheckCategory and prints savings_str = clusters[0].get('EstimatedSavings','') (reporter_phase_b.py:1071-1073) — i.e. the shim's raw strings 'Estimated: 20-40% price-performance improvement' / '30-50%' / '30-60% vs On-Demand' / the Valkey prose. It NEVER renders rec['EstimatedMonthlySavings'] (the counted dollar computed at elasticache.py:62). The cards therefore display a percentage next to a headline dollar derived from a different flat factor (0.20/0.30); advisory (superseded/Reserved) cards render identical percentage strings with no indication they are not counted; per-cluster dollars are invisible.
- **Impact:** Legibility/trust desync: the executive headline counts e.g. 20% of node price while the card says '20-40%'. Counted total cannot be reconciled against the visible cards.
- **Fix:** Render each rec's EstimatedMonthlySavings dollar (and a counted/advisory marker driven by rec['Counted']) in the card, and either drop the raw percentage string or relabel it as 'list/marketing range'. Visually separate Counted==False recs so the rendered detail matches the counted headline.

#### 🟡 M4 · Outer exception handler classifies permission errors as a generic warn instead of ctx.permission_issue  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/elasticache.py:163-164`
- **Evidence:** The outer guard is `except Exception as e: ctx.warn(f"Could not analyze ElastiCache: {e}", "elasticache")` (shim:163-164). An elasticache:DescribeCacheClusters AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation is reported as a generic warning rather than ctx.permission_issue, unlike the network adapter pattern (services/_aws_errors.record_aws_error).
- **Impact:** Permission gaps that zero out the entire ElastiCache tab are reported as ordinary warnings, not actionable permission issues — harder to triage a misconfigured IAM policy.
- **Fix:** Route the outer except through record_aws_error so AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation/OptInRequired become ctx.permission_issue('elasticache') and other errors remain ctx.warn.

#### 🟢 L1 · Doc drift: get_elasticache_node_monthly_price() is documented in two CLAUDE.md files but does not exist; the adapter uses get_instance_monthly_price  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `core/CLAUDE.md + services/adapters/CLAUDE.md:services/adapters/CLAUDE.md:32; core/CLAUDE.md PricingEngine Public Methods table row 'get_elasticache_node_monthly_price(engine, node_type)'`
- **Evidence:** Both CLAUDE.md rows claim elasticache prices via get_elasticache_node_monthly_price(). grep of core/pricing_engine.py finds no such method — only get_instance_monthly_price (pricing_engine.py:740), which the adapter calls as get_instance_monthly_price('AmazonElastiCache', node_type) (elasticache.py:60). The documented signature even takes an `engine` arg the real path lacks (and which C2 shows it SHOULD use).
- **Impact:** Documentation misleads maintainers about the pricing entry point and falsely implies engine-aware pricing that does not exist (related to C2).
- **Fix:** Update the elasticache.py row in services/adapters/CLAUDE.md and the core/CLAUDE.md PricingEngine table to reference get_instance_monthly_price('AmazonElastiCache', node_type); note engine-awareness is a gap (C2), not an existing feature.

#### 🟢 L2 · Coverage gaps: ElastiCache Serverless not scanned, and Reserved-Nodes trigger (NumCacheNodes>=2) effectively never fires for Redis replication-group members  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/elasticache.py:60-119`
- **Evidence:** The shim iterates describe_cache_clusters(ShowCacheNodeInfo=True) with pagination (shim:60-61, good) and skips status!='available' (shim:70-71). ElastiCache Serverless caches are not CacheCluster resources, so they are never enumerated (silently out of scope). For Redis, describe_cache_clusters returns each replication-group member as a separate CacheCluster with NumCacheNodes==1, so reserved_nodes num_nodes>=2 (shim:109) realistically only fires for Memcached; per-node Valkey/Graviton/Underutilized recs are emitted per member (priced per node, acceptable for those levers).
- **Impact:** ElastiCache Serverless spend (ECPU/GB) is invisible to the cost scan; Reserved-Nodes advisory coverage is skewed to Memcached. Neither fabricates dollars, but both are coverage blind spots.
- **Fix:** Document Serverless as an explicit out-of-scope limitation (or add a describe_serverless_caches path); base the Reserved advisory on describe_replication_groups node counts rather than per-member NumCacheNodes so it covers Redis/Valkey clusters.

---

### File Systems (EFS/FSx) — `services/adapters/file_systems.py`

**Module identity:** key="file_systems", cli_aliases=("efs","fsx","file_systems"), display_name="File Systems", requires_cloudwatch=True, reads_fast_mode=True, required_clients()=("efs","fsx","cloudwatch") — all confirmed against services/adapters/file_systems.py:32-40. The adapter (FileSystemsModule.scan) aggregates services/efs_fsx.py (get_efs_findings, get_fsx_findings, counts) plus pure logic in services/file_systems_logic.py, emitting three SourceBlocks (efs_lifecycle_analysis counted, fsx_optimization_analysis counted, advisory uncounted) under one File Systems tab via the Phase-A special case reporter_phase_a.render_file_systems (html_report_generator.py:3309-3310, before PHASE_A_DESCRIPTORS). Neither Cost Optimization Hub nor Compute Optimizer covers EFS/FSx, so there is no CoH/CO source to consume and a "missing CoH/CO" finding is out of scope (correct per code). Pricing strategy: live PricingEngine.get_efs_monthly_price_per_gb / get_efs_ia_access_price_per_gb / get_fsx_storage_price_per_gb (region-correct), with region-scaled FALLBACK_EFS_*/FALLBACK_FSX_* constants on the pricing_engine=None path; multiplier applied once (engine path returns region-correct, never re-multiplied). The services/adapters/CLAUDE.md file_systems.py row accurately reflects the real code (CloudWatch-gated EFS IA-lifecycle net of access charge, Windows-only SSD→HDD, advisory Lustre/ONTAP/OpenZFS, no CoH/CO) — no doc/code mismatch.

**Verdict:** The two counted paths are cost-defensible and rate-accurate: every EFS and FSx-Windows rate the adapter can count was validated live and matches the engine fallbacks to the cent, region scaling is applied exactly once (engine path region-correct, fallback path x pricing_multiplier — no double-apply), the EFS IA-lifecycle saving is correctly evidence-gated on CloudWatch metrics and netted of the IA access charge, SSD->HDD is correctly Windows-only above the real 2000 GiB HDD floor, dedupe_counted enforces one counted finding per fs_id, and advisory findings are structurally segregated so they never touch the headline. The one genuine cost-correctness bug is M1: idle-EFS delete prices all bytes (including IA/Archive-tiered bytes) at the Standard rate, over-counting the saving for idle-but-tiered systems. Remaining items are low-severity hardening: a missing >0 guard on the idle branch (L1), parseable advisory $-strings relying solely on SourceBlock segregation (L2), unpaginated describe_file_caches (L3), a cents-level render/headline rounding desync (L4), dead Phase-B/extractor code (L5), and the conservative-by-design cold_gb dimensional mismatch (L6). No fabricated-from-nothing counted dollar, no cross-adapter/cross-source double-count, and no blank-card/unrendered source.

**Pricing validation:** Live-validated via AWS Pricing MCP (AmazonEFS / AmazonFSx, us-east-1). EFS storageClass rates all MATCH the code's FALLBACK_EFS_GB_MONTH_BY_CLASS: General Purpose $0.30, Infrequent Access $0.025, One Zone-General Purpose $0.16, One Zone-Infrequent Access $0.0133, Archive $0.008; EFS IA DataAccess (read==write) $0.01 MATCHES FALLBACK_EFS_IA_ACCESS_GB. FSx Windows MATCHES FALLBACK_FSX_GB_MONTH/FALLBACK_FSX_MULTI_AZ_GB_MONTH: SSD Single-AZ $0.130, HDD Single-AZ $0.013, SSD Multi-AZ $0.230, HDD Multi-AZ $0.025. SKU selection is deterministic: _select_efs_storage_rate/_select_efs_access_rate use MaxResults=100 and filter on usagetype (TimedStorage vs DataAccess) so the per-GB access rate cannot masquerade as the storage rate; _fetch_fsx_storage_price pins location+productFamily+fileSystemType+storageType+deploymentOption so the lone storage SKU is returned even under _call_pricing_api MaxResults=1 (backup rows lack storageType and are excluded). Note: the audit BRIEF cites EFS IA at '$0.016/GB-mo' — this is STALE; the live API returns $0.025 and the code's 0.025 is correct. ONTAP/Lustre/OpenZFS rates were not re-validated because those types never reach a counted branch (advisory only).

**Cost checks:**

| Check | Status | Trigger | Savings basis |
|---|---|---|---|
| EFS idle file-system delete | counted | LifeCycleState in (available,""); NumberOfMountTargets==0 and total_gb>0 (efs_fsx.py:319) | efs_idle_savings(total_gb, std_rate) = total_gb x std_rate (100% of storage cost). std_rate=_efs_rate(std_class) where std_class=One Zone if AvailabilityZoneName else Standard. Rate source: PricingEngine.get_efs_monthly_price_per_gb (live, $0.30 GP / $0.16 One Zone us-east-1, validated) or FALLBACK_EFS_GB_MONTH_BY_CLASS x pricing_multiplier |
| EFS IA-lifecycle NET saving | counted | not has_ia_policy and standard_gb>=EFS_MIN_LIFECYCLE_GB(1.0); cloudwatch present and access metrics return datapoints; est.net_savings>0 and est.cold_gb>=1.0 (efs_fsx.py:340-363) | efs_lifecycle_net_savings: cold_gb=max(standard_gb - monthly_access_gb,0); gross=cold_gb x (std-ia); access_charge=monthly_access_gb x ia_access; net=gross-access_charge. Data: ValueInStandard + CloudWatch DataReadIOBytes+DataWriteIOBytes summed over 30d /1024^3. Rates: get_efs_monthly_price_per_gb(std/ia) + get_efs_ia_access_price_per_gb ($0.30/$0.025/$0.01 validated) |
| EFS IA-lifecycle not-cost-effective | advisory | metrics present but net_savings<=0 or cold_gb<1.0 (efs_fsx.py:389-410) | non-parseable string 'not cost-effective: N GB cold but net $X/month after IA access charges'; Counted:False; never summed |
| EFS IA-lifecycle gross indicative | advisory | no metric evidence (fast_mode, no cloudwatch client, or no datapoints) and gross>0 (efs_fsx.py:411-439) | efs_lifecycle_savings(standard_gb, std, ia, EFS_IA_TRANSITION_FRACTION=0.5) = standard_gb x (std-ia) x 0.5; string 'up to ~$X/month gross before IA read-access charges'; Counted:False |
| EFS One Zone migration | advisory | not is_one_zone and total_gb>=EFS_ONE_ZONE_MIN_GB(1.0) and mount_targets>0 and oz_savings>0 (efs_fsx.py:444-455) | efs_one_zone_savings(total_gb, std_rate, oz_rate)=total_gb x (Standard-OneZone delta); deterministic but DURABILITY tradeoff so advisory; string '~$X/month if migrated (durability tradeoff)'; Counted:False |
| EFS Archive storage missing | advisory | not is_one_zone and not has_archive_policy and total_gb>10 (efs_fsx.py:458-466) | no $ ('Depends on cold-data share (no access-pattern data)'); Counted:False |
| EFS Provisioned->Elastic throughput | advisory | ThroughputMode==provisioned (efs_fsx.py:467-475) | no $ ('Depends on provisioned-vs-used throughput'); Counted:False |
| FSx Windows SSD->HDD swap | counted | Lifecycle in (AVAILABLE,""); storage_type==SSD and fs_type in _FSX_HDD_COUNTED_ELIGIBLE({WINDOWS}) and capacity>=FSX_SSD_TO_HDD_MIN_GB(2000) and savings>0 (efs_fsx.py:510-514) | fsx_ssd_to_hdd_savings(capacity, ssd_rate, hdd_rate)=capacity x (SSD-HDD delta). _fsx_rate pins (fs_type,storage,deployment): Windows SSD/HDD Single-AZ $0.130/$0.013, Multi-AZ $0.230/$0.025 (all live-validated). Engine get_fsx_storage_price_per_gb or FALLBACK_FSX_(MULTI_AZ_)GB_MONTH x multiplier |
| FSx Lustre storage optimization | advisory | fs_type==LUSTRE and storage_type==SSD (efs_fsx.py:534-538) | Best-practice string, no $ (Lustre HDD is Persistent-only at a different throughput tier, no like-for-like delta); Counted:False |
| FSx Lustre/OpenZFS Intelligent-Tiering | advisory | fs_type in (LUSTRE,OPENZFS) and storage_type not in (INT,INTELLIGENT_TIERING) (efs_fsx.py:539-541) | Best-practice, no $; Counted:False |
| FSx Windows data deduplication | advisory | fs_type==WINDOWS (efs_fsx.py:542-544) | Best-practice, no $; Counted:False |
| FSx Windows Single-AZ migration | advisory | fs_type==WINDOWS and DeploymentType contains MULTI (efs_fsx.py:545-547) | Best-practice, no $; Counted:False |
| FSx ONTAP data efficiency / capacity-pool tiering | advisory | fs_type==ONTAP (efs_fsx.py:548-554) | Best-practice, no $ (cold-byte tiering needs DescribeVolumes/SVMs not read); Counted:False |
| FSx backup retention | advisory | AutomaticBackupRetentionDays>EXCESSIVE_BACKUP_RETENTION_DAYS(30) (efs_fsx.py:556-566) | no $ ('Depends on backup storage size (not reported by API)'); Counted:False |
| FSx File Cache sizing | advisory | any FileCache from describe_file_caches (efs_fsx.py:568-578) | no $ ('Depends on cache hit rate / utilization'); Counted:False |

**Findings:**

#### 🟡 M1 · Idle-EFS delete prices ALL bytes at the Standard rate, over-counting IA/Archive-tiered idle systems  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/efs_fsx.py:318-333`
- **Evidence:** if mount_targets == 0 and total_gb > 0:\n    savings = efs_idle_savings(total_gb, std_rate)  # file_systems_logic.py:84-86 = total_gb x std_rate\n total_gb = size.get('Value') (efs_fsx.py:297) is the metered size across ALL classes (Standard+IA+Archive), but std_rate is only the Standard/One-Zone rate. Live-validated rates: Standard $0.30, IA $0.025 (12x lower), Archive $0.008 (37x lower).
- **Impact:** An idle file system (0 mount targets) that previously tiered data to IA/Archive has its counted saving over-stated by (std_rate - ia_rate) x ia_bytes + (std_rate - archive_rate) x archive_bytes. On fully-IA-tiered idle bytes the saving is inflated ~12x; on Archive ~37x. Real over-count of a COUNTED dollar (headline + rendered card). Prevalence is low (idle yet tiered), hence MEDIUM not HIGH.
- **Fix:** Price per class using the breakdown DescribeFileSystems already returns: saving = ValueInStandard x std_rate + ValueInIA x ia_rate + ValueInArchive x archive_rate (+ One Zone variants), rather than total_gb x std_rate. The size sub-fields and _efs_rate(class) lookups are already available in scope.

#### 🟢 L1 · Idle-EFS counted branch lacks the 'if savings > 0' guard every other counted branch has  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/efs_fsx.py:319-333`
- **Evidence:** The idle branch appends the counted finding unconditionally after computing savings, whereas lifecycle uses 'if est.net_savings > 0' (363), one-zone 'if oz_savings > 0' (447), and FSx 'if savings > 0' (514). efs_idle_savings returns total_gb x max(std_rate,0).
- **Impact:** Latent $0-counted risk: if std_rate ever resolved to 0 (a future rate path returning 0 rather than a positive fallback), a '$0.00/month' counted finding with _savings=0 would be emitted and rendered. Not currently exploitable because get_efs_monthly_price_per_gb always returns a positive fallback, so no live $0 today.
- **Fix:** Wrap the append in 'if savings > 0:' for parity with the other three counted branches and the brief's 'a counted $0 is a bug' invariant.

#### 🟢 L2 · Advisory gross/One-Zone strings carry a parseable '$X/month'; counted-safety relies solely on SourceBlock segregation  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/efs_fsx.py:422-425`
- **Evidence:** Advisory EstimatedSavings 'up to ~${gross:.2f}/month gross before IA read-access charges...' (422-425) and '~${oz_savings:.2f}/month if migrated (durability tradeoff)' (453) both match parse_dollar_savings' regex (_savings.py:31-35 returns the figure for unit 'month') AND reporter_phase_a._fs_savings' loose $-regex (reporter_phase_a.py:100). They are safe ONLY because the adapter sums savings over efs_counted/fsx_counted exclusively (file_systems.py:63-64) and render_file_systems routes the 'advisory' SourceBlock to a non-summed bucket (reporter_phase_a.py:40,73-86).
- **Impact:** No current $ leakage (advisory recs never reach either parser as counted). Fragile: any future code that sums advisory EstimatedSavings, or a misrouted finding, would fabricate the GROSS 0.5-fraction figure (or the durability-tradeoff One-Zone delta) as a counted saving. Brief Phase 2.4 explicitly asked this be confirmed unparseable; it is not.
- **Fix:** Drop the '/month' unit from the indicative advisory strings (e.g. 'up to ~$X gross/mo-equivalent') or route every advisory through services._savings.mark_zero_savings_advisory so the gate, not the SourceBlock name, enforces $0.

#### 🟢 L3 · FSx describe_file_caches is unpaginated and called twice  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/efs_fsx.py:225,569`
- **Evidence:** caches = fsx.describe_file_caches().get('FileCaches', []) in get_fsx_file_system_count (225) and again in get_fsx_findings (569) — neither uses the paginator/NextToken, unlike describe_file_systems which is correctly paginated (220-223, 491-494).
- **Impact:** Coverage gap only on accounts with more File Caches than fit one page: trailing caches are silently dropped from the count and the advisory list. No dollar impact (File Cache findings are advisory $0). Two API calls per scan is minor inefficiency.
- **Fix:** Paginate describe_file_caches with NextToken (or fsx.get_paginator if available) and read once, passing the result through, mirroring the describe_file_systems pattern.

#### 🟢 L4 · Render per-group sum uses unrounded _savings while the headline parses the 2-decimal string  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `reporter_phase_a.py:92-101`
- **Evidence:** render_file_systems sums _fs_savings(r) (reporter_phase_a.py:51) which returns the full-precision _savings float (94-96); the adapter headline total_monthly_savings sums parse_dollar_savings('${savings:.2f}/month') over the SAME recs (file_systems.py:63-64), i.e. the value rounded to cents.
- **Impact:** Counted==rendered holds to the cent for a single finding (<= $0.005 each), but across many counted file systems the rendered per-group total and the executive-summary headline can diverge by a few cents. Cosmetic; no fabricated or dropped dollar.
- **Fix:** Have _fs_savings and the headline read the same value — e.g. round(_savings, 2) in both, or have the adapter sum _savings directly instead of re-parsing its own formatted string.

#### 🟢 L5 · Dead Phase-B renderer and resource extractor for file_systems (confusion, not a bug)  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `reporter_phase_b.py:1368-1369,1584`
- **Evidence:** render_generic_per_rec dispatches to _render_generic_file_systems_rec (reporter_phase_b.py:1368-1369,1584), but file_systems is in _PHASE_B_SKIP_PER_REC (2523) so should_fallback_to_per_rec returns False, and html_report_generator.py:3309-3310 special-cases file_systems to render_file_systems BEFORE PHASE_A_DESCRIPTORS. Separately _extract_file_systems_resources (html_report_generator.py:391-414) is registered (421) but _get_affected_resources_list is skipped for file_systems (3148-3174). Both paths are unreachable in the normal flow.
- **Impact:** No double-render or double-count (confirmed: render_file_systems is the sole live renderer; the extractor never fires). Pure maintenance risk — a future editor could wire the dead per-rec path and desync rendering.
- **Fix:** Remove _render_generic_file_systems_rec and the file_systems branch in render_generic_per_rec, plus _extract_file_systems_resources and its _RESOURCE_EXTRACTORS entry, or add a comment marking them dead under the Phase-A special case.

#### 🟢 L6 · cold_gb subtracts a 30-day cumulative throughput (flow) from a point-in-time size  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/file_systems_logic.py:59-76`
- **Evidence:** cold_gb = max(standard_gb - max(monthly_access_gb,0), 0) where standard_gb is a stored-byte SIZE and monthly_access_gb is sum(DataReadIOBytes+DataWriteIOBytes) over 30d /1024^3 (a transfer VOLUME). For an actively-read FS the 30d transfer can exceed the stored size, clamping cold_gb (and the counted saving) to 0.
- **Impact:** Dimensionally inconsistent but strictly CONSERVATIVE: it can only shrink cold_gb, so it under-counts (never over-counts) the saving — no fabricated dollar. Brief Phase file_systems-specific item blesses this as conservative. Side effect: genuinely-cold-but-occasionally-touched systems may be pushed to the advisory branch and lose a real (smaller) counted saving.
- **Fix:** Acceptable as-is for cost-safety. If higher recall is wanted, gate 'hot' on a per-file access metric (e.g. unique bytes via DataReadIOBytes percentile or EFS lifecycle Transition metrics) rather than cumulative IO volume; keep the conservative clamp until then.

---

### Glue — `services/adapters/glue.py`

**Module identity:** key="glue", cli_aliases=("glue",), display_name="Glue", required_clients()=("glue",). The adapter does NOT declare requires_cloudwatch or reads_fast_mode and makes NO CloudWatch / get_job_runs reads — the saving has no usage signal. It is NOT wired to Cost Optimization Hub (not in scan_orchestrator _HUB_SERVICES/type_map) nor Compute Optimizer (no services/advisor.py Glue helper), so CoH/CO axes correctly do not apply. Pricing is local module constants in GlueModule.scan (GLUE_DPU_HOURLY=0.44, GLUE_RIGHTSIZE_FACTOR=0.30, ASSUMED_MONTHLY_DPU_HOURS=160); there is no PricingEngine method for Glue. Render is Phase A (glue in _PHASE_A_SERVICES, reporter_phase_b.py:2507; PHASE_A_DESCRIPTORS["glue"] savings_mode="conditional", close_div_location="inner"; should_skip_section_header("glue")=True).

**Verdict:** The Glue adapter's counted dollars are unreliable. Two CRITICAL bugs dominate: (C1) a dict.get key-shadowing defect prices every current-gen worker-based job at $0 silently because the shim always injects MaxCapacity=0, so only legacy MaxCapacity>10 jobs ever count; and (C2) the only non-zero figures come from a fabricated fixed 160 DPU-hours/month with no get_job_runs/CloudWatch evidence. The render path is desynced (cards show static '20-40%'/'$316' strings while the headline sums a different computed float), dev endpoints advertise $316 but count $0 while the real ~$1,606/mo saving is missed, and worker-vs-DPU / WorkerType / Flex / streaming pricing is wrong. CoH/CO correctly do not apply. The $0.44 base rate is live-validated and correct; the DPU count and assumed hours are the broken inputs.

**Pricing validation:** Validated LIVE against AWS Pricing API (serviceCode=AWSGlue, us-east-1, version 20260623, effectiveDate 2026-06-01): standard ETL DPU-hour = $0.44 (USE1-ETL-DPU-Hour, SKU CXGYW3G8GS2SN9UG) — confirms GLUE_DPU_HOURLY=0.44 for G.1X/G.2X standard jobs. Flex ETL = $0.29/DPU-hr (USE1-ETL-Flex-DPU-Hour, SKU CW2STD52Z73SFDTA, ~34% cheaper) — flat 0.44 is wrong for Flex. Dev endpoint = $0.44/DPU-hr (USE1-DEVED-DPU-Hour, SKU H5SXAYMQH485TMM7) → 5-DPU always-on = $1,606/mo, contradicting the static '$316/month' string. Memory-optimized = $0.52 (USE1-ETL-M-DPU-Hour, SKU 8B8U9Y67DA2X92AD). The flat $0.44 per-DPU rate is correct; the DPU COUNT (workers≠DPU) and the hours (160) are the unsourced/fabricated inputs — neither validatable via Pricing API and flagged needs-usage-evidence (get_job_runs).

**Cost checks:**

| Check | Status | Trigger | Savings basis |
|---|---|---|---|
| job_rightsizing | counted | services/glue.py:37 — a job from the get_jobs paginator has MaxCapacity > 10 OR NumberOfWorkers > 10 | services/adapters/glue.py:66-73 — rec_savings = GLUE_DPU_HOURLY(0.44 $/DPU-hr us-east-1) × dpu_count × ASSUMED_MONTHLY_DPU_HOURS(160) × ctx.pricing_multiplier × GLUE_RIGHTSIZE_FACTOR(0.30). dpu_count = rec.get('MaxCapacity', rec.get('NumberOfWorkers')) at line 52. $0.44 validated live (AWSGlue USE1-ETL-DPU-Hour, SKU CXGYW3G8GS2SN9UG). 160 hrs and 0.30 factor are unsourced constants. |
| dev_endpoints | advisory | services/glue.py:55 — a dev endpoint from the (non-paginated) get_dev_endpoints() call has Status == 'READY' | No savings is computed: the dev_endpoint rec carries no MaxCapacity/NumberOfWorkers keys, so services/adapters/glue.py:52-58 resolves dpu_count=None and sets EstimatedMonthlySavings=0.0 + PricingWarning. The rec still carries the static EstimatedSavings='$316/month per endpoint' string (services/glue.py:61). Real cost: 5 DPU × $0.44/DPU-hr (validated, USE1-DEVED-DPU-Hour SKU H5SXAYMQH485TMM7) × 730 = $1,606/mo always-on while READY. |
| crawler_optimization | advisory | Never fires — the crawler check was removed (services/glue.py:66-74 iterates get_crawlers but only does `_ = (crawler_name, schedule)`); the SourceBlock is emitted with count=0 and renders no card. | None — no recommendation is appended; the empty source is skipped at reporter_phase_a.py:413 (count>0 guard), so no blank card. |

**Findings:**

#### 🔴 C1 · Worker-based (current-gen) jobs priced at $0 — MaxCapacity=0 shadows the NumberOfWorkers fallback  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/glue.py:52-58 (with services/glue.py:33-43)`
- **Evidence:** Adapter: `dpu_count = rec.get("MaxCapacity", rec.get("NumberOfWorkers"))`. The shim ALWAYS injects both keys: `max_capacity = job.get("MaxCapacity", 0)` and `number_of_workers = job.get("NumberOfWorkers", 0)`, then writes `"MaxCapacity": max_capacity, "NumberOfWorkers": number_of_workers` (services/glue.py:33-35,41-43). For a worker-based job (NumberOfWorkers=20, no MaxCapacity in the API response) the rec has MaxCapacity=0, so dict.get returns 0 (the key exists) and NEVER falls through to NumberOfWorkers. Verified: `{'MaxCapacity':0,'NumberOfWorkers':20}.get('MaxCapacity', .get('NumberOfWorkers')) == 0`. dpu_count=0 → monthly_cost=0 → rec_savings=0.0, and because 0 is not None and float(0) succeeds, NO PricingWarning is set.
- **Impact:** Every modern Glue job (NumberOfWorkers + WorkerType is the current API; MaxCapacity is legacy) that triggers on `number_of_workers > 10` is counted as a recommendation but contributes $0 to the tab total and exec-summary headline, silently and with no warning. Only legacy MaxCapacity>10 jobs ever produce a non-zero counted dollar. A G.2X/20-worker job that should show ~$844.80/mo savings (0.44×40DPU×160×0.30) is counted as $0.
- **Fix:** Resolve capacity with truthiness, not key-presence: `dpu_count = rec.get("MaxCapacity") or rec.get("NumberOfWorkers")` (or have the shim omit the zero key). Then apply the WorkerType→DPU multiplier from H3 so NumberOfWorkers is converted to DPU before pricing.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Real exactly as described. Adapter line 52: dpu_count = rec.get("MaxCapacity", rec.get("NumberOfWorkers")). The shim (services/glue.py:33 max_capacity = job.get("MaxCapacity", 0); line 41 writes "MaxCapacity": max_capacity) ALWAYS injects the MaxCapacity key. For a worker-based job (NumberOfWorkers=20, no MaxCapacity in the API response) the rec has MaxCapacity=0, so dict.get finds the key and returns 0 -- it never falls through to NumberOfWorkers. Line 53 'if dpu_count is None' is False (0 is not None), float(0) succeeds, so monthly_cost = 0.44*0*160*mult = 0, rec_savings = 0, EstimatedMonthlySavings = 0.0, and NO PricingWarning is set. The trigger 'number_of_workers > 10' (services/glue.py:37) still adds the rec, so it is counted but contributes $0. Mechanism, lines, and silent-no-warning behavior are all confirmed. Note: the illustrative ~$844.80 figure assumes a G.2X 2-DPU/worker multiplier the code does not apply (that is the separate H3 issue); within the code's own 1:1 worker=DPU logic a fixed 20-worker job would have computed 0.44*20*160*0.30 = $422.40. The core $0 bug is unaffected by that quibble.  _Correction:_ Confirmed at glue.py:52-58 / services/glue.py:33,41. The example dollar value (~$844.80) presupposes the H3 worker-type fix; the code's own (still-flawed) logic would yield $422.40 for that job were the shadow bug absent. The central claim -- worker-based jobs priced at $0 with no warning -- is correct.

#### 🔴 C2 · ASSUMED_MONTHLY_DPU_HOURS=160 fabricates always-runs hours with no usage evidence  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/glue.py:44-49, 66-74`
- **Evidence:** `ASSUMED_MONTHLY_DPU_HOURS: int = 160` is multiplied into every counted job saving (monthly_cost = 0.44 × dpu_count × 160 × pricing_multiplier). The adapter reads NO usage signal — no get_job_runs (ExecutionTime/DPUSeconds), no CloudWatch (requires_cloudwatch/reads_fast_mode are not declared). The comment itself calls 160 a fixed '8 hr/day × 20 workdays' assumption.
- **Impact:** Any counted Glue dollar is fabricated. A job that runs once a week for 10 minutes is priced as if it consumed 160 DPU-hours/month; an always-on streaming job is under-counted. The dollar bears no relation to the account's actual Glue spend, so the headline saving is not account-specific.
- **Fix:** Derive monthly DPU-hours from glue.get_job_runs aggregate (Σ ExecutionTime×DPU or DPUSeconds over a trailing window) and declare requires_cloudwatch/reads_fast_mode if CloudWatch is used; when no run history is available, emit the rec as a $0 advisory (Counted=False) instead of fabricating 160 hrs. Record an AuditBasis(rate/region/DPU/hours/formula) on each counted finding.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Real. ASSUMED_MONTHLY_DPU_HOURS = 160 (glue.py:48) is multiplied into every counted saving at lines 66-71 (monthly_cost = 0.44 * dpu_count * 160 * pricing_multiplier), gated only by the 0.30 rightsize factor. Verified the adapter reads NO usage signal: get_enhanced_glue_checks (services/glue.py) only calls get_jobs, get_dev_endpoints, get_crawlers -- no get_job_runs (ExecutionTime/DPUSeconds) and no CloudWatch. The GlueModule class declares no requires_cloudwatch / reads_fast_mode attribute. The 160 value is a hard-coded '8 hr/day x 20 workdays' batch assumption (per the comment at lines 46-47) applied identically to a once-a-week 10-minute job and an always-on streaming job. The counted dollar is therefore an assumption, not account-specific usage. Mechanism and lines confirmed.

#### 🟠 H1 · String-vs-float render desync: card shows static EstimatedSavings string, headline counts the computed float  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `reporter_phase_a.py:450-454 (with services/adapters/glue.py:73 and core/result_builder.py:72)`
- **Evidence:** Phase A renders the static string: `if resources[0].get("EstimatedSavings"): ... Estimated Savings: {resources[0].get("EstimatedSavings")}` — i.e. '20-40% with auto-scaling' (services/glue.py:45) or '$316/month per endpoint' (services/glue.py:61). The tab/exec total instead sums the float the adapter computes into `rec["EstimatedMonthlySavings"]` (glue.py:73) → ServiceFindings.total_monthly_savings → summary total (result_builder.py:72). The computed float is never rendered on the card.
- **Impact:** The per-resource card and the headline disagree. A job card says '20-40% with auto-scaling' while the headline counts a precise (often $0 — see C1) DPU figure; a dev-endpoint card says '$316/month per endpoint' while the headline counts $0. Readers cannot reconcile cards to the total.
- **Fix:** Pick one source of truth: render the computed EstimatedMonthlySavings float per card (format as $/mo) and drop or relabel the static EstimatedSavings string, OR have the adapter overwrite EstimatedSavings with the formatted computed value so card == counted.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Real string-vs-float desync. glue's Phase A descriptor sets savings_mode='conditional' (reporter_phase_a.py:307); the card renders the static EstimatedSavings string at lines 450-454 (resources[0].get('EstimatedSavings')) -- i.e. '20-40% with auto-scaling' (services/glue.py:45) or '$316/month per endpoint' (services/glue.py:61). The computed float lives in rec['EstimatedMonthlySavings'] (glue.py:73) and is summed into ServiceFindings.total_monthly_savings (glue.py:82) -> summary total_monthly_savings (result_builder.py:72). Confirmed the float is never rendered on the glue card: glue is in _PHASE_A_SERVICES (reporter_phase_b.py:2507) so should_skip_source_loop() routes it exclusively through Phase A render_grouped_by_category, which only emits EstimatedSavings (the Phase B EstimatedMonthlySavings render at reporter_phase_b.py:1039 is in the containers handler and never reached for glue). Card and headline genuinely disagree.

#### 🟠 H2 · Dev-endpoint advertises $316/mo but is counted as $0; the real ~$1,606/mo saving is missed  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/glue.py:50-64 (with services/adapters/glue.py:52-58)`
- **Evidence:** The dev_endpoint rec carries only EndpointName/Status/Recommendation/EstimatedSavings/CheckCategory — no MaxCapacity/NumberOfWorkers. So the adapter resolves dpu_count=None and sets EstimatedMonthlySavings=0.0 + PricingWarning. The static string is '$316/month per endpoint'. Live pricing: AWSGlue USE1-DEVED-DPU-Hour = $0.44/DPU-hr (SKU H5SXAYMQH485TMM7); a default 5-DPU dev endpoint that is READY bills continuously = 5×0.44×730 = $1,606/mo (not $316).
- **Impact:** A READY dev endpoint is the largest, most concrete Glue saving (delete it) yet it is counted as $0 and even its advertised $316 string understates the true ~$1,606/mo by ~5×. Real account savings are dropped entirely.
- **Fix:** Price dev endpoints from their own DPU footprint: use NumberOfWorkers/WorkerType (or the 5-DPU default) × $0.44 × 730 as the counted saving, with an AuditBasis; remove the hardcoded $316 string.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Mechanism confirmed from code. The dev_endpoint rec (services/glue.py:56-63) carries only EndpointName/Status/Recommendation/EstimatedSavings/CheckCategory -- the shim discards any DPU/worker fields the API returns. So in the adapter rec.get("MaxCapacity", rec.get("NumberOfWorkers")) -> None (both keys absent), line 53 sets EstimatedMonthlySavings = 0.0 + PricingWarning. The card shows the static '$316/month per endpoint' string while the headline counts $0 for a READY endpoint. The missed-savings direction is solid. Caveat: the precise ~$1,606/mo (and the ~5x understatement) rests on AWS pricing facts not derivable from code -- a dev endpoint's actual provisioned DPU (the 5-DPU default minimum), the $0.44/DPU-hr rate, and continuous 730-hr billing. The shim discards the endpoint's real DPU count, so the exact figure cannot be settled from the repo alone, but the core claim (counted $0, real savings dropped, $316 too low) is confirmed.  _Correction:_ Confirmed: READY dev endpoints are counted as $0 (no DPU fields reach the adapter) and the advertised $316 string is never counted. The specific ~$1,606/mo / ~5x magnitude depends on the endpoint's provisioned DPU (default 5), the $0.44 rate, and 730 hrs -- external pricing facts; the shim discards the DPU count so the exact value is not code-verifiable, though the under-statement direction is sound.

#### 🟠 H3 · NumberOfWorkers treated as DPU count and flat $0.44 ignores WorkerType/Flex/streaming  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/glue.py:39-41, 52, 66-72`
- **Evidence:** dpu_count is taken directly from NumberOfWorkers (line 52) with no WorkerType multiplier, and GLUE_DPU_HOURLY is a flat 0.44 regardless of execution class. WorkerType is captured by the shim (services/glue.py:34,42) but never read by the adapter. AWS: G.1X=1 DPU/worker, G.2X=2, G.4X=4, G.8X=8, G.025X(Python-shell)=0.0625 DPU/worker; Flex = $0.29/DPU-hr (validated, USE1-ETL-Flex-DPU-Hour SKU CW2STD52Z73SFDTA, ~34% cheaper) and memory-optimized = $0.52 (USE1-ETL-M-DPU-Hour SKU 8B8U9Y67DA2X92AD). Streaming (always-on) jobs are not modeled at all.
- **Impact:** Even after C1 is fixed, G.2X/G.4X/G.8X jobs are under-priced 2-8× (workers≠DPU), G.025X Python-shell jobs are over-priced ~16×, Flex jobs over-priced ~34%, and always-on streaming jobs (the biggest spend) are mis-modeled by the 160-hr batch assumption. The counted dollar is wrong by type.
- **Fix:** Compute DPU = NumberOfWorkers × dpu_per_worker(WorkerType) (G.1X→1, G.2X→2, G.4X→4, G.8X→8, G.025X→0.0625); select the rate by execution class (Flex $0.29 vs standard $0.44 vs M-DPU $0.52); model streaming separately (730 hrs) from batch.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Real structural mispricing. dpu_count is taken directly from MaxCapacity-or-NumberOfWorkers (glue.py:52) with no WorkerType multiplier, and GLUE_DPU_HOURLY is a flat 0.44 (glue.py:41) regardless of execution class. Confirmed WorkerType is captured by the shim (services/glue.py:34,42) but never read anywhere in the adapter (grep shows no WorkerType reference in services/adapters/glue.py). So worker-based jobs are priced 1 worker = 1 DPU, ignoring G.2X=2 / G.4X=4 / G.8X=8 / G.025X=0.0625 DPU-per-worker, the Flex ($0.29) and memory-optimized ($0.52) rates, and always-on streaming (mis-modeled by the 160-hr batch assumption). The DPU-per-worker ratios and alt rates are external AWS facts, but the code-level defects (WorkerType captured-but-unused, flat single rate, no execution-class/streaming handling) are confirmed. Note the finding's own framing is correct that this only manifests AFTER C1 is fixed: currently the MaxCapacity=0 shadow forces those worker-based jobs to $0, so today they are not 'under-priced 2-8x' -- they are $0; the 2-8x under-pricing is the latent post-C1 behavior.

#### 🟡 M1 · GLUE_RIGHTSIZE_FACTOR=0.30 is an arbitrary reduction factor, not an exact current→target DPU delta  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/glue.py:42-44, 72`
- **Evidence:** `rec_savings = monthly_cost * GLUE_RIGHTSIZE_FACTOR` with GLUE_RIGHTSIZE_FACTOR=0.30. The static string separately claims '20-40%'. There is no target DPU (e.g. an auto-scaling floor) — savings are a blanket 30% of an already-assumed cost.
- **Impact:** Counted savings are a flat fraction of a fabricated cost rather than (current_DPU − target_DPU) × rate × hours, so the figure is not defensible per job. Conflicts with the '20-40%' card string.
- **Fix:** Replace the flat factor with an explicit delta against a defensible target (auto-scaling floor or observed peak DPU from get_job_runs): savings = (current_DPU − target_DPU) × rate × hours.

#### 🟡 M2 · `> 10` DPU/worker gate makes every small over-provisioned job invisible  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/glue.py:37`
- **Evidence:** `if max_capacity > 10 or number_of_workers > 10:` is the only path that appends a job_rightsizing rec.
- **Impact:** A fleet of many ≤10-DPU/worker jobs that are collectively over-provisioned produces zero recommendations and zero counted savings; coverage is gated to a hardcoded threshold.
- **Fix:** Lower or remove the threshold and instead gate on actual utilization (peak vs allocated DPU from get_job_runs), so small over-provisioned jobs are surfaced.

#### 🟡 M3 · $0 advisory recs are not marked Counted=False, so the header counts them as 'counted'  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/glue.py:53-64 (with html_report_generator.py:371-388)`
- **Evidence:** When dpu_count is None/0 the adapter sets EstimatedMonthlySavings=0.0 + PricingWarning but does NOT set rec['Counted']=False. html_report_generator._counted_advisory_counts treats any rec without `Counted is False` as counted (line 384). So dev-endpoint and capacity-less $0 recs inflate the 'X counted' figure while contributing $0 to savings.
- **Impact:** The tab header 'N (X counted, Y advisory)' is dishonest: $0 recs are labeled counted next to a savings total that excludes them, desyncing count from counted-savings. Mirrors the metric-gated-$0 nudge anti-pattern Lambda solves with Counted=False.
- **Fix:** When the adapter cannot price a rec (None/0 dpu_count → $0 + PricingWarning), set rec['Counted']=False so it renders as advisory and is excluded from the counted tally.

#### 🟡 M4 · get_dev_endpoints is not paginated  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/glue.py:50-51`
- **Evidence:** `dev_endpoints = glue.get_dev_endpoints()` is a single call with no paginator and no NextToken loop, unlike get_jobs (line 29) and get_crawlers (line 66) which use `glue.get_paginator(...)`. The Glue GetDevEndpoints API is paginated (returns NextToken).
- **Impact:** In accounts with many dev endpoints, only the first page is examined; READY endpoints beyond the first page are never flagged — real always-on dev-endpoint savings are silently missed.
- **Fix:** Use `glue.get_paginator("get_dev_endpoints").paginate()` and iterate all pages, matching the get_jobs/get_crawlers pattern.

#### 🟢 L1 · Single broad except wraps all three Glue APIs and never classifies permission errors  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/glue.py:26-76`
- **Evidence:** One `try:` spans get_jobs, get_dev_endpoints, and get_crawlers; the handler is `except Exception as e: ctx.warn(f"Could not analyze Glue resources: {e}", "glue")`. AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation on any one API aborts the remaining APIs and is reported only via ctx.warn — never ctx.permission_issue.
- **Impact:** An IAM denial on (say) get_dev_endpoints kills get_crawlers/get_jobs coverage in the same iteration and is misclassified as a generic warning, so the report does not surface a permission gap. Loss of coverage is silent.
- **Fix:** Wrap each API call in its own try/except and route errors through the permission-aware path (AccessDenied/Unauthorized/OptInRequired → ctx.permission_issue, else ctx.warn), mirroring services/_aws_errors.record_aws_error used by the network adapter.

---

### Lambda — `services/adapters/lambda_svc.py`

**Module identity:** Module identity matches services/adapters/CLAUDE.md with NO drift. services/adapters/lambda_svc.py:52-65 declares key="lambda", cli_aliases=("lambda",), display_name="Lambda", required_clients()==("lambda","compute-optimizer","cloudwatch"), requires_cloudwatch=True, reads_fast_mode=True. The `_svc` filename suffix is the documented Python-reserved-word workaround; the module key/alias/display are plain "lambda". The CLAUDE.md row claims (a) PC priced from an arch-aware module constant region-scaled once, (b) CloudWatch-gated on ProvisionedConcurrencyUtilization with saving = unused fraction (1-max_util), (c) no metric -> $0 advisory, (d) requires_cloudwatch/reads_fast_mode, (e) each PC finding carries a structured AuditBasis, (f) Excessive-Memory & ARM are $0 advisory (Counted=False), (g) CO opt-in placeholder -> ctx.warn + dropped, (h) cross-source dedup by normalized bare function name CoH>CO>enhanced. Every clause is confirmed true in code.
