**Findings:**

#### 🟠 H1 · PC utilization metric read by FunctionName-only dimension silently zeroes the only counted enhanced lever for alias/version-configured PC  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **❌ refuted**
- **Location:** `services/lambda_svc.py:83-107, 207-239`
- **Evidence:** _read_pc_max_utilization queries Dimensions=[{'Name':'FunctionName','Value':function_name}] only (lines 95-103) and returns None when Datapoints is empty (lines 104-106). But Provisioned Concurrency can ONLY be configured on a published version or an alias (never $LATEST); the configs come from list_provisioned_concurrency_configs whose FunctionArn carries the qualifier. CloudWatch publishes ProvisionedConcurrencyUtilization keyed with the alias/version 'Resource' dimension, and a query must match the exact published dimension set, so a FunctionName-only query commonly returns no datapoints. The shim then passes max_util=None to the adapter, which sets EstimatedMonthlySavings=0.0 + PricingWarning='requires ProvisionedConcurrencyUtilization metric' and mark_zero_savings_advisory flags Counted=False (adapters/lambda_svc.py:172-176,209-211). The two existing tests (test_pc_utilization_attached_when_metric_present, test_pc_saving_metric_gated_x86) use a fake CloudWatch that returns datapoints for the bare FunctionName, so the gap is uncovered.
- **Impact:** Under-report (safe direction, no false $). PC is documented as 'the only counted enhanced lever', yet for the realistic alias/version PC case it degrades to a $0 advisory even though the allocation bills 24/7 at $0.0000041667/GB-s. A 2048MB function with PC=10 at us-east-1 silently loses ~$614/mo of detectable saving per unused fraction.
- **Fix:** In the shim, read ProvisionedConcurrencyUtilization per PC config using the alias/version Resource dimension, e.g. Dimensions=[{'Name':'FunctionName','Value':name},{'Name':'Resource','Value': f'{name}:{qualifier}'}] where qualifier is derived from pc_config (FunctionArn suffix / alias). Fall back to the FunctionName-only query only if the qualified query has no datapoints. Add a test with a Resource-dimensioned datapoint.
- **Verifier (refuted):** Code mechanism is accurately quoted: services/lambda_svc.py:95-103 queries ProvisionedConcurrencyUtilization with Dimensions=[{FunctionName}] only and returns None on empty datapoints (104-106); services/adapters/lambda_svc.py:172-176 then sets EstimatedMonthlySavings=0.0 + PricingWarning='requires ProvisionedConcurrencyUtilization metric' and mark_zero_savings_advisory (209-211) flags Counted=False. BUT the load-bearing AWS claim is wrong. AWS docs (Lambda 'Viewing metrics for Lambda functions', monitoring-metrics-view.html) state the FunctionName dimension provides 'aggregate metrics for ALL versions and aliases of a function', with Resource being the per-alias/version view and no carve-out excluding the provisioned-concurrency metrics. Lambda publishes these metrics at multiple dimension granularities including FunctionName-only, exactly as for Invocations -- which this same module queries FunctionName-only at line 255 (the standard working pattern). So the asserted 'dimension-mismatch silently zeroes savings' mechanism is contradicted by documentation. The only genuine no-datapoints case is the metric's emission nature, not dimension keying: AWS docs (monitoring-metrics-types.html / monitoring-concurrency.html) say ProvisionedConcurrencyUtilization is derived from ProvisionedConcurrentExecutions and is NOT emitted when the function is inactive/not receiving requests -- so an idle (max-savings) PC allocation emits nothing at ANY dimension, Resource included; querying by qualifier would not recover it. The code docstring at services/lambda_svc.py:88-90 already anticipates this and degrades to a conservative $0 advisory rather than fabricating savings. The finding itself concedes 'safe direction, no false $', so there is zero false-dollar exposure and the deliberate, documented conservative under-report does not warrant HIGH. The tests-don't-cover-the-gap note is a test-fidelity observation (fake CloudWatch keys only on MetricName), not proof of a real cost-correctness defect.

#### 🟡 M1 · Cross-source dedup drops the counted Provisioned-Concurrency rec whenever the same function also appears in CoH or Compute Optimizer  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/lambda_svc.py:112-138`
- **Evidence:** seen_functions is seeded from CoH (lines 113-117) then extended with every kept CO rec (lines 124-131). The enhanced loop then drops ALL enhanced recs for any function already in seen_functions: `for rec in enhanced_recs: fn=_normalize_lambda_fn_name(rec.get('FunctionName','')); if fn not in seen_functions: deduped_enhanced.append(rec)` (lines 133-137). CoH/CO Lambda recommendations are memory-rightsizing only (advisor._normalize_lambda_co_rec emits memorySize options; CO never prices provisioned concurrency). The enhanced PC rec is a DISTINCT lever (the 24/7 allocation cost), but it is dropped together with the advisory Memory/ARM recs.
- **Impact:** Under-report + missing card. When a PC-configured function also has a CoH/CO memory rec, the entire PC counted dollar is silently dropped and its card disappears from the tab. Memory/ARM enhanced recs are already $0 advisory so dropping them is harmless; only PC suffers.
- **Fix:** Exempt the Provisioned-Concurrency category from the cross-source filter (only dedup Excessive-Memory and ARM enhanced recs against seen_functions, since those overlap the memory-rightsizing lever). Keep PC unless the colliding source actually prices provisioned concurrency. Add a test: function in CO memory rec + PC config -> both CO dollar and PC dollar counted.

#### 🟢 L1 · Dead Phase B handler and source-label entry for ('lambda','compute_optimizer') are unreachable  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `reporter_phase_b.py:2362, 2448; html_report_generator.py:3311-3313`
- **Evidence:** html_report_generator dispatch short-circuits to render_grouped_by_category for any service_key in PHASE_A_DESCRIPTORS, and 'lambda' is registered there (reporter_phase_a.py:265, savings_mode 'always'); 'lambda' is also in reporter_phase_b._PHASE_A_SERVICES (line 2503). The Phase B source-loop never runs for lambda, so PHASE_B_HANDLERS[('lambda','compute_optimizer')] = _render_compute_optimizer_source (line 2448) and source_type_label[('lambda','compute_optimizer')]='ML Backed' (line 2362) are dead bindings.
- **Impact:** No functional harm (all three sources render via Phase A render_grouped_by_category and surface in the single Lambda tab). Confusion/maintenance risk only; a future reader may assume CO recs use the unified CO renderer's typesetting.
- **Fix:** Remove the two dead ('lambda','compute_optimizer') bindings or annotate them as intentional in-flight-JSON legacy. No snapshot change expected.

#### 🟢 L2 · Counted PC card renders the prose EstimatedSavings string, not the computed account-specific dollar  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `reporter_phase_a.py:450-451`
- **Evidence:** render_grouped_by_category with savings_mode='always' emits `resources[0].get('EstimatedSavings','Cost optimization')` per category card. For a counted PC rec this is the shim's prose 'Up to 90% if not needed' (services/lambda_svc.py:234), while the real computed dollar lives in EstimatedMonthlySavings/AuditBasis and is only reflected in the tab headline (_counted_advisory_counts + total_monthly_savings).
- **Impact:** Counted total and rendered cards still reconcile at the headline (no leakage), but the per-function card does not display the concrete PC dollar/AuditBasis, weakening report-alone defensibility for the one counted enhanced lever.
- **Fix:** For lambda PC recs render EstimatedMonthlySavings (when Counted) instead of/alongside the prose string. Intentional rendering change -> refresh reporter snapshots.

#### 🟢 L3 · list_provisioned_concurrency_configs is read without pagination  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/lambda_svc.py:206-213`
- **Evidence:** provisioned = lambda_client.list_provisioned_concurrency_configs(FunctionName=function_name); pc_configs = provisioned.get('ProvisionedConcurrencyConfigs', []) — single call, no NextMarker loop (contrast list_functions which uses a paginator at line 168 and CO which loops nextToken).
- **Impact:** A function with more PC configs than one page (many aliases/versions) would have later configs silently omitted, under-counting PC savings. Low likelihood in practice.
- **Fix:** Loop on the response NextMarker (or use get_paginator if available) to enumerate all ProvisionedConcurrencyConfigs.

#### 🟢 L4 · Excessive-Memory and ARM are structurally $0 advisory (no Duration/GB-seconds metric collected)  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/lambda_svc.py:189-200 (shim), services/adapters/lambda_svc.py:148-200`
- **Evidence:** The shim reads only Invocations (line 252), never Duration, so per-invocation GB-seconds cannot be derived; the adapter therefore forces EstimatedMonthlySavings=0.0 + PricingWarning for both Excessive Memory and ARM (adapters/lambda_svc.py:153-154,198-199). This is the documented honesty choice, not leakage.
- **Impact:** No incorrect dollar (both are Counted=False, rendered-not-counted). These nudges never realize a counted saving even when the underlying function is materially over-provisioned; they also correctly avoid recommending against free-tier-covered usage.
- **Fix:** OPTIONAL: wire AWS/Lambda Duration (Average) x Invocations x mem_gb to derive GB-seconds and price Excessive-Memory at the exact current->target memory delta, gated like PC (real metric or stay $0). Until then keep them advisory; do NOT let either become a config-only counted number.

#### 🟢 M2 · ARM runtime allowlist drift and Image-package exclusion permanently skip the ARM nudge for newer/container runtimes  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/lambda_svc.py:47-60, 247`
- **Evidence:** ARM_SUPPORTED_RUNTIMES is a hardcoded tuple ending at python3.12 / nodejs20.x / dotnet8 and omits python3.13, nodejs22.x, ruby3.x, provided.al2023, dotnet9. The ARM gate requires `runtime in ARM_SUPPORTED_RUNTIMES` (line 247); a container-image function has no Runtime key (defaults to 'Unknown') and is never matched. All are Graviton-capable.
- **Impact:** Missed nudge only, NOT a wrong dollar: ARM Migration is forced to $0 advisory regardless (adapters/lambda_svc.py:198-199), so no counted savings are affected. Pure coverage/awareness gap.
- **Fix:** Either broaden ARM_SUPPORTED_RUNTIMES (and add a container-image branch), or flip the test to an exclusion allowlist of known-x86-only runtimes. Lowest priority because the lever carries no $.

---

### Lightsail — `services/adapters/lightsail.py`

**Module identity:** key="lightsail", cli_aliases=("lightsail",), display_name="Lightsail", required_clients()=("lightsail",) — confirmed in services/adapters/lightsail.py lines 19-25. No CloudWatch read and no fast_mode gating (correctly absent — there is no metric read; the oversized check is pure config). Lightsail consumes NEITHER Cost Optimization Hub NOR Compute Optimizer ("lightsail" absent from scan_orchestrator._HUB_SERVICES; no get_lightsail_compute_optimizer_recommendations helper) — so "missing CoH/CO" is not a fair finding. Pricing is NOT live: the adapter abandoned get_instance_monthly_price("AmazonLightsail",...) as structurally dead (returned 0) and prices every rec from the hardcoded module dict services/lightsail.py:_BUNDLE_COSTS (us-east-1 anchored) × ctx.pricing_multiplier. Renders via Phase A (PHASE_A_DESCRIPTORS["lightsail"], savings_mode="conditional", close_div_location="inner"); no PHASE_B_HANDLERS entry.

**Verdict:** The lightsail adapter is a Phase-A, bundle-dict-priced, no-CoH/no-CO adapter whose counted savings are systematically unreliable. CRITICAL: oversized_instances sums the FULL bundle cost into total_monthly_savings while its card displays only 30% and it has no utilization metric — fabricated, inflated, and desynced. The _BUNDLE_COSTS dict is a synthetic ×2 series mis-rated 14-25% vs the live AmazonLightsail API; Windows is priced as Linux (~45% under); unknown/missing bundle ids fabricate a flat $20 / medium price; and unused static IPs display $3.65 but count $0. Coverage omits databases, load balancers, disks, and snapshots (declared-but-empty source keys), and the single coarse try/except mis-classifies permission failures. Counted ≠ displayed in both directions, so neither the tab headline nor the per-rec cards are individually defensible.

**Pricing validation:** Validated LIVE via AWS Pricing MCP (AmazonLightsail, us-east-1, publicationDate 2026-06-12). Lightsail Instance Linux standard bundles (USE1-BundleUsage:<mem>, hourly×744): 0.5GB $0.00672/hr=$5.00, 1GB $0.0094=$6.99, 2GB $0.01612=$11.99, 4GB $0.03225=$23.99, 8GB $0.05913=$43.99, 16GB $0.1129=$84.00, 32GB $0.22043=$164.00 — proving the dict's small/medium/large are 14-25% high and nano is 30% low (H1). Windows bundles (USE1-BundleUsage:<mem>_win) validated ~1.83× Linux: 4GB_win $0.05913/hr=$43.99 vs Linux $23.99 (H2). Lightsail Networking USE1-UnusedStaticIP confirmed $0.005/hr (first hour free) ≈ $3.65/mo ×730 — the hardcoded string is correct for us-east-1 (H4). _DEFAULT_BUNDLE_COST=20.00 and the medium_2_0 default correspond to NO live bundle (H3). All rates fetched live; none trusted from memory.

**Cost checks:**

| Check | Status | Trigger | Savings basis |
|---|---|---|---|
| idle_instances | counted | instance state == "stopped" (services/lightsail.py:61); a stopped Lightsail instance is still billed, so deletion is a real saving | Display string f"${get_lightsail_bundle_cost(bundle_id):.2f}/month" (line 68). Adapter COUNTS full get_lightsail_bundle_cost(BundleId) × ctx.pricing_multiplier (adapter lines 49-52). Constant source: _BUNDLE_COSTS dict (line 21-29), fallback _DEFAULT_BUNDLE_COST=20.00. us-east-1 anchored, region-scaled once. |
| oversized_instances | counted | state == "running" AND ("xlarge" in bundleId.lower() OR "large" in bundleId.lower()) (services/lightsail.py:73). Pure size heuristic, NO utilization metric. | Display string f"${get_lightsail_bundle_cost(bundle_id) * 0.3:.2f}/month potential" (line 82) — 0.3 reduction factor, no target bundle. BUT adapter COUNTS the FULL bundle cost (keys on BundleId presence, ignores the 0.3) → counted is 3.33× the displayed value. |
| unused_static_ips | advisory | static_ip has no attachedTo (services/lightsail.py:92). Unattached static IP is billed $0.005/hr after first free hour. | Display string hardcoded "$3.65/month" (line 98) = $0.005/hr × 730 (live AmazonLightsail USE1-UnusedStaticIP confirmed $0.005/hr). Rec carries NO BundleId → adapter loop (lines 49-50) skips it → contributes $0 to total_monthly_savings. |
| load_balancer_optimization | advisory | Source key declared in checks dict (services/lightsail.py:45) but NEVER populated — no code scans get_load_balancers. | Always empty SourceBlock (count=0). No savings. Renders nothing. |
| database_optimization | advisory | Source key declared in checks dict (services/lightsail.py:46) but NEVER populated — no code scans get_relational_databases. | Always empty SourceBlock (count=0). No savings. Renders nothing. |

**Findings:**

#### 🔴 C1 · oversized_instances counted at 100% of bundle cost (metric-less nudge) while card displays 30% — fabricated/inflated counted dollars + headline desync  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/lightsail.py / services/lightsail.py:adapter 48-52; shim 73-86`
- **Evidence:** Shim writes display string EstimatedSavings=f"${get_lightsail_bundle_cost(bundle_id) * 0.3:.2f}/month potential" (shim line 82) and its own Note: 'verify actual utilization before downsizing' (line 84). The adapter sums the FULL cost: `bundle_name=rec.get("BundleId",""); if bundle_name: monthly=get_lightsail_bundle_cost(bundle_name)*ctx.pricing_multiplier; savings+=monthly` (adapter 49-52) — it never applies the 0.3 factor. There is NO utilization metric (no CloudWatch read).
- **Impact:** For a running large_2_0 the card reads '$16.47/month potential' but the headline (html_report_generator.py:3179-3188 uses total_monthly_savings) counts the full $54.90 — a 3.33× over-count of a saving that has no usage basis at all. Every oversized rec fabricates counted dollars and desyncs the tab headline from its own cards.
- **Fix:** Make oversized advisory: set Counted=False and contribute $0 to total_monthly_savings (mirror Lambda metric-gated $0 advisory), OR compute the EXACT current_bundle−target_bundle delta against a concrete one-size-down bundle and count THAT. Stop summing full bundle cost for a 'verify utilization' nudge. Skip oversized recs in the adapter's savings loop (they should not carry a counted BundleId) until backed by a real metric.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Disproof attempt failed; finding holds at the cited lines. services/lightsail.py:82 builds the card string as get_lightsail_bundle_cost(bundle_id)*0.3 (30% nudge) with Note at :84 'verify actual utilization before downsizing', and the oversized trigger (:73) is purely name-based ('xlarge'/'large' in bundle_id) with NO CloudWatch/utilization read anywhere in the module. The adapter loop services/adapters/lightsail.py:49-52 sets bundle_name=rec.get('BundleId','') (oversized recs DO carry BundleId, set at services/lightsail.py:77), so the branch fires and adds get_lightsail_bundle_cost(bundle_name)*pricing_multiplier — the FULL bundle cost, never the 0.3 factor. For large_2_0 the card shows $54.90*0.3=$16.47 while counted=$54.90 (3.33x over-count, 1/0.3). I confirmed the card IS rendered (reporter_phase_a.py:452-454 prints resources[0]['EstimatedSavings'] for lightsail's conditional savings_mode) and the headline IS the full sum (html_report_generator.py:3179/3187-3188 renders total_monthly_savings; _calculate_service_savings:3078-3079 returns the canonical total unchanged). Headline-vs-card desync and metric-less fabricated counted dollars both real.

#### 🟠 H1 · Fabricated mid-tier _BUNDLE_COSTS (synthetic ×2 geometric series, not AWS list prices)  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/lightsail.py:21-29`
- **Evidence:** _BUNDLE_COSTS = {nano_2_0:3.50, micro_2_0:6.86, small_2_0:13.72, medium_2_0:27.45, large_2_0:54.90, xlarge_2_0:80.00, 2xlarge_2_0:160.00} — a 3.43→6.86→13.72→27.45→54.90 doubling series. Live AmazonLightsail (Lightsail Instance, us-east-1, Linux, hourly×744) validated via Pricing MCP: 2GB(small)=$0.01612/hr=$11.99 (dict +14.4%); 4GB(medium)=$0.03225/hr=$23.99 (dict +14.4%); 8GB(large)=$0.05913/hr=$43.99 (dict +24.8%); 0.5GB(nano)=$0.00672/hr=$5.00 (dict −30%); 16GB(xlarge)=$84.00 (dict −4.8%); 32GB(2xlarge)=$164.00 (dict −2.4%).
- **Impact:** Every idle/oversized counted dollar is mis-rated: small/medium/large overstated 14-25%, nano understated 30%. AWS's real progression ($5→$7→$12→$24→$44→$84→$164) is not a ×2 series; the dict diverges most exactly where instances are most common (medium/large).
- **Fix:** Replace each dict value with the live per-bundle monthly price = AmazonLightsail Lightsail Instance hourly (USE1-BundleUsage:<mem>) × 730. Record an AuditBasis (rate/region/formula) per bundle. Prefer fetching from the Pricing API keyed on the bundle usagetype rather than a static dict so it tracks AWS price changes.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Validated against live AWS Pricing API (AmazonLightsail, Lightsail Instance, us-east-1, Linux, OnDemand, x744). _BUNDLE_COSTS (services/lightsail.py:21-29) vs real monthly: nano_2_0 $3.50 vs $5.00 (-30%); micro_2_0 $6.86 vs $6.99 (-1.9%); small_2_0 $13.72 vs $11.99 (+14.4%); medium_2_0 $27.45 vs $23.99 (+14.4%); large_2_0 $54.90 vs $43.99 (+24.8%); xlarge_2_0 $80.00 vs $84.00 (-4.8%); 2xlarge_2_0 $160.00 vs $164.00 (-2.4%). The dict is a synthetic x2 series (6.86->13.72->27.45->54.90 are exact doublings) whereas AWS's real progression is $5->$7->$12->$24->$44->$84->$164. Divergence is largest exactly at medium/large (+14-25%), the most common sizes, overstating every idle/oversized counted dollar there; nano understated 30%. Finding's per-tier numbers match live data exactly.

#### 🟠 H2 · Windows instances priced as Linux (operatingSystem ignored)  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✏️ revised**
- **Location:** `services/lightsail.py:57-68 (read), 21-36 (dict/lookup)`
- **Evidence:** The shim reads only instance.get("bundleId") (line 59) and never instance.get("operatingSystem") nor the bundle's _win_ suffix; get_lightsail_bundle_cost keys solely on bundle_id (line 34-36). Live MCP: 4GB Windows USE1-BundleUsage:4GB_win = $0.05913/hr = $43.99/mo vs Linux 4GB $0.03225/hr = $23.99/mo (Windows ≈1.83×); 2GB_win $21.99 vs Linux $11.99; 16GB_win $124 vs Linux $84.
- **Impact:** A stopped/oversized Windows instance is priced at the Linux dict value → counted saving understated ~45%. (Compounding: Windows bundle ids like medium_win_2_0 are also absent from the dict, so they actually hit the $20 default — see H3.)
- **Fix:** Read operatingSystem (or detect the _win_ token in bundleId) and select an OS-aware price (separate Windows entries, or pin the AmazonLightsail usagetype <mem>_win). Map OS before pricing.
- **Verifier (revised):** The underlying gap is real but the stated mechanism/magnitude is wrong. Confirmed: the module reads only instance.get('bundleId') (services/lightsail.py:59), never operatingSystem, and get_lightsail_bundle_cost keys solely on bundle_id (:34-36) against a 7-entry Linux-only dict with no Windows prices. BUT a real Windows Lightsail instance returns a bundleId containing '_win_' (e.g. medium_win_2_0), which is NOT a key in _BUNDLE_COSTS, so it falls to _DEFAULT_BUNDLE_COST=$20 (:31,36) — it does NOT get 'the Linux dict value', and the '~45% understated' figure (which assumes the Linux medium price) is not the actual path. This collapses into H3's $20-default behavior. The finding's own impact note concedes this. Real issue: OS dimension dropped + no Windows prices in dict; corrected mechanism: Windows ids miss the dict and hit the $20 default (e.g. medium_win 4GB real $43.99 counted at $20, ~55% understated), not a Linux-dict-value substitution.  _Correction:_ Windows instances are NOT priced at a Linux dict value; their '_win_' bundle ids are absent from _BUNDLE_COSTS and resolve to the $20 _DEFAULT_BUNDLE_COST (same path as H3). Real consequence: e.g. medium_win_2_0 (4GB Windows, real ~$43.99/mo) is counted at $20 (~55% understatement), not at the Linux medium price ~$23.99. The genuine defect is that operatingSystem is ignored and no Windows list prices exist in the dict.

#### 🟠 H3 · $20 default and medium_2_0 missing-bundle default fabricate counted dollars for gen-3 / Windows / optimized bundles  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/lightsail.py:31, 34-36, 59`
- **Evidence:** _DEFAULT_BUNDLE_COST=20.00 (line 31); get_lightsail_bundle_cost returns _BUNDLE_COSTS.get(bundle_id, _DEFAULT_BUNDLE_COST) (line 36) — silently invents $20 for any id not in the 7-entry _2_0-Linux-standard dict. get_instances returns gen-3 (medium_3_0), Windows (medium_win_2_0), and ComputeOptimized/MemoryOptimized ids — NONE are in the dict → all priced at flat $20. Separately, a missing bundleId defaults to bundle_id=instance.get("bundleId") or "medium_2_0" (line 59) → fabricates the medium price.
- **Impact:** A counted saving with no real basis: $20 is unrelated to the actual bundle (real gen-3/optimized prices range $5–$1764), and medium_2_0 forces $27.45 onto an unknown instance. Both leak fabricated dollars into total_monthly_savings exactly like a $0/placeholder leak.
- **Fix:** On an unknown bundle id, ctx.warn(...) and SKIP the rec from the counted total (do not invent $20); the adapter loop already only sums recs with a BundleId, so emit no BundleId / Counted=False for unknown bundles. Remove the `or "medium_2_0"` default — warn and skip when bundleId is missing. Extend the dict (or live lookup) to cover gen-3, Windows, and Compute/Memory-optimized bundle ids.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Code matches the finding exactly. services/lightsail.py:31 _DEFAULT_BUNDLE_COST=20.00; :34-36 get_lightsail_bundle_cost returns _BUNDLE_COSTS.get(bundle_id, _DEFAULT_BUNDLE_COST), so any id outside the 7-entry _2_0-Linux-standard dict (gen-3 medium_3_0, Windows *_win_*, Compute/Memory/StorageOptimized — the live API confirms these bundle families exist, e.g. ComputeOptimizedBundleUsage:4GB) silently resolves to $20. Idle (stopped) recs carry a BundleId for ANY bundle (:66), so the adapter (services/adapters/lightsail.py:49-52) counts that $20 into total_monthly_savings — a fabricated figure unrelated to the real bundle, whose true range is ~$5 (nano) to ~$1764 (256GB) per live pricing. Separately, :59 bundle_id = instance.get('bundleId') or 'medium_2_0' forces $27.45 onto any instance missing a bundleId. Both leak fabricated counted dollars exactly as described.

#### 🟠 H4 · unused_static_ips displayed '$3.65/month' but contributes $0 to the counted total (displayed-but-uncounted real saving)  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/lightsail.py / services/lightsail.py:adapter 48-53; shim 91-101`
- **Evidence:** Shim sets EstimatedSavings="$3.65/month" (line 98) and emits NO BundleId. Adapter loop: `bundle_name=rec.get("BundleId",""); if bundle_name: ... savings+=monthly` (adapter 49-52) — the static-IP rec has no BundleId so the branch is skipped → $0 counted. Live MCP confirms the rate is real: AmazonLightsail USE1-UnusedStaticIP $0.005/hr (first hour free) ≈ $3.65/mo (×730), so the saving genuinely exists.
- **Impact:** The card advertises $3.65/month per unattached static IP but the tab headline omits it entirely; the executive-summary per-service total (html_report_generator.py:2280-2286 / _calculate_service_savings 3076-3079 returns the canonical total) under-reports by $3.65 × (#unused IPs). Counted ≠ displayed in the under-count direction.
- **Fix:** Count the static-IP saving: write a per-rec dollar (e.g. EstimatedMonthlySavings = 0.005*730*pricing_multiplier) onto the rec and add it to total_monthly_savings, OR give the adapter a static-IP branch. Region-scale the $3.65 string instead of hardcoding us-east-1. Make counted == displayed.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Confirmed displayed-but-uncounted under-count. services/lightsail.py:93-100 emits the unused_static_ips rec with EstimatedSavings='$3.65/month' (:98) and NO BundleId key. The adapter (services/adapters/lightsail.py:49-53) does bundle_name=rec.get('BundleId',''); if bundle_name: ... savings+=monthly — the static-IP rec yields '' so the branch is skipped (explicit comment :53 'else: bundle unknown; skip'), contributing $0 to total_monthly_savings. Yet the card IS rendered: lightsail's conditional savings_mode prints resources[0]['EstimatedSavings'] (reporter_phase_a.py:452-454), and _extract_lightsail_details (:177-182) lists each StaticIpName, so '$3.65/month' is shown per category. The headline (html_report_generator.py:3188) and exec-summary per-service sum (2280-2286 via _calculate_service_savings:3078-3079 canonical total) therefore omit $3.65 x (#unused IPs). Counted < displayed in the under-count direction, as claimed.

#### 🟡 M1 · Whole Lightsail resource classes never scanned (databases, load balancers, disks, snapshots) — declared source keys always empty  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/lightsail.py:41-47 (checks dict), 49-101 (only get_instances + get_static_ips called)`
- **Evidence:** The shim calls only get_paginator("get_instances") (line 51) and get_static_ips() (line 88). load_balancer_optimization and database_optimization keys are declared (lines 45-46) but never appended to. No call to get_relational_databases / get_load_balancers / get_disks / get_instance_snapshots / get_disk_snapshots. Live billable surfaces exist (productFamily list from MCP: Lightsail Database, Lightsail Load Balancing, Lightsail Storage, Lightsail Snapshot).
- **Impact:** Real saving surfaces missed: idle/oversized Lightsail DBs (~$0.0806/hr 2GB-HA), load balancers (~$18/mo each, 0-target LBs), unattached block-storage disks ($0.10/GB-mo), and manual snapshots ($0.05/GB-mo). The two declared keys render nothing (empty SourceBlocks, skipped by the count>0 guard in render_grouped_by_category line 413 — not a broken card, but dead keys).
- **Fix:** Either implement scans for get_relational_databases / get_load_balancers / get_disks / snapshots (each with its own live rate + AuditBasis), or remove the unused database_optimization / load_balancer_optimization keys and document the coverage scope in CLAUDE.md.

#### 🟡 M2 · oversized gated to hardcoded 'large'/'xlarge' substring allowlist — running non-large instances never evaluated  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/lightsail.py:73`
- **Evidence:** if instance_state == "running" and ("xlarge" in bundle_id.lower() or "large" in bundle_id.lower()). "large" is itself a substring of "xlarge"/"2xlarge", so the explicit "xlarge" clause is redundant; more importantly any running instance whose bundle id lacks the 'large' token (nano/micro/small/medium, and all gen-3/optimized names) is never considered for rightsizing regardless of utilization.
- **Impact:** Coverage gated to a size-name allowlist (mirrors the EC2 prev-gen t2-only finding). A low-utilization running medium_2_0 is silently ignored. Combined with C1, the check both over-fires (counts 100%) and under-covers (only 'large' names).
- **Fix:** Drive rightsizing from a utilization signal (CloudWatch CPUUtilization/metric) across all running bundles, not a name substring; or document that only large/xlarge are in scope. Remove the redundant "xlarge" clause.

#### 🟡 M3 · Coarse single try/except with generic ctx.warn — no AccessDenied→permission_issue classification; one describe failure aborts the whole scan  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/lightsail.py:49-104`
- **Evidence:** A single try wraps BOTH get_instances pagination AND get_static_ips (lines 49-101); the only handler is `except Exception as e: ctx.warn(f"Could not analyze Lightsail resources: {e}", "lightsail")` (lines 103-104). No classification of AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation/OptInRequired to ctx.permission_issue (contrast services/_aws_errors.record_aws_error used by network.py).
- **Impact:** A static-IP permission gap (lightsail:GetStaticIps) raises and loses the already-collected instance findings too (silent under-reporting). Permission failures are logged as a generic warning, not surfaced as a permission_issue, so the operator cannot distinguish 'no resources' from 'access denied'.
- **Fix:** Split into per-call try blocks (instances independent of static IPs) and classify AccessDenied/Unauthorized/OptInRequired via record_aws_error → ctx.permission_issue; keep partial results when one call fails.

#### 🟢 D1 · services/adapters/CLAUDE.md lightsail row is stale (claims live AWS Pricing API)  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/CLAUDE.md:Live Pricing table, lightsail.py row`
- **Evidence:** CLAUDE.md lists lightsail.py under 'Live Pricing (19 adapters)' with Method `get_instance_monthly_price("AmazonLightsail", ...)` and Pricing Source 'AWS Pricing API'. The adapter explicitly abandoned that path as dead (adapter lines 41-46: 'The previous get_instance_monthly_price() path was structurally dead (returned 0 every time)') and prices from the hardcoded _BUNDLE_COSTS dict; the adapter does not import get_instance_monthly_price.
- **Impact:** Doc/code mismatch: the row mis-classifies lightsail as live-priced when it is a hardcoded bundle-dict adapter, obscuring the fabricated-price risk (H1-H3) from reviewers.
- **Fix:** Move lightsail.py to a 'bundle-dict / flat-rate' description: Method = get_lightsail_bundle_cost(bundle_id) over _BUNDLE_COSTS (×pricing_multiplier), Pricing Source = 'module dict (NOT live)'.

#### 🟢 L1 · get_static_ips() is a single un-paginated call — large accounts silently truncate  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/lightsail.py:88-89`
- **Evidence:** static_ips_response = lightsail.get_static_ips(); static_ips = static_ips_response.get("staticIps", []) — one call, no paginator (contrast get_instances which IS paginated via get_paginator at line 51). get_static_ips returns a nextPageToken that is never followed.
- **Impact:** An account with many static IPs silently drops the unused IPs beyond the first page → missed savings, no warning.
- **Fix:** Loop on the nextPageToken from get_static_ips (it accepts pageToken) until exhausted, mirroring the get_instances paginator.

#### 🟢 L2 · Flat us-east-1 bundle prices region-scaled by the EC2-derived pricing_multiplier (does not track Lightsail per-region list prices); $3.65 IP string not region-scaled  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/lightsail.py:51 (multiplier); services/lightsail.py:98 (IP string)`
- **Evidence:** monthly = get_lightsail_bundle_cost(bundle_name) * ctx.pricing_multiplier (adapter line 51). pricing_multiplier is an EC2-region factor (core/scan_context.py:42); Lightsail publishes its own per-region bundle prices that do not track the EC2 curve. The applied-once pattern is correct for a constant (per services/adapters/CLAUDE.md), but the multiplier is the wrong curve. Separately the static-IP "$3.65/month" string (shim line 98) is a bare us-east-1 constant never region-scaled.
- **Impact:** Region error in non-us-east-1 bundle savings (direction depends on region); the multiplier is applied once (not doubled), so this is an approximation, not a double-count. Static-IP string is mis-stated outside us-east-1 (but it is uncounted anyway — see H4).
- **Fix:** Prefer the real per-region Lightsail bundle price (Pricing API keyed on region), or document the EC2-multiplier approximation explicitly in an AuditBasis. Region-scale the static-IP rate from $0.005/hr × 730 × multiplier when counted.

---

### MediaStore — `services/adapters/mediastore.py`

**Module identity:** CONFIRMED, matches services/adapters/CLAUDE.md. mediastore.py row reads "get_s3_monthly_price_per_gb(\"STANDARD\") | AWS Pricing API" — reality matches: services/adapters/mediastore.py:15-22 declares key="mediastore", cli_aliases=("mediastore",), display_name="MediaStore", reads_fast_mode=True, required_clients()->("mediastore","cloudwatch"). Pricing: when ctx.pricing_engine present the adapter calls ctx.pricing_engine.get_s3_monthly_price_per_gb("STANDARD") (region-correct, no multiplier; core/pricing_engine.py:668-680); else fallback 0.023*ctx.pricing_multiplier (mediastore.py:46). There is NO get_mediastore_* PricingEngine method — the S3-Standard rate is borrowed, as documented. Not in _HUB_SERVICES/type_map and pulls no Compute Optimizer helper (grep of scan_orchestrator.py/advisor.py for "mediastore" returns nothing) — so the "no CoH/CO" structure is correct and a missing-CoH finding is out of scope. Deviation from doc: CLAUDE.md does NOT mention that the adapter reads 4 CloudWatch metrics yet omits requires_cloudwatch (inherits _base.py:24 default False) — see finding M3.

**Verdict:** The mediastore adapter is a thin borrowed-rate wrapper: it emits a single 'enhanced_checks' SourceBlock from get_enhanced_mediastore_checks (services/mediastore.py) with exactly ONE live check — Unused Resource Cleanup (ACTIVE container, zero RequestCount+BytesDownloaded+BytesUploaded over 14 days) priced at the S3-Standard $/GB rate times last-datapoint BucketSizeBytes average. It is correctly outside CoH/Compute Optimizer scope; renders via the generic per-rec fallback (no PHASE_B_HANDLERS entry, not skip-per-rec, not Phase A). The borrowed S3-Standard rate is VALIDATED defensible — live AWS Pricing shows MediaStore's own Standard storage SKU bills at $0.0230/GB-mo, identical to S3 STANDARD; the $0.02/GB ingest constant is also correct. Region scaling is single-applied (no double-multiply). CRITICAL bug C1: per-metric `except: continue` plus bare excepts silently turn a throttled/denied CloudWatch read into total_activity=0, falsely flagging an active container as deletable AND fabricating a storage saving — failed activity reads must abstain and classify permission errors. HIGH bug H1: an empty/size-read-failed container yields a $0 rec that is still counted by total_recommendations=len(recs) (no Counted=False) — count-hygiene violation. MEDIUM: render-vs-count desync (card shows the helper's fallback-rate savings_str, not the counted engine-rate EstimatedMonthlySavings) M1; no fast-mode gating despite reads_fast_mode=True M2; requires_cloudwatch undeclared M3; ListContainers AccessDenied routed to generic warn not permission_issue M4; no structured AuditBasis M5. LOW limitations: no pagination L1, no under-utilization check L2, Standard-class assumption vs cheaper MediaStore IA L3, and the ingest term is structurally always $0 so the 'dropped ingest' concern is moot L4. Read-only audit; no files modified. Fix order: C1 -> H1 -> M1..M5 -> L1..L4.

**Pricing validation:** Validated against the LIVE AWS Pricing API (AWSElementalMediaStore, us-east-1) — MediaStore is NOT fully retired from the Price List API and has its OWN dedicated pricing: (1) STANDARD storage SKU HUGWWZUKMZ9M573N, productFamily 'Storage', storageclass 'Standard' = $0.0230/GB-month — EXACTLY equal to the borrowed S3 STANDARD rate (core/pricing_engine.py:207 FALLBACK_S3_GB_MONTH['STANDARD']=0.023 and adapter fallback 0.023). The borrowed-rate model is therefore DEFENSIBLE for Standard-class storage. (2) Ingest SKU USE1-Ingest-Optimized-Bytes = $0.0200/GB — confirms the helper's hardcoded 0.02 ingest constant (services/mediastore.py:87) is correct (though structurally always 0 in fired recs, see L4). (3) MediaStore Infrequent-Access storage SKU FGWYKK54QUCW8MZ4 = $0.0125/GB-month (matches S3 STANDARD_IA) — the adapter always assumes Standard, so it overstates ~1.84x for IA-stored bytes (L3). Region scaling verified single-applied: engine path get_s3_monthly_price_per_gb('STANDARD') returns region-correct $/GB with NO adapter-side multiplier (adapters/mediastore.py:42-43), fallback applies 0.023*ctx.pricing_multiplier exactly once (46) — no double-apply. Pricing-filter determinism (MaxResults/SKU selection) is owned by the audited S3 engine path (_fetch_s3_price), out of mediastore scope.

**Cost checks:**

| Check | Status | Trigger | Savings basis |
|---|---|---|---|
| Unused MediaStore Container Cleanup (unused_containers) | counted | Container Status==ACTIVE (services/mediastore.py:36) AND total_activity==0 over trailing 14 days, where total_activity = sum of CloudWatch Sum datapoints for RequestCount + BytesDownloaded + BytesUploaded (services/mediastore.py:41-56,95). | Adapter-counted EstimatedMonthlySavings = EstimatedStorageGB * S3-STANDARD $/GB. EstimatedStorageGB = LAST BucketSizeBytes Average datapoint over 14d / 1024^3 (services/mediastore.py:60-71). Rate = ctx.pricing_engine.get_s3_monthly_price_per_gb('STANDARD') (region-correct, no multiplier) OR 0.023*ctx.pricing_multiplier fallback (services/adapters/mediastore.py:41-49). Ingest cost (monthly_ingest_gb*0.02) is computed in the helper but DROPPED by the adapter's recompute (and is structurally always $0 here, see L4). A delete saving = 100% of measured storage cost. |
| access_optimization bucket | advisory | Bucket initialized at services/mediastore.py:25 but NEVER populated anywhere in the helper. | Emits no recommendations; contributes 0 to count and savings. |
| cors_policies bucket | advisory | Bucket initialized at services/mediastore.py:25 but NEVER populated anywhere in the helper. | Emits no recommendations; contributes 0 to count and savings. |

**Findings:**

#### 🔴 C1 · Silent CloudWatch read failures yield false-unused + fabricated saving (no warn, no permission classification)  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/mediastore.py:45-58, 60-73, 75-89, 95-109`
- **Evidence:** Per-activity-metric loop swallows ANY error and just skips the metric: `for metric_name in metrics_to_check: try: ...get_metric_statistics(...) total_activity += sum(...) except Exception: continue` (lines 46-58). The size read uses a bare `except Exception: storage_gb = 0` (72-73) and the ingest read `except Exception: ingest_cost = 0` (88-89). NONE of these call ctx.warn/ctx.permission_issue. The unused-container rec is appended solely on `if total_activity == 0:` (95). So a throttle/AccessDenied/transient error on the 3 activity reads leaves total_activity at its initialized 0 while the independent size read can still succeed with storage_gb>0 -> an ACTIVE, in-use container is flagged 'no activity ... consider deletion' with a non-zero EstimatedMonthlySavings.
- **Impact:** Most dangerous bug: (a) SAFETY — recommends deleting a live media container whose activity reads merely failed; (b) $ — fabricates a storage saving on a non-idle resource; (c) permission gaps are invisible (AccessDenied on cloudwatch:GetMetricStatistics is swallowed, never surfaced as a permission_issue). A failed activity read must abstain, not assert 'unused'.
- **Fix:** Wrap each get_metric_statistics call so AccessDenied/Unauthorized/OptInRequired route to ctx.permission_issue and throttling to ctx.warn via services/_aws_errors.record_aws_error; on ANY activity-metric read failure, set a `read_failed` flag and SKIP the container (do not append an unused rec). Only emit when all three activity reads succeeded AND returned datapoints. Mirror the _report_aws_error/record_aws_error pattern used in services/efs_fsx.py / network adapters.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified exactly as described in services/mediastore.py. Activity loop (45-58) uses bare `except Exception: continue` with no ctx.warn; size read (60-73) -> `except Exception: storage_gb = 0`; ingest read (75-89) -> `except Exception: ingest_cost = 0`. None classify permissions. The outer `except ... ctx.warn` at 110-112 does NOT cover these because the inner blocks fully consume their own exceptions, so nothing propagates and no warn fires. A throttle/AccessDenied/transient failure on the 3 activity reads leaves total_activity at its initialized 0, and line 95 `if total_activity == 0:` appends the 'no activity ... consider deletion' rec (102-105). The size read is an independent try block, so it can succeed (storage_gb>0) while activity reads fail, and the adapter attaches a non-zero EstimatedMonthlySavings (services/adapters/mediastore.py:49). Read-failure is indistinguishable from genuine zero activity (abstain-vs-assert safety bug). AccessDenied on cloudwatch:GetMetricStatistics is swallowed, never surfaced via the codebase's own services/_aws_errors.record_aws_error permission path. All cited line ranges (45-58, 60-73, 75-89, 95-109) match. The fabricated-$ sub-claim is correctly scoped to the partial-failure case (size read succeeds); the false-unused safety bug holds in all failure cases.

#### 🟠 H1 · $0 no-storage recommendation is counted in total_recommendations (count-hygiene)  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/mediastore.py:47-56, 60`
- **Evidence:** `if estimated_gb > 0: rec_savings = ...; rec['EstimatedMonthlySavings']=round(...) ... else: rec['EstimatedMonthlySavings']=0.0; rec['PricingWarning']='requires EstimatedStorageGB for quantified savings'` (47-54). The $0 rec is NOT removed from `recs` and is NOT marked `Counted=False`, then `total_recommendations=len(recs)` (60) counts it. The helper appends the rec whenever total_activity==0 regardless of storage_gb (services/mediastore.py:95), so an empty (or size-read-failed) container produces a $0 rec. _counted_advisory_counts (html_report_generator.py:371-388) treats it as counted because Counted!=False.
- **Impact:** A $0 'recommendation' inflates the per-service and executive-summary recommendation headline with no realizable dollar — counted-without-dollars, the exact hygiene violation the brief calls out (mirror S3 total_recs hygiene / Lambda mark_zero_savings_advisory).
- **Fix:** When estimated_gb<=0, set rec['Counted']=False (advisory) and exclude it from total_recommendations, e.g. total_recommendations = sum(1 for r in recs if r.get('Counted') is not False). Keep total_monthly_savings as the float sum (already 0 for these).
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified in services/adapters/mediastore.py. The else branch (52-54) sets rec['EstimatedMonthlySavings']=0.0 + PricingWarning but does NOT remove the rec or set Counted=False; total_recommendations=len(recs) at line 60 counts it. Confirmed downstream: core/result_builder.py:71 computes the executive-summary total as sum(f.total_recommendations for f in findings.values()), so the $0 rec inflates the headline. The reporter recomputes per-service total_recs as len(recs) (html_report_generator.py:3000-3014) and _counted_advisory_counts (line 384) marks a rec advisory only when `rec.get('Counted') is False` -- the mediastore $0 rec has no Counted key, so it is tallied as counted with $0.00 savings (the exact counted-without-dollars hygiene violation). The services/_savings.py:72 mark_zero_savings_advisory helper used by network/lambda/file_systems is never called here. The $0 rec genuinely occurs: services/mediastore.py:95 appends whenever total_activity==0 regardless of storage_gb, and line 100 sets EstimatedStorageGB=storage_gb=0 for empty or size-read-failed containers, driving estimated_gb<=0 into the else branch. Cited lines (47-56, 60) match.

#### 🟡 M1 · Rendered 'Estimated Savings' (helper savings_str) desyncs from counted EstimatedMonthlySavings  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/mediastore.py:91-93, 106 (vs services/adapters/mediastore.py:48-49; reporter_phase_b.py:1874-1875)`
- **Evidence:** Helper computes `storage_cost_per_gb = 0.023 * ctx.pricing_multiplier` and `estimated_savings = (storage_gb*storage_cost_per_gb)+ingest_cost`, stored as rec['EstimatedSavings']=savings_str (91-93,106). The adapter OVERWRITES rec['EstimatedMonthlySavings'] with storage_gb * engine-rate (adapters/mediastore.py:48-49) but does NOT update rec['EstimatedSavings']. The generic per-rec card renders rec['EstimatedSavings'] (reporter_phase_b.py:1874-1875), i.e. the helper's fallback-rate string, while the headline sums EstimatedMonthlySavings.
- **Impact:** Counted != rendered. In non-us-east-1 regions the card shows 0.023*multiplier while the total uses the region-correct S3 engine rate; the card also still adds ingest_cost (always 0 here, but the formula diverges). Reader cannot reconcile the per-rec card against the tab/headline total. Magnitude small (rates coincide at $0.023 in us-east-1) but it is a real reporting desync.
- **Fix:** Have the adapter rewrite rec['EstimatedSavings'] = f"${rec['EstimatedMonthlySavings']:.2f}/month" after computing the counted value, so the rendered string equals the counted number; or render EstimatedMonthlySavings in the card.

#### 🟡 M2 · No fast-mode gating despite reads_fast_mode=True — full 14-day CloudWatch sweep in fast mode  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/mediastore.py:23-58 (vs services/adapters/mediastore.py:18)`
- **Evidence:** Adapter declares reads_fast_mode=True (adapters/mediastore.py:18) but get_enhanced_mediastore_checks(ctx) (23) never reads ctx.fast_mode; every ACTIVE container runs up to 5 get_metric_statistics calls (3 activity + size + ingest) over 14 days unconditionally. core/CLAUDE.md guidance step 5 says CloudWatch adapters must check ctx.fast_mode and bail cheaply.
- **Impact:** fast_mode promise is unmet: full CloudWatch cost/latency in fast scans. Per-container 5 CW API calls add up; no early-out.
- **Fix:** At the top of the per-container ACTIVE branch (or helper entry), if ctx.fast_mode: skip the CloudWatch sweep and either emit nothing or an advisory ($0, Counted=False) rec, mirroring the Lambda/file_systems fast-mode bail.

#### 🟡 M3 · requires_cloudwatch not declared though four CloudWatch metrics are read  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/mediastore.py:12-22`
- **Evidence:** MediastoreModule does not set requires_cloudwatch, so it inherits the BaseServiceModule default False (services/_base.py:24), yet the helper reads RequestCount/BytesDownloaded/BytesUploaded/BucketSizeBytes/BytesUploaded (services/mediastore.py:41-89). Siblings that read CloudWatch declare it True (services/adapters/rds.py:45, s3.py:38).
- **Impact:** Contract/consistency gap: mediastore is the outlier among CloudWatch-reading adapters. A --no-cloudwatch opt-out or orchestrator pre-fetch keyed on requires_cloudwatch cannot account for mediastore, and the declared contract misrepresents the adapter's dependencies. (No core consumer of the flag exists today, so functional impact is latent, not active.)
- **Fix:** Add `requires_cloudwatch: bool = True` to MediastoreModule, mirroring s3.py/rds.py.

#### 🟡 M4 · AccessDenied on mediastore:ListContainers routed to generic ctx.warn, not permission_issue  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/mediastore.py:27-29, 110-115`
- **Evidence:** Outer `except Exception as e: ctx.warn(f"Could not analyze MediaStore resources: {e}", "mediastore")` (114-115) covers list_containers() (29) and the per-container block; the inner per-container handler also uses ctx.warn (110-111). Neither classifies AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation/OptInRequired as a permission_issue (services/_aws_errors.is_permission_error / record_aws_error exists at services/_aws_errors.py:47-56 but is unused here).
- **Impact:** An IAM gap on ListContainers (or the metric reads) is reported as a soft warning instead of a permission_issue, so the run looks like 'no MediaStore findings' rather than 'could not assess due to missing permission' — silent under-coverage.
- **Fix:** Replace the bare ctx.warn calls (27-29 wrapping and 110-115) with services/_aws_errors.record_aws_error(ctx, exc, service='mediastore', context=...) so AccessDenied/Unauthorized/OptInRequired -> ctx.permission_issue.

#### 🟡 M5 · Counted rec carries no structured AuditBasis (rate/region/metric-window/formula)  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/mediastore.py:95-109`
- **Evidence:** The unused_containers rec contains ContainerName, ActivityLast14Days, EstimatedStorageGB, IngestCost, Recommendation, EstimatedSavings, CheckCategory — but no structured AuditBasis stating the borrowed S3-STANDARD rate, the region, the BucketSizeBytes 14-day/last-point window, or the storage_gb*rate formula. Lambda (per brief) attaches AuditBasis on each priced finding.
- **Impact:** The saving is not self-explanatory from the report alone; an auditor cannot see that the rate is the borrowed S3-Standard rate at the scan region applied to the last BucketSizeBytes average. Defensibility/reproducibility gap.
- **Fix:** Attach AuditBasis to each counted rec: {rate: '$/GB-mo S3 STANDARD (borrowed)', rate_source: 'PricingEngine' | 'fallback 0.023*multiplier', region, metric: 'BucketSizeBytes Average, last datapoint over 14d', formula: 'storage_gb * rate'}.

#### 🟢 L1 · list_containers not paginated — NextToken ignored  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/mediastore.py:29-31`
- **Evidence:** `response = mediastore.list_containers(); containers = response.get('Containers', [])` — single call, response['NextToken'] never followed. The MediaStore ListContainers API paginates via MaxResults/NextToken.
- **Impact:** Accounts with more containers than one page returns would have the overflow silently skipped (coverage gap). Low real-world risk: MediaStore is retired (no new containers) and most accounts are empty/small.
- **Fix:** Loop on NextToken (or use a get_paginator('list_containers')) and accumulate Containers across pages.

#### 🟢 L2 · Only fully-idle ACTIVE containers fire; low-but-nonzero usage with large idle storage is skipped  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/mediastore.py:36, 95`
- **Evidence:** Gate is `status == 'ACTIVE'` (36) AND strict `total_activity == 0` (95). A container with a handful of requests but TBs of cold storage produces total_activity>0 and is excluded; non-ACTIVE (CREATING/DELETING) correctly skipped. No under-utilization / IA-lifecycle check exists.
- **Impact:** Misses real savings on barely-used, large-storage containers (no down-tier or lifecycle recommendation). Intentional today; documented coverage gap.
- **Fix:** Optionally add an under-utilization/cold-storage advisory (e.g., very low RequestCount relative to BucketSizeBytes -> recommend MediaStore IA storage class at $0.0125/GB-mo, evidence-gated like the S3 Standard->IA check).

#### 🟢 L3 · Borrowed S3-Standard rate is numerically correct but always assumes Standard class (MediaStore IA is cheaper)  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/mediastore.py:41-49 (core/pricing_engine.py:668-680)`
- **Evidence:** Live AWS Pricing API (AWSElementalMediaStore, us-east-1) shows MediaStore Standard storage SKU HUGWWZUKMZ9M573N = $0.0230/GB-mo — IDENTICAL to S3 STANDARD ($0.023, FALLBACK_S3_GB_MONTH['STANDARD'] core/pricing_engine.py:207). So the borrowed rate is DEFENSIBLE. However MediaStore also has an Infrequent-Access storage class SKU FGWYKK54QUCW8MZ4 = $0.0125/GB-mo; the adapter always prices at Standard.
- **Impact:** For containers whose bytes are in MediaStore IA storage, the $0.023 rate overstates the saving by ~1.84x. CloudWatch BucketSizeBytes does not expose storage class, so the class is unknowable from metrics — a structural caveat, not an easily-fixable bug. Standard remains the safe/typical default.
- **Fix:** Document the Standard-class assumption in AuditBasis (M5). No code change required unless a storage-class signal becomes available.

#### 🟢 L4 · Ingest cost is structurally always $0 in any emitted rec (dead term) — 'dropped ingest' concern is moot  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/mediastore.py:41-42, 75-92, 95`
- **Evidence:** total_activity = RequestCount + BytesDownloaded + BytesUploaded sums (41-56). The rec only fires when total_activity==0 (95); since all CloudWatch Sum values are non-negative, total_activity==0 implies BytesUploaded sum==0, hence monthly_ingest_gb==0 and ingest_cost = monthly_ingest_gb*0.02 == 0 (85-87). The $0.02/GB ingest rate itself is CORRECT (live API USE1-Ingest-Optimized-Bytes = $0.0200/GB).
- **Impact:** The brief's 'dropped ingest cost' is therefore immaterial for fired recs (it is always 0 whether or not the adapter re-adds it). The ingest computation (75-89) is effectively dead code in the emitted path. No understatement/overstatement results. No rate-as-monthly-total bug (the $0.02 is multiplied by a measured GB quantity, not summed raw).
- **Fix:** Remove the dead ingest computation, or (if an under-utilization check is added per L2) reuse it there. No correctness change to current savings.

---

### Monitoring (CloudWatch) — `services/adapters/monitoring.py`

**Module identity:** CONFIRMED. services/adapters/monitoring.py:14-26 — key="monitoring", cli_aliases=("monitoring",), display_name="Monitoring & Logging", required_clients()=("cloudwatch","logs","cloudtrail","backup","route53"), requires_cloudwatch=True, reads_fast_mode NOT set (inherits False from services/_base.py:25). Composite of FOUR AWS domains via three shim files: services/monitoring.py (get_cloudwatch_checks + get_cloudtrail_checks), services/backup.py (get_backup_checks), services/route53.py (get_route53_checks). Emits FOUR SourceBlocks: cloudwatch_checks, cloudtrail_checks, backup_checks, route53_checks (monitoring.py:77-82). All four are registered in PHASE_B_HANDLERS (reporter_phase_b.py:2489-2492 → _render_monitoring_enhanced_checks) and monitoring is in _PHASE_B_SKIP_PER_REC (reporter_phase_b.py:2525), so every source has a handler — no silent-blank source. No CoH/CO consumption (not in scan_orchestrator _HUB_SERVICES; no advisor helper). No standalone BackupModule/Route53Module in services/__init__.py ALL_MODULES — backup/route53 flow ONLY through monitoring. Dead PHASE_A_DESCRIPTORS["backup"]/["route53"] (reporter_phase_a.py:337-354) and html_report_generator.py:3166-3167 service-order entries are INERT (no service emits those JSON keys, so they never dispatch and cannot double-render or double-count). DOC DRIFT: services/adapters/CLAUDE.md lists monitoring only as "Parse-rate / Fixed per-rec estimates" with no mention of the 4-domain composite, the 4 SourceBlocks, the two advisory-only domains, or that it prefers a numeric EstimatedMonthlySavings field over parse_dollar_savings.

**Verdict:** Audited the monitoring composite adapter (services/adapters/monitoring.py + shims services/monitoring.py, services/backup.py, services/route53.py) read-only, traced reporter wiring, and validated all three material rates against the live AWS Pricing API. Module identity and the 4-source Phase-B wiring are correct (all four sources have PHASE_B_HANDLERS entries; no silent-blank source; dead backup/route53 Phase-A descriptors proven inert). All hardcoded rates (CW Logs $0.03/GB-mo, custom-metric 0.30/0.10/0.05, Route 53 $0.50/$0.10) are CORRECT. Live-emitting counted checks: never_expiring_logs, unused_custom_metrics (CloudWatch) and unused_hosted_zones, duplicate_private_zones (Route 53). Backup (excessive_retention, daily_static_data) and CloudTrail are advisory by construction (non-$ / percentage strings → parse_dollar_savings=0 → Counted=False), confirmed they do not enter the count. Four HIGH confirmed bugs: (H1) CloudWatch permission/throttle failures drop COUNTED checks with logger-only output and no ctx.warn/permission_issue; (H2) never_expiring_logs counts 100% of storedBytes as deletable with no age evidence (overstated $); (H3) unused_custom_metrics fabricates a 50%-removable quantity (count//2) from a count>100 threshold — a 'review necessity' hygiene nudge counted as $; (H4) a low-record private zone that is also a duplicate is counted in BOTH Route 53 checks, double-summing the same zone's $. Two MEDIUM: (M1) Route 53 (global) savings wrongly scaled by the regional pricing_multiplier (non-1.0 in most regions); (M2) Backup/Route 53 errors funnel to ctx.warn with no AccessDenied→permission_issue split. Five LOW limitations (dead CloudTrail walk, missing 4th custom-metric tier, no fast_mode gating, render-string desync, doc drift). Fix order: H1, H4, M1 (correctness of the counted total) first; then H2/H3 (demote to evidence-gated/advisory); then M2 and the LOWs. No CoH/CO applies. No state was mutated; no live AWS scan run (no creds).

**Pricing validation:** Validated the 3 material counted rates against the LIVE AWS Pricing API (2026-06-27 publication). (1) CloudWatch Logs storage CW_LOGS_GB_MONTH=0.03 — CONFIRMED: AmazonCloudWatch productFamily 'Storage Snapshot', us-east-1, $0.03/GB-Mo; the code-cited SKU JRHJQ2UMPUB5K73A is now 'Legacy' (superseded by Current SKU 6K9ADYQAHV5KX9KZ) but identical $0.03 rate. (2) CloudWatch custom-metric tiers 0.30/0.10/0.05 at 10k/250k — CONFIRMED: AmazonCloudWatch productFamily 'Metric', SKU KG586CTNGQ4VRZKZ (CW:MetricMonitorUsage): $0.30 first 10,000, $0.10 next 240,000 (to 250k), $0.05 next 750,000 (to 1M), $0.02 over 1,000,000. Code models the first three tiers/breakpoints exactly correctly; the 4th tier ($0.02 >1M) is NOT modeled (finding L2). (3) Route 53 hosted-zone 0.50/0.10, limit 25 — CONFIRMED: AmazonRoute53 productFamily 'DNS Zone', SKU KVPGEJE88UW8S779, $0.50 per HostedZone first 25, $0.10 additional, location 'Any' (GLOBAL). The global location proves the regional pricing_multiplier in route53.py is misapplied (finding M1). Backup/CloudTrail carry no counted $, so no rate to validate; confirmed they stay advisory (parse_dollar_savings returns 0.0 on their non-$ strings, verified statically).

**Cost checks:**

| Check | Status | Trigger | Savings basis |
|---|---|---|---|
| cloudwatch: never_expiring_logs | counted | log_group.retentionInDays is None (services/monitoring.py:127) | stored_bytes/1024^3 × CW_LOGS_GB_MONTH(0.03) × pricing_multiplier; numeric EstimatedMonthlySavings set (monitoring.py:129,137). $0.03/GB-mo VALIDATED vs live API. |
| cloudwatch: unused_custom_metrics | counted | non-AWS/ namespace with metric count > 100 (services/monitoring.py:176-177) | _cw_custom_metrics_monthly_cost(count) − _cw_custom_metrics_monthly_cost(count//2), tiered 0.30/0.10/0.05, × multiplier (monitoring.py:179-181). FABRICATED 50% reduction factor, no staleness evidence. |
| cloudwatch: excessive_logging / high_resolution_metrics / unused_alarms / duplicate_metrics | advisory | buckets declared but never populated — findings removed (monitoring.py:142-143,156-158) | none emitted |
| cloudtrail: all checks (multi_region_trails, data_events_all_s3/lambda, duplicate_trails, expensive_storage_trails, unused_insights) | advisory | function walks trails + get_event_selectors but appends NOTHING — ct_recs always empty (monitoring.py:206-273) | none emitted |
| backup: excessive_retention | advisory | rule Lifecycle.DeleteAfterDays > 2555 (services/backup.py:61) | EstimatedSavings string 'Reduce retention to lower storage costs' — NO $, no numeric field → parse_dollar_savings=0.0 (verified) |
| backup: daily_static_data | advisory | schedule contains 'daily' or 'cron(0 ' (services/backup.py:75) | EstimatedSavings string 'Weekly/monthly backups can reduce costs by 70-85%' — percentage, no numeric field → parse=0.0 (verified) |
| route53: unused_hosted_zones | counted | zone ResourceRecordSetCount <= 2 (services/route53.py:86) | _route53_zone_monthly_cost(1, base=len(zones)) × pricing_multiplier; numeric EstimatedMonthlySavings set (route53.py:88-99). $0.50/$0.10 tiers VALIDATED vs live API (global). |
| route53: duplicate_private_zones | counted | same private-zone Name appears >1 time (services/route53.py:159-160) | _route53_zone_monthly_cost(count-1, base=len(zones)) × pricing_multiplier; numeric EstimatedMonthlySavings set (route53.py:161-172) |
| route53: unnecessary_health_checks / complex_routing_simple_use / old_records_deleted_resources | advisory | removed — walks health checks/records but appends nothing (route53.py:122-124,140-143) | none emitted |

**Findings:**

#### 🟠 H1 · CloudWatch counted savings vanish silently on permission/throttle errors (logger-only, no ctx.warn/permission_issue)  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/monitoring.py:160-161, 193-194, 196-197`
- **Evidence:** All three except blocks do `logger.warning(f"Warning: Could not ...: {e}")` only — never call ctx.warn or ctx.permission_issue. The outer block (196-197) wraps describe_log_groups (feeds COUNTED never_expiring_logs); the inner block (193-194) wraps list_metrics (feeds COUNTED unused_custom_metrics). Contrast services/backup.py:112/115/122 and services/route53.py:127/146/178 which DO call ctx.warn.
- **Impact:** An AccessDenied / throttle / OptInRequired on logs:DescribeLogGroups or cloudwatch:ListMetrics drops the two COUNTED CloudWatch checks with ZERO user-visible signal (logger.warning is not in scan_warnings/permission_issues, not in the report). User sees an empty/partial Monitoring tab and assumes $0 savings when they actually lack IAM permissions. Also no AccessDenied→permission_issue classification.
- **Fix:** Replace the three logger.warning calls with ctx.warn / ctx.permission_issue, classifying via the error code (AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation/OptInRequired → ctx.permission_issue('...','monitoring', action); else ctx.warn('...','monitoring')). Mirror services/_aws_errors.record_aws_error used by the network adapter.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified in services/monitoring.py: line 161 (`except Exception as e: logger.warning(...)` for describe_alarms), 193-194 (list_metrics → COUNTED unused_custom_metrics), and 196-197 (outer try at line 110 wrapping describe_log_groups → COUNTED never_expiring_logs) all use module-level `logger.warning` only. `logger` is `logging.getLogger(__name__)` (line 12), entirely disconnected from ScanContext. ScanContext.warn (scan_context.py:49) appends to `_warnings` and ScanContext.permission_issue (scan_context.py:59) appends to `_permission_issues` + prints — the structured channels the report reads. Confirmed contrast: services/route53.py:127/146/178 and services/backup.py:112/115/122 both call `ctx.warn(...)`. The errors are swallowed *inside* get_cloudwatch_checks, so they never reach the adapter for higher-level handling. No AccessDenied→permission_issue classification exists anywhere in the file. An AccessDenied/throttle on logs:DescribeLogGroups (196-197) or cloudwatch:ListMetrics (193-194) silently zeroes both counted CloudWatch checks with no scan_warnings/permission_issues entry. The finding's line-to-check mapping is precise (it does not claim 160-161 feeds a counted check; it attributes the two counted checks to 193-194 and 196-197 correctly).

#### 🟠 H2 · never_expiring_logs overstates counted $ — charges 100% of storedBytes with no age evidence  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/monitoring.py:127-140`
- **Evidence:** stored_gb = stored_bytes/1024^3; monthly_savings = stored_gb * CW_LOGS_GB_MONTH * pricing_multiplier — the FULL stored volume is counted as saved 'if 30-day retention enforced'. No CloudWatch/age-distribution read; retention only deletes bytes older than the window. $0.03/GB-mo rate itself VALIDATED (live API SKU JRHJQ2UMPUB5K73A / 6K9ADYQAHV5KX9KZ).
- **Impact:** A log group actively written with all data younger than the proposed retention window saves $0 but is counted at full storage cost. Inflated counted savings, scaling with the largest log groups. Violates the evidence-gated discipline the S3 adapter is the canonical model for.
- **Fix:** Either gate on a measured 'bytes older than retention window' signal (no API exposes this directly → make it a $0 advisory like S3's no-evidence path), or apply an explicit documented fraction with an AuditBasis. Do not count full storedBytes as deletable.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified services/monitoring.py:127-140. When retention_days is None, stored_gb = stored_bytes/1024**3 (full stored volume, line 128) and monthly_savings = stored_gb * CW_LOGS_GB_MONTH(0.03) * pricing_multiplier (line 129). No CloudWatch/age-distribution read exists in the function — the only logs API call is describe_log_groups (line 115), which returns aggregate storedBytes with no age breakdown. A retention policy only deletes bytes older than the window, so a log group whose data is all younger than the proposed 30-day window realizes $0 but is counted at full storage cost. The rec carries a positive EstimatedMonthlySavings (137), so the adapter's mark_zero_savings_advisory (services/adapters/monitoring.py:70) does NOT demote it (only zero-byte groups parse to $0 → advisory, per the adapter comment), and it is summed into total_monthly_savings (line 69-71). Counted-savings overstatement scales with the largest log groups, as described. Rate $0.03/GB-mo acknowledged validated.

#### 🟠 H3 · unused_custom_metrics fabricates a 50%-removable quantity (count(N) − count(N//2)) with no staleness evidence  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/monitoring.py:176-191`
- **Evidence:** current_cost = _cw_custom_metrics_monthly_cost(count); reduced_cost = _cw_custom_metrics_monthly_cost(count // 2); monthly_savings = (current_cost - reduced_cost)*multiplier. Trigger is purely count>100; Recommendation text is 'High number of custom metrics (N) - review necessity'. Static check: count=200 → $60−$30 = $30/month COUNTED. No per-metric datapoint/staleness check exists.
- **Impact:** A flat 50%-reduction factor invented from a count threshold produces a counted dollar with zero evidence any metric is unused — a 'review necessity' hygiene nudge dressed as a quantified saving (the #1 monitoring scope-leakage risk). Tier rates 0.30/0.10/0.05 themselves VALIDATED.
- **Fix:** Drive the saving from a real signal (e.g. metrics with no datapoints in N days via list_metrics + GetMetricData), or demote to $0 advisory (Counted=False) like the Lambda excessive-memory/ARM checks. Never use count//2 as the removable quantity.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified services/monitoring.py:176-191. Trigger is purely `count > 100` (line 177) over non-AWS namespaces. monthly_savings = (_cw_custom_metrics_monthly_cost(count) − _cw_custom_metrics_monthly_cost(count // 2)) * multiplier (lines 179-181). Static check confirmed: count=200 → tier-1 cost(200)=200*0.30=$60, cost(100)=$30, savings=$30/month COUNTED. The metrics come from list_metrics (line 165), which returns metric identities only — no GetMetricData/datapoint/last-published read exists anywhere in the function, so there is zero staleness evidence. Recommendation text is exactly 'High number of custom metrics ({count}) - review necessity' (line 186), a hygiene nudge. The rec carries positive EstimatedMonthlySavings so it survives mark_zero_savings_advisory and is counted. The flat 50%-reduction factor invented from a count threshold is confirmed. Tier rates 0.30/0.10/0.05 acknowledged validated.

#### 🟠 H4 · Route 53 savings double-counted: a low-record private zone that is also a duplicate is counted in BOTH checks  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/route53.py:86-102 and 148-175`
- **Evidence:** unused_hosted_zones fires on record_count<=2 for ANY zone (incl. private); duplicate_private_zones fires on repeated private-zone Name. A private zone with <=2 records AND a duplicate name matches both, and each rec carries its own numeric EstimatedMonthlySavings with Counted=True. Static check (two recs, $0.50 each, both categories): mark_zero_savings_advisory leaves both Counted=True → counted sum = $1.00 for ONE removable zone.
- **Impact:** The same removable zone's monthly $ is summed twice into total_monthly_savings. Inflated counted savings whenever a duplicate private zone also has <=2 records (common for stub/internal zones).
- **Fix:** Dedup by normalized HostedZoneId across the two Route 53 checks before summing (authority: count the zone once). E.g. skip a zone in duplicate_private_zones if it was already emitted by unused_hosted_zones, or compute a single consolidated Route 53 savings set.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified the double-count path end-to-end. services/route53.py:86-102 appends an `unused_hosted_zones` rec for ANY zone (private included) with record_count<=2, each with positive EstimatedMonthlySavings (line 99). services/route53.py:159-175 separately appends a `duplicate_private_zones` rec per repeated private-zone Name with removable=len(zone_ids)-1 and its own positive EstimatedMonthlySavings (line 172). Both loops are independent — no shared key, no cross-removal. In services/adapters/monitoring.py:46-71 (the actual `monitoring` ServiceModule), r53_recs (containing BOTH categories) are concatenated into all_recs (line 52) and summed: `savings = sum(_rec_savings(rec) for rec in all_recs if rec.get('Counted', True))` (line 69) with NO dedup key across categories. mark_zero_savings_advisory (line 70) only demotes $0 recs, so both positive-dollar recs stay Counted=True. A private zone that is both <=2 records and a duplicate has its $0.50 counted once in unused_hosted_zones and once again in duplicate_private_zones → $1.00 for one removable zone. Minor imprecision (does not change verdict): the recs do not literally carry a Counted=True field from route53.py; Counted defaults to True via rec.get('Counted', True) after mark_zero_savings_advisory leaves positive recs untouched — functionally identical to the finding's claim. Double-count confirmed.

#### 🟡 M1 · Route 53 (global service) savings scaled by regional pricing_multiplier  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/route53.py:88-90 and 162-164`
- **Evidence:** Both checks do `_route53_zone_monthly_cost(...) * pricing_multiplier`. pricing_multiplier is region-specific and non-1.0 for most regions (cost_optimizer.py REGIONAL_PRICING: sa-east-1=1.25, af-south-1=1.20, ap-east-1=1.18, ap-southeast-2=1.15, etc.). Live Pricing API confirms Route 53 hosted-zone pricing is GLOBAL (location 'Any', $0.50 first-25 / $0.10 additional, SKU KVPGEJE88UW8S779). Shim comment (route53.py:60-62) even acknowledges Route 53 is global but keeps the multiplier 'for consistency'.
- **Impact:** Scanning a non-us-east-1 region inflates Route 53 zone savings by the regional premium (e.g. +25% in sa-east-1). Counted $ wrong by region.
- **Fix:** Do not multiply Route 53 zone savings by pricing_multiplier (pass 1.0). Add AuditBasis region='global'.

#### 🟡 M2 · Backup/Route 53 permission errors funneled to ctx.warn with no AccessDenied→permission_issue split  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/backup.py / services/route53.py:backup.py:112,115,122; route53.py:127,146,178`
- **Evidence:** Every except in these shims calls ctx.warn(...) regardless of error code; none inspects ClientError Error.Code for AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation/OptInRequired to route to ctx.permission_issue. e.g. backup.py:122 `ctx.warn(f"Could not perform AWS Backup checks: {e}", "backup")`.
- **Impact:** A backup:ListBackupPlans or route53:ListHostedZones AccessDenied is recorded as a generic warning rather than a permission issue, so the report's permission_issues section under-reports missing IAM grants. Less severe than H1 (at least surfaced), but inconsistent with the permission-issue contract.
- **Fix:** Classify the error code in each except and call ctx.permission_issue for AccessDenied/Unauthorized/OptInRequired, else ctx.warn (shared helper services/_aws_errors.record_aws_error).

#### 🟢 L1 · CloudTrail walk is dead cost — emits nothing but still calls describe_trails + get_event_selectors per trail  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/monitoring.py:206-273`
- **Evidence:** All CloudTrail findings were removed (comments at 232-234,247-250,258-264); ct_recs is provably always empty, yet the function still calls cloudtrail.describe_trails() (un-paginated, line 219) and cloudtrail.get_event_selectors() per trail (237). On TrailNotFound/AccessDenied it emits logger.warning only (252-256).
- **Impact:** Wasted API calls (one get_event_selectors per trail) and noisy logger warnings with no output. describe_trails being un-paginated has no output impact (nothing emitted) but would silently truncate if a finding were ever re-added.
- **Fix:** Either delete the CloudTrail walk entirely (it produces no cost recommendation) or gate it behind a real priced check; if retained, paginate describe_trails and route errors through ctx.

#### 🟢 L2 · Custom-metrics 4th pricing tier ($0.02 above 1M) not modeled  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/monitoring.py:31-51`
- **Evidence:** _cw_custom_metrics_monthly_cost models only 0.30/0.10/0.05 with breakpoints 10k/250k. Live API (SKU KG586CTNGQ4VRZKZ) has a 4th tier: $0.02/metric-month above 1,000,000. Static check: cost(2,000,000)=$114,500 modeled vs $84,500 true.
- **Impact:** For a single namespace with >1M custom metrics the cost (and the derived saving) is overstated. Extreme edge case. First three tiers + breakpoints are exactly correct.
- **Fix:** Add the 1,000,000 breakpoint at $0.02 to _cw_custom_metrics_monthly_cost. (Secondary — the H2 fabricated-quantity issue dominates.)

#### 🟢 L3 · reads_fast_mode not declared and no shim gates on ctx.fast_mode  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/monitoring.py:22-26`
- **Evidence:** Adapter sets requires_cloudwatch=True but not reads_fast_mode (defaults False, services/_base.py:25). None of the four shims reference ctx.fast_mode (grep: zero hits). get_cloudwatch_checks runs describe_log_groups pagination + list_metrics + describe_alarms unconditionally; S3/Lambda/file_systems adapters both declare reads_fast_mode=True and self-gate on ctx.fast_mode.
- **Impact:** Under --fast the monitoring adapter still does full describe/list pagination. Not a $-correctness bug (these are config/describe reads, not GetMetricData), but inconsistent with sibling fast-mode discipline and slower than intended.
- **Fix:** Declare reads_fast_mode=True and short-circuit the list_metrics/describe_alarms (and optionally describe_log_groups) reads when ctx.fast_mode is True, or document the intentional always-on behavior.

#### 🟢 L4 · Per-category card shows only resources[0]['EstimatedSavings'] — display desyncs from the counted total  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `reporter_phase_b.py:1223-1233`
- **Evidence:** _render_monitoring_enhanced_checks groups recs by CheckCategory and renders savings_str = resources[0].get('EstimatedSavings') for the whole group, then lists every resource. For a category with N counted resources (e.g. several never-expiring log groups) the displayed single '$X/month' is only the first resource's, while total_monthly_savings sums all N. Advisory backup cards display a '70-85%' percentage under the 'Estimated Savings' label with no per-card advisory marker (the tab header does show the counted/advisory split via _counted_advisory_counts).
- **Impact:** Cosmetic/transparency only — the counted total itself is correct. The rendered per-category $ understates the category's counted contribution, and advisory percentage strings appear under a 'savings' label.
- **Fix:** Render a per-category sum of counted EstimatedMonthlySavings (and label advisory cards), rather than echoing resources[0]'s raw string.

#### 🟢 L5 · Doc drift + dead Phase-A backup/route53 descriptors  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/CLAUDE.md / reporter_phase_a.py:CLAUDE.md monitoring row; reporter_phase_a.py:337-354`
- **Evidence:** CLAUDE.md describes monitoring only as 'Parse-rate / Fixed per-rec estimates' — omitting that it is a 4-domain composite (CloudWatch+CloudTrail+Backup+Route53) across two shim files emitting 4 SourceBlocks, that CloudTrail/Backup are advisory-only, and that it prefers a numeric EstimatedMonthlySavings field. PHASE_A_DESCRIPTORS['backup']/['route53'] and html_report_generator.py:3166-3167 still list backup/route53 though no module emits those service keys.
- **Impact:** No functional double-render/double-count (PROVEN: no services['backup']/['route53'] JSON key is ever produced, so the Phase-A descriptors and service-order entries never dispatch). Maintainability/accuracy only.
- **Fix:** Update the CLAUDE.md monitoring row to reflect the 4-domain composite; remove the inert backup/route53 Phase-A descriptors and service-order entries.
