### MSK — `services/adapters/msk.py`

**Module identity:** Module identity matches the brief: services/adapters/msk.py defines MskModule(BaseServiceModule) with key="msk" (line 15), cli_aliases=("msk",) (line 16), display_name="MSK" (line 17), required_clients()->("kafka",) (lines 19-21). It emits a single SourceBlock named "enhanced_checks" (line 58) with count=len(recs). DOC DRIFT vs services/adapters/CLAUDE.md: MSK is absent from EVERY pricing table there. The "Flat-rate (1 adapter)" section lists only batch.py, yet msk.py's header and class docstring both call it a "Flat-rate adapter / Flat-rate savings strategy"; and MSK is NOT in the Live-Pricing (19-adapter) table even though it calls a live PricingEngine method get_msk_broker_hourly_price plus a module-constant storage rate 0.10. MSK is genuinely a hybrid (live broker leg + module-const storage leg + a 0.30 blanket factor) and is undocumented. The CLAUDE.md row should be added/corrected. Orchestrator reconcile confirms the brief: MSK is NOT in core/scan_orchestrator.py _HUB_SERVICES (lines 52-74) and there is no MskCluster entry in type_map (lines 86-113), so no Cost Hub consumption; the adapter pulls no Compute Optimizer helper and declares neither requires_cloudwatch nor reads_fast_mode — all correct for a service AWS CoH/CO do not cover, so a "missing CoH/CO source" finding is not raised.

**Verdict:** MSK is a thin flat-rate adapter (services/adapters/msk.py) whose counted total and rendered cards come from two unrelated code paths. The single most material defect (C1) is that the entire counted total_monthly_savings is a blanket (broker+storage) x 0.30 factor with NO utilization metric and NO target instance — fabricated dollars whose own Note admits throughput is unverified. Feeding that formula, the live broker-price lookup is 100% dead (H1): _fetch_msk_broker_price filters on 'instanceType', which I proved live is NOT a valid AmazonMSK attribute (valid: computeFamily/usagetype/storageFamily/...), so every broker price silently falls back to get_ec2_hourly_price x 1.4 = ~$0.1344/hr vs the real $0.21/hr broker rate (~36% low). The counted number also never equals what the card shows (H2): the headline is the 0.30 figure while each card prints the unparsed string '$200/month potential' / '20% with gp3...'; parse_dollar_savings / mark_zero_savings_advisory are unused. The storage leg of every counted rec assumes a phantom 100 GB because BrokerStorageGB is never set (H3). Secondary issues: the volume>1000 storage rec is counted in the rec-count but contributes $0 and is never marked Counted=False (M1); the source inherits a 'Metric Backed' badge though the checks are pure config heuristics, needing the S3-style ('msk','enhanced_checks')->'Audit Based' override (M2); kafka:ListClusters AccessDenied is a generic ctx.warn not ctx.permission_issue and the list_clusters_v2 block swallows failures with a bare except: pass (M3); and the trigger gates on a name substring + ACTIVE-only rather than utilization (M4). Validated facts: storage literal 0.10 is us-east-1-correct and region-scaled once; broker leg correctly not double-multiplied; MSK consumes no Cost Hub / Compute Optimizer (correct — AWS does not cover MSK). MSK is also undocumented in services/adapters/CLAUDE.md and its rendering path correctly falls through to render_generic_per_rec -> _render_generic_other_rec (resource id resolves via ClusterName; no blank card). Pricing rates validated live against the AWS Pricing API on 2026-06-27.

**Pricing validation:** Validated live against the AWS Pricing API (us-east-1) on 2026-06-27. (1) DEAD FILTER PROVEN: get_pricing_service_attributes('AmazonMSK') returns ['computeFamily','description','group','location','locationType','memoryGib','operation','productFamily','regionCode','servicecode','servicename','storageFamily','termType','usagetype','vcpu'] — there is NO 'instanceType' attribute. A get_pricing call filtered on instanceType='m5.large' returns error_type 'empty_results' (zero rows). _fetch_msk_broker_price (pricing_engine.py:1275-1280) filters Field='instanceType' -> never matches -> _call_pricing_api returns None -> get_msk_broker_hourly_price always falls back. (2) REAL BROKER RATE: AmazonMSK computeFamily='m5.large', productFamily='Managed Streaming for Apache Kafka (MSK)', usagetype 'USE1-Kafka.m5.large', operation RunBroker = $0.21/broker-hour. (3) FALLBACK UNDERSTATES: EC2 m5.large Linux on-demand = $0.096/hr (live); fallback = 0.096 x 1.4 = $0.1344/hr vs real $0.21 -> ~36% low (0.1344/0.21 = 0.64). (4) STORAGE LITERAL CORRECT: AmazonMSK usagetype 'USE1-Kafka.Storage.GP2', storageFamily GP2 = $0.10/GB-Mo — the inline 0.10 literal (msk.py:52) is us-east-1-correct and is region-scaled via pricing_multiplier exactly once; the broker leg is correctly NOT multiplied again (msk.py:45-47).

**Cost checks:**

| Check | Status | Trigger | Savings basis |
|---|---|---|---|
| Cluster Rightsizing | counted | services/msk.py:42 — state == 'ACTIVE' and instance_type and 'large' in instance_type (substring match on the broker InstanceType from list_clusters paginator). Pure config heuristic, NO utilization metric. | Counted in adapter msk.py:48-54 as (broker_monthly + storage_monthly) * 0.30, where broker_monthly = get_msk_broker_hourly_price(InstanceType) * 730 * num_brokers and storage_monthly = volume_size(=100 default) * 0.10 * num_brokers * pricing_multiplier. The rendered card instead shows the helper's unparsed string EstimatedSavings='$200/month potential' (services/msk.py:50). Two unrelated numbers. |
| MSK Storage Optimization | advisory | services/msk.py:61 — EBSStorageInfo.VolumeSize > 1000 (config heuristic, no metric). | Carries VolumeSize but NO InstanceType, so the adapter savings loop (gated on rec.get('InstanceType'), msk.py:44) skips it -> contributes $0 to total_monthly_savings, yet it is still counted in total_recommendations=len(recs) (msk.py:62). Rendered string 'EstimatedSavings=20% with gp3 migration + retention optimization' (services/msk.py:67) is never quantified. NOT marked Counted=False. |

**Findings:**

#### 🔴 C1 · Counted savings = (broker+storage) x 0.30 blanket factor with no utilization metric and no target instance — fabricated dollars  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/msk.py:40-56`
- **Evidence:** savings += (broker_monthly + storage_monthly) * 0.30 (line 54). The 0.30 is a hardcoded 'downsize ~30%' assumption with zero usage/throughput evidence — the adapter declares no CloudWatch and the helper reads none. The rec's own Note admits the gap: 'Verify actual throughput and utilization before downsizing' (services/msk.py:52). There is no current->target instance delta; the saving is conjured from a config dimension (instance name) alone.
- **Impact:** The ENTIRE counted total_monthly_savings for MSK is fabricated. Every ACTIVE cluster whose type contains 'large' is asserted to yield 30% off broker+storage with no signal that the cluster is over-provisioned. Recommending downsizing a fully-utilized Kafka cluster also risks an availability incident, not just a wrong number.
- **Fix:** Either (a) compute an exact current->target broker price delta (one size down via get_msk_broker_hourly_price for both, mirror ec2.py's price-delta approach) gated on a real utilization signal, or (b) demote the rec to a $0 advisory (mark_zero_savings_advisory, Counted=False, mirror lambda_svc.py's metric-gated pattern). Record a structured AuditBasis (rate/region/formula/absence-of-metric) on any finding that stays counted.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** services/adapters/msk.py:54 is the ONLY place `savings` is incremented: `savings += (broker_monthly + storage_monthly) * 0.30`. The 0.30 is a hardcoded literal applied to every rec carrying an InstanceType. There is no utilization input: required_clients() returns only ('kafka',) (line 21) and the helper get_enhanced_msk_checks reads no CloudWatch / throughput metric — it flags a cluster purely on `state == 'ACTIVE' and instance_type and 'large' in instance_type` (services/msk.py:42). No current->target instance delta exists; broker_monthly = hourly*730*num_brokers at the SAME instance type (line 49), then 30% of it is asserted as savings. The rec's own Note 'Verify actual throughput and utilization before downsizing' (services/msk.py:52) confirms the missing evidence. The entire counted total_monthly_savings (line 63) is this fabricated figure. Confirmed at the cited lines and severity.

#### 🟠 H1 · Dead live-price filter: _fetch_msk_broker_price filters on non-existent AmazonMSK attribute 'instanceType' -> silent EC2x1.4 fallback ~36% low  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `core/pricing_engine.py:1275-1280 (filter), 716-738 (fallback)`
- **Evidence:** filters=[{'Field':'instanceType',...},{'Field':'location',...}] against AmazonMSK (line 1277). Live API proves 'instanceType' is not a valid AmazonMSK attribute (valid: computeFamily/usagetype/storageFamily/vcpu/memoryGib/location/productFamily...) and a query on it returns empty_results. _call_pricing_api (line 1601, MaxResults=1) gets no PriceList -> returns None -> get_msk_broker_hourly_price falls back to get_ec2_hourly_price(clean_type)*1.4 (line 730) or 0.15 (line 732). Real m5.large broker = $0.21/hr; fallback = $0.096x1.4 = $0.1344/hr (~36% low).
- **Impact:** The live broker-price path is 100% dead for ALL broker types; every counted broker cost silently uses an EC2-derived proxy that understates the real MSK broker rate by ~36%, biasing the (already heuristic) savings low. The 1.4 markup is not calibrated to the real broker premium (real premium m5.large = 0.21/0.096 = ~2.19x, not 1.4x).
- **Fix:** Replace the filter with real attributes: Field='computeFamily' Value=clean_type plus productFamily='Managed Streaming for Apache Kafka (MSK)' (and/or usagetype pattern 'Kafka.<type>'), pinned so MaxResults=1 is deterministic and selects the Broker-hours/RunBroker SKU. Validate against the Pricing API. Recalibrate or remove the 1.4 fallback markup; region-scale the 0.15 last-ditch constant.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Confirmed with live evidence. (1) Dead filter: _fetch_msk_broker_price (core/pricing_engine.py:1275-1280) filters AmazonMSK on Field 'instanceType'. Live get_pricing_service_attributes('AmazonMSK') returns [computeFamily, description, group, location, locationType, memoryGib, operation, productFamily, regionCode, servicecode, servicename, storageFamily, termType, usagetype, vcpu] — 'instanceType' is NOT present. A live get_pricing on AmazonMSK with Field=instanceType returns status=error/empty_results. So _call_pricing_api (line 1590, MaxResults=1 at 1601) gets no PriceList -> returns None (1604-1610) for EVERY broker type. (2) Fallback always taken: get_msk_broker_hourly_price (716-738) then computes get_ec2_hourly_price(clean_type)*1.4 (line 730), or 0.15 (732). (3) Understatement quantified: live AmazonMSK rate for Kafka.m5.large = $0.21/broker-hr (sku CBMW8TY4JC6XHKHM, keyed by computeFamily='m5.large'/usagetype='USE1-Kafka.m5.large'); fallback = EC2 m5.large $0.096 * 1.4 = $0.1344, i.e. (0.21-0.1344)/0.21 = ~36% low; real premium 0.21/0.096 = ~2.19x, not the hardcoded 1.4x. Finding's lines, mechanism, and numbers all hold.

#### 🟠 H2 · Counted != rendered: tab total is the 0.30-factor number while each card shows the unparsed EstimatedSavings string  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/msk.py:39-58 (count path) + services/msk.py:50,67 + reporter_phase_b.py:1874-1875`
- **Evidence:** The adapter computes total_monthly_savings via the 0.30 formula (msk.py:54) and never reads the helper's EstimatedSavings strings; parse_dollar_savings / mark_zero_savings_advisory are not imported. The card is rendered by render_generic_per_rec -> else branch -> _render_generic_other_rec (reporter_phase_b.py:1381), which prints rec['EstimatedSavings'] verbatim (lines 1874-1875): '$200/month potential' for rightsizing, '20% with gp3 migration...' for storage. html_report_generator._calculate_service_savings returns the canonical total_monthly_savings (line 3078), so the headline = computed 0.30 number, the visible card = '$200/month potential' — different numbers from different code paths.
- **Impact:** Reporting-integrity defect: the per-rec dollar a reader sees ('$200/month potential') does not equal the per-tab headline, and neither '$200' nor '20%' is the counted figure. The executive-summary reconciliation footnote (html_report_generator.py:2261-2290) sums the canonical per-service totals, so the headline silently diverges from the cards.
- **Fix:** Make the counted number and the rendered string the same code path: have the adapter set EstimatedSavings to the formatted counted dollar (e.g. f"${value:.0f}/month") per rec, OR route MSK through a dedicated PHASE_B_HANDLERS renderer that prints the counted value. Drop the free-text '$200/month potential' / '20%' strings.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Counted != rendered, confirmed across both code paths. COUNT: msk.py builds total_monthly_savings via the 0.30 formula (line 54/63) and never reads EstimatedSavings; its imports are only core.contracts/services._base/services.msk — parse_dollar_savings / mark_zero_savings_advisory are not imported. RENDER: ('msk','enhanced_checks') is NOT in PHASE_B_HANDLERS (reporter_phase_b.py:2436-2492) and 'msk' is NOT in _PHASE_B_SKIP_PER_REC (2516-2530), so should_fallback_to_per_rec('msk') is True (2548-2550) and html_report_generator.py:3362 calls render_generic_per_rec('msk', ...). In render_generic_per_rec, 'msk' matches none of the special service_key branches, so it hits the else -> _render_generic_other_rec (line 1381), which prints rec['EstimatedSavings'] verbatim (1874-1875): '$200/month potential' (services/msk.py:50) and '20% with gp3 migration...' (services/msk.py:67). HEADLINE: _calculate_service_savings returns the canonical total_monthly_savings when >0 (html_report_generator.py:3078-3079), and the reconciliation footnote sums those canonical per-service totals (2280-2286). Net: card dollars ('$200'/'20%') diverge from the per-tab/headline computed 0.30 figure. Confirmed.

#### 🟠 H3 · Phantom 100 GB storage default in the counted formula — BrokerStorageGB is never set, so every counted rec assumes 100 GB  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/msk.py:50-53`
- **Evidence:** volume_size = rec.get('BrokerStorageGB', 100) (line 50). The helper (services/msk.py) never sets BrokerStorageGB on any rec — it sets VolumeSize only on the storage rec (line 65), and storage recs are skipped by the savings loop (no InstanceType). So for every counted rightsizing rec, volume_size always defaults to 100 GB and storage_monthly = 100 * 0.10 * num_brokers * multiplier regardless of the cluster's actual EBS size.
- **Impact:** The storage leg of every counted MSK saving is mis-priced: clusters with large EBS (precisely those the >1000 GB storage check flags) are understated, small-EBS clusters overstated. The cluster's real per-broker volume size (available from BrokerNodeGroupInfo.StorageInfo.EBSStorageInfo.VolumeSize in the helper) is discarded.
- **Fix:** Pass the real per-broker EBS size onto the rightsizing rec in the helper (e.g. add BrokerStorageGB from EBSStorageInfo.VolumeSize) and read it in the adapter, instead of defaulting to 100. If the size is unknown, omit the storage leg rather than assuming 100 GB.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** services/adapters/msk.py:50 reads volume_size = rec.get('BrokerStorageGB', 100). Grep/inspection of services/msk.py shows BrokerStorageGB is never set on any rec: the cluster_rightsizing rec sets only ClusterName/InstanceType/Recommendation/EstimatedSavings/CheckCategory/Note/NumberOfBrokerNodes (lines 44-54); the storage_optimization rec sets VolumeSize (line 65) but has no InstanceType, so the savings loop skips it (`if instance_type:` at msk.py:44). Therefore every counted rightsizing rec falls back to 100, making storage_monthly = 100 * 0.10 * num_brokers * pricing_multiplier (lines 51-52) regardless of real EBS size. The real per-broker size is available in the helper via BrokerNodeGroupInfo.StorageInfo.EBSStorageInfo.VolumeSize (services/msk.py:57-59) but is discarded for the counted leg. Confirmed at the cited lines.

#### 🟡 M1 · Storage rec is counted-but-unpriced: $0 contribution yet still in total_recommendations, never marked Counted=False  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/msk.py:61-70 (emit) + services/adapters/msk.py:44,62`
- **Evidence:** The volume>1000 rec carries VolumeSize but no InstanceType, so msk.py:44 (`if instance_type:`) skips it -> $0 savings, but it is still included in total_recommendations=len(recs) (msk.py:62) and rendered as a card with the unquantified '20%' string. parse_dollar_savings/mark_zero_savings_advisory are unused, so it is never flagged Counted=False.
- **Impact:** A tab can show N recommendations while only a subset carry counted dollars; the rec count and the savings total describe different populations. The '20% with gp3 migration' string implies a saving that is never computed.
- **Fix:** Mark the storage rec as a $0 advisory (Counted=False via mark_zero_savings_advisory) OR quantify it (current GP2 $0.10 vs GP3 rate x VolumeSize x num_brokers) and count it under a single owner — but pre-empt the intra-adapter double-count with C1/H3 (a large cluster matches BOTH rightsizing and storage>1000).

#### 🟡 M2 · Confidence mislabel: enhanced_checks inherits generic 'Metric Backed' badge though MSK checks are pure config heuristics  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `reporter_phase_b.py:2377-2378 (generic default) + 2349-2375 (no msk override)`
- **Evidence:** _GENERIC_SOURCE_TYPES['enhanced_checks'] = 'Metric Backed' (line 2378). SOURCE_TYPE_MAP has no ('msk','enhanced_checks') entry, so source_type_label('msk','enhanced_checks') resolves to 'Metric Backed'. But MSK's checks are name-substring + volume>1000 with no metric. The S3 audit set the precedent at line 2367: ('s3','enhanced_checks') -> 'Audit Based'.
- **Impact:** Misrepresents the confidence of every MSK card as metric-backed when it is a config audit, overstating trust in a number that is already heuristic.
- **Fix:** Add SOURCE_TYPE_MAP[('msk','enhanced_checks')] = 'Audit Based' (mirror the S3 fix).

#### 🟡 M3 · Permission/throttle failures swallowed: generic ctx.warn instead of ctx.permission_issue, and a bare v2 except: pass  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/msk.py:80-81 (v2 swallow) + 83-84 (generic warn)`
- **Evidence:** Outer handler: `except Exception as e: ctx.warn(f'Could not analyze MSK resources: {e}', 'msk')` (lines 83-84) — an AccessDenied / UnauthorizedOperation / OptInRequired on kafka:ListClusters is reported as a generic warn, not ctx.permission_issue (which exists, core/scan_context.py:59). Inner list_clusters_v2 block: `except Exception: pass` (lines 80-81) discards any v2 permission/throttle error silently.
- **Impact:** A real permission gap on MSK enumeration is misclassified (not surfaced as a permission_issue the report can act on), and a throttled/denied list_clusters_v2 vanishes with no trace. Both are the 'silent failure' anti-pattern.
- **Fix:** Classify the outer exception: AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation/OptInRequired -> ctx.permission_issue(action='kafka:ListClusters'); else ctx.warn (mirror services/_aws_errors.record_aws_error used by the network adapter). Replace the inner `except: pass` with at least a ctx.warn so v2 failures are recorded.

#### 🟡 M4 · Name-substring + ACTIVE-only trigger: over-matches all *.large/*.xlarge/*.2xlarge, excludes t3.small / small graviton, skips non-ACTIVE clusters  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/msk.py:42`
- **Evidence:** `if state == 'ACTIVE' and instance_type and 'large' in instance_type:` — the substring 'large' is contained in 'xlarge'/'2xlarge', so it flags every large-and-up broker, while t3.small and any small graviton broker that could still be over-provisioned are never considered. The gate is also restricted to state=='ACTIVE'.
- **Impact:** Coverage is gated by instance NAME, not utilization: large clusters are flagged for a 30% saving with no usage evidence (compounds C1), and genuinely idle small clusters are invisible. UPDATING/MAINTENANCE clusters are skipped (acceptable for safety, but undocumented).
- **Fix:** Replace the name-substring gate with a utilization-based gate (CloudWatch BytesIn/Out per broker, CPU) before recommending downsizing; if no metric is available, emit a $0 advisory. Document the ACTIVE-only scope.

#### 🟢 L1 · Pricing-miss / engine-None paths emit counted-zero recs and a region-blind $0.15 fabricated fallback with no warning  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/msk.py:40,56 + core/pricing_engine.py:728-736`
- **Evidence:** When ctx.pricing_engine is None, savings stays 0.0 but recs are still emitted and counted in total_recommendations (msk.py:40,56,62) with their human strings — a tab showing recommendations but $0 counted savings and no warning. When the EC2 fallback itself fails, get_msk_broker_hourly_price returns a hardcoded 0.15 (pricing_engine.py:732) that is NOT region-scaled (unlike the 0.10 storage literal which is multiplied by pricing_multiplier).
- **Impact:** Low-frequency, but produces either a silent $0-savings tab full of recs, or a fabricated region-blind broker number with no audit trace.
- **Fix:** When pricing is unavailable, mark the recs $0 advisory (Counted=False) and/or ctx.warn so the report explains the $0. Region-scale the 0.15 last-ditch constant (x fallback_multiplier) like the EFS/network fallbacks.

#### 🟢 L2 · Express brokers, MSK Serverless (DCU), and Tiered storage are un-priced — documented coverage gaps  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/msk.py:72-79 + services/adapters/msk.py:35`
- **Evidence:** list_clusters_v2 results are intentionally discarded (line 79); the DCU-hour serverless comparison is a TODO ($0.06/DCU-hour, msk.py:35). The storage leg assumes GP2 $0.10/GB-Mo; Express brokers (express.m7g.*, t3.small) and Tiered storage are priced differently and are not handled.
- **Impact:** Serverless, Express-broker, and Tiered-storage clusters yield no MSK savings — a coverage gap, not a wrong number. Acceptable provided it is documented, but no warning tells the operator these were skipped.
- **Fix:** Document the gap in services/adapters/CLAUDE.md (intentional, like the RDS Aurora-Serverless gap). Optionally emit a $0 advisory noting un-priced cluster classes so they are visible rather than silent.

---

### Network & Infrastructure — `services/adapters/network.py`

**Module identity:** NetworkModule (key="network", display_name="Network & Infrastructure"), services/adapters/network.py. Composite adapter over 5 sub-domains: services/elastic_ip.get_elastic_ip_checks, services/nat_gateway.get_nat_gateway_checks, services/vpc_endpoints.get_vpc_endpoints_checks, services/load_balancer.get_load_balancer_checks, and the ASG path services/ec2.get_auto_scaling_checks. Emits 5 per-domain SourceBlocks: elastic_ips / nat_gateways / vpc_endpoints / load_balancers / auto_scaling_groups (network.py:136-157). DISTINCT from network_cost.py (NetworkCostModule, "Data Transfer") which is out of scope. Pricing via PricingEngine.get_eip_monthly_price / get_nat_gateway_monthly_price / get_vpc_endpoint_monthly_price / get_alb_monthly_price / get_nlb_monthly_price / get_gwlb_monthly_price, each with a region-scaled FALLBACK_* applied once on the pricing_engine=None path. Reconciliation vs services/adapters/CLAUDE.md network row: largely accurate, two drifts — (1) the row claims ALL sub-shim failures route through services/_aws_errors.record_aws_error, but the ASG path (services/ec2.get_auto_scaling_checks) catches its own exceptions with ctx.warn directly and never routes through record_aws_error; (2) the row lists get_clb_monthly_price() among the adapter's pricing methods, but load_balancer.py never calls it (the Classic-ELB check emits a "10-20%" advisory string, no CLB price lookup). ASG block is advisory (Counted=False) — confirmed $0 counted.

**Verdict:** Audited NetworkModule (services/adapters/network.py) end-to-end across its 5 sub-domains (EIP, NAT, VPC endpoints, ELB, ASG), the PricingEngine methods, and the reporter wiring; validated the 4 material rates live. Commit 90723e3 claims mostly HOLD: render desync RESOLVED — all 5 sources (elastic_ips/nat_gateways/vpc_endpoints/load_balancers/auto_scaling_groups) are registered in PHASE_B_HANDLERS->_render_network_enhanced_checks (reporter_phase_b.py:2484-2488), each SourceBlock carries count=len(recs), there is no network entry in _RECOMMENDATION_FILTERS so no render-time drop, and the handler renders both counted and advisory recs, so detail cards never blank while savings are counted. ALB pricing FIXED (own 'Load Balancer-Application' SKU, validated $16.43, != Classic). ASG dedup HOLDS (all asg_recs forced Counted=False via _mark_advisory -> $0 counted, no overlap with the EC2 rightsizing tab; DesiredCapacity==0 skipped; ASG paginated). NAT same-AZ/cross-AZ dedup HOLDS (same-AZ counts (count-1) per AZ as pure waste; cross-AZ counts only the incremental (num_azs-1); dev/test counted only when sole-in-VPC; verified non-overlapping across multiple topologies). Silent failures: the four services/ sub-shims route through record_aws_error, BUT the ASG path (services/ec2.get_auto_scaling_checks) still uses ctx.warn directly (NET-04). Material cost defects: NET-01 (HIGH) — ALB consolidation savings both speculative and double-counted across single_service_albs (full per-ALB cost as if all eliminable) and shared_alb_opportunity (lump (n-2) again), the largest source of inflated counted Network savings; NET-02 (MEDIUM) — interface endpoints double-counted across interface_endpoints_in_nonprod and duplicate_endpoints; NET-03 (LOW) — stopped-instance EIPs double-counted across eips_on_stopped_instances and multiple_eips_per_instance. Limitations: NET-04 ASG error misclassification ($0 impact), NET-05 dead idle/no-traffic categories (missed savings + overstated description), NET-06 duplicate gateway-endpoint advisory, NET-07 VPC-endpoint fetch not Hrs-constrained (currently correct, latent). EIP in-use billing model verified — those $3.65 removals are real, not false positives. Counted==rendered holds; advisory $0 recs are rendered-not-counted as intended.

**Pricing validation:** Live AWS Price List API (us-east-1, effectiveDate 2026-06-01, retrieved 2026-06-27). (1) Public IPv4 / EIP — AmazonVPC group=VPCPublicIPv4Address returns USE1-PublicIPv4:InUseAddress=$0.005/hr AND USE1-PublicIPv4:IdleAddress=$0.005/hr -> $3.65/mo; CONFIRMS in-use public IPv4 is billed, so public_ips_should_be_private and eips_on_stopped_instances $3.65 savings are legitimate (NOT false positives), and matches FALLBACK_EIP_MONTH=3.65 plus _fetch_eip_price (AmazonVPC, group filter). (2) NAT Gateway — AmazonEC2 productFamily='NAT Gateway' operation='NatGateway': NatGateway-Hours=$0.045/hr -> $32.85/mo; matches FALLBACK_NAT_MONTH=32.85 and _fetch_nat_gateway_price (uses _call_pricing_api_hourly to correctly skip the $0.045/GB and Gbps rows). (3) Interface VPC endpoint — AmazonVPC productFamily='VpcEndpoint' endpointType='PrivateLink': VpcEndpoint-Hours=$0.01/hr -> $7.30/mo per AZ; matches FALLBACK_VPC_ENDPOINT_MONTH=7.30 and the per-AZ billing logic (_interface_az_count). Caveat NET-07: the same filter also returns the $0.01/GB Bytes SKU and the fetch is not Hrs-constrained. (4) ELB — get_pricing_attribute_values(AWSELB, productFamily) returns FOUR distinct families: 'Load Balancer' (Classic), 'Load Balancer-Application' (ALB), 'Load Balancer-Network' (NLB), 'Load Balancer-Gateway' (GWLB). ALB LoadBalancerUsage=$0.0225/hr -> $16.43/mo; CONFIRMS ALB != Classic and that get_alb_monthly_price's productFamily='Load Balancer-Application' (with _fetch_lb_base_hourly excluding TS-/Outposts- variants) is correct — the H1 ALB-priced-as-Classic fix holds. Classic 'Load Balancer' SKU is distinct; get_clb_monthly_price (FALLBACK_CLB_MONTH=18.25) is defined but unused by the adapter.

**Cost checks:**

| Check | Status | Trigger | Savings basis |
|---|---|---|---|
| elastic_ip.unassociated_eips | counted | EIP with no InstanceId and no NetworkInterfaceId (describe_addresses) | eip_monthly per EIP ($3.65 live-validated) |
| elastic_ip.eips_on_stopped_instances | counted | EIP whose InstanceId resolves to a stopped instance | eip_monthly per EIP |
| elastic_ip.multiple_eips_per_instance | counted | instance with eip_count>1 | (eip_count-1)*eip_monthly reduction to 1 |
| elastic_ip.public_ips_should_be_private | counted | running instance with PublicIpAddress in subnet MapPublicIpOnLaunch=False | eip_monthly per public IP (in-use IPv4 billed, validated) |
| nat_gateway.multiple_nat_gateways (same-AZ) | counted | >1 available NAT in same (vpc,az) | (count-1)*nat_monthly, full waste |
| nat_gateway.unnecessary_nat_per_az (cross-AZ) | counted | available NATs span >1 AZ in a VPC | (num_azs-1)*nat_monthly incremental to same-AZ |
| nat_gateway.nat_in_dev_test | counted | NAT Environment tag in dev/test/development/staging AND sole NAT in VPC | nat_monthly when sole-in-VPC, else $0 |
| nat_gateway.nat_for_aws_services / low_throughput_nat_gateways | advisory | VPC w/ NAT missing S3/DDB endpoint; every available NAT | $0.01/GB rate / CW-gated -> parses to $0 |
| vpc_endpoints.interface_endpoints_in_nonprod | counted | Interface endpoint Environment tag in nonprod | vpc_ep_monthly * az_count (per-AZ, validated $7.30) |
| vpc_endpoints.duplicate_endpoints | counted | >2 interface endpoints for same vpc:service | sum(vpc_ep_monthly*az_count) over removable[2:] |
| vpc_endpoints.missing_gateway_endpoints / unused_interface_endpoints / no_traffic_endpoints | advisory | VPC missing S3/DDB gateway; (latter two never populated) | $0.01/GB rate / dead categories -> $0 |
| load_balancer.idle_listeners | counted | LB (any type) with 0 listeners | lb_rate_by_type[type] if deleted (ALB/NLB/GWLB) |
| load_balancer.single_service_albs | counted | application LB with exactly 1 listener | full alb_monthly 'per ALB eliminated through consolidation' |
| load_balancer.shared_alb_opportunity | counted | alb_count>5 and standalone>2 (or k8s_managed>3) | (standalone-2)*alb_monthly and/or (k8s-2)*alb_monthly |
| load_balancer.nlb_vs_alb / old_classic_elbs / zero_traffic_albs | advisory | NLB present; Classic ELB age>365d; (zero_traffic dead) | $0 CW-gated / '10-20%' percentage / dead -> $0 |
| ec2.get_auto_scaling_checks.oversized_instances (ASG) | advisory | ASG launch-template type xlarge+ AND DesiredCapacity>0 | _compute_ec2_savings delta, forced Counted=False by _mark_advisory |

**Findings:**

#### 🟠 NET-01 · ALB consolidation savings are speculative AND double-counted across single_service_albs and shared_alb_opportunity  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/load_balancer.py:158-180 (single_service_albs), 204-228 (shared_alb_opportunity)`
- **Evidence:** single_service_albs emits per single-listener ALB EstimatedSavings='Up to ${alb_monthly:.2f}/month per ALB eliminated through consolidation' (line 164/176) which parse_dollar_savings reads as 16.43 -> Counted=True. Independently, shared_alb_opportunity (line 212/224) emits EstimatedSavings='Save ${(standalone_count-2)*alb_monthly:.0f}/month by consolidating to 2 ALBs' (and a second (k8s-2) variant) -> also Counted=True. Both findings cover the SAME standalone ALBs: with N single-service standalone ALBs and alb_count>5, single_service_albs counts N*16.43 (implying every ALB is eliminable) while shared_alb_opportunity counts (N-2)*16.43 on top. Neither is metric-gated; consolidation merges services onto a surviving ALB so all of them cannot be eliminated.
- **Impact:** Inflates counted Network savings by roughly (N + (N-2))*$16.43 versus the true ceiling of (N-2)*$16.43; e.g. 6 single-service ALBs count $98.58 + $65.72 = $164.30 vs a real max of ~$65.72. Violates the scope rule that every counted rec yield a concrete account-specific dollar.
- **Fix:** Make single_service_albs and shared_alb_opportunity $0 advisory (Counted=False), mirroring nlb_vs_alb/old_classic_elbs; OR keep only ONE counted and make it incremental (count at most (standalone_count-2) ALBs once, never per-ALB AND lump). Cleanest: emit a $0 advisory string for single_service_albs and keep shared_alb_opportunity advisory, since neither is backed by per-ALB LCU/traffic evidence.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified the double-count is real and survives commit 90723e3. single_service_albs (services/load_balancer.py:159-168 non-k8s, 171-180 k8s) emits EstimatedSavings 'Up to $16.43/month per ALB eliminated through consolidation' for EACH application ALB with exactly 1 listener; parse_dollar_savings (services/_savings.py:31-34) returns 16.43 on the first '$X/month' token, and mark_zero_savings_advisory leaves it Counted (16.43>0). shared_alb_opportunity (services/load_balancer.py:207-216 standalone, 219-228 k8s) independently emits 'Save $66/month by consolidating to 2 ALBs' = (standalone_count-2)*alb_monthly, also parsed positive and Counted. In services/adapters/network.py both flow into all_recs (line 126) and into total_savings (line 130 sums every rec with Counted truthy); LB recs are NOT marked advisory (only ASG is, lines 121-124), and there is NO dedup between the per-ALB and pool-level sources. Both fire on the same standalone ALB pool when alb_count>5 and standalone_count>2, and neither is metric-gated, so the same consolidation opportunity is counted twice. Commit 90723e3 addressed ALB pricing, ASG/NAT dedup, render desync, and silent failures but added no ALB-consolidation dedup; the render-desync fix actually makes the inflated load_balancers block now both counted and rendered. Mechanism, cited lines, HIGH severity, and impact direction are all accurate. Minor imprecision only: the shared rec uses ':.0f' formatting, so the parsed value is $66 (not $65.72) and the worked example total is $98.58 + $66 = $164.58 (finding states $164.30) — a trivial rounding detail that does not change the substance or the verdict.  _Correction:_ Same finding; only the exact figures shift due to ':.0f' rounding of the shared rec: for 6 single-service standalone ALBs the counted total is $98.58 (6 x $16.43) + $66 (shared, rounded from 65.72) = $164.58 vs a true consolidation ceiling of ~$66 (eliminate 4 of 6 ALBs). Inflation is roughly N*$16.43 on top of the legitimate (N-2)*$16.43.

#### 🟡 NET-02 · Interface VPC endpoint counted twice when a nonprod endpoint is also a 3rd+ duplicate  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/vpc_endpoints.py:111-125 (interface_endpoints_in_nonprod), 132-150 (duplicate_endpoints)`
- **Evidence:** The loop at 98-130 appends EVERY nonprod interface endpoint to interface_endpoints_in_nonprod with EstimatedSavings='${vpc_ep_monthly*az_count}/month per endpoint' (Counted=True) and also adds it to interface_by_service. The duplicate loop at 132-150 then counts removable=service_endpoints[2:] for any vpc:service group with >2 endpoints, each at vpc_ep_monthly*az_count (Counted=True). A dev/test-tagged endpoint that is the 3rd+ of its service is counted in BOTH findings.
- **Impact:** Over-counts the VPC-endpoint domain by vpc_ep_monthly*az_count (>= $7.30/AZ) per overlapping endpoint. Triggers when a VPC has >2 same-service interface endpoints all tagged nonprod (a common dev pattern), so inflation can be several multiples of $7.30/mo.
- **Fix:** Make the checks mutually exclusive: when building duplicate_endpoints, exclude endpoints already in interface_endpoints_in_nonprod (track VpcEndpointIds in a set), or count each endpoint once and attribute the nonprod reasoning as metadata rather than a second counted finding.

#### 🟢 NET-03 · Stopped instance with multiple EIPs counted in both eips_on_stopped_instances and multiple_eips_per_instance  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/elastic_ip.py:65-82 (eips_on_stopped_instances), 84-96 (multiple_eips_per_instance)`
- **Evidence:** For each EIP on a stopped instance the loop appends one eips_on_stopped_instances rec at eip_monthly (line 79, Counted=True). The same instance also increments instance_eip_count (line 69); if eip_count>1 the multiple_eips_per_instance check (line 93) adds (eip_count-1)*eip_monthly (Counted=True). A stopped instance with 2 EIPs is counted as 2*$3.65 + 1*$3.65 = $10.95 while its true public-IPv4 cost is 2*$3.65 = $7.30/mo.
- **Impact:** Over-counts by (eip_count-1)*eip_monthly per stopped instance holding multiple EIPs. Narrow trigger (stopped + >=2 EIPs) so dollar impact is small, but a real double count.
- **Fix:** When an instance contributes per-EIP findings via eips_on_stopped_instances, skip it in multiple_eips_per_instance (or vice-versa) so each EIP's $3.65 is attributed once; e.g. exclude instance_ids already in eips_on_stopped_instances from the multiple_eips_per_instance loop.

#### 🟢 NET-04 · ASG sub-shim bypasses record_aws_error; permission failures misclassified as warnings (H4 incomplete)  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/ec2.py:911-913, 925-929 (get_auto_scaling_checks)`
- **Evidence:** Unlike the four services/ sub-shims (elastic_ip/nat_gateway/vpc_endpoints/load_balancer) which call services/_aws_errors.record_aws_error, get_auto_scaling_checks catches its describe_auto_scaling_groups / describe_policies / launch-template failures with ctx.warn(...) directly (lines 912, 926, 929). Because the outer try/except swallows the exception internally, it never reaches _safe_collect (network.py:61-65) where record_aws_error would classify it. An autoscaling:DescribeAutoScalingGroups AccessDenied is recorded as a generic warning, not ctx.permission_issue.
- **Impact:** Operator-visibility gap only: ASG findings are advisory (Counted=False), so a misclassified permission error costs $0 in counted savings but understates the IAM/permission picture and contradicts the CLAUDE.md claim that all sub-shim failures route through record_aws_error.
- **Fix:** Route the get_auto_scaling_checks except blocks through services/_aws_errors.record_aws_error(ctx, e, service=..., context=...) so AccessDenied/OptInRequired land on ctx.permission_issue, matching the other four sub-shims.

#### 🟢 NET-05 · Declared idle/no-traffic categories never populated; 'Unused VPC endpoints' description unbacked  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/vpc_endpoints.py:36-42 (checks dict); load_balancer.py:73-83 (zero_traffic_albs)`
- **Evidence:** vpc_endpoints.py declares 'unused_interface_endpoints' and 'no_traffic_endpoints' in the checks dict but no code appends to them; load_balancer.py declares 'zero_traffic_albs' but never populates it. The adapter advertises 'Unused VPC endpoints' (network.py:167-170) and 'Idle, low-traffic ... Load Balancers', yet there is no CloudWatch traffic check (interface-endpoint bytes, ALB RequestCount) to detect a configured-but-idle resource.
- **Impact:** Coverage gap: truly idle interface endpoints ($7.30/AZ each) and zero-traffic ALBs ($16.43 each) that are configured (have subnets/listeners) are not surfaced, so real savings are missed. No incorrect dollars emitted; understates rather than overstates.
- **Fix:** Implement a CloudWatch-gated idle check populating these categories (advisory if fast_mode/no metrics, counted on proven 0 traffic), or remove the dead categories and trim the descriptions to match what is detected.

#### 🟢 NET-06 · Missing S3/DynamoDB gateway-endpoint advisory emitted by two sub-shims (duplicate noise)  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/nat_gateway.py:125-148 (nat_for_aws_services) vs services/vpc_endpoints.py:71-93 (missing_gateway_endpoints)`
- **Evidence:** nat_gateway.py emits a 'Create VPC endpoints for S3/DynamoDB' rec per VPC-with-NAT ($0.01/GB advisory), and vpc_endpoints.py independently emits a 'Missing S3/DynamoDB Gateway Endpoint' rec per VPC ($0.01/GB advisory). Both render under the network tab for the same VPC.
- **Impact:** No dollar impact (both parse to $0 and are advisory), but the same recommendation appears twice across the nat_gateways and vpc_endpoints cards, double-listing the same VPC.
- **Fix:** Consolidate the missing-gateway-endpoint recommendation into one sub-shim (vpc_endpoints.py already enumerates all VPCs) and drop nat_for_aws_services, or cross-reference so the same VPC is reported once.

#### 🟢 NET-07 · VPC interface-endpoint price fetch not constrained to the hourly dimension  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `core/pricing_engine.py:1539-1548 (_fetch_vpc_endpoint_price)`
- **Evidence:** _fetch_vpc_endpoint_price filters productFamily=VpcEndpoint + endpointType=PrivateLink and calls _call_pricing_api (MaxResults=1; _extract_usd takes the first SKU's first priceDimension) rather than _call_pricing_api_hourly (which selects unit=='Hrs'). The live API returns BOTH a per-hour SKU ($0.01/hr) and a per-GB data-processing SKU ($0.01/GB base tier) for this filter; with MaxResults=1 the result depends on row order and is correct only because both are coincidentally $0.01 in us-east-1.
- **Impact:** Currently correct ($7.30/mo) but latent: in any region/schedule where the interface-endpoint per-hour rate diverges from the $0.01/GB rate, the per-AZ endpoint cost (and the counted interface_endpoints_in_nonprod / duplicate_endpoints savings) could silently take the wrong dimension. NAT already guards this via _call_pricing_api_hourly.
- **Fix:** Switch _fetch_vpc_endpoint_price to _call_pricing_api_hourly (or add a usagetype.endswith('VpcEndpoint-Hours') / unit=='Hrs' guard) so it always selects the hourly endpoint SKU rather than relying on per-GB == per-hour coincidence.

---

### Network (Data Transfer) — `services/adapters/network_cost.py`

**Module identity:** CONFIRMED. services/adapters/network_cost.py defines NetworkCostModule with key="network_cost", cli_aliases=("network_cost","data_transfer"), display_name="Data Transfer", required_clients()=("ce","ec2"), requires_cloudwatch=False, reads_fast_mode=False, stat_cards (3), grouping=GroupingSpec(by="check_category") (lines 47-85). Registered in services/__init__.py:31,83 (NetworkCostModule() in ALL_MODULES) so findings are live. Confirmed NOT in core/scan_orchestrator.py _HUB_SERVICES (lines 52-74) and not in type_map (lines 86-113) — no Cost Optimization Hub / Compute Optimizer axis applies, so a "missing CoH/CO source" finding is out of scope, as the brief states. services/adapters/CLAUDE.md does NOT list network_cost in any pricing table (Live/Parse-rate/Flat-rate) — it is an undocumented adapter whose "rates" are module constants (CROSS_AZ_SAVINGS_FACTOR=0.5, CLOUDFRONT_SAVINGS_FACTOR=0.40, TGW_ATTACHMENT_COST_PER_GB=0.05, TGW_PROCESSING_COST_PER_GB=0.02, plus an inline 0.30); the doc row should be added if fixes land (Phase 0a). Data source = one CE get_cost_and_usage call (USAGE_TYPE_GROUP=["AWS Data Transfer"], grouped by USAGE_TYPE, UnblendedCost+UsageQuantity, MONTHLY, 30d, NextPageToken-paginated) plus EC2 describe_vpc_peering_connections (active only) + describe_transit_gateways. Emits 4 SourceBlocks: cross_region_transfer, cross_az_transfer, internet_egress, tgw_vs_peering. Savings carried as snake_case numeric monthly_savings; total_monthly_savings=sum(monthly_savings for Counted) after mark_zero_savings_advisory.

**Verdict:** network_cost prices 30-day Cost Explorer 'AWS Data Transfer' spend into three counted reduction-factor recs (cross-region x0.30, cross-AZ x0.50, egress x0.40) plus a tgw_vs_peering source with two $0 advisories and one counted derived rec. Module identity reconciles with the brief; it correctly uses neither CoH nor CO. The headline defect (C1, CRITICAL, validated live) is that the usage-type classifier is built on bare substrings that scramble the buckets against the real AWS usage-type catalog: cross-AZ `DataTransfer-Regional-Bytes` is swallowed by the 'region' branch (scored as cross-region x0.30), real inter-region `USE1-USW2-AWS-Out-Bytes` falls through to the egress catch-all (x0.40), and the cross_az keyword set is effectively dead — so two of three categories get the wrong factor and wrong tab. H1: every counted dollar is an unbacked percentage of the CE bill with no usage metric/target/AuditBasis. H2: the TGW branch-(c) formula reduces algebraically to transfer_spend*0.20 over the cross-region+cross-AZ spend already counted — a circular intra-adapter double count. H3: CE and both EC2 describes swallow exceptions with logger.warning only (no ctx.warn/permission_issue, unlike the sibling network adapter which uses record_aws_error), so an AccessDenied/OptInRequired produces a silent empty tab and wastes the $0.01 CE call. M1 (validated): TGW_ATTACHMENT_COST_PER_GB=0.05 is actually $0.05/attachment-HOUR, mislabeled as $/GB. M2: EC2 topology calls are unpaginated and TGW count lacks a state/ownership filter. L1/L2: badge confidence is wrong ('Metric Backed' on a heuristic), the adapter stat_cards and the html multi_source_cards descriptors diverge (HTML drops Monthly Savings), and although the cross-`network` overlap is conceptually present, the network adapter's counted NAT savings are gateway-HOURS (a different cost line) and it keeps per-GB NAT savings advisory, so no literal same-dollar double count is demonstrated today. Confirmed bugs: C1, H1, H2, H3, M1. Limitations: M2, L1, L2.

**Pricing validation:** Validated live against AWS Pricing API (aws-pricing-mcp-server, 2026-06-25 publication). (1) TGW unit error CONFIRMED: AmazonVPC us-east-1 usagetype `USE1-TransitGateway-Hours` = $0.05 per attachment-HOUR (unit 'hour', e.g. '$0.05 per Transit Gateway VPC Attachment Hour', SKU 9N2FHGMMCZBKDCGH; same $0.05/hr for VPC/VPN/DirectConnect/Connect/Peering attachment types), while `USE1-TransitGateway-Bytes` = $0.02 per GB (unit 'GigaBytes', SKU 7W9NVPG8YS74A6WC). The scanner's TGW_ATTACHMENT_COST_PER_GB=0.05 conflates the per-attachment-hour fee with a per-GB rate. TGW_PROCESSING_COST_PER_GB=0.02 is correct. (2) Classifier scramble CONFIRMED via get_pricing_attribute_values: AWSDataTransfer usagetype list contains `DataTransfer-Regional-Bytes`/`USE2-DataTransfer-Regional-Bytes` (canonical cross-AZ, contains 'regional' -> matched by the 'region' substring in the cross_region branch) and `USE1-USW2-AWS-Out-Bytes`/`-In-Bytes` (canonical inter-region, contains no 'region'/'az'/'egress'/'data-transfer-out' token -> falls to the catch-all egress bucket). (3) The 0.30/0.50/0.40 reduction factors are not AWS rates at all — they are unbacked percentages of a CE bill, so no SKU validation applies; the bug is that they are fabricated, not that a rate lookup is wrong. (4) No double-multiply: multiplier is accepted but unused / explicitly discarded (lines 116-118, 329) — correct, because CE returns region-priced dollars; NOT a bug.

**Cost checks:**

| Check | Status | Trigger | Savings basis |
|---|---|---|---|
| cross_region_transfer (_analyze_cross_region) | counted | usage_breakdown['cross_region'] > 0 (CE spend bucketed by the 'interregion'/'cross-region'/'region' keyword branch) | monthly_savings = cross_region_spend * 0.30 (hardcoded inline factor, line 253). multiplier param accepted but unused (correct — CE dollars are already region-priced). No usage metric, no target, no AuditBasis. |
| cross_az_transfer (_analyze_cross_az) | counted | usage_breakdown['cross_az'] > 0 (CE spend bucketed by the 'transfer-region'/'az'/'availability-zone' keyword branch — largely DEAD against real usage-type names) | monthly_savings = cross_az_spend * CROSS_AZ_SAVINGS_FACTOR(0.5) (line 290). No usage metric, no target, no AuditBasis. In practice this bucket is almost always empty because real cross-AZ usage type 'DataTransfer-Regional-Bytes' is swallowed by the cross_region branch first. |
| internet_egress (_analyze_internet_egress) | counted | usage_breakdown['egress'] > 0 (CE spend matching 'egress'/'internet'/'data-transfer-out' OR the catch-all else branch) | monthly_savings = egress_spend * CLOUDFRONT_SAVINGS_FACTOR(0.40) (line 330). multiplier explicitly discarded (_ = multiplier, line 329 — correct). No usage metric, no target, no AuditBasis. Catch-all else absorbs unmatched usage types incl. real inter-region transfer. |
| tgw_vs_peering branch (a) — TGW present | advisory | tgw_count > 0 (lines 400-414) | monthly_savings = 0.0; current_value/reason embed conflated string '${tgw_total_per_gb:.2f}/GB' = '$0.07/GB' (0.05+0.02). Demoted to Counted=False by mark_zero_savings_advisory. |
| tgw_vs_peering branch (b) — peering only | advisory | peering_count > 0 and tgw_count == 0 (lines 416-430) | monthly_savings = 0.0; advisory nudge to consider TGW at scale. Demoted to Counted=False. |
| tgw_vs_peering branch (c) — mixed TGW+peering | counted | tgw_count > 0 and peering_count > 0 and transfer_spend>0 and potential_savings>1.0 (lines 432-450) | monthly_savings = (transfer_spend/0.02)*TGW_PROCESSING_COST_PER_GB(0.02)*0.20, which algebraically reduces to transfer_spend*0.20 where transfer_spend = cross_region_spend + cross_az_spend — the SAME dollars already counted by the cross_region (x0.30) and cross_az (x0.50) recs. Circular derivation; the /0.02 x 0.02 cancels. |

**Findings:**

#### 🔴 C1 · Usage-type classifier scrambles the three transfer buckets against real AWS usage-type names (validated live)  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/network_cost.py:219-228`
- **Evidence:** Classifier: `if any(kw in usage_type for kw in ('interregion','cross-region','region')): breakdown['cross_region'] += cost  elif any(kw in usage_type for kw in ('transfer-region','az','availability-zone')): breakdown['cross_az']  elif any(kw in usage_type for kw in ('egress','internet','data-transfer-out')): breakdown['egress']  else: breakdown['egress']`. Validated against the live AWS Pricing usage-type catalog (get_pricing_attribute_values, AWSDataTransfer/AmazonVPC): (1) real cross-AZ usage type is `DataTransfer-Regional-Bytes` (and `USE2-DataTransfer-Regional-Bytes`, etc.) — 'regional' contains the substring 'region', so it matches the FIRST (cross_region) branch and is bucketed cross-region (x0.30), never reaching the cross_az branch; (2) real inter-region usage type is `USE1-USW2-AWS-Out-Bytes` (region-pair + AWS-Out/In-Bytes) — contains none of 'interregion'/'cross-region'/'region', none of the az keywords, and none of the egress keywords, so it falls through to the catch-all `else -> egress` (x0.40); (3) real internet egress `DataTransfer-Out-Bytes` lowercases to 'datatransfer-out-bytes' which does NOT contain the dashed keyword 'data-transfer-out', so it too only lands in egress via the catch-all. The cross_az keyword set ('transfer-region'/'az'/'availability-zone') is effectively dead, and 'az' is additionally over-broad.
- **Impact:** The two largest transfer categories get the wrong reduction factor AND the wrong report tab: genuine cross-AZ spend is scored at x0.30 in the Cross-Region tab; genuine inter-region spend is scored at x0.40 in the Internet Egress tab. The cross_az_transfer SourceBlock is almost always empty in practice. Every counted dollar in this adapter is mis-attributed; the headline cross-region figure (also surfaced as the 'Cross-Region Spend' stat card) is actually cross-AZ traffic.
- **Fix:** Anchor classification on full AWS usage-type tokens, not bare substrings. Match inter-region on the `<SRC>-<DST>-AWS-(In|Out)-Bytes` region-pair pattern (two region codes); match cross-AZ on `DataTransfer-Regional-Bytes`; match egress on `DataTransfer-Out-Bytes`/`-Out-ABytes`. Test cross-AZ (Regional) BEFORE the inter-region match, and drop the bare 'region'/'az' substrings. Add a unit test feeding `USE1-DataTransfer-Regional-Bytes` and asserting it lands in cross_az, and `USE1-USW2-AWS-Out-Bytes` asserting cross_region.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** network_cost.py:219-228 contains the exact classifier described. Substring tracing against the cited live usage-type names disproves any benign reading: (1) cross-AZ 'DataTransfer-Regional-Bytes' lowercases to 'datatransfer-regional-bytes' and 'regional' contains 'region', so it matches the FIRST branch (cross_region) and is scored at x0.30 instead of x0.50 in the wrong tab; (2) inter-region 'USE1-USW2-AWS-Out-Bytes' -> 'use1-usw2-aws-out-bytes' matches none of interregion/cross-region/region, none of transfer-region/az/availability-zone, none of egress/internet/data-transfer-out, so it falls to the catch-all else -> egress (x0.40); (3) 'DataTransfer-Out-Bytes' -> 'datatransfer-out-bytes' does NOT contain the dashed 'data-transfer-out' but still lands in egress via the catch-all (correct bucket by luck, as the evidence itself states). The cross_az keyword set is effectively dead; the cross_region/cross_az_spend buckets and the 'Cross-Region Spend' stat card (extras.cross_region_spend_30d, lines 112,159) are mis-attributed. Mechanism, lines, and impact all hold.

#### 🟠 H1 · All counted savings are unbacked reduction factors (0.30 / 0.50 / 0.40) applied to a raw 30-day CE bill  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/network_cost.py:253, 290, 330`
- **Evidence:** `potential_savings = monthly_est * 0.30` (cross-region, line 253), `* CROSS_AZ_SAVINGS_FACTOR(0.5)` (line 290), `* CLOUDFRONT_SAVINGS_FACTOR(0.40)` (line 330). Each is a flat percentage of the CE spend with NO per-resource evidence, NO target architecture, NO usage metric — the universal 'reduction factor instead of exact price delta' + 'savings from a config dimension alone' anti-patterns. All three set monthly_savings>0 so mark_zero_savings_advisory keeps them Counted=True. The constants are not in services/adapters/CLAUDE.md and carry no AuditBasis.
- **Impact:** The entire counted total of this adapter is fabricated $ — e.g. a recommendation to 'consolidate regions' or 'route through CloudFront' assumes a fixed 30-50% of the bill is recoverable with no proof any of it is movable. Inflates total_monthly_savings, which result_builder._summary sums into the executive headline (core/result_builder.py:72).
- **Fix:** Demote the three to $0 advisory (Counted=False) unless each can be backed by a calibrated, labelled factor plus a structured AuditBasis (rate/region/metric-window/formula) — mirror lambda_svc.py's mark_zero_savings_advisory pattern. At minimum gate cross-AZ savings on a real co-location signal and egress savings on a CloudFront price-delta computed from CE egress GB x (egress rate - CloudFront rate), not a flat 40%.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Lines 252-253 (monthly_est = cross_region_spend; *0.30), 289-290 (*CROSS_AZ_SAVINGS_FACTOR=0.5, line 30), 324-330 (*CLOUDFRONT_SAVINGS_FACTOR=0.40, line 31) each multiply a raw 30-day CE total (_time_period at lines 36-44) by a flat reduction factor with no per-resource evidence, no target architecture, no usage metric. The rec dicts (255-268, 292-304, 332-344) carry no AuditBasis. services/_savings.py:72-89 mark_zero_savings_advisory only sets Counted=False when savings<=0, so these positive values stay Counted=True and are summed at network_cost.py:133 and again into the executive headline at core/result_builder.py:72. network_cost is absent from services/adapters/CLAUDE.md pricing tables. Confirmed as the 'reduction factor instead of exact price delta' anti-pattern.

#### 🟠 H2 · TGW branch (c) is circular and double-counts cross-region + cross-AZ spend already scored elsewhere  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/network_cost.py:432-450`
- **Evidence:** `transfer_spend = usage_breakdown['cross_region'] + usage_breakdown['cross_az']; estimated_tgw_data_gb = transfer_spend / 0.02; potential_savings = estimated_tgw_data_gb * TGW_PROCESSING_COST_PER_GB(0.02) * 0.20`. The `/0.02` and `*0.02` cancel exactly, so potential_savings == transfer_spend * 0.20. transfer_spend is precisely the cross_region_spend (already counted at x0.30 by _analyze_cross_region) plus cross_az_spend (already counted at x0.50 by _analyze_cross_az).
- **Impact:** When tgw_count>0 AND peering_count>0 AND the derived figure exceeds the $1 floor, the same CE dollars are counted a second time (an extra 20%), inflating total_monthly_savings. The GB derivation is cosmetic — no real per-GB data drives it.
- **Fix:** Remove branch (c) or convert it to a $0 advisory. If a TGW-route-optimization saving is wanted, derive it from actual TGW-Bytes UsageQuantity (the CE response already requests UsageQuantity) x the validated $0.02/GB processing rate, and subtract from (not add to) the cross-region/cross-AZ recs to keep single ownership.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Lines 432-450: transfer_spend = usage_breakdown['cross_region'] + ['cross_az']; estimated_tgw_data_gb = transfer_spend/0.02; potential_savings = estimated_tgw_data_gb * TGW_PROCESSING_COST_PER_GB(0.02, line 33) * 0.20. The /0.02 and *0.02 cancel exactly, so potential_savings == transfer_spend*0.20 and the GB figure is cosmetic. cross_region and cross_az are already counted by _analyze_cross_region (x0.30) and _analyze_cross_az (x0.50) at lines 116-117. Gated on tgw_count>0 AND peering_count>0 AND potential_savings>1.0 (line 437); the positive value stays Counted=True (mark_zero_savings_advisory) and is added at line 133. Double-count confirmed exactly as described.

#### 🟠 H3 · CE and EC2 failures are swallowed with logger.warning only — no ctx.warn / ctx.permission_issue anywhere  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/network_cost.py:104-105, 230-231, 363-364, 370-371`
- **Evidence:** `_fetch_transfer_spend`: `except Exception as e: logger.warning(...)` then returns zeros (230-231). `_fetch_network_topology`: both describe calls `except Exception as e: logger.warning(...)` (363-364, 370-371). `scan`: `if not ce: return self._empty_findings()` (104-105) with no signal. The codebase has services/_aws_errors.record_aws_error (classifies AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation/OptInRequired -> ctx.permission_issue, else ctx.warn) and the sibling network adapter uses it (services/nat_gateway.py:68), but network_cost never imports it. core/scan_context.py exposes warn (line 49) and permission_issue (line 59).
- **Impact:** A CE AccessDenied/OptInRequired/throttle, or either EC2 describe failure, vanishes from the report: peering_count/tgw_count silently 0 and all transfer buckets silently 0, producing a blank/zero tab even when real transfer spend exists — and the $0.01 CE request is wasted with no operator signal. Permission gaps are invisible in scan_warnings/permission_issues.
- **Fix:** Route all three except blocks through record_aws_error(ctx, e, service='network_cost', context=...). For the `if not ce` early return, emit ctx.warn('Cost Explorer client unavailable; data-transfer tab skipped'). Pass ctx into the fetch helpers (currently they only receive the client).
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Confirmed at all four cited sites: line 104-105 'if not ce: return self._empty_findings()' emits no signal; 230-231, 363-364, 370-371 use only logger.warning and return zeros. grep confirms network_cost.py imports only core.contracts, services._base, and (inline) services._savings — it never imports services._aws_errors and has zero ctx.warn / ctx.permission_issue calls. The convention exists and works: services/_aws_errors.py:47-56 record_aws_error routes AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation/OptInRequired -> ctx.permission_issue else ctx.warn; sibling nat_gateway.py:15,68,194 uses it; core/scan_context.py:49 (warn) and :59 (permission_issue) accumulate into _permission_issues. So a CE AccessDenied/OptInRequired/throttle or either EC2 describe failure is invisible in scan_warnings/permission_issues and silently zeroes the tab. Confirmed.

#### 🟡 M1 · TGW_ATTACHMENT_COST_PER_GB is a unit error — $0.05 is per attachment-HOUR, not per GB (validated live)  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/network_cost.py:32, 398, 406, 410, 428`
- **Evidence:** Constant `TGW_ATTACHMENT_COST_PER_GB = 0.05` (line 32). Live AWS Pricing API (AmazonVPC, us-east-1): SKU 9N2FHGMMCZBKDCGH usagetype `USE1-TransitGateway-Hours` = '$0.05 per Transit Gateway VPC Attachment Hour', unit 'hour' (~$36.50/mo per attachment); only SKU 7W9NVPG8YS74A6WC `USE1-TransitGateway-Bytes` = '$0.02 per GB Data Processed', unit 'GigaBytes'. The code computes `tgw_total_per_gb = TGW_ATTACHMENT_COST_PER_GB + TGW_PROCESSING_COST_PER_GB = 0.07` and renders it as the string '${tgw_total_per_gb:.2f}/GB' = '$0.07/GB' (lines 398,406,410,428), conflating an hourly per-attachment fee with a per-GB processing rate.
- **Impact:** No counted-$ impact (the constant only appears in the two $0 advisory branches' display strings), but the '$0.07/GB' current_value/reason shown to the operator is materially wrong and undermines report credibility; it also misleads any future code that reuses the constant as a per-GB rate.
- **Fix:** Rename to TGW_ATTACHMENT_COST_PER_HOUR=0.05 and report it as a monthly attachment fee (0.05*730*attachments) separate from the $0.02/GB processing rate; stop summing an hourly fee and a per-GB rate into a single '$/GB' string.

#### 🟡 M2 · EC2 topology calls are unpaginated and TGW count has no state/ownership filter  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/network_cost.py:361-371`
- **Evidence:** `describe_vpc_peering_connections(Filters=[{'Name':'status-code','Values':['active']}])` and `describe_transit_gateways()` are single calls with no NextToken loop. Peering is filtered to active, but `tgw_count = len(resp.get('TransitGateways', []))` counts ALL returned TGWs with no state filter and no owner filter — including shared/cross-account RAM-shared TGWs and any in 'deleting'/'pending' state.
- **Impact:** Large accounts truncate peering_count/tgw_count at the first page, under-reporting topology and suppressing the tgw_vs_peering branches; counting shared/cross-account or deleting TGWs can wrongly trip branch (a)/(c) for resources the account does not own or pay attachment fees on.
- **Fix:** Paginate both describes (get_paginator or NextToken loop). Filter TGWs to state in {'available'} and (optionally) OwnerId == ctx.account_id to exclude RAM-shared gateways.

#### 🟢 L1 · tgw_vs_peering badge is 'Metric Backed' (wrong confidence); the other three sources have no badge; stat-card descriptors duplicate and diverge  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `reporter_phase_b.py:2397`
- **Evidence:** `_GENERIC_SOURCE_TYPES['tgw_vs_peering'] = 'Metric Backed'` (line 2397), but the rec is a CE/heuristic estimate (no CloudWatch metric). cross_region_transfer/cross_az_transfer/internet_egress are absent from both SOURCE_TYPE_MAP and _GENERIC_SOURCE_TYPES, so they render with NO badge. Separately, the adapter declares stat_cards = (Transfer Spend 30d, Cross-Region Spend, Monthly Savings) (network_cost.py:60-76) while html_report_generator.py:170-177 defines a network_cost multi_source_cards descriptor = (30-Day Transfer Spend, Cross-Region Spend, VPC Peerings, TGW Attachments); _get_service_stats (html_report_generator.py:3244-3249) renders the multi_source_cards version, so the HTML report shows VPC Peerings/TGW Attachments and DROPS the Monthly Savings card.
- **Impact:** Inconsistent confidence labelling (one source over-claims 'Metric Backed', three are unlabelled) and a divergent stat row that omits the single most material number (Monthly Savings) in favor of two counts already visible elsewhere. Cosmetic — no $ miscount and cards still render (network_cost is not in _PHASE_B_SKIP_PER_REC, so render_generic_per_rec -> _render_generic_other_rec renders all four sources).
- **Fix:** Re-label these CE-derived sources 'Audit Based' (add cross_region_transfer/cross_az_transfer/internet_egress to SOURCE_TYPE_MAP under ('network_cost', ...) and change tgw_vs_peering off 'Metric Backed'). Reconcile the two stat-card descriptors to a single source of truth that keeps Monthly Savings.

#### 🟢 L2 · Cross-adapter overlap with `network`, plus scope/negative-cost coverage notes  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/network_cost.py:129-133, 212-228`
- **Evidence:** core/result_builder.py:72 sums total_monthly_savings across ALL tabs with no cross-tab dedup. The `network` adapter counts NAT savings, but those are NAT-gateway HOURS (services/nat_gateway.py:89-120, (count-1)*nat_monthly and (azs-1)*nat_monthly) — a fixed gateway-hour cost line distinct from CE 'AWS Data Transfer' per-GB spend — and network keeps NAT data-processing/per-GB savings as $0 advisory (nat_gateway.py:145, 186-188). So a literal same-dollar double count across the two tabs is NOT demonstrated, but the two tabs both present 'data transfer' savings with no shared `covered` set. Scope: USAGE_TYPE_GROUP is limited to 'AWS Data Transfer' only (lines 190-195), excluding transfer billed under EC2:Other / S3 transfer-out / inter-region replication. Negative-cost rows are skipped via `if cost <= 0: continue` (line 215), so credits/refunds don't subtract from buckets but SP-covered transfer at $0 simply doesn't appear.
- **Impact:** Low literal double-count risk today (different cost lines), but the executive headline adds the network NAT savings and the network_cost transfer savings as if independent, and there is no guard if the network adapter ever promotes its per-GB NAT savings to counted. The 'AWS Data Transfer'-only scope under-reports total movable transfer spend.
- **Fix:** Document the single-owner rule (CE-measured spend in network_cost is authoritative for transfer bytes; network owns NAT gateway-hours) and add a shared `covered` set if network ever counts per-GB NAT savings. Document the USAGE_TYPE_GROUP scope as intentional in the adapter docstring and CLAUDE.md.

---

### OpenSearch — `services/adapters/opensearch.py`

**Module identity:** CONFIRMED matches contract: services/adapters/opensearch.py lines 21-27 declare key="opensearch", cli_aliases=("opensearch",), display_name="OpenSearch", required_clients()=("opensearch",). RECONCILE GAPS vs services/adapters/CLAUDE.md: (1) The CLAUDE.md row lists opensearch.py under "Parse-rate (5 adapters) / Keyword-based" — INACCURATE. The adapter is a HYBRID: storage recs priced from a module constant (GP3_PRICE_PER_GB_MONTH=0.11 x STORAGE_SAVINGS_FACTOR=0.20 x pricing_multiplier, lines 13-15,60) and instance recs priced LIVE via ctx.pricing_engine.get_instance_monthly_price("AmazonES", type) (lines 61-64). It does not parse dollar amounts from text at all. (2) The doc says nothing about the CoH bucket although core/scan_orchestrator.py wires opensearch into _HUB_SERVICES + type_map (lines 58,93). (3) Undeclared dependencies: the shim (services/opensearch.py lines 127-133) uses a cloudwatch client and ctx.account_id, but required_clients() returns only ("opensearch",) and the module sets neither requires_cloudwatch nor reads_fast_mode (defaults in services/_base.py lines 24-25 remain False).

**Verdict:** The opensearch adapter is a thin delegator over services/opensearch.py that re-prices five heuristic check categories. Tracing real code (not the brief's assumptions) surfaced that the actual data flow is worse than documented: only Graviton and Storage recs ever produce a counted dollar, because the shim omits InstanceType/InstanceCount on the Idle and Underutilized recs, so BOTH price to $0 and are dropped (C2 CRITICAL idle, C3 HIGH underutilized; the 0.30 downsize rate is unreachable dead code), and the shim omits InstanceCount on the Graviton rec so even that lever is undercounted to a single node (H1). The CoH bucket ctx.cost_hub_splits['opensearch'] is populated by the orchestrator (OpenSearchDomain) but never read by scan(), a silent orphan drop with no warning (C1 CRITICAL). The renderer prints the human percentage string and ignores Counted, guaranteeing a counted!=rendered desync (H2), and when the adapter nets $0 the headline fabricates $50/rec because opensearch is in _FLAT_SAVINGS_SERVICES (H4). The gp3 storage constant is understated ~10% and the gp2->gp3 saving overstated ~1.7x vs live Pricing API (H3, validated). Medium issues: CloudWatch read not fast_mode-gated and undeclared clients (M1), per-domain failures logger-only with no permission classification (M2), undefended flat reduction factors (M3), pricing-miss $0 (M4), and Serverless/UltraWarm/0-node coverage gaps (M5). Eight confirmed bugs (2 CRITICAL), four limitations. Fix order: C1, C2, C3, H1-H4, then M1-M5/L1-L2. All findings cite exact file+lines and are fixable without re-reading the whole adapter.

**Pricing validation:** LIVE AWS Pricing API (AmazonES, us-east-1, validated 2026-06-27, publicationDate 2026-06-16): ES:GP3-Storage = $0.122/GB-mo (productFamily 'Amazon OpenSearch Service Volume', operation ESDomain) vs adapter constant GP3_PRICE_PER_GB_MONTH=0.11 -> understated ~10%. ES:GP2-Storage = $0.135/GB-mo; true gp2->gp3 migration delta = $0.013/GB-mo (~9.6% of gp2), but the adapter bills 0.11 x 0.20 = $0.022/GB-mo (~1.7x overstatement) -> H3. ES:Managed-Storage (UltraWarm) = $0.024/GB-mo (~80% cut vs gp3), confirming STORAGE_SAVINGS_FACTOR's 'cold-tier/UltraWarm' docstring is unrelated to the gp2->gp3 trigger. Instance: r6g.large.search = $0.167/hr (productFamily 'Amazon OpenSearch Service Instance', operation ESDomain, usagetype ESInstance:r6g.large) => $121.91/mo; instanceType carries the '.search' suffix exactly as boto3 returns it, and the bare instanceType filter resolves to a single SKU (MaxResults=1 deterministic here, L1). Region scaling verified single-apply: storage uses 0.11 x pricing_multiplier (constant path, once); instance path uses region-correct PricingEngine and is NOT multiplied by pricing_multiplier (no double-apply).

**Cost checks:**

| Check | Status | Trigger | Savings basis |
|---|---|---|---|
| Reserved Instances Opportunity | advisory | ClusterConfig.InstanceCount >= 2 (services/opensearch.py L81) | Shim string '30-60% vs On-Demand'; adapter forces Counted=False (commitment lever, opensearch.py L66-67); priced $0 |
| Graviton Migration | counted | InstanceType not startswith m7g/r7g/m6g/r6g/c7g/c6g/t4g (services/opensearch.py L93-96) | value = get_instance_monthly_price('AmazonES', type) x instance_count x 0.25 (opensearch.py L61-64). BUG: shim graviton rec carries NO InstanceCount (services/opensearch.py L97-105) so instance_count defaults to 1 -> per-node-only |
| Storage Optimization (gp2->gp3) | counted | EBSOptions.VolumeType == 'gp2' (services/opensearch.py L111) | value = EBSVolumeSize x 0.11 x pricing_multiplier x 0.20 (opensearch.py L58-60). Live gp3=$0.122, gp2=$0.135; real gp2->gp3 delta ~$0.013/GB-mo but adapter bills $0.022/GB-mo |
| Idle Domain (delete) | advisory | avg CPUUtilization < 5 over 14d CloudWatch (services/opensearch.py L146) | Shim string '100% of domain cost'; adapter value=0.0 (no 'Idle Domain' key in rate_by_category L46-49 AND idle rec carries no InstanceType L147-155) -> dropped by keep guard L87 |
| Underutilized Domain (downsize) | advisory | 5 <= avg CPUUtilization < 20 (services/opensearch.py L156) | rate_by_category['Underutilized Domain']=0.30 (opensearch.py L48) is DEAD CODE: shim rec carries no InstanceType (L157-165) so the elif at L61 (requires instance_type) is never entered -> value=0.0 -> dropped |
| Old engine version | advisory | Intentionally removed (services/opensearch.py L107-109) | Emits nothing (no cost delta); confirmed no rec produced |

**Findings:**

#### 🔴 C1 · Orphaned Cost Optimization Hub bucket: ctx.cost_hub_splits['opensearch'] populated but never consumed  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/opensearch.py + core/scan_orchestrator.py:opensearch.py 29-100 (scan); scan_orchestrator.py 58, 93, 144`
- **Evidence:** scan_orchestrator._prefetch_advisor_data lists 'opensearch' in _HUB_SERVICES (L58) and maps 'OpenSearchDomain'->'opensearch' in type_map (L93), then stores ctx.cost_hub_splits=splits (L144). OpensearchModule.scan (opensearch.py L29-100) calls only get_enhanced_opensearch_checks(ctx); grep for cost_hub_splits in both opensearch files returns no match. The orchestrator's 'no service bucket' warning (L135-142) only fires for UNbucketed types, so a populated-but-unconsumed bucket drops silently.
- **Impact:** AWS-authoritative OpenSearchDomain rightsizing dollars are silently dropped on every scan that selects opensearch, with no warning. Unknown $ leak (account-specific, can be the largest real saving).
- **Fix:** In scan(), read getattr(ctx,'cost_hub_splits',{}).get('opensearch',[]), emit each renderable CoH rec, and add authority dedup CoH > heuristic by normalized domain id (strip ARN) mirroring services/rds_logic.py (normalize + suppress heuristic for CoH-covered ids). Demote OpenSearch RI/commitment CoH recs to advisory.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified in real code. scan_orchestrator._prefetch_advisor_data lists 'opensearch' in _HUB_SERVICES (L58), maps 'OpenSearchDomain'->'opensearch' (L93), and stores ctx.cost_hub_splits=splits (L144). OpensearchModule.scan (services/adapters/opensearch.py L29-100) calls only get_enhanced_opensearch_checks(ctx) and never references cost_hub_splits (grep over both opensearch files returns NONE). The only code that would consume the opensearch bucket is cost_optimization_hub.py._collect_prefetched (iterates ctx.cost_hub_splits.values(), L155/178), but CostOptimizationHubModule is explicitly retired from ALL_MODULES (services/__init__.py L71-74, commented out) so it never runs in a scan. The orchestrator's unbucketed-type warning (L135-142) only fires when bucket is empty/unmapped; OpenSearchDomain IS mapped, so the populated-but-unconsumed bucket drops with no warning. AWS-authoritative OpenSearchDomain CoH rightsizing recs are silently dropped on any scan that selects opensearch.

#### 🔴 C2 · Idle Domain priced at $0 - largest real saving (full domain delete) never counted  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/opensearch.py + services/opensearch.py:opensearch.py 46-49, 58-64, 87; services/opensearch.py 147-155`
- **Evidence:** rate_by_category (opensearch.py L46-49) has keys only for 'Graviton Migration' and 'Underutilized Domain' -> 'Idle Domain' falls to rate 0.0. Compounding: the shim idle rec (services/opensearch.py L147-155) carries NO InstanceType and NO InstanceCount, so even the elif branch (L61, requires instance_type) is skipped -> value stays 0.0. keep guard L87 (...and EstimatedMonthlySavings > 0) then sets Counted=False and excludes it. EngineVersion string is '100% of domain cost'.
- **Impact:** A genuinely idle domain (delete = 100% of instance+storage cost) contributes $0 to the headline. This is a counted-savings LEAK (inverse of over-count). Worst case the same domain is instead counted for a 25% Graviton lever on one node (see C2 dedup interaction).
- **Fix:** Add 'Idle Domain' handling that prices the FULL domain cost = get_instance_monthly_price(type) x InstanceCount + storage. Requires the shim to carry InstanceType+InstanceCount (+EBS) on the idle rec (L147-155). Ensure the idle (delete) lever wins the per-domain dedup over Graviton/downsize once priced.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified. rate_by_category (services/adapters/opensearch.py L46-49) has keys only 'Graviton Migration' and 'Underutilized Domain'; 'Idle Domain' falls to rate_by_category.get(category,0.0)=0.0. The idle shim rec (services/opensearch.py L147-155) carries DomainName/AvgCPU/Recommendation/EstimatedSavings/CheckCategory but NO InstanceType and NO InstanceCount, so in the adapter instance_type=None and the elif at L61 (requires instance_type) is skipped; value stays 0.0 (and would be 0.0 anyway since 'Idle Domain' rate is 0). EstimatedMonthlySavings=0.0. keep guard L87 requires EstimatedMonthlySavings>0, so Counted=False and the full-domain-delete saving is excluded from the counted total. Genuine idle domain contributes $0 to the headline — a real counted-savings leak. The dedup note is also accurate: the $0 idle rec participates in best_instance but loses to any >0 graviton rec, so the domain is instead counted for a 25% graviton lever on one node.

#### 🟠 C3 · Underutilized Domain priced at $0 - the 0.30 downsize rate is unreachable dead code  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/opensearch.py + services/opensearch.py:opensearch.py 48, 61-64; services/opensearch.py 157-165`
- **Evidence:** The shim underutilized rec (services/opensearch.py L157-165) carries DomainName/AvgCPU/Recommendation/EstimatedSavings/CheckCategory but NO InstanceType and NO InstanceCount. In the adapter, instance_type=rec.get('InstanceType') is None, so the elif at L61 (ctx.pricing_engine is not None and instance_type) is never entered and value stays 0.0. The rate_by_category['Underutilized Domain']=0.30 (L48) is therefore never multiplied by anything. The rec is dropped by the keep>0 guard.
- **Impact:** Every 5<=CPU<20 downsize opportunity contributes $0 to the headline; the documented 0.30 downsize model does not execute. Counted-savings leak.
- **Fix:** Carry InstanceType+InstanceCount on the underutilized rec in the shim, OR replace the flat 0.30 with a concrete current->one-size-down price delta (see M3). Until then it must be rendered as an explicit $0 advisory, not a silent drop.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified. The underutilized shim rec (services/opensearch.py L157-165) carries DomainName/AvgCPU/Recommendation/EstimatedSavings='30-50%'/CheckCategory but NO InstanceType and NO InstanceCount. In the adapter instance_type=rec.get('InstanceType')=None, so the elif at L61 (ctx.pricing_engine is not None and instance_type) is never entered and value stays 0.0. rate_by_category['Underutilized Domain']=0.30 (L48) is therefore never multiplied — dead code. The rec is dropped by the keep>0 guard (L87). Every 5<=CPU<20 downsize opportunity contributes $0; confirmed counted-savings leak.

#### 🟠 H1 · Graviton saving ignores data-node count (instance_count defaults to 1)  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/opensearch.py + services/opensearch.py:opensearch.py 56, 61-64; services/opensearch.py 97-105`
- **Evidence:** The shim graviton rec (services/opensearch.py L97-105) carries InstanceType but NOT InstanceCount (only the Reserved rec L82-91 carries InstanceCount). In the adapter, instance_count = rec.get('InstanceCount', 1) or 1 (L56) -> always 1 for the graviton path. value = monthly x 1 x 0.25 (L64).
- **Impact:** Graviton savings on any multi-node domain are undercounted by the node-count factor N (e.g. a 6-node r5 domain is priced as 1 node). Systematic under-count of the one lever that IS counted.
- **Fix:** Carry ClusterConfig.InstanceCount on the graviton rec in the shim (L97-105) so the adapter multiplies by the real data-node count.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified. The graviton shim rec (services/opensearch.py L97-105) carries InstanceType (L100) but NOT InstanceCount; only the reserved shim (L82-91) carries InstanceCount (L86), even though describe_domain reads instance_count at L77. In the adapter, instance_count = rec.get('InstanceCount',1) or 1 (L56) is therefore always 1 on the graviton path, and value = monthly * 1 * 0.25 (L62-64). Graviton savings on any multi-node domain are undercounted by the node-count factor N. Confirmed systematic under-count of the one lever that is actually counted.

#### 🟠 H2 · Renderer shows the human percentage string, not the priced dollar, and ignores Counted  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `reporter_phase_b.py:1102-1113`
