| enhanced_checks: Unused Resources (empty bucket) | advisory | list_objects_v2 KeyCount==0 AND bucket_age>30d | '$0.00/month - empty bucket incurs no storage cost' (L1307-1309) |
| enhanced_checks: Static Website Optimization (CloudFront) | advisory | _is_static_website_bucket True | '$0.00/month - data transfer dependent (CloudFront CDN)'; filtered out of counted other_recs by _DEDICATED_CATEGORIES (L1324-1327) |

**Findings:**

#### 🟡 S3-N1 · CloudWatch metric-read AccessDenied/Throttling logged at debug only, not surfaced on ctx  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/s3.py:945-960, 791-796`
- **Evidence:** In the per-class BucketSizeBytes loop the except branch routes only endpoint-unreachable errors to ctx (via _mark_region_dead/ctx.warn); every other error (incl. CloudWatch AccessDenied / Throttling on cloudwatch:GetMetricStatistics) falls to `logger.debug("Error getting S3 metrics for %s/%s: %s", ...)` + continue (L954-960). Same pattern in _assess_bucket_coldness GetRequests read: non-endpoint errors -> `logger.debug(...)` then `return "unknown"` (L794-796). Neither path calls ctx.permission_issue or ctx.warn.
- **Impact:** A cloudwatch:GetMetricStatistics denial or sustained throttling silently zeroes total_size_gb for every bucket -> EstimatedMonthlyCost=0 and StandardGB unset -> no saving credited, and coldness degrades to 'unknown' -> $0 advisory. The user gets an empty/under-reported S3 cost+savings picture with NO permission_issue or warning. Safe direction (no fabricated dollars) but a real visibility/silent-failure defect explicitly in the brief's known-issue catalogue (Phase 5.10/5.12).
- **Fix:** Classify the caught exception in both metric-read sites: AccessDenied/Unauthorized/OptInRequired -> ctx.permission_issue(action='cloudwatch:GetMetricStatistics'); ThrottlingException/RequestLimitExceeded -> ctx.warn; keep endpoint-unreachable -> _mark_region_dead. Mirror the existing _route_bucket_error classification used for the S3 describe calls.

#### 🟢 S3-N2 · Cost Hub orphan: cost_hub_splits['s3'] populated but never consumed (dead wiring)  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `core/scan_orchestrator.py:52-60, 86-95, 144`
- **Evidence:** _prefetch_advisor_data lists 's3' in _HUB_SERVICES (L60) and maps 'S3Bucket':'s3' in type_map (L95), so splits['s3'] is created and assigned to ctx.cost_hub_splits (L144). grep over services/s3.py and services/adapters/s3.py for cost_hub_splits / cost_hub / _HUB_SERVICES returns ZERO hits — no S3 code reads the bucket. Because 'S3Bucket' IS in type_map, the unbucketed-type warning (L135-142) never fires either.
- **Impact:** Practically inert today: AWS Cost Optimization Hub does not currently emit currentResourceType=='S3Bucket' recommendations, so splits['s3'] is empty and ~$0 is dropped. But it is orphan/dead wiring: if AWS adds S3 CoH coverage, those recs would be fetched, bucketed, and silently dropped with no warning, and a naive future consumer could double-count against s3_bucket_analysis.
- **Fix:** Either remove 's3' from _HUB_SERVICES and 'S3Bucket' from type_map (drop the dead wiring), OR have the adapter consume ctx.cost_hub_splits.get('s3', []) and dedup by normalized bucket id with authority CoH > heuristic (a CoH-surfaced bucket must not also be counted by s3_bucket_analysis).

#### 🟢 S3-N3 · _render_s3_enhanced_checks uses an ad-hoc parser that would count a per-unit rate string (render-vs-count desync, latent)  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `reporter_phase_b.py:827-836`
- **Evidence:** Per-category total: `total_savings += float(savings_str.replace('$','').split('/')[0].replace(',',''))`. For a hypothetical '$0.01/GB' this yields 0.01 and renders a positive saving, whereas the adapter's parse_dollar_savings (services/_savings.py L31-35) rejects per-unit '/GB' rates -> 0. The renderer and the headline would then disagree.
- **Impact:** Latent only: every enhanced_checks record currently emits '$0.00/month - <reason>' which parses to 0.0 in both parsers, so counted==rendered holds today. Becomes a live desync the moment any enhanced check emits a '$/GB' or '$/request' string.
- **Fix:** Reuse parse_dollar_savings(rec.get('EstimatedSavings','')) in _render_s3_enhanced_checks instead of the bespoke replace/split, so render and count share one rate-string-rejection rule.

#### 🟢 S3-N4 · intelligent_tiering opportunity class (has lifecycle, no IT) is credited the IA delta; brief expected exclusion; IT monitoring fee + IA minimums ignored  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/s3.py:109-111, 651-670, 1038-1058`
- **Evidence:** _GAP_OPPORTUNITY_CLASSES includes 'intelligent_tiering' (L109-111). _classify_opportunities returns 'intelligent_tiering' when has_lifecycle=True and has_tiering=False (L666-669), so such a bucket IS eligible for the evidence-gated saving — contrary to the brief's Phase 4.9 expectation that 'a bucket WITH a lifecycle policy ... is intentionally excluded'. Credited delta = standard_gb x (Standard-IA) but the rendered action is 'Enable Intelligent-Tiering'.
- **Impact:** Defensible (cold Standard bytes despite an existing lifecycle policy mean that policy is not transitioning them, so enabling IT/adding a transition rule does save). But the credit ignores the IT monitoring fee (~$0.0025/1000 objects/mo) and the Standard-IA 128 KB min-billable-object-size and 30-day min-duration, so savings can be overstated for buckets of many small objects. Object count is not read. Small $.
- **Fix:** Either exclude 'intelligent_tiering' from _GAP_OPPORTUNITY_CLASSES (align with brief) OR keep it but net out an estimated IT monitoring fee and gate on average object size when object count is available; document the chosen behavior in the adapter docstring so it matches the brief.

#### 🟢 S3-N5 · list_buckets not paginated — >10k-bucket accounts silently under-enumerated  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/s3.py:831-833, 1157-1158`
- **Evidence:** Both helpers do `response = s3.list_buckets(); buckets = response.get('Buckets', [])` with no ContinuationToken / MaxBuckets handling. The brief asserts 'no pagination needed — S3 returns all in one call'.
- **Impact:** AWS raised the per-account general-purpose bucket limit (up to ~1M) and ListBuckets now paginates (default ~10,000/page). An account with >10k buckets would have buckets beyond the first page silently omitted from both cost analysis and enhanced checks -> missed coverage. Low impact (most accounts < 10k buckets).
- **Fix:** Paginate ListBuckets with ContinuationToken (or use a paginator) in both get_s3_bucket_analysis and get_enhanced_s3_checks; loop until no token.

---

### SageMaker — `services/adapters/sagemaker.py`

**Module identity:** Confirmed against services/adapters/CLAUDE.md and the brief. SageMakerModule (services/adapters/sagemaker.py:368) declares key="sagemaker", cli_aliases=("sagemaker",), display_name="SageMaker", required_clients()=("sagemaker","cloudwatch") (line 391-392), requires_cloudwatch=True (388), reads_fast_mode=True (389), grouping=GroupingSpec(by="check_category") (386), plus four stat_cards (379-384). It emits exactly four SourceBlocks — idle_endpoints, idle_notebooks, spot_training, multi_model_consolidation (421-436) — matching the four module-level _check_* functions and the four optimization_descriptions keys (443-460). Single-file adapter: no services/sagemaker.py shim, no sagemaker_logic.py. Recs use a lowercase snake_case schema (endpoint_name/notebook_name/job_name, instance_type, check_category, current_value, recommended_value, monthly_savings, reason); there is NO EstimatedSavings string and NO Counted flag anywhere. Pricing is instance-monthly-only via _get_instance_monthly -> ctx.pricing_engine.get_sagemaker_instance_monthly (pricing_engine.py:939). No Cost Optimization Hub / Compute Optimizer consumed (confirmed: not in scan_orchestrator type_map; SageMakerSavingsPlans routes to commitment_analysis at scan_orchestrator.py:112, not this adapter). RECONCILE GAP: services/adapters/CLAUDE.md Live Pricing table (19 adapters) does NOT list sagemaker even though it uses live get_sagemaker_instance_monthly — the missing row should read: sagemaker | get_sagemaker_instance_monthly(instance_type) | AWS Pricing API (AmazonSageMaker; EC2x1.15 fallback). sagemaker is correctly absent from PHASE_A_DESCRIPTORS, _PHASE_B_SKIP_PER_REC and PHASE_B_HANDLERS, so it renders via the generic per-rec fallback (see L1).

**Verdict:** The sagemaker adapter (single file, instance-monthly priced via live get_sagemaker_instance_monthly, no CoH/CO) is functionally sound on the happy path but has several cost-correctness defects, all confirmed by tracing real code. Most material: (C1) idle_notebooks flags EVERY running notebook for its full monthly cost with zero idle evidence, fabricating real dollars on actively-used notebooks. (C2) there is no mark_zero_savings_advisory gate, so idle_endpoints/idle_notebooks count $0 placeholder recs (pricing miss or instance_type=='unknown') in both the count and dollar total — inconsistent with spot/consolidation, which guard instance_monthly<=0. (H1) spot_training sums a one-time, speculative per-run cost into the recurring monthly headline. (H2) an idle endpoint is double-counted at full cost in idle_endpoints AND inside its consolidation group with no dedup. Medium: every AWS error is swallowed with no ctx.warn/permission_issue (AccessDenied reads as 'no usage'); only variants[0]/one instance is priced (InstanceCount>1 and 2nd+ variants understate savings); fast_mode is honored by only 1 of 4 checks; the EC2 fallback is dead for ml.* types -> silent $0; and the MaxResults=1 SageMaker SKU filter is non-deterministic (latent $0/free-tier risk, though all ml.m5.xlarge components currently price identically at $0.23/hr). Low: sagemaker renders via the generic per-rec path whose PascalCase resolver misses the lowercase endpoint_name/notebook_name keys, so every card titles 'Resource' and the saving renders unstyled (counted==rendered numerically holds); _list_endpoints drops pages on paginator failure; active_endpoint_count includes idle endpoints; and services/adapters/CLAUDE.md omits the sagemaker Live-Pricing row. Live Pricing API (2026-06-27) confirms ml.m5.xlarge=$0.23/hr across all components and EC2 m5.xlarge=$0.192/hr (real premium ~1.20). Fix order: C1, C2, H1, H2 first (dollar-impacting), then M1-M5, then L1-L4. No live scan run (read-only/no-creds).

**Pricing validation:** Validated live against AWS Pricing MCP (AmazonSageMaker / AmazonEC2, us-east-1, publicationDate 2026-06-27). (1) AmazonSageMaker exposes a `component` attribute distinguishing Hosting / Notebook / Training / Processing / BatchTransform / AsyncInf / Studio-Notebook / studio-jupyterlab / RStudio / Cluster / Cluster-Reserved / Monitor-Free-Tier / Training-Debug-Free-Tier. The adapter's _fetch_sagemaker_instance_price filters only on instanceType+location with MaxResults=1, so it picks one component SKU non-deterministically (M5). (2) For ml.m5.xlarge every component currently prices at $0.23/hr -> monthly = 0.23*730 = $167.90, so Hosting==Notebook==Training today (the SKU conflation is harmless on price for this type, contrary to the brief's assumption that the three families differ; reported as a limitation, not a material mispricing). (3) The `instanceType` filter does return results on AmazonSageMaker (valid alias of instanceName), so the adapter's filter field is correct. (4) EC2 m5.xlarge Linux on-demand = $0.192/hr vs SageMaker ml.m5.xlarge $0.23/hr => real premium ~1.198, so SAGEMAKER_OVER_EC2=1.15 is slightly low but defensible; however this constant is academic because the EC2 fallback is dead code for ml.* types (M4: get_ec2_hourly_price('ml.m5.xlarge') -> None -> 0.0). SPOT_SAVINGS_RATE=0.70 and CONSOLIDATION_SAVINGS_RATE=0.30 are reduction factors not validated against any concrete delta (H1/check-4). Live scan deliberately not executed (read-only, no-creds constraint).

**Cost checks:**

| Check | Status | Trigger | Savings basis |
|---|---|---|---|
| idle_endpoints | counted | list_endpoints (paginated) -> EndpointStatus=='InService'; under fast_mode the check only counts active and continues (no findings); otherwise CloudWatch AWS/SageMaker Invocations Sum over IDLE_ENDPOINT_DAYS=7 at Period=86400. Skips when invocations is None OR >0 (sagemaker.py:133-137). | Full monthly price of variants[0].InstanceType: _get_instance_monthly(ctx, instance_type) = get_sagemaker_instance_monthly() (sagemaker.py:155,164). Window = 7-day Invocations==0. NOT recorded as a structured AuditBasis on the rec. |
| idle_notebooks | counted | list_notebook_instances(StatusEquals='InService') paginated; flags EVERY running notebook. NO usage metric, NO idle signal, NO fast_mode guard (sagemaker.py:175-217). | Full monthly price of nb['InstanceType']: _get_instance_monthly (sagemaker.py:200,209). No evidence the notebook is idle -> fabricated saving on actively-used notebooks. |
| spot_training | counted | list_training_jobs(StatusEquals='Completed', MaxResults=100, NextToken-paginated) -> per job with TrainingTimeInSeconds>=3600 (MIN_TRAINING_SECONDS) and describe_training_job EnableManagedSpotTraining==False; skip if instance_type=='unknown', instance_monthly<=0, or savings<0.50 (sagemaker.py:244-285). | (instance_monthly/730) * training_hours * SPOT_SAVINGS_RATE(0.70) on ONE historical completed run (sagemaker.py:275-281). Labeled monthly_savings but is a one-time, retrospective, speculative ('similar future jobs') figure. |
| multi_model_consolidation | counted | list_endpoints -> InService endpoints grouped by variants[0].InstanceType; for any group with len>1 (sagemaker.py:312-339). | (len(group)-1) * instance_monthly * CONSOLIDATION_SAVINGS_RATE(0.30) (sagemaker.py:349). Arbitrary reduction factor, not an exact price delta to a concrete consolidated target; assumes zero added capacity. |

**Findings:**

#### 🔴 C1 · idle_notebooks fabricates a full-monthly saving for EVERY running notebook with zero idle evidence  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/sagemaker.py:175-217`
- **Evidence:** _check_idle_notebooks lists notebook_instances with StatusEquals='InService' and unconditionally appends a rec for every one: monthly_savings=round(_get_instance_monthly(ctx, instance_type),2) (lines 200-213). There is no CloudWatch metric, no describe_notebook_instance LastModifiedTime, no connection/idle signal of any kind. The reason text even hedges: 'consider stopping if not actively in use' (210-211). Unlike spot/consolidation it does not guard on fast_mode. Live Pricing API confirms a running ml.m5.xlarge notebook bills at $0.23/hr = $167.90/mo, so each actively-used notebook contributes its full real cost to the headline as a 'saving'.
- **Impact:** Largest real-dollar overstatement in the adapter: every running notebook (including ones in active use) adds its full monthly cost to total_monthly_savings (summed at line 414) and to total_recommendations. A FinOps headline of fabricated, non-actionable dollars.
- **Fix:** Gate on a real idle signal (describe_notebook_instance LastModifiedTime age, or a CW agent metric) and only count when proven idle; otherwise emit as a Counted=False $0 advisory. Honor ctx.fast_mode (skip the describe work).
- **Verifier (confirmed):** _check_idle_notebooks (services/adapters/sagemaker.py:175-217) paginates list_notebook_instances with StatusEquals='InService' (line 183) and, for EVERY returned notebook, unconditionally appends a rec with monthly_savings=round(instance_monthly,2) (instance_monthly computed line 200, used line 209). There is no CloudWatch metric call, no describe_notebook_instance / LastModifiedTime check, and no connection/idle signal anywhere in the function — the only filter is the InService status used by the list call itself. The reason text self-hedges 'consider stopping if not actively in use' (210-211). The function signature takes (sm, ctx, pricing_multiplier) and scan() calls it without fast_mode (line 409), so unlike spot/consolidation it has no fast_mode short-circuit and, unlike spot (272-273) / consolidation (343-344), no instance_monthly<=0 guard. Each rec's full monthly cost flows into total_savings=sum(monthly_savings) (line 414) and total_recommendations=len(all_recs) (line 418). Mechanism, lines, and impact match the finding exactly. The specific live dollar figure ($167.90/mo for ml.m5.xlarge) is an unverified live-pricing claim, but the core defect — full monthly cost claimed as savings for every running notebook with zero idle evidence — is fully code-confirmed.

#### 🟠 C2 · No mark_zero_savings_advisory gate: $0 recs are counted in both rec-count and dollar total  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/sagemaker.py:155-168, 200-213, 413-414`
- **Evidence:** _get_instance_monthly returns 0.0 on any pricing miss or instance_type=='unknown' (lines 35-50). _check_idle_endpoints (instance_type defaults to 'unknown' when describe/config fails, line 150) and _check_idle_notebooks append recs with monthly_savings=round(0.0,2) WITHOUT any instance_monthly<=0 guard. Contrast spot_training (272-273) and consolidation (343-344) which DO `if instance_monthly <= 0: continue`. scan() computes total_savings = sum(r['monthly_savings']) with no Counted filter (413-414); the file never imports services/_savings.mark_zero_savings_advisory. _counted_advisory_counts (html_report_generator.py:371-388) treats any rec lacking Counted==False as counted, so $0 idle findings inflate total_recommendations and present as counted cards.
- **Impact:** Rec count inflated by non-actionable $0 placeholders ('Delete endpoint'/'Stop notebook' with $0.00). Inconsistent with spot/consolidation which skip. Headline shows counted findings with no realizable dollars.
- **Fix:** Import mark_zero_savings_advisory; call mark_zero_savings_advisory(all_recs, lambda r: r['monthly_savings']) before the sum and total only Counted!=False recs (mirror lambda_svc/network). Add the same instance_monthly<=0 skip the other two checks already have.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** _get_instance_monthly returns 0.0 on any pricing miss or unknown type (sagemaker.py:44-50). _check_idle_endpoints defaults instance_type='unknown' when describe/config fails (line 142, only overwritten at 150 if variants exist) and appends the rec at 157-168 with NO instance_monthly<=0 guard; _check_idle_notebooks likewise appends at 202-213 with no guard. By contrast _check_spot_training (272-273) and _check_multi_model_consolidation (343-344) both 'if instance_monthly <= 0: continue'. scan() sets total_recommendations=len(all_recs) (418) and total_monthly_savings=sum(monthly_savings) (414/419) with no Counted/advisory filter. Grep confirms sagemaker.py never imports services._savings.mark_zero_savings_advisory (it exists at _savings.py:72 and would set rec['Counted']=False for <=0 savings, as used by lambda_svc/network/monitoring). The reporter's _counted_advisory_counts (html_report_generator.py:371-388) classifies a rec as advisory ONLY when rec.get('Counted') is False, else counts it — so sagemaker's $0 idle endpoint/notebook recs are presented as counted cards and inflate the rec count. All evidence, line cites, and the contrast with spot/consolidation hold.

#### 🟠 H1 · spot_training one-time per-run cost is summed into the recurring MONTHLY headline  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/sagemaker.py:275-299, 414`
- **Evidence:** savings = (instance_monthly/730) * training_hours * 0.70 is the cost of ONE already-completed run (the rec text says '${savings:.2f} per equivalent run', 296-297). It is stored under key monthly_savings (294) and scan() sums all monthly_savings into total_monthly_savings (414), which feeds the per-tab and executive headline (_calculate_service_savings returns the canonical total, html_report_generator.py:3078-3079). A retrospective single-run figure is neither recurring nor monthly, and the saving only materializes if a comparable job is re-run with Managed Spot enabled ('for similar future jobs', 293) — speculative, not an existing cost.
- **Impact:** Monthly savings headline is overstated/mislabeled by non-recurring one-off amounts. If many historical jobs match, the inflation compounds.
- **Fix:** Either amortize to a true monthly rate, or (preferred) mark spot recs Counted=False advisory since the saving is speculative future spend, and label the figure 'per-run, one-time'. Record an AuditBasis (rate/training_hours/0.70).
- **Verifier (confirmed):** In _check_spot_training (sagemaker.py:275-299): hourly_rate=instance_monthly/730, training_hours=training_time/3600, on_demand_cost=hourly_rate*training_hours, savings=on_demand_cost*SPOT_SAVINGS_RATE — this is the Spot delta on ONE already-completed run's wall-clock duration, derived from the job's TrainingTimeInSeconds. It is stored under the key monthly_savings (line 294) and the rec text confirms it is retrospective/speculative: '${savings:.2f} per equivalent run' (297) and 'for similar future jobs' (293). scan() sums it into total_monthly_savings (line 414/419), and _calculate_service_savings (html_report_generator.py:3078-3079) returns total_monthly_savings as the canonical service headline. A one-off per-run figure (typically << a month of runtime, and only realized if a comparable job is re-run with Managed Spot) is thus mislabeled and summed into a recurring monthly headline. Mechanism, lines, and impact verified.

#### 🟠 H2 · Intra-adapter double count: an idle endpoint is billed at full cost AND inflates its consolidation group  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/sagemaker.py:114-172, 306-365`
- **Evidence:** _check_idle_endpoints and _check_multi_model_consolidation both call _list_endpoints(sm) and both key off variants[0].InstanceType. An InService endpoint with 0 invocations is counted at full instance_monthly by idle_endpoints (line 164) and, if another InService endpoint shares its instance_type, the same endpoint is part of the consolidation group, adding (len-1)*instance_monthly*0.30 (349). The idle endpoint's dollars are claimed by two sources with no dedup; there is no normalized-id reconciliation between the blocks.
- **Impact:** Same compute counted twice whenever >=2 InService endpoints share an instance type and >=1 is idle. Over-counts total_monthly_savings.
- **Fix:** Dedup by endpoint id with idle-delete superseding consolidation: exclude endpoints already flagged idle (zero invocations) from the consolidation grouping population, or drop them from one source. Single owner = idle deletion.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** _check_idle_endpoints (114-172) and _check_multi_model_consolidation (306-365) independently call _list_endpoints(sm) (122, 312) and both read variants[0].InstanceType (150, 331). An InService endpoint with 0 invocations gets a rec at full instance_monthly via idle_endpoints (line 164). The same endpoint, if it shares an instance_type with >=1 other InService endpoint, is grouped at 334 and contributes to a consolidation rec savings=(len(group)-1)*instance_monthly*CONSOLIDATION_SAVINGS_RATE (line 349). scan() simply concatenates all_recs = idle_ep_recs + notebook_recs + spot_recs + consolidation_recs (413) and sums every monthly_savings (414) with no normalized-id reconciliation between the two blocks — confirmed there is no cross-block dedup in the adapter. In the minimal 2-endpoint case the consolidation rec exists only because the idle endpoint is in the group (len would drop to 1 and be skipped at 339 if it were removed), so the idle endpoint's dollars are claimed by both sources. The double-count whenever >=2 InService endpoints share an instance type and >=1 is idle is real, and it inflates total_monthly_savings. Lines and impact verified.

#### 🟡 M1 · All AWS errors swallowed silently — AccessDenied/throttle never recorded on ctx  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/sagemaker.py:44-50, 64-79, 82-95, 98-111, 169-170, 191-192, 214-215, 239-240, 252-256, 300-301, 335-336`
- **Evidence:** Every helper and per-item loop uses bare `except Exception: pass/continue/return None/return recs,0` with no ctx.warn / ctx.permission_issue: _get_instance_monthly (48-49), _get_cloudwatch_invocations_sum (77-78), _list_endpoints double-swallow (89-94), _describe_endpoint (102-103), _describe_endpoint_config (110-111), and the per-check handlers. ScanContext exposes warn() and permission_issue() (core/scan_context.py:49,59) and services/_aws_errors.record_aws_error (line 47) is the canonical classifier used by network. A list_endpoints / list_notebook_instances / CloudWatch AccessDenied therefore reads as 'no resources' or 'no usage -> skip', producing a false clean bill.
- **Impact:** Permission/throttle gaps are invisible: missing sagemaker:ListEndpoints or cloudwatch:GetMetricStatistics silently yields zero findings, hiding both blind spots and potential savings.
- **Fix:** Wrap list/describe/CloudWatch calls and classify via services/_aws_errors.record_aws_error (AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation/OptInRequired -> ctx.permission_issue, else ctx.warn). At minimum record on ctx in each except.

#### 🟡 M2 · Saving prices only ProductionVariants[0] and ignores InstanceCount>1 — understates real cost  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/sagemaker.py:148-155, 331, 349`
- **Evidence:** idle_endpoints reads variants[0].get('InstanceType') only (148-150) and prices a single instance (155,164); InstanceCount on the variant and any 2nd+ ProductionVariants are ignored. Consolidation likewise groups on variants[0].InstanceType (331). Deleting an idle endpoint that runs InstanceCount=4 across two variants saves the full fleet, but the rec prices one instance of one variant.
- **Impact:** Correctness: idle/consolidation savings are understated (under-counted dollars) for multi-instance and multi-variant endpoints. Also a coverage gap for Serverless/Async inference, Studio/KernelGateway apps which are never priced.
- **Fix:** Sum price over all ProductionVariants and multiply each by its InstanceCount for the idle-delete saving; consolidation should account for per-endpoint instance counts.

#### 🟡 M3 · reads_fast_mode=True honored only by idle_endpoints; the other three checks run full list/describe under fast_mode  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/sagemaker.py:394-411, 133-134, 175-217, 220-303, 306-365`
- **Evidence:** scan() reads fast_mode (406) and passes it only to _check_idle_endpoints, which skips the CloudWatch read (133-134). _check_idle_notebooks, _check_spot_training and _check_multi_model_consolidation receive no fast_mode and execute list_notebook_instances / list_training_jobs+describe_training_job / list_endpoints+describe_endpoint regardless.
- **Impact:** Contract violation: the reads_fast_mode=True declaration implies cheap fast-mode behavior, but 3 of 4 checks issue unbounded describe/list traffic (e.g. describe_training_job per completed job) in fast mode.
- **Fix:** Pass fast_mode into all four checks and bail cheaply (or skip metric/describe-heavy work) when set, as idle_endpoints does.

#### 🟡 M4 · SageMaker Pricing API fallback is dead for ml.* types -> silent $0  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `core/pricing_engine.py:939-956, 1067-1085`
- **Evidence:** get_sagemaker_instance_monthly falls back to get_ec2_hourly_price(instance_type) * SAGEMAKER_OVER_EC2 * 730 (947-948) on API miss, but instance_type is an ml.* string (e.g. 'ml.m5.xlarge'). _fetch_ec2_price passes it verbatim as instanceType (1077) and AmazonEC2 has no 'ml.m5.xlarge' SKU -> _call_pricing_api returns None -> get_ec2_hourly_price returns 0.0 via _use_fallback. So fallback_price = 0.0*1.15*730 = 0.0. Live API confirms EC2 m5.xlarge=$0.192/hr vs SageMaker ml.m5.xlarge=$0.23/hr (ratio ~1.20, so 1.15 slightly low but moot).
- **Impact:** Whenever the AmazonSageMaker Pricing call misses (unsupported region, throttle, unknown type) the price silently becomes 0.0, which idle_endpoints/idle_notebooks then count as a $0 finding (compounds C2).
- **Fix:** Strip the 'ml.' prefix before the EC2 fallback (get_ec2_hourly_price(instance_type.removeprefix('ml.'))); recalibrate SAGEMAKER_OVER_EC2 toward ~1.20 per live data.

#### 🟡 M5 · Non-deterministic SageMaker SKU filter (MaxResults=1 across many component SKUs)  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `core/pricing_engine.py:1282-1288, 1590-1613`
- **Evidence:** _fetch_sagemaker_instance_price filters ONLY on instanceType + location (1283-1286) and _call_pricing_api uses MaxResults=1, returning PriceList[0] (1601-1611). Live AmazonSageMaker exposes a `component` attribute with many SKUs per instance type (Hosting, Notebook, Training, Processing, BatchTransform, AsyncInf, Studio-Notebook, studio-jupyterlab, RStudio, Cluster, Cluster-Reserved, Monitor-Free-Tier, Training-Debug-Free-Tier). For ml.m5.xlarge ALL components currently price at $0.23/hr, so the conflation is harmless on price today; but the filter has no deterministic pin, and if a Reserved or *-Free-Tier SKU (which can serialize first) carries a $0 rate, _extract_usd returns None -> fallback -> $0. The adapter also uses this single method for endpoints, notebooks AND training (conceptually distinct usage families), and prices SP/Reserved-covered capacity as on-demand.
- **Impact:** Latent non-determinism and a $0-pricing risk if a free-tier/reserved SKU is picked first; conceptually wrong SKU family even when the number happens to match.
- **Fix:** Pin the `component` per call site (Hosting for endpoints, Notebook for notebook instances, Training for training jobs) so the lookup is deterministic and family-correct.

#### 🟢 L1 · Generic renderer key mismatch: card title resolves to 'Resource' and savings render unstyled  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `reporter_phase_b.py:1345-1385, 1812-1876`
- **Evidence:** sagemaker is not in PHASE_B_HANDLERS, _PHASE_A_SERVICES or _PHASE_B_SKIP_PER_REC (2436-2530), so render_generic_per_rec dispatches to _render_generic_other_rec (1381). The title resolver checks PascalCase EndpointName/NotebookInstanceName (1843-1844) but recs carry lowercase endpoint_name/notebook_name/job_name; the resolver chain is gated by `if rec.get('resourceArn') else 'Resource'` (1859-1860) and SageMaker recs have no resourceArn, so resource_id=='Resource' for every card. The styled .savings line only prints if rec has EstimatedSavings (1874-1875), which SageMaker recs lack; the dollar appears only via the generic key-loop as `<p>Monthly Savings: 123.45</p>` (1865-1869) — unstyled, no $/mo. check_category also double-prints (lowercase key not in the exclude list 1866).
- **Impact:** Render fidelity only: counted==rendered numerically (same float is shown), but every card titles as '<Category>: Resource' and the saving is unstyled with no currency formatting.
- **Fix:** Add lowercase endpoint_name/notebook_name/job_name to the _render_generic_other_rec resolver and format monthly_savings as currency, or register a small sagemaker PHASE_B handler.

#### 🟢 L2 · _list_endpoints pagination fallback drops pages on paginator failure  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/sagemaker.py:82-95`
- **Evidence:** On paginator exception _list_endpoints falls back to a single sm.list_endpoints() call (91) with no NextToken loop, capping at one page (~max 100) and silently swallowing a second failure (93-94).
- **Impact:** Accounts with >100 endpoints under-covered if the paginator path fails; also no ctx warning (see M1).
- **Fix:** Drop the non-paginating fallback or loop on NextToken; record the failure on ctx.

#### 🟢 L3 · active_endpoint_count stat counts idle endpoints as active; CLAUDE.md Live Pricing table omits sagemaker  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/sagemaker.py:125-131, 439-441`
- **Evidence:** active_count increments for every InService endpoint at line 131, before the zero-invocations test, so an idle endpoint is reported under both 'Active Endpoints' (extras.active_endpoint_count) and 'Idle Endpoints' stat cards. Separately, services/adapters/CLAUDE.md lists 19 Live-Pricing adapters but not sagemaker despite its live get_sagemaker_instance_monthly usage.
- **Impact:** Minor stat-card overlap (idle endpoints shown as active) and a documentation drift the brief asks to reconcile.
- **Fix:** Document that active includes idle (or subtract idle), and add the sagemaker row to the CLAUDE.md Live Pricing table (method get_sagemaker_instance_monthly, source AWS Pricing API / AmazonSageMaker).

### Step Functions — `services/adapters/step_functions.py`

**Module identity:** key="step_functions", cli_aliases=("step_functions",), display_name="Step Functions", reads_fast_mode=True, requires_cloudwatch=True, required_clients()=("states","cloudwatch") (services/adapters/step_functions.py:15-24). Two-file adapter: services/adapters/step_functions.py (StepFunctionsModule.scan, constants, 30-day CloudWatch re-read, eligible_for_migration gate) + legacy shim services/step_functions.py (get_enhanced_step_functions_checks, STEP_FUNCTIONS_OPTIMIZATION_DESCRIPTIONS, 7-day CloudWatch read + daily_avg>100 gate). Emits a SINGLE SourceBlock "enhanced_checks". Pricing is a module constant STEP_FUNCTIONS_PER_1K_TRANSITIONS=0.025 (line 42), NOT PricingEngine (no SFN method in core/pricing_engine.py). No Cost Optimization Hub and no Compute Optimizer consumption (not in scan_orchestrator type_map/_HUB_SERVICES, no services.advisor helper) — those axes correctly dropped. Rendered via Phase A: PHASE_A_DESCRIPTORS["step_functions"] (reporter_phase_a.py:319-327, savings_mode="always") and _PHASE_A_SERVICES (reporter_phase_b.py:2509). MODULE-IDENTITY DRIFT vs services/adapters/CLAUDE.md "Live Pricing" row "step_functions.py | CloudWatch ExecutionsStarted -> $0.025/1K": the row implies a working CloudWatch-driven COUNTED saving, but the eligible_for_migration gate is dead so nothing is ever counted; the only rendered dollars are the reporter's flat-$50 substitution (step_functions in _FLAT_SAVINGS_SERVICES, html_report_generator.py:82). CLIENT-NAME drift: declares "states" but scan calls ctx.client("stepfunctions"); required_clients() is never consumed by production code so the mismatch is declarative-only.

**Verdict:** The step_functions adapter is a two-file design (legacy shim services/step_functions.py + StepFunctionsModule in services/adapters/step_functions.py) whose only populated check is standard_vs_express. The central defect is a dead counted lever feeding a fabricated flat-$50: eligible_for_migration=(state_count>25 and avg_duration_sec<60) is ALWAYS False because StateCount/AvgDurationSec are never set (default 5 and 0; describe_state_machine never called), so the savings block (lines 87-92) never runs and total_monthly_savings is structurally $0 (C1). Because step_functions is in _FLAT_SAVINGS_SERVICES, the reporter then substitutes $50/rec with no rate/metric/basis into the tab headline, executive summary, and reconciliation footnote (C2). The dollar math is independently fabricated: an invented AVG_STATES_PER_EXECUTION=5 times an uncalibrated 0.60 factor applied to the Standard ($0.025/1K) cost, when the Express target is a different model ($1/M requests + $0.00001667/GB-s, validated live) — the code comment admits savings can be 95%+ or negative (H1). The result is a counted-vs-rendered desync of three different numbers per rec: card '~90%', counted $0, headline $50 (H2). Supporting bugs: silent per-machine CloudWatch failures swallowed with no warn/permission_issue (M1), the shim's CloudWatch read not gated on fast_mode so reads_fast_mode is only half-honored (M2), and a wasted double-read of ExecutionsStarted with inconsistent 7-day/30-day windows (M3). Limitations: required_clients declares 'states' instead of 'stepfunctions' but is never consumed (L1), no free-tier subtraction (L2), STANDARD-only coverage with three orphaned dead-config categories (L3), and a CLAUDE.md row that overstates the adapter as a working counted saving (L4). Standard $0.025/1K confirmed correct against live AmazonStates pricing; the only fabricated number reaching the report is the reporter's flat-$50. Recommended direction: demote standard_vs_express to advisory (Counted=False) and remove step_functions from _FLAT_SAVINGS_SERVICES until a real ASL-state-count + Express-model delta is computed; never the flat $50 and never the 0.60 factor on a fabricated transition count. No file was modified (read-only audit).

**Pricing validation:** Validated live against AWS Pricing API (mcp__aws-pricing-mcp-server__get_pricing, service_code=AmazonStates, region=us-east-1, OnDemand) on 2026-06-27. (1) Standard state transition: SKU 5NX6NBD43SV57CH3, usagetype USE1-StateTransition, group SFN-StateTransitions, pricePerUnit USD 0.0000250000 = $0.000025/transition = $0.025/1K -> CONFIRMS STEP_FUNCTIONS_PER_1K_TRANSITIONS=0.025 (us-east-1). beginRange 0 -> Inf with no free band, so the first 4,000 transitions/month/account free tier is a billing credit not in the SKU (L2). (2) Express requests: SKU AJJXM66BP92T8UX4, USE1-StepFunctions-Request, USD 0.0000010000/request = $1.00/M. (3) Express duration: SKU TFDWDW6V2TSZF7M2, USE1-StepFunctions-GB-Second, USD 0.0000166700/GB-s (first tier) -> CONFIRMS Express is a fundamentally different model (requests + GB-seconds), so the 0.60 reduction factor applied to the STANDARD transition cost (H1) is not a valid Standard->Express model. Service code AmazonStates is correct (AWSStepFunctions returns empty, per brief). Region scaling: ctx.pricing_multiplier is applied exactly once inside the savings expression (services/adapters/step_functions.py:91) — not double — but is moot because the block never runs (C1).

**Cost checks:**

| Check | Status | Trigger | Savings basis |
|---|---|---|---|
| standard_vs_express (shim, only populated category) | counted | sm_type=="STANDARD" AND 7-day CloudWatch ExecutionsStarted daily_avg>100 (services/step_functions.py:45,64) | Rendered card prints the literal percentage string EstimatedSavings="Up to 90% cost reduction for high-volume workflows" (render-only, never parsed to $). Counted dollar path is the adapter formula (monthly_transitions/1000)*0.025*0.60*pricing_multiplier (services/adapters/step_functions.py:87-92) gated on eligible_for_migration=(state_count>25 and avg_duration_sec<60); state_count defaults to AVG_STATES_PER_EXECUTION=5 and avg_duration_sec defaults to 0, so the gate is ALWAYS False -> counted $ is ALWAYS 0. Because total_monthly_savings==0 and step_functions in _FLAT_SAVINGS_SERVICES, html_report_generator._calculate_service_savings substitutes $50/rec. So three different numbers: card="Up to 90%", counted=$0, rendered headline=$50/rec. |
| excessive_transitions (shim) | advisory | Key initialized in checks dict (services/step_functions.py:31) but NEVER appended to -> dead config, emits nothing | none (never populated) |
| polling_workflows (shim) | advisory | Key initialized in checks dict (services/step_functions.py:32) but NEVER appended to -> dead config, emits nothing | none (never populated) |
| nonprod_24x7 (shim) | advisory | Key initialized in checks dict (services/step_functions.py:33) AND advertised in STEP_FUNCTIONS_OPTIMIZATION_DESCRIPTIONS (services/step_functions.py:20-24) but NEVER populated (finding removed, comment line 81-82) -> orphaned descriptor | none (never populated) |

**Findings:**

#### 🔴 C1 · Counted savings lever is dead: eligible_for_migration is always False, so total_monthly_savings is always $0  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/step_functions.py:73-92`
- **Evidence:** state_count = rec.get("StateCount", AVG_STATES_PER_EXECUTION)  # default 5; avg_duration_sec = rec.get("AvgDurationSec", 0)  # default 0; eligible_for_migration = state_count > 25 and avg_duration_sec < 60 -> (5>25)=False -> always False. The savings += (...)*0.025*0.60*pricing_multiplier block (lines 87-92) is gated on eligible_for_migration and therefore NEVER executes. grep confirms StateCount and AvgDurationSec are NEVER set anywhere (shim emits only StateMachineArn/Name/Type/DailyExecutions/Recommendation/EstimatedSavings/CheckCategory), and describe_state_machine is never called. Even the 30-day MonthlyExecutions re-read (lines 51-71) is wasted: its result feeds monthly_transitions which is only used inside the dead block.
- **Impact:** No Standard->Express dollar is ever counted; total_monthly_savings returned by scan() is structurally 0 for every account. The CLAUDE.md 'CloudWatch ExecutionsStarted -> $0.025/1K' counted-saving promise is unreachable. Root cause of the fabricated flat-$50 (see C2).
- **Fix:** Either (a) demote standard_vs_express to advisory (set Counted=False on the rec, return total_monthly_savings=0 honestly), or (b) compute a real delta: fetch the ASL via describe_state_machine to count states, read actual avg duration/memory, and model Express ($1/M requests + $0.00001667/GB-s) vs Standard ($0.025/1K transitions) as current-minus-target — never the 5-state x 0.60 heuristic. Remove the dead eligible_for_migration gate or feed it real StateCount/AvgDurationSec.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified at services/adapters/step_functions.py:73-92. state_count=rec.get('StateCount',5) and avg_duration_sec=rec.get('AvgDurationSec',0); eligible_for_migration = state_count>25 and avg_duration_sec<60. Repo-wide grep confirms StateCount/AvgDurationSec/MonthlyExecutions exist ONLY as .get() defaults inside this adapter and are set by no producer; describe_state_machine is never called anywhere. The shim get_enhanced_step_functions_checks (services/step_functions.py:65-77) emits recs with keys StateMachineArn/StateMachineName/Type/DailyExecutions/Recommendation/EstimatedSavings/CheckCategory only. Therefore state_count is always 5, 5>25 is always False, the savings+= block at lines 87-92 is unreachable, and scan() returns total_monthly_savings=savings=0.0 for every account (also 0 in fast_mode, which skips the whole block). The 30-day re-read (51-71) feeds monthly_transitions (78) which is consumed only inside the dead eligible_for_migration branch. Structurally $0 confirmed.

#### 🔴 C2 · Flat-$50-per-rec fabrication renders as account savings with no rate/metric/basis  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `html_report_generator.py:82, 3076-3094, 3113-3119`
- **Evidence:** _FLAT_SAVINGS_SERVICES = {"opensearch", "api_gateway", "step_functions"} (line 82). _calculate_service_savings: if total_monthly_savings>0 return it (line 3078); else for rec in recommendations: if service_key in _FLAT_SAVINGS_SERVICES: total_savings += 50 (lines 3093-3094). Since C1 guarantees total_monthly_savings==0, every standard_vs_express rec becomes exactly $50. _get_service_content overwrites service_data['total_monthly_savings'] = calculated_savings (lines 3117-3119), and the same fabricated number flows to the executive summary reconciliation footnote (line 2281-2286) and the accessible chart table (line 2831).
- **Impact:** Every high-volume Standard state machine silently becomes a fabricated $50/month saving in the per-tab headline, executive summary, and reconciliation footnote — with no rate, no metric window, no formula, no AuditBasis. Violates the 'every recommendation must produce a concrete account-specific dollar saving' scope. Untestable by the golden fixture (tests/fixtures/golden_scan_results.json lines 436-446 has step_functions with 0 recs/$0, so this path is never exercised).
- **Fix:** Remove "step_functions" from _FLAT_SAVINGS_SERVICES and have the adapter mark the rec advisory (Counted=False) so the reporter renders advisory $0 (rendered-not-counted) instead of $50. Note opensearch and api_gateway share this flat-$50 mechanism — flag as follow-up, do not fix unprompted.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified html_report_generator.py:82 _FLAT_SAVINGS_SERVICES={'opensearch','api_gateway','step_functions'}. _calculate_service_savings (3076-3109): returns early only if total_monthly_savings>0 (3078); otherwise iterates each source's recommendations and does total_savings+=50 when service_key in _FLAT_SAVINGS_SERVICES (3093-3094). Given C1 forces total_monthly_savings==0, every standard_vs_express rec yields exactly $50. _get_service_content (3113-3119) copies service_data and overwrites total_monthly_savings=calculated_savings. Same calc flows to the executive-summary reconciliation footnote (2281-2286) and the accessible chart-table (2831). No rate/metric/formula/AuditBasis attached. Golden fixture tests/fixtures/golden_scan_results.json:436-446 has step_functions total_recommendations=0 and recommendations=[] so the flat-$50 loop is never exercised there. Confirmed.

#### 🟠 H1 · Fabricated AVG_STATES_PER_EXECUTION=5 dimension and uncalibrated 0.60 reduction factor applied to the wrong (Standard) pricing model  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✏️ revised**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/step_functions.py:43, 78, 80-92`
- **Evidence:** AVG_STATES_PER_EXECUTION = 5 (line 43) invents the per-execution transition count; the real count comes from the ASL definition which is never fetched (describe_state_machine absent). monthly_transitions = monthly_executions * 5 (line 78). Savings = transitions x $0.025/1K x 0.60 (line 87-92) models Standard->Express as 60% of the STANDARD transition cost, but live AWS Pricing API (AmazonStates, us-east-1) shows Express is a different model: USE1-StepFunctions-Request $0.000001/req ($1/M) + USE1-StepFunctions-GB-Second $0.00001667/GB-s. The code comment (lines 80-86) itself admits 'real savings can be 95%+ ... or negative'.
- **Impact:** Even if C1 were repaired, the dollar would be doubly fabricated: an invented 5-state volume times an uncalibrated 0.60 factor on a pricing model that does not apply to the target type. Could be off by any magnitude (95%+ to negative). No defensible AuditBasis.
- **Fix:** Drop the 0.60 factor and the flat 5-state assumption. To count a real delta, fetch the state count from describe_state_machine's ASL definition and compute Standard cost (transitions x $0.025/1K, minus free tier) minus Express cost (requests x $1/M + GB-seconds x $0.00001667) from actual execution count, memory, and duration. Otherwise keep advisory $0.
- **Verifier (revised):** All cited code facts are accurate: AVG_STATES_PER_EXECUTION=5 (line 43), monthly_transitions=monthly_executions*AVG_STATES_PER_EXECUTION (line 78, note it uses the constant 5, not the read state_count), savings=transitions*0.025*0.60*pricing_multiplier (87-92) modeling Standard->Express as 60% of the STANDARD transition cost, and the code comment (80-86) itself admits Express uses a different model ($1/M req + GB-s) and that real savings can be 95%+ to negative. However the finding overstates impact: this savings block is the exact dead code from C1 (eligible_for_migration is always False), so it NEVER executes, produces $0, and contributes nothing to any rendered number. The dollar that actually reaches the report is the unrelated flat-$50 fabrication (C2), which does not use this formula at all. The Express-pricing-model specifics were not independently verified against the live Pricing API (would need live evidence) but are corroborated by the in-code comment. This is a latent/unreachable defect, not an active fabrication source.  _Correction:_ Severity LOW (latent dead-code defect, not an active fabrication). The 5-state hardcode and uncalibrated 0.60 factor on a Standard-only pricing model are real, but the block is unreachable (C1), so it currently emits $0 and feeds no output. The critique only becomes load-bearing if C1 is repaired; until then the rendered $50/rec comes entirely from the flat-savings path (C2), not this formula. Express-model mismatch claim is code-corroborated but live Pricing API confirmation not performed.

#### 🟠 H2 · Render-string vs counted-number desync: rec counts as 'counted' yet contributes $0 while headline shows fabricated $50 and card shows a percentage  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `reporter_phase_a.py:450-451`
- **Evidence:** render_grouped_by_category with savings_mode="always" prints resources[0].get("EstimatedSavings") = the literal 'Up to 90% cost reduction for high-volume workflows' (services/step_functions.py:74). The rec carries NO Counted key, so html_report_generator._counted_advisory_counts (lines 371-388: advisory only when rec.get("Counted") is False) classifies it as COUNTED — but its counted dollar contribution is $0 (C1), and the rendered tab headline is the flat-$50 (C2). Three different numbers for the same rec: card='Up to 90%', counted=$0, headline=$50.
- **Impact:** Counted != rendered. The tab header shows 'N (N counted, 0 advisory)' implying real counted dollars, the headline shows $50/rec of fabrication, and the card text shows an unrelated percentage. An adversarial reader sees three irreconcilable figures; the headline cannot be reconciled to the per-rec sum.
- **Fix:** Set Counted=False on the standard_vs_express rec so _counted_advisory_counts reports it as advisory and the headline shows advisory $0 (with C2's removal from _FLAT_SAVINGS_SERVICES). Stop rendering the percentage string as a savings figure, or replace it with the structured AuditBasis once a real delta exists.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified reporter_phase_a.py:450-451: under savings_mode=='always' the card prints resources[0].get('EstimatedSavings'). The step_functions descriptor sets savings_mode='always' (reporter_phase_a.py:325), and the shim sets EstimatedSavings='Up to 90% cost reduction for high-volume workflows' (services/step_functions.py:74). The recs carry no 'Counted' key, so html_report_generator._counted_advisory_counts (371-388: advisory only when rec.get('Counted') is False, else counted at 386-387) classifies each as COUNTED. Yet the counted dollar (adapter total_monthly_savings) is $0 per C1, while the tab headline shows the fabricated $50 per C2. Result: three irreconcilable figures for the same rec — card='Up to 90%', counted contribution=$0, headline=$50 — and the tab header 'N (N counted, 0 advisory)' implies real counted dollars that do not exist. Confirmed.

#### 🟡 M1 · Silent per-machine CloudWatch failures swallowed with no ctx.warn / ctx.permission_issue  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/step_functions.py:78-79`
- **Evidence:** Inner per-machine block: except Exception: pass (lines 78-79) swallows get_metric_statistics failure for each STANDARD machine — a throttled or AccessDenied metric read silently drops that machine with no classification. Mirror failure in services/adapters/step_functions.py:70 (except Exception: monthly_executions = 0) swallows the 30-day re-read failure. Only the OUTER except (services/step_functions.py:84-85) calls ctx.warn, but it does not classify AccessDenied/Unauthorized/OptInRequired as permission_issue.
- **Impact:** Throttling or missing cloudwatch:GetMetricStatistics permission makes high-volume Standard machines silently disappear from the scan (under-coverage) with no operator signal. AccessDenied is not surfaced as a permission_issue.
- **Fix:** Replace the bare except: pass at services/step_functions.py:78 and the except->0 at services/adapters/step_functions.py:70 with services/_aws_errors.record_aws_error (AccessDenied/Unauthorized/OptInRequired -> ctx.permission_issue, else ctx.warn). Classify the outer except (line 84-85) the same way.

#### 🟡 M2 · fast_mode hole: shim CloudWatch read runs unconditionally; reads_fast_mode only half-honored  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/step_functions.py:47-59`
- **Evidence:** The adapter declares reads_fast_mode=True (services/adapters/step_functions.py:18) and gates its dollarization on if not ctx.fast_mode (line 47). BUT the shim's per-machine get_metric_statistics (services/step_functions.py:50-59) has NO ctx.fast_mode check (grep shows no fast_mode reference in services/step_functions.py) — it runs for every STANDARD machine regardless of fast mode.
- **Impact:** fast_mode does not skip the expensive per-machine CloudWatch read; the declared reads_fast_mode contract is violated. A --fast scan still pays one get_metric_statistics call per Standard machine.
- **Fix:** Gate the shim's CloudWatch read on ctx.fast_mode (mirror the Lambda fast-mode fix): in fast mode skip get_metric_statistics and the daily_avg>100 gate, emitting nothing or an advisory.

#### 🟡 M3 · Double CloudWatch read of the same ExecutionsStarted metric with inconsistent windows; the second read is entirely wasted  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/step_functions.py:51-71`
- **Evidence:** The shim reads ExecutionsStarted Sum over 7 days, Period=86400 (services/step_functions.py:50-59) for the daily_avg>100 gate; the adapter re-reads ExecutionsStarted Sum over 30 days, Period=2592000 (services/adapters/step_functions.py:58-69) for the SAME StateMachineArn. Because MonthlyExecutions is never set on the rec, the monthly_executions<=0 branch (line 51) always fires, so the 30-day read always runs (when not fast_mode) — but its result only feeds the dead eligible_for_migration block (C1), so it is 100% wasted API work.
- **Impact:** Two get_metric_statistics calls per Standard machine for the same metric with inconsistent windows (7-day daily_avg gate vs 30-day Sum), the second producing data that is never used. Wasteful and inconsistent.
- **Fix:** Have the shim pass through MonthlyExecutions (or the raw 30-day Sum) on the rec so the adapter does not re-read; consolidate to a single CloudWatch read and a single window.

#### 🟢 L1 · required_clients declares 'states' but the adapter uses the 'stepfunctions' boto3 client; declaration is wrong but never consumed  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/step_functions.py:22-24`
- **Evidence:** required_clients() returns ("states", "cloudwatch") (line 24) but the shim calls ctx.client("stepfunctions") (services/step_functions.py:37); boto3's client id is 'stepfunctions' ('states' is only the CloudWatch namespace AWS/States). grep across the codebase shows .required_clients() is invoked only by tests/test_s3_adapter.py — no production caller (ClientRegistry has no 'states' alias), so the mismatch causes no runtime failure.
- **Impact:** Declarative contract is wrong: the actually-used 'stepfunctions' client is undeclared and a non-existent 'states' client is declared. Harmless today but misleading and a latent bug if required_clients ever becomes a preflight check.
- **Fix:** Change required_clients() to ("stepfunctions", "cloudwatch").

#### 🟢 L2 · Free tier (first 4,000 state transitions/month/account) not subtracted from any counted formula  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/step_functions.py:42, 87-92`
- **Evidence:** STEP_FUNCTIONS_PER_1K_TRANSITIONS=0.025 (line 42) is applied to the full monthly_transitions with no free-tier deduction. Live AWS Pricing API (AmazonStates) shows USE1-StateTransition beginRange 0 -> Inf at $0.000025 with no free band (the 4,000/month free transitions are a billing credit, not in the SKU).
- **Impact:** Any future counted Standard saving overstates the dollar for low-volume Standard machines by up to 4,000 transitions/month/account. (Currently masked because the lever is dead — C1.)
- **Fix:** When counting a real Standard cost, subtract the 4,000-transition free-tier allotment before applying $0.025/1K, and record it in the AuditBasis.

#### 🟢 L3 · STANDARD-only coverage plus orphaned dead config (excessive_transitions / polling_workflows / nonprod_24x7)  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/step_functions.py:29-34, 45, 81-82`

The checks dict declares excessive_transitions, polling_workflows, nonprod_24x7 (lines 31-33) that are never appended to, and STEP_FUNCTIONS_OPTIMIZATION_DESCRIPTIONS advertises nonprod_24x7 (lines 20-24) which is never emitted (removed, comment lines 81-82).
- **Impact:** Express workflow cost is invisible to the scanner. Three declared categories and one advertised descriptor are dead config that can mislead maintainers into thinking those checks run.
- **Fix:** Remove the unused excessive_transitions/polling_workflows/nonprod_24x7 keys and the orphaned nonprod_24x7 descriptor, or implement them. Decide and document whether Express coverage is intentionally out of scope.

### Transfer — `services/adapters/transfer.py`

**Module identity:** CONFIRMED vs services/adapters/CLAUDE.md. services/adapters/transfer.py:15-21 declares key="transfer", cli_aliases=("transfer",), display_name="Transfer Family"; scan() returns ServiceFindings(service_name="Transfer Family"). required_clients() returns ("transfer",) only — the shim ALSO calls ctx.client("cloudwatch") (transfer_svc.py:63) which is NOT declared; ctx.client delegates to ClientRegistry (core/scan_context.py:70-72) which lazily builds any client, so this is a contract/doc gap, NOT a runtime failure. Pricing is a MODULE CONSTANT (TRANSFER_PER_PROTOCOL_HOUR=0.30, transfer.py:41) — confirmed there is NO get_transfer_* method in core/pricing_engine.py (grep empty). Transfer is absent from core/scan_orchestrator.py _HUB_SERVICES (lines 52-72: ec2/lambda/ebs/rds/elasticache/opensearch/redshift/s3/eks_cost/dynamodb/containers/commitment_analysis) and pulls no services.advisor Compute Optimizer helper — so CoH/CO axes correctly dropped. Single emitted SourceBlock "enhanced_checks" (transfer.py:65); total_recommendations==len(recs) (transfer.py:69). Reporter: NO ("transfer",*) entry in PHASE_B_HANDLERS (reporter_phase_b.py:2436-2498); transfer absent from _PHASE_A_SERVICES (2500-2514) and _PHASE_B_SKIP_PER_REC (2516-2530), so should_fallback_to_per_rec("transfer")=True (2548-2550) → html_report_generator.py:3361-3362 routes to render_generic_per_rec → _render_generic_other_rec (reporter_phase_b.py:1380-1381,1812). Doc row in CLAUDE.md ("transfer.py | $0.30/protocol/hour × 730 | Module constant") is accurate on the constant but MISLABELED by being filed under the "Live Pricing (19 adapters)" section whose preamble says "Use ctx.pricing_engine ... for AWS Pricing API lookups" — transfer makes no live API call.

**Verdict:** Transfer is a thin single-source adapter (services/adapters/transfer.py -> get_enhanced_transfer_checks in services/transfer_svc.py) that re-prices each shim rec with a module constant and emits one enhanced_checks SourceBlock; no PricingEngine method, no Cost Hub, no Compute Optimizer (all correctly out of scope). The $0.30/protocol-hr constant is accurate (live API confirmed for SFTP/FTPS/FTP/AS2). Three material confirmed bugs: (C1, CRITICAL) the counted EstimatedMonthlySavings multiplies $0.30 by ctx.pricing_multiplier even though live API proves ProtocolHours is region-FLAT ($0.30 in both us-east-1 and ap-southeast-2), so the headline is inflated 8-25% off us-east-1 and the rendered string ($219/protocol, unscaled and actually correct) disagrees with the counted number — proven by an in-memory drive (Sydney: string $438 vs counted $503.70); (H1, HIGH) STOPPED/OFFLINE servers get a fabricated counted protocol-removal saving ($438 for a 3-protocol stopped server) layered on the non-dollar 'Full server hourly costs' string; (H2, HIGH) protocol_optimization counts (len(protocols)-1) protocols as savable with no per-protocol usage evidence. Plus MEDIUM silent-failure/declaration gaps (CW inner except swallows AccessDenied/throttle with no warn; outer except never classifies permission issues; missing requires_cloudwatch/reads_fast_mode; no AuditBasis) and LOW issues (wrong $0.09/GB data note vs validated $0.04+$0.04; dead endpoint_optimization branch and $0 recs rendered as counted; CLAUDE.md 'Live Pricing' mislabel + undeclared cloudwatch client). Renders via render_generic_per_rec -> _render_generic_other_rec (no PHASE_B_HANDLERS entry); counted==rendered in row count but the dollar shown (string) differs from the dollar counted (numeric). The existing regression/reporter snapshots exercise transfer with ZERO servers (golden fixture: 0 recs/$0), so none of these bugs are currently caught. Fix plan: C1 single-source + drop the multiplier; H1 skip re-pricing on unused servers; H2 gate protocol savings to $0 advisory absent per-protocol evidence; M1/M2 classify AccessDenied to permission_issue; M3 declare CW/fast_mode flags; M4 add AuditBasis; L1 correct data-note rate; L2 remove dead branch + mark $0 advisory; L3 fix doc.

**Pricing validation:** Validated live against the AWS Pricing API (service_code AWSTransfer), 2026-06 price list. (1) ProtocolHours constant 0.30 is ACCURATE: USE1-ProtocolHours = $0.30/Hour for SFTP (sku 4D8PEFFNWYG7MPE7), FTPS (Y9N6Z7B9Y3EK8M3T), FTP (XSG9BXMKKN9VCC5R) and AS2 (PM56EXU73VCC54JW) in us-east-1; x730 = $219.00/protocol/month. (2) REGION-FLAT: APS2-ProtocolHours (ap-southeast-2/Sydney) is ALSO $0.30/Hour for all of SFTP/FTPS/FTP/AS2 — ProtocolHours does NOT vary us-east-1 vs ap-southeast-2. Therefore applying ctx.pricing_multiplier (cost_optimizer.py:44 ap-southeast-2=1.15, sa-east-1=1.25) to this rate OVER-COUNTS the saving in every non-us-east-1 region (root of C1); the un-scaled $219/protocol string is the correct figure. (3) Data-transfer note rate $0.09/GB is WRONG: USE1-UploadBytes = $0.04/GB and USE1-DownloadBytes = $0.04/GB (confirmed across SFTP/FTPS/FTP and both S3 and EFS backends), i.e. $0.04 up + $0.04 down; PGP DecryptBytes is a separate $0.10/GB SKU (L1). Connectors (AFS1/USE1-SFTPConnectorCall-*, -RetrieveBytes/-SendBytes) and WebAppHours are distinct SKUs the adapter does not (and by design need not) price; the re-pricing loop's isinstance(protocols,list) guard (transfer.py:54) prevents a non-endpoint shape from being priced at the protocol rate.

**Cost checks:**

| Check | Status | Trigger | Savings basis |
|---|---|---|---|
| protocol_optimization | counted | state == 'ONLINE' and len(protocols) > 1 (transfer_svc.py:49) | Shim string EstimatedSavings = f"${removable*0.30*730:.2f}/mo..." with removable=len(protocols)-1, NO region scaling (transfer_svc.py:50,54). Adapter re-prices numeric EstimatedMonthlySavings = removable*0.30*730*ctx.pricing_multiplier (transfer.py:58-62). The numeric is summed into total_monthly_savings; the string is what renders. The two disagree off us-east-1 (C1). Live API confirms $0.30/protocol-hr. |
| unused_servers | counted | state in ['STOPPED','OFFLINE'] (transfer_svc.py:93) | Shim writes EstimatedSavings='Full server hourly costs' (non-dollar string, transfer_svc.py:100) with NO RemovableProtocols field. Adapter re-pricing loop (transfer.py:44-63) still runs: Protocols is a list, so removable=max(0,len(protocols)-1) and a POSITIVE EstimatedMonthlySavings = (n-1)*0.30*730*mult is written AND added to savings — fabricated for a stopped/non-billing endpoint (H1). Empirically: STOPPED 3-protocol server -> $438 counted. |

Never counted. Rate $0.09/GB is WRONG (live Transfer Family fee = $0.04/GB up + $0.04/GB down); also a 14-day Sum mislabeled '/mo' (L1). |

**Findings:**

#### 🔴 C1 · Counted savings region-scale a region-FLAT Transfer rate, inflating the headline and desyncing from the rendered string  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/transfer.py; services/transfer_svc.py:transfer.py:59-63; transfer_svc.py:54`
- **Evidence:** Numeric counted path: endpoint_monthly = removable*0.30*730*ctx.pricing_multiplier (transfer.py:59-62); savings += endpoint_monthly (63). Shim string: EstimatedSavings = f"${removable*0.30*730:.2f}/mo..." with NO multiplier (transfer_svc.py:54). Live AWS Pricing API (AWSTransfer): USE1-ProtocolHours = $0.30/hr AND APS2-ProtocolHours (Sydney) = $0.30/hr — ProtocolHours is identical across regions, i.e. region-FLAT. cost_optimizer.py:44 sets pricing_multiplier['ap-southeast-2']=1.15 (sa-east-1=1.25). In-memory drive of TransferModule.scan in ap-southeast-2: ONLINE rec string='$438.00/mo from removing 2 protocol(s)' but counted numeric=503.70 — true value is $438.00. The renderer (_render_generic_other_rec, reporter_phase_b.py:1874-1875) prints the string; result_builder.py:72 + the per-tab headline count the inflated numeric.
- **Impact:** In EVERY non-us-east-1 region the counted total_monthly_savings (and the executive-summary/pie headline via _calculate_service_savings, html_report_generator.py:3076-3079) is over-stated by the multiplier (+8% to +25%), and the operator sees two different dollar figures on the same card (string vs the dumped 'Estimatedmonthlysavings' field). pricing_multiplier is a coarse EC2-derived index, wrong scalar for a Transfer rate that does not vary by region.
- **Fix:** Single-source the value: have the shim carry an integer RemovableProtocols and let the adapter own ONE region-correct dollar string + number. Do NOT apply pricing_multiplier to the ProtocolHours rate (it is region-flat at $0.30 per live API) — or use a Transfer-specific per-region rate. Then string == numeric in all regions. Attach an AuditBasis (rate/region/formula).
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified end-to-end in real code plus live pricing. Counted path: transfer.py:59-62 endpoint_monthly = removable*0.30*730*ctx.pricing_multiplier; line 63 savings += endpoint_monthly; line 70 returns this as total_monthly_savings. String path: transfer_svc.py:54 EstimatedSavings = f"${removable*0.30*730:.2f}/mo..." with NO multiplier. cost_optimizer.py:44 confirms ap-southeast-2=1.15, :59 sa-east-1=1.25. The load-bearing empirical claim is CONFIRMED by the live AWS Pricing API (queried this run): AWSTransfer ProtocolHours is $0.30/hr identically in us-east-1 (USE1-ProtocolHours), ap-southeast-2 (APS2-ProtocolHours), and sa-east-1 (SAE1-ProtocolHours) across all protocol/operation SKUs - i.e. region-FLAT - so applying the EC2-derived pricing_multiplier (1.08-1.25) genuinely inflates the counted figure by +8% to +25% over the true price. Numbers check out: 2 protocols -> string 2*0.30*730=$438.00, counted 438.00*1.15=$503.70 in ap-southeast-2. Rendering desync confirmed: ('transfer','enhanced_checks') has no PHASE_B_HANDLERS entry and transfer is not in _PHASE_B_SKIP_PER_REC, so recs route to _render_generic_other_rec (reporter_phase_b.py:1812); lines 1865-1869 dump every numeric field (so EstimatedMonthlySavings=503.7 prints as 'Estimated Monthly Savings: 503.7') while lines 1874-1875 print the EstimatedSavings string ($438.00) - two different dollar figures on the same card. Headline counts the inflated numeric via result_builder.py:72 and html_report_generator.py:3078-3079 (_calculate_service_savings returns total_monthly_savings when >0). All sub-claims and cited line numbers accurate.

#### 🟠 H1 · STOPPED/OFFLINE servers get a fabricated, counted protocol-removal saving layered on the 'Full server hourly costs' string  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/adapters/transfer.py:transfer.py:44-63 (re-pricing loop runs on every rec including unused_servers from transfer_svc.py:93-103)`
- **Evidence:** unused_servers rec (transfer_svc.py:94-103) has Protocols as a list, EstimatedSavings='Full server hourly costs', no RemovableProtocols. The adapter loop therefore takes the else branch (transfer.py:53), computes removable=max(0,len(protocols)-1) (58) and writes EstimatedMonthlySavings=(n-1)*0.30*730*mult, adding it to savings (62-63). In-memory drive (us-east-1): s-STOPPED with 3 protocols -> EstimatedMonthlySavings=438.0 counted while string still reads 'Full server hourly costs'; total_monthly_savings=876.0 of which $438 is from the stopped server.
- **Impact:** A stopped/offline endpoint is the subject of a 'terminate it' recommendation, yet the counted number ($438) is a partial (n-1) protocol-removal figure that is both semantically inconsistent with 'terminate the whole server' and not evidenced as a billed cost. Inflates the headline by the full fabricated amount (50% of total in the test). String and counted number disagree.
- **Fix:** Skip the re-pricing loop when rec state is STOPPED/OFFLINE (or CheckCategory=='Unused Transfer Servers'); mark the unused_servers rec Counted=False (advisory) OR price the true full-server saving only when billing is evidenced. Never add a protocol-removal number to an unused-server rec.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified. unused_servers recs (transfer_svc.py:93-103) carry Protocols as a list, EstimatedSavings='Full server hourly costs', and NO RemovableProtocols key. They are flattened into all_recommendations (transfer_svc.py:108-110) and returned as result['recommendations'], which the adapter reads as recs (transfer.py:36) and iterates unconditionally (transfer.py:44). For these recs explicit_removable=rec.get('RemovableProtocols')=None, so the loop falls to the else branch (transfer.py:52-58): protocols is a list, removable=max(0,len(protocols)-1), then transfer.py:59-63 writes EstimatedMonthlySavings=(n-1)*0.30*730*mult and adds it to savings. For a STOPPED 3-protocol server in us-east-1 (mult=1.0): removable=2, counted=2*0.30*730=438.0, while the rendered EstimatedSavings string still reads 'Full server hourly costs'. So a stopped/offline 'terminate it' rec gets a counted partial (n-1) protocol-removal figure that disagrees with its own string and inflates the headline. Mechanism, line citations, and arithmetic all confirmed.

#### 🟠 H2 · 'Remove all-but-one protocol' counts (len(protocols)-1) protocols as savable with no per-protocol usage evidence  ·  `confirmed_bug` — **✅ confirmed**
- **Location:** `services/transfer_svc.py; services/adapters/transfer.py:transfer_svc.py:49-54; transfer.py:58`
- **Evidence:** removable = len(protocols) - 1 (transfer_svc.py:50; transfer.py:58) assumes every protocol beyond the first is unused. The only usage signal read is aggregate BytesUploaded/BytesDownloaded (transfer_svc.py:67-82), which is NOT per-protocol and is used only for an informational note. There is no evidence any specific protocol is idle.
- **Impact:** Counts a concrete dollar (n-1 protocols x $219/mo) that may be entirely unrealizable if the protocols are in use — the universal 'usage target with no evidence' anti-pattern. For a 3-protocol server this counts $438/mo of unproven savings.
- **Fix:** Demote the protocol_optimization saving to $0 advisory (Counted=False) unless per-protocol usage evidence exists, mirroring the S3/file_systems CloudWatch-evidence-gating pattern; or count only protocols with zero traffic if per-protocol metrics become available.
- **Verifier (confirmed):** Verified. removable = len(protocols)-1 appears in both the string path (transfer_svc.py:50) and the counted path (transfer.py:58), assuming every protocol beyond the first is unused. The only usage signal collected is aggregate BytesUploaded/BytesDownloaded over 14 days (transfer_svc.py:67-82), which is server-level (Dimensions=ServerId), NOT per-protocol, and is used solely to populate the informational DataTransferCostNote (lines 84-85) - never to gate or reduce the protocol-removal saving. No per-protocol idle evidence exists. Thus (n-1) protocols x $219/mo (0.30*730=219) are counted as savable with no evidence any specific protocol is unused; for a 3-protocol server this counts $438/mo of unproven savings. The 'usage target with no evidence' anti-pattern is real as described; HIGH severity appropriate.

#### 🟡 M1 · Inner CloudWatch except silently swallows GetMetricStatistics failures (no warn/permission_issue)  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/transfer_svc.py:transfer_svc.py:86-91`
- **Evidence:** except Exception: rec['DataTransferCostNote'] = 'CloudWatch unavailable — consider monitoring ... (~$0.09/GB) awareness'. No ctx.warn / ctx.permission_issue. A throttled or AccessDenied cloudwatch:GetMetricStatistics is recorded only as a cosmetic note.
- **Impact:** An IAM gap or throttle on cloudwatch:GetMetricStatistics vanishes from the scan's warnings/permission-issue ledger; the operator never learns the data-transfer evidence was unavailable. (Note never counted, so $0 impact, but masks a permission problem.)
- **Fix:** Classify the exception: AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation/OptInRequired -> ctx.permission_issue(..., 'transfer', 'cloudwatch:GetMetricStatistics'); else ctx.warn(..., 'transfer'). Reuse services/_aws_errors.record_aws_error as network does.

#### 🟡 M2 · Outer except always warns; never classifies AccessDenied on transfer:ListServers to permission_issue  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/transfer_svc.py:transfer_svc.py:105-106`
- **Evidence:** except Exception as e: ctx.warn(f'Could not analyze Transfer Family resources: {e}', 'transfer'). No branch routing AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation from transfer:ListServers / DescribeServer to ctx.permission_issue.
- **Impact:** An IAM gap on transfer:ListServers is reported as a generic warning rather than a permission issue, so it is not surfaced in the permission-issues channel — the whole adapter silently returns zero recs and the gap is easy to miss.
- **Fix:** Inspect the botocore error code; route AccessDenied/UnauthorizedOperation/OptInRequired to ctx.permission_issue('...', 'transfer', 'transfer:ListServers'); else ctx.warn.

#### 🟡 M3 · Module declares neither requires_cloudwatch nor reads_fast_mode despite reading CloudWatch gated on fast_mode  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/transfer.py:transfer.py:12-21 (class body); cf. transfer_svc.py:61-85 reads CW under 'if not ctx.fast_mode'`
- **Evidence:** TransferModule sets no requires_cloudwatch/reads_fast_mode; BaseServiceModule defaults both to False (services/_base.py:24-25). Yet the shim reads AWS/Transfer metrics and gates that read on ctx.fast_mode (transfer_svc.py:61).
- **Impact:** Contract/declaration desync: the orchestrator/registry cannot know transfer consumes CloudWatch or honors fast mode. Mirrors the Lambda/file_systems fix where these flags are declared. (No live $ impact, but a correctness-of-contract gap.)
- **Fix:** Declare requires_cloudwatch = True and reads_fast_mode = True on TransferModule (and add 'cloudwatch' to required_clients()) if the CW note is kept; or remove the CW read if the note is dropped.

#### 🟡 M4 · The one counted check carries no structured AuditBasis (rate/region/formula)  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/transfer.py:transfer.py:59-62`
- **Evidence:** EstimatedMonthlySavings is written as a bare rounded float; no AuditBasis dict (rate=$0.30/protocol-hr, hours=730, region, multiplier, removable count) is attached, unlike the Lambda PC findings.
- **Impact:** The counted number is not defensible from the report alone; an operator cannot see the rate/region/formula behind the dollar figure.
- **Fix:** Attach an AuditBasis (rate 0.30, hours 730, region, removable, multiplier) to each counted protocol_optimization rec.

#### 🟢 L1 · Data-transfer note uses $0.09/GB (generic S3 egress) instead of the Transfer Family fee $0.04/GB up + $0.04/GB down; 14-day Sum mislabeled '/mo'  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/transfer_svc.py:transfer_svc.py:82-85, 90`
- **Evidence:** DataTransferCostNote = f'~${total_gb*0.09:.2f}/mo S3 data transfer' (line 85) and fallback '~$0.09/GB' (line 90). Live AWS Pricing API (AWSTransfer): USE1-UploadBytes=$0.04/GB and USE1-DownloadBytes=$0.04/GB (both S3 and EFS backends; PGP DecryptBytes is a separate $0.10/GB). Also total_gb is a 14-day Sum (Period=86400*14, start=end-14d, transfer_svc.py:65-82) but the string says '/mo'.
- **Impact:** Misinforms the operator on the data fee (over-states per-GB by ~12% if read as the Transfer fee, or understates the round-trip $0.08/GB; and the monthly figure is computed from a 14-day window). Note is never counted, so $0 to the headline.
- **Fix:** Use $0.04/GB uploaded + $0.04/GB downloaded against the actual upload/download split (not the combined total), and project the 14-day window to a monthly figure (x30/14) or relabel as 14-day.

#### 🟢 L2 · Dead endpoint_optimization branch and $0 recs (non-endpoint fallback, single-protocol unused server) render as counted findings  ·  `confirmed_bug`
- **Location:** `services/transfer_svc.py; services/adapters/transfer.py:transfer_svc.py:28; transfer.py:54-57`
- **Evidence:** checks['endpoint_optimization'] is declared (transfer_svc.py:28) but never appended -> always empty. transfer.py:54-57: when Protocols is not a list, rec.setdefault('EstimatedMonthlySavings', 0.0) + continue leaves a $0 rec in recs. Empirically a STOPPED/OFFLINE single-protocol server yields EstimatedMonthlySavings=0.0 yet still appears as a recommendation. No rec ever sets Counted=False, so _counted_advisory_counts (html_report_generator.py:371-388) counts these $0 recs as 'counted', and render_generic_per_rec renders them.
- **Impact:** A $0.00 'counted' opportunity renders without the advisory marker, padding the recommendation count with zero-dollar cards (e.g. 'Estimated Savings: Full server hourly costs' + 'Estimatedmonthlysavings: 0.0'). Confuses the counted-vs-advisory split.
- **Fix:** Remove the unused endpoint_optimization key; set Counted=False on any rec whose EstimatedMonthlySavings<=0 (use services._savings.mark_zero_savings_advisory) so $0 recs are advisory not counted.

#### 🟢 L3 · Doc mislabels transfer under 'Live Pricing' and required_clients omits 'cloudwatch'  ·  `limitation`
- **Location:** `services/adapters/CLAUDE.md; services/adapters/transfer.py:CLAUDE.md 'Live Pricing (19 adapters)' table transfer.py row; transfer.py:19-21`
- **Evidence:** CLAUDE.md files transfer (and glue/dynamodb/containers/apprunner) under the 'Live Pricing' section whose preamble says to use ctx.pricing_engine for AWS Pricing API lookups, but transfer uses only a module constant (transfer.py:41) and never calls the Pricing API. required_clients() returns ('transfer',) only though the shim uses ctx.client('cloudwatch') (transfer_svc.py:63) — lazily provided by ClientRegistry (scan_context.py:70-72) so no runtime failure.
- **Impact:** Documentation/contract drift; a reader expects a live API call and a declared cloudwatch dependency that are absent.
- **Fix:** Move the transfer row to a 'Module constant' grouping (or relabel the section), and add 'cloudwatch' to required_clients() with requires_cloudwatch/reads_fast_mode (see M3).
